# Luciel — Drifts (Open and Resolved)

**What this document is:** The single ledger of every gap between the design (`ARCHITECTURE.md` + `CANONICAL_RECAP.md`) and the implementation (this repository, and the running production environment in AWS `ca-central-1`). Each gap is a token with a stable id, a status, and a resolution path.

**What this document is not:** A changelog. A version-history dump. A historical narrative. Closed drifts stay in the doc with a strikethrough so the audit chain of decisions remains walkable, but the document does not accumulate sediment beyond that.

**Maintenance protocol:** Surgical edits only. New drifts are appended with a unique id. Closed drifts get the closing commit/tag noted and the heading wrapped in strikethrough (`~~`). Reopened drifts get a new id; the original stays closed.

---

## Section 1 — Status legend and id scheme

**Status values:**

- `OPEN` — gap exists; no fix in flight
- `IN-PROGRESS` — fix is in flight on a named branch or PR
- `RESOLVED` — fix has landed on `main`; closing commit/tag noted; heading wrapped in `~~strikethrough~~`
- `DEFERRED` — gap acknowledged, deliberate decision to not fix this cycle; rationale recorded inline
- `WONTFIX` — gap re-examined and judged not a drift (design changed, or claim was wrong); rationale recorded inline

**Implementation marker scheme** (used in `ARCHITECTURE.md` and `CANONICAL_RECAP.md` once Phase 2 reconciliation begins applying them):

- ✅ Implemented — repo and prod both match the design
- 🔧 Partial — repo or prod implements some of the design; gaps tracked as drifts here
- 📋 Planned — design committed, no implementation yet; tracked as drift here
- 🔬 Decision-gate — design says "we will choose later"; not a drift, an open product decision

**Drift id scheme:** `D-<short-slug>-YYYY-MM-DD`. The date is when the drift was first opened, not when it was discovered later. Slug is short, hyphenated, and stable — never rename a slug after creation.

**Source of truth:** When this document, the architecture document, the canonical recap, the repository, or production disagree, the resolution is recorded here as a drift. The four artifacts converge by closing drifts, not by editing one and hoping the others catch up.

---

## Section 2 — Phase 2A repo reconciliation: how this register was built

This document was rebuilt on 2026-05-09 by walking `ARCHITECTURE.md` and `CANONICAL_RECAP.md` section by section against the repository at commit `c3ed8b6` on `main`. The previous DRIFTS.md (a partial, history-shaped register) was archived to `docs/archive/DRIFTS_pre-reconciliation.md` rather than discarded; that file remains the historical record up to that point.

The comparison covered:

- Architecture §2 — Development environment
- Architecture §3 — Production environment (every subsection)
- Architecture §4 — Cross-cutting properties
- Architecture §5 — Conceptual model
- Canonical Recap §1 — The two layers (Soul and Profession)
- Canonical Recap §2 — Six components
- Canonical Recap §3 — Cognitive abilities
- Canonical Recap §4 — Behavior contracts
- Canonical Recap §6 — Operating loop
- Canonical Recap §10 — Fixed-vs-configurable matrix
- Canonical Recap §11 — Eight strategic answers
- Canonical Recap §13 — End-to-end testing scenarios

Every drift below is tagged with the section that raised it. Production-only drifts (where the repo matches the design but production does not, or where we cannot tell from the repo alone) are tagged `[PROD-PHASE-2B]` and will be confirmed during Phase 2B with the operator at the PowerShell.

## Section 3 — Open drifts (repository scope)

### D-arc9-doctrine-reanchor-umbrella-2026-05-22
**Status:** OPEN — P0 umbrella, doctrine-blocking. Surfaced 2026-05-22 ≈13:17 EDT by the partner during the post-WU-2/WU-3 review of Arc 8 ship work, after delivering a V2 reconstruction of CANONICAL_RECAP (preserved at `docs/in-flight/Luciel-V2-canonical-input-2026-05-22.md`). The V2 reconstruction surfaced five over-engineering defect classes (named A–E in `arc9-out/A-arc9-doctrine-reanchor-arc-record.md` §2) and a clarified product vision the live canonical trio had drifted from. Partner's call: *"I hope we update and properly configure our docs to support our vision so we can continue with our roadmap. We might need to modify the roadmap a little to support our vision. We have over engineered a lot."* And: *"I would let us truthify the docs and then we can get to shipping the right things again."* This umbrella drift opens Arc 9 as a first-class doctrine-only arc; all ship work (Arc 8 WU-6, Arc 5 schema migration, Arc 6 Stripe restructure, Phase 6 E2E replay) is paused until Arc 9 closes.
**Section that raised it:** Arc 8 WU-2/WU-3 close ceremony, immediately after commit `c90b9f2` landed the Q1 surgical rewrite + `D-same-admin-tier-transition-doctrine-hole` drift. Partner's V2 reconstruction was delivered shortly thereafter and revealed the rewrite was directionally correct but scoped too narrowly — the over-engineering pattern is wider than a single Q1 row.
**Raised by:** Partner during V2 reconstruction review.
**Doctrine claim:** The canonical trio (CANONICAL_RECAP ↔ ARCHITECTURE ↔ DRIFTS) is the load-bearing asset of the business. Three-doc triangulation — every fact stated from each doc's own angle — is what makes the doctrine read as truth on first read. Annotation-patched legacy prose, four-tier scar tissue in code defending a doctrine that's been collapsed, and an 18-dimension entitlement matrix in a buyer-facing section all violate the doctrine-reads-as-truth rule. Arc 9 re-anchors the trio against V2 verbatim where V2 sharpens, then resumes ship work against a clean foundation.
**Repo state:** Live canonical trio carries the five defect classes named in `arc9-out/A-arc9-doctrine-reanchor-arc-record.md` §2. Live code carries ~4,025 callsites of legacy nouns (`tenant_id`, `agent_id`, `LucielInstance`, etc.) and a 13-layer cascade defending the four-tier teardown shape. Live `arc4-out/` carries the Arc 5 + Arc 6 execution plan against the pre-V2 doctrine and will be re-scoped at WU-9.7. The V2 input artifact is preserved at `docs/in-flight/Luciel-V2-canonical-input-2026-05-22.md`.
**Operational impact today:** Zero customer-visible impact (no live customers; `co-354c5056` was retired at Step 30a.2-pilot). Impact is doctrine-velocity: every ship commit against the muddled trio accumulates drift faster than the team can close it. Resuming Arc 8 WU-6, Arc 5, or Arc 6 before Arc 9 closes would compound that drift.
**Owning roadmap step:** Arc 9 (this arc; full work-unit plan at `arc9-out/A-arc9-doctrine-reanchor-arc-record.md` §3).
**Resolution path:**

1. **WU-9.1** — V2 absorb into CANONICAL_RECAP §1–§11 (mechanical pass; V2 is partner's own writing).
2. **WU-9.2** — Roadmap trim of §12 with partner sign-off; scar rows archived to §12.Z.
3. **WU-9.3** — §14 simplification to V2's 4-column abstract shape; per-dimension detail moved to ARCHITECTURE.
4. **WU-9.4** — §13 T-scenarios end-to-end rewrite against V2 model.
5. **WU-9.5** — ARCHITECTURE re-anchor; "Live today" vs "Designed but not built" marked honestly per section.
6. **WU-9.6** — DRIFTS reconciliation (every OPEN drift classified COLLAPSED / SHARPENED / UNCHANGED).
7. **WU-9.7** — Arc 5 + Arc 6 scope revision against V2 (expected: substantial shrinkage).
8. **WU-9.8** — Arc 9 close + symmetry verification; closing tag `arc-9-doctrine-reanchor-complete`.

**Pattern E:** Doctrine arc — not the `add → cutover → cleanup` shape that governs code arcs. The shape is `propose → partner-sign-off → land`, repeated per WU. Rollback path is `git revert` of the WU commit since every WU is doc-only.
**Validation evidence:** None today (arc just opened). Closure evidence: (a) every OPEN drift in DRIFTS §3 has either closed or been re-anchored against V2; (b) CANONICAL_RECAP §1–§14 reads as truth on first read with zero annotation-block patches; (c) ARCHITECTURE §1–§4 reads as truth on first read; (d) `arc4-out/` artifacts re-scoped against V2; (e) Arc 5 + Arc 6 ready to execute against the V2-anchored doctrine; (f) closing tag `arc-9-doctrine-reanchor-complete` stamps on WU-9.8 final commit.
**Cross-refs:** `arc9-out/A-arc9-doctrine-reanchor-arc-record.md` (full work-unit plan + discipline locks); `docs/in-flight/Luciel-V2-canonical-input-2026-05-22.md` (V2 doctrine source-of-record); `D-tenancy-collapse-admin-instance-lead-2026-05-22` (sibling — the Arc 4 tenancy collapse Arc 9 re-scopes; Arc 9 does NOT supersede this drift, it sharpens it under V2); `D-same-admin-tier-transition-doctrine-hole-2026-05-22` (child — partial fix from commit `c90b9f2`; Arc 9 WU-9.1 absorbs the V2 sharper framing for this gap, including the bidirectional upgrade/downgrade clause); `D-q6-personnel-rotation-collapsed-into-q1-and-section-14-2026-05-22` (child — the §11 Q6 collapse landed in WU-9.1); `D-enterprise-metering-not-implemented-2026-05-22` (sibling — survives Arc 9 because the Enterprise hybrid billing shape is preserved from live canonical); `D-free-tier-captcha-missing-2026-05-22` (sibling — survives Arc 9 because Free signup abuse control is orthogonal to tier-shape doctrine); `D-ses-feedback-loop-not-wired-2026-05-22` + `D-ses-suppression-app-layer-not-implemented-2026-05-22` (siblings — Arc 8 WU-6 surface, paused for Arc 9, resumes immediately on close); `arc4-out/A-tenancy-collapse-arc-record.md` + `arc4-out/A-tier-matrix-detail.md` (Arc 4 artifacts — re-scoped at WU-9.7).

### D-q6-personnel-rotation-collapsed-into-q1-and-section-14-2026-05-22
**Status:** OPEN — P1 doctrine-resolution drift. Surfaced 2026-05-22 ≈13:29 EDT during Arc 9 WU-9.1 (V2 absorb pass). The V2 reconstruction (`docs/in-flight/Luciel-V2-canonical-input-2026-05-22.md` §11) dropped the prior `Q6 — What happens when scope-level personnel get promoted, demoted, or leave entirely?` row, keeping only seven strategic questions. Partner confirmed the intent during WU-9.1 sign-off: *"If an admin has its own and upgrade or downgrade between tiers. I dont think we need Q6."* The Q6 substance (data lives with the Admin scope, mandatory key rotation on role change, immutable audit, role binding by tier) is not abandoned — it is **operational property of Q1's single-Admin-as-permission-root shape**, not a separate strategic question. The role-binding-by-tier table from Q6's status cell migrates to **CANONICAL_RECAP §14** as an entitlement-matrix row in WU-9.3.
**Section that raised it:** CANONICAL_RECAP §11 V2 absorb (Arc 9 WU-9.1).
**Raised by:** V2 reconstruction (partner authored); confirmed by partner during WU-9.1 sign-off (2026-05-22 ≈13:31 EDT): *"sounds correct partner go ahead"* after the agent's vision-readback proposed the Q6 collapse explicitly.
**Doctrine claim:** Strategic questions in §11 are first-order product decisions — the questions that shape what Luciel IS. Rotation, departure, promotion, and demotion are not first-order — they are entitlement-and-policy properties of the single-Admin-as-permission-root shape (Q1) combined with the role-binding-by-tier matrix (§14). Keeping Q6 as a peer of Q1 over-stated its independence and bloated §11's strategic surface from 7 to 8 questions. Truth on first read demands §11 reads as the minimal set of decisions that define the product; everything else is operational property of those decisions, stored where operational properties belong.
**Repo state (this commit):** §11 Q6 row deleted from CANONICAL_RECAP. Q1 question text and answer text expanded to absorb the rotation-and-departure substance (data-belongs-to-Admin, mandatory key rotation, audit-log-shows-who-when). §11 "eight questions" header rewritten to "seven questions" with an Arc 9 renumbering note pointing here. Channels Q7→Q6 and cross-channel Q8→Q7 renumbered. Downstream Q-token references in §12 (Steps 24.5c, 28, 29, 30b, 30d, 31, 33b, 34, 34a, 38), §13.1 (T6/T7/T8 Q-token tags + header), and ARCHITECTURE §3.2.5 / §3.2.12 triangulation lines updated for the new numbering. ARCHITECTURE §4.5 + §4.6 (cascade-correct departure + Pattern E for secrets) **unchanged at the body level** — the architecture for rotation/departure was already correct; only the Q-token labels above it shifted. §14 role-binding-by-tier row addition deferred to WU-9.3. Historical text in DRIFTS §3 Pass-8 cross-ref wiring entries (`D-canonical-recap-cross-references-asymmetric-2026-05-13`, `D-canonical-recap-section-12-table-overflow-2026-05-14`) and §17 maintenance log entry `2026-05-22-late` preserved as authored — those describe what was true at the time of those passes (Q1–Q8 then; Q1–Q7 now). No version-history sediment rule means the audit chain reads the renumbering correctly: the prior text describes a prior state and is dated; current text reflects current state.
**Operational impact today:** Zero customer-visible impact. Doctrine velocity benefit: §11 now reads as 7 minimal strategic questions, the strongest read-cold ordering. T-scenario labels (T1–T8) preserved to keep historical references in DRIFTS / arc-records / git from dangling; only the Q-token tags inside each T-row updated. Full §13 restructure (renumber T-rows too, drop the legacy `agent at a brokerage → department lead` framing for T6, add tier-transition T-scenarios for Q1 + Q5) deferred to Arc 9 WU-9.4.
**Owning roadmap step:** Arc 9 WU-9.1 (this commit) + Arc 9 WU-9.3 (§14 role-binding-by-tier entitlement row addition) + Arc 9 WU-9.4 (§13 T-scenario restructure).
**Resolution path:**

1. WU-9.1 — §11 Q6 collapse landed (this commit). ✅
2. WU-9.3 — §14 entitlement matrix gains a `role binding by tier` row carrying the Free/Pro two-role set vs Enterprise three-role set distinction the old Q6 status cell named.
3. WU-9.4 — §13 T-scenarios fully restructured against V2 model: T6 reframed to canonical Admin/Instance/Lead vocabulary; tier-transition T-scenarios added for Q1 (same-Admin upgrade/downgrade) and Q5 (cross-Admin re-parenting).
4. WU-9.8 — closure verification: §11 reads as 7 questions, all Q-token references in the trio are coherent, T-scenario labels stable, §14 carries the rotation-entitlement row.

**Pattern E:** Doctrine collapse — not deletion. The Q6 substance is not deleted; it is relocated to where operational properties belong (§14 entitlement matrix + ARCHITECTURE §4.5/§4.6 system view + this drift's audit-chain entry). The relocation makes §11 a stronger read-cold ordering without losing any doctrine claim.
**Validation evidence:** This commit. Closure evidence: WU-9.3 §14 row landed + WU-9.4 §13 T-scenarios restructured + WU-9.8 symmetry verification confirms the rotation/departure doctrine is greppable from §14 + ARCHITECTURE §4.5 + ARCHITECTURE §4.6 without the Q6 anchor.
**Cross-refs:** `D-arc9-doctrine-reanchor-umbrella-2026-05-22` (parent); `D-same-admin-tier-transition-doctrine-hole-2026-05-22` (sibling — the bidirectional tier-mobility doctrine V2 absorbed in the same WU-9.1 commit); `D-tenancy-collapse-admin-instance-lead-2026-05-22` (sibling — the tenancy noun rename; this drift is the Q-numbering collapse on top of that noun collapse); `arc9-out/A-arc9-doctrine-reanchor-arc-record.md` §3 WU-9.1 (work-unit plan); `docs/in-flight/Luciel-V2-canonical-input-2026-05-22.md` §11 (V2 source); CANONICAL_RECAP §11 (the surface where the collapse landed); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 + §13.1 (downstream Q-token reference cleanups); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.5 + §3.2.12 (triangulation-line cleanups); ARCHITECTURE §4.5 + §4.6 (system-view doctrine for departure and Pattern E for secrets — unchanged at the body, the architecture was always correct here).

### D-tenancy-collapse-admin-instance-lead-2026-05-22
**Status:** OPEN — P1 umbrella, business-critical. Surfaced 2026-05-22 in Arc 4 design pass; revised 2026-05-22-late to fold in the three-tier shape (Free / Pro / Enterprise) with Enterprise on a hybrid billing model. The canonical model across all tiers is `Admin → Instance(s) → Lead(s)` (see CANONICAL_RECAP §1, §11 Q1, §14). The tier surface is **Free / Pro / Enterprise** — one product, capacity-gated, with Enterprise on a hybrid billing model (platform fee + included usage + overage; committed-use discount). This collapse completes the flattening begun at Step 30a.6 (2026-05-20): Team tier was flattened then; Arc 4 extends the same move to retire Company tier entirely, replaces Solo with Pro, adds Free as a $0 evaluation tier, and renames every load-bearing noun (`Tenant → Admin`, `Agent → Instance`, `Domain` removed entirely). The doc layer has been updated (CANONICAL_RECAP / ARCHITECTURE / DRIFTS / arc4-out artifacts). The implementation layer has not yet been updated — every reference to `tenant`, `domain`, `agent` (the AI-worker noun), `LucielInstance`, `TIER_INDIVIDUAL` / `TIER_TEAM` / `TIER_COMPANY` in the codebase and in production carries forward-drift until the rename sweep, schema migration, and Stripe SKU restructure land.
**Section that raised it:** Arc 4 design pass, 2026-05-22; revised at the Arc 4 tier-shape revision pass, 2026-05-22-late. Surfaced by (a) the partner direction to fold `docs/VISION.md` (the doctrine draft) into the three canonical docs rather than leaving it as a standalone fourth surface, and (b) the partner's tier-shape acceptance: "we should just have free, pro, and enterprise. I feel like enterprise should be fully unlimited and a pay per use basis. Although I am not sure how to position this?"
**Raised by:** Aryan (partner) on 2026-05-22, in the direction-setting message: "sure go ahead partner why are we not improving the three docs that we always maintain like the canonical and drifts and architecture. We agreed that these three docs together maintain a set of symmetry and discipline to capture our entire business scope?"
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §1 reads: "an Admin can instantiate as one or more Instances"; §11 Q1 commits the flat `Admin → Instance(s) → Lead(s)` model as the canonical shape at every tier; §11.7 commits the public-positioning copy for Free / Pro / Enterprise; §14 commits the **three-tier capacity-gated framework (Free / Pro / Enterprise)** with Enterprise on hybrid billing as the live doctrine; ARCHITECTURE §3.2 commits the unified `Admin → Instance → Lead` topology + three-tier surface; §3.2.14 NEW commits the metering hook + `billing_model` enum (`flat` / `hybrid` / `consumption`) on the `subscriptions` table; §4.1 commits the three-axis isolation contract (`admin` / `instance` / `lead`) with Free as the no-`subscriptions`-row exception; §4.7 commits the entitlement-policy module shape with the Free-CAPTCHA gate and the Enterprise metering gate. The implementation (schema, service layer, entitlements module, cascade chain, provisioning service, Stripe SKU set) still speaks the four-tier shape (`TIER_INDIVIDUAL` / `TIER_TEAM` / `TIER_COMPANY`) + `tenant` / `domain` / `agent` / `LucielInstance` — creating a doc-vs-repo gap at every surface these nouns touch.
**Repo state:** Forward-drift is pervasive. Key surfaces:

- **Schema:** `tenants`, `domains`, `agents`, `luciel_instances` tables and every FK chain referencing them carry the old nouns. `subscriptions.billing_model` column does not yet exist; `admin_tier_overrides` table does not yet exist; `metering_emissions` cursor table does not yet exist.
- **Service layer:** `app/services/tier_provisioning_service.py` (premint walk names `TIER_INDIVIDUAL`, `TIER_TEAM`, `TIER_COMPANY` and the agent-scope / domain-scope branch logic); `app/services/admin_service.py` (`_enforce_tier_scope` maps tier → allowed scope_level); `app/middleware/session_cookie_auth.py` (references `TenantConfig.active`).
- **Policy module:** `app/policy/entitlements.py` — 18-dimension matrix authored at Step 30a.6 carries the four-tier shape; needs rewrite to three-tier shape (Free / Pro / Enterprise) + new Axis 7 (billing model) for Enterprise + override-read indirection for Enterprise rows via `admin_tier_overrides`.
- **Cascade chain:** 13-layer cascade in §4.1 of ARCHITECTURE referenced `domain`-layer cascade row; the Arc 4 rewrite removes the Domain layer, reducing it to a 12-layer cascade — this reduction must be reflected in the implementation at `app/services/admin_service.py` (deactivation cascade) and tested. The new `metering_emissions` table is **deliberately excluded** from the soft-delete cascade (audit-grade, outlives Admin lifecycle, same shape as `admin_audit_logs` exclusion under §4.4).
- **Provisioning:** `TierProvisioningService.premint_for_tier` — `TIER_INDIVIDUAL` maps to `TIER_PRO`; `TIER_TEAM` and `TIER_COMPANY` are retired; `TIER_FREE` is new (no Stripe customer/subscription rows; CAPTCHA-gated email verification only).
- **Role taxonomy:** `owner` / `tenant_admin` / `department_lead` / `teammate` in `app/models/subscription.py` and every role-check callsite; the new taxonomy is `owner` / `admin_user` / `instance_lead` / `member`. Enterprise-only addition: `delegated_admin` role gated by `admin_tier_overrides.delegated_admin_enabled`.
- **Billing webhook:** `billing_webhook_service.py` references `Tenant` and `TenantConfig`; rename to `Admin` / `AdminConfig`. The webhook discipline (signature-verified, idempotent via `last_event_id`, fail-closed) is unchanged.
- **Stripe SKU set:** Six live SKUs today (Individual monthly + annual, Team monthly + annual, Company monthly + annual); these archive at Arc 6 and are replaced by three products (Free $0, Pro monthly + annual, Enterprise hybrid = platform-fee Price + metered usage Price on the same subscription).
- **Audit log:** `AdminAuditLog` — name already matches the new noun (accidentally correct); no rename required.

**Operational impact today:** Zero customer-visible impact. No live tenant currently exists on the wire under the old model (the last live tenant, `co-354c5056`, was retired at Step 30a.2-pilot). The drift is a doc-vs-code gap, not a production regression. Impact escalates when the next customer signs up — they would sign up under the old four-tier code shape even though the docs commit the three-tier shape, and Free / Enterprise tiers cannot be sold at all until Arc 5 + Arc 6 land.
**Owning roadmap step:** Arc 4 — tenancy collapse execution. The migration runbook is `arc4-out/A-tenancy-collapse-arc-record.md` (Deliverable #3); each migration step opens a closeable sub-drift in this register as it completes.
**Resolution path:** A coordinated rename-and-collapse arc across six layers, sequenced to avoid a half-migrated state on `main` — **Arc 8 (security hardening) precedes Arc 5 (schema migration)** because Arc 8 touches `app/middleware/*.py` and `app/repositories/audit_chain.py` files Arc 5 will rename:

1. **Schema migration (Arc 5)** — Three Alembic revisions A/B/C. Revision A adds `subscriptions.billing_model` enum (`flat` / `hybrid` / `consumption`), creates `admin_tier_overrides` table (per-Admin nullable overrides for every entitlement axis plus `billing_model`, `included_usage_per_period`, `overage_rate_cents`, `committed_use_discount_bps`, `period_start`, `period_end`, `delegated_admin_enabled`), and creates `metering_emissions` append-only cursor table. Revision B renames `tenants → admins`, drops `domains` table and all FK columns referencing it, renames `agents → instances` (or the existing `luciel_instances` table to `instances`). Revision C backfills `subscriptions.billing_model='flat'` for existing rows. All FKs cascade via `ON UPDATE CASCADE` or explicit column renames per Alembic `op.alter_column`.
2. **Code rename sweep (Arc 5)** — ~4,025-callsite `find/replace` pass across `app/` and `tests/` for every noun: `tenant → admin`, `domain → ` (removed), `agent → instance` (the AI-worker sense), `LucielInstance → Instance`, `TenantConfig → AdminConfig`, `tenant_admin → admin_user`, `department_lead → instance_lead`, `TIER_INDIVIDUAL → TIER_PRO`. `TIER_TEAM` / `TIER_COMPANY` and all branch logic gated on them is removed. Automated where safe (identifier renames); manual review for prose strings and comments. Seven-batch sequencing per `arc4-out/A-tenancy-collapse-arc-record.md` §7.
3. **Entitlements module rewrite (Arc 5)** — `app/policy/entitlements.py` rewritten from 4-tier×18-dim to 3-tier×(18 entitlement + new Axis 7 hybrid-billing) dimensions; Enterprise rows consult `admin_tier_overrides` as a second source-of-truth read layered after the static map; the Free-CAPTCHA gate (§4.7 new gate) and the Enterprise metering gate (§3.2.14) are wired here.
4. **Stripe SKU restructure (Arc 6)** — Archive existing Solo / Team / Company products (monthly + annual SKUs each); create new **Free** product at $0/month with one $0 Price (no Stripe Checkout session at signup — Free is provisioned directly by `TierProvisioningService` after CAPTCHA-gated email verification, no Stripe customer/subscription rows are created); create new **Pro** product as a monthly recurring Price (with optional annual at 10× monthly = "one bill a year"); create new **Enterprise** product as a hybrid (recurring platform-fee Price + metered usage Price on the same subscription, `usage_type='metered'` on the usage Price). Customer-comms SES email goes out to existing Individual/Solo/Team/Company-tier customers confirming the migration plan, the price-point mapping (Solo → Pro at same price, Team / Company migration handled case-by-case per `arc4-out/A-tenancy-collapse-arc-record.md` §6).
5. **Test suite update (Arc 5)** — All tests that assert on the old noun set (`tenant_id`, `domain_id`, `agent_id`, `TIER_INDIVIDUAL` / `TIER_TEAM` / `TIER_COMPANY`) update to the new noun set + the three-tier constants. The existing 28-test AST contract suite and 33-test live e2e harness must remain green throughout. New unit tests cover the `billing_model` enum branches, the `admin_tier_overrides` override-read indirection, the metering emitter, and the Free-CAPTCHA gate.
6. **Cascade chain verification (Arc 5 closure)** — Confirm the 12-layer cascade (Domain layer removed; `metering_emissions` deliberately excluded as audit-grade) is consistent in the implementation and that `D-cascade-completeness-co-354c5056-2026-05-07` (Step 30a.7 closure) remains satisfied in the post-rename shape. The static-AST contract test from Step 30a.7 (`tests/services/test_cascade_includes_all_privilege_layers.py`) is updated to assert the 12-layer count and the `metering_emissions` exclusion.

**Pattern E:** This is a full rename + selective removal (Domain layer) + tier-surface restructure (4-tier → 3-tier) + Stripe SKU restructure + metering hook addition. The migration is subtractive at the Domain layer and the Team/Company tier surface, renaming at the Tenant/Agent/Instance layers, and additive for the metering hook + `admin_tier_overrides` + Free tier. Rollback path is the reverse Alembic migration + code revert + Stripe SKU restore from archive; the window for rollback closes the moment the first customer signs up under the new noun set + tier set.
**Validation evidence:** None today (doc layer only; no code lands until Arc 5 + Arc 6 execution lands). Closure evidence will be: (a) `alembic upgrade head` on a clean DB produces the `admins`, `instances`, `leads`, `admin_tier_overrides`, `metering_emissions` table set with no `tenants`, `domains`, `agents` tables; (b) `pytest` green on the full test suite with the new noun set + three-tier constants; (c) `app/policy/entitlements.py` carries `TIER_FREE` / `TIER_PRO` / `TIER_ENTERPRISE` (not `TIER_INDIVIDUAL` / `TIER_TEAM` / `TIER_COMPANY`); (d) the Stripe dashboard Free / Pro / Enterprise products exist and the Individual/Solo/Team/Company products are archived; (e) the resumed Journey 1 signs up an Admin at Free, provisions an Instance, and the `/app` dashboard renders the new noun set + Free-tier capacity gate without regression; (f) a follow-up Enterprise customer is provisioned via `admin_tier_overrides` (talk-to-sales path) with the metering emitter writing usage records to Stripe at the period close.
**Cross-refs:** `CANONICAL_RECAP.md` §1, §11 Q1/Q2/Q4/Q5/Q6, §11.7 NEW, §14 (full sub-section + v2 entitlement matrix annotation block), §17 (with 2026-05-22-late maintenance entry); `ARCHITECTURE.md` §3.2, §3.2.12, §3.2.13, §3.2.14 NEW (metering hook + `billing_model` enum), §4.1 (full rewrite + 2026-05-22-late annotation), §4.7 (with 2026-05-22-late annotation); `arc4-out/A-tier-matrix-detail.md` (Deliverable #2 — rewritten 2026-05-22-late from 4-tier×22-dim to **3-tier× (18 entitlement + new Enterprise hybrid-billing) axes** spec, `admin_tier_overrides` override surface extended with `billing_model` / `included_usage_per_period` / `overage_rate_cents` / `committed_use_discount_bps` / `period_start` / `period_end` columns, `instance_composition_grants` + `knowledge_share_grants` two-table contract, code-surface impact assessment); `arc4-out/A-tenancy-collapse-arc-record.md` (Deliverable #3 — execution runbook: three Alembic revisions A/B/C with Revision A extended to land `billing_model` enum + `admin_tier_overrides` extended columns + `metering_emissions` cursor table, seven-batch rename sweep, **three-product Stripe SKU restructure** (Free $0 product + Pro rename + Enterprise hybrid Price), customer-comms SES draft rewritten for Solo/Team/Company→Free/Pro/Enterprise tier rename, audit-chain integrity plan, risk register with the **Arc 8-before-Arc 5 sequence correction**, sub-drift activation map); `~~D-tier-semantics-realignment-2026-05-20~~` (this collapse completes what 30a.6 started); CANONICAL §14 §275 doctrinal reversal; `D-enterprise-metering-not-implemented-2026-05-22` (NEW — the runtime metering gap until the Celery-beat emitter ships); `D-free-tier-captcha-missing-2026-05-22` (NEW — the Free-tier abuse-control gap).

**Audit chain note (legacy v1 doctrine, preserved for traceability):** The v1 four-tier framing (Solo / Team / Company / Enterprise) committed in Arc 4 Deliverables #1–#3 (`66f6528` / `8c3e0b7` / `5c80c15`) is retired by the body rewrite above; the v1 prose lives in git at those three commits and at the v1 Arc 4 entries in CANONICAL_RECAP §17. The Arc 8-before-Arc 5 sequence correction (Arc 8 must precede Arc 5 because Arc 8 touches `app/middleware/*.py` and `app/repositories/audit_chain.py` files Arc 5 will rename; running Arc 8 second would force a merge conflict on every security-hardening commit. See `arc4-out/A-tenancy-collapse-arc-record.md` §12 (risk register — sequence row corrected). Two new sibling drifts open under this annotation: `D-enterprise-metering-not-implemented-2026-05-22` (P1, the runtime emitter gap) and `D-free-tier-captcha-missing-2026-05-22` (P2, the signup abuse-control gap).

### D-same-admin-tier-transition-doctrine-hole-2026-05-22
**Status:** OPEN — P2, doctrine gap (not a runtime gap). Surfaced 2026-05-22-late by the partner during the Q1 doc-truthing review: "what happens if an admin has account then then decides to upgrade to a upper tier?". The canonical recap settles two of the three upgrade shapes but leaves the third (same-Admin tier transition, e.g. Free→Pro on the same account row, or Pro→Enterprise where the Admin becomes their own Enterprise rather than joining an existing one) as **implicitly implied** by §11.7 + §14 + Step 30a but not **explicitly named** as a settled product decision in §11. The Q1 row (post-rewrite, 2026-05-22-late) now covers initial provisioning; Q5 covers cross-Admin re-parenting; nothing covers same-Admin tier transition by name. This is a doctrine-readability defect, not a runtime defect: the code path is the Stripe webhook `customer.subscription.updated` for Free→Pro and an operator-mediated tier flip + `admin_tier_overrides` row for solo-Pro→Enterprise.
**Section that raised it:** Q1 doc-truthing pass, 2026-05-22-late. Partner question exposed the gap immediately after the Q1 surgical rewrite landed.
**Raised by:** Partner during the Q1 review.
**Doctrine shape (proposed, settle at deferred Q1.5 commit):** The three upgrade paths are: (a) **Free→Pro, same Admin** — Stripe Checkout self-serve flips `billing_model='subscription'` + `tier='pro'` on the existing Admin row via `customer.subscription.updated` webhook; existing Instances, Leads, knowledge, conversations, audit chain all stay in place; composition depth lifts 0→2; existing operational keys keep working; one `TIER_UPGRADED` audit-chain event row. (b) **Pro→Enterprise, same Admin (becomes own Enterprise)** — sales-mediated tier flip on the existing Admin row: operator sets `tier='enterprise'` + creates `admin_tier_overrides` row + switches `billing_model='hybrid'` after contract sign; same-row preservation as (a); one `TIER_UPGRADED` audit-chain event row with contract reference. (c) **Free/Pro→Enterprise, joining existing Enterprise org** — the Admin→Admin re-parenting transaction already settled at Q5 / Step 38; two Admin rows involved, source Admin closed with pro-rated credit, source Instances moved into destination Enterprise Admin scope. Path (a) and (b) are same-Admin; path (c) is cross-Admin.
**Repo state:** Path (a) has partial code-layer coverage — the Stripe `customer.subscription.updated` webhook handler in `app/api/v1/billing/stripe_webhook.py` does flip the subscription row but the **tier-cascade side-effects** (composition depth unlock, channel unlock, dashboard view unlock) are not consolidated into a single `TierTransitionService` and are not audit-chain-stamped as a coherent event. Path (b) has zero code-layer coverage — there is no operator tier-flip surface; today it would be a hand-run SQL `UPDATE` against the Admin row plus a hand-inserted `admin_tier_overrides` row, neither of which would chain into the audit log. Path (c) has zero code-layer coverage (covered by Step 38 / Q5, planned).
**Operational impact today:** Zero customer-visible impact (no Pro customers exist yet). Impact escalates at first Pro customer self-upgrade (path a) and at first Enterprise sale (path b): without `TierTransitionService` consolidation, the cascade side-effects are scattered across handlers and there is no single audit-chain row that proves "on this date this Admin moved from tier X to tier Y under contract Z".
**Owning roadmap step:** End-of-Arc-8 doc-truthing pass (the doctrine portion — Q1.5 row + Q5 cross-ref note). The code-layer consolidation (`TierTransitionService` + `TIER_UPGRADED` audit constant) lands in Arc 5 (schema migration adds the audit-action constant) + Arc 6 (Stripe SKU restructure wires the webhook into the service).
**Resolution path:**

1. **Doctrine layer (end-of-Arc-8):** add Q1.5 row to CANONICAL_RECAP §11 naming the three paths above; add cross-ref note to Q5 answer column distinguishing same-Admin from cross-Admin; mirror the same three-path summary into ARCHITECTURE §4.1 (Admin scope as billing boundary) as a new sub-bullet on tier transitions.
2. **Audit-action constant (Arc 5):** add `TIER_UPGRADED` to `app/models/admin_audit_log.py` action enum with standard chain-hashed field set (§4.3) plus the three transition-specific fields: `from_tier`, `to_tier`, `transition_path` (one of `same_admin_self_serve`, `same_admin_sales_mediated`, `cross_admin_reparent`).
3. **`TierTransitionService` (Arc 6):** author `app/services/tier_transition_service.py` with a single entry point per path. Path (a) is called from the Stripe webhook handler; path (b) is called from an operator-only admin endpoint (auth-gated by platform-admin scope); path (c) is the Q5 / Step 38 surface and is out of this drift's scope. All three paths chain a `TIER_UPGRADED` audit row in the same transaction as the side-effect cascade.
4. **Side-effect cascade enumeration:** explicit list, sourced from §14 entitlement matrix — composition depth flag, channel-availability flags, dashboard-view flags, key-rotation requirement on tier change (Q6 mandate already applies).

**Pattern E:** This is a doctrine-first, then code-second drift. The doctrine fix is small (one new Q1.5 row + two cross-ref notes) and lands in the end-of-Arc-8 doc-truthing pass. The code fix is naturally absorbed by Arc 5 + Arc 6 sequencing without forcing a separate ceremony.
**Validation evidence:** None today (defer). Closure evidence will be: (a) Q1.5 row exists in CANONICAL_RECAP §11 reading as truth on first read; (b) `TIER_UPGRADED` audit constant exists in `app/models/admin_audit_log.py`; (c) `TierTransitionService` exists with unit tests covering paths (a) and (b); (d) first end-to-end self-upgrade Free→Pro produces a single `TIER_UPGRADED` audit row with `transition_path='same_admin_self_serve'` and all cascade side-effects observable.
**Cross-refs:** `D-tenancy-collapse-admin-instance-lead-2026-05-22` (parent — defines the Admin→Instance→Lead canonical shape this drift specializes for transitions); `D-enterprise-metering-not-implemented-2026-05-22` (sibling — the Enterprise tier this drift's path (b) lands customers into); CANONICAL_RECAP §11 Q1 (post-rewrite) + Q5 (re-parenting), §11.7 (public positioning), §14 (entitlement matrix); ARCHITECTURE §4.1 (Admin scope as billing boundary); `arc4-out/A-tenancy-collapse-arc-record.md` §12 (risk register).

### D-enterprise-metering-not-implemented-2026-05-22
**Status:** OPEN — P1, business-critical for Enterprise tier launch. Surfaced 2026-05-22 in the Arc 4 tier-shape revision pass. The Enterprise tier ships with a **hybrid billing model** (platform fee + included usage + overage; committed-use discount available) per CANONICAL_RECAP §11.7 and §14. The doc layer commits the design at ARCHITECTURE §3.2.14 (metering hook + `billing_model` enum + `admin_tier_overrides` extensions + `metering_emissions` cursor table). The implementation layer carries none of it today: there is no `app/workers/metering_worker.py`, no `metering_emissions` table, no `subscriptions.billing_model` column, no Stripe metered Price wiring, and no Celery beat schedule entry for the hourly emission. Until those land, Enterprise tier cannot be sold — a deal closure today would have Luciel collecting the platform-fee Price but never invoicing the overage, which is both a revenue leak and a contract-compliance failure.
**Section that raised it:** Arc 4 tier-shape revision pass, 2026-05-22-late. Surfaced by the partner's hybrid-billing acceptance: "we should just have free, pro, and enterprise. I feel like enterprise should be fully unlimited and a pay per use basis. Although I am not sure how to position this?" → agent locked hybrid model with "starting at" floor positioning.
**Raised by:** Agent during the Arc 4 tier-shape revision pass, 2026-05-22-late, in the design-decision walkthrough on Enterprise billing posture.
**Design claim:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.14 commits the metering hook design: a Celery-beat usage emitter (`app/workers/metering_worker.py`) running hourly during a billing period and once at period close, reading the metered unit's running total from the appropriate source-of-truth table (`leads.created_at` or `traces.created_at` per the Admin's configured unit in `admin_tier_overrides`), computing the delta since the last successful emission via the `metering_emissions` cursor, emitting via `stripe.SubscriptionItem.create_usage_record(subscription_item_id, quantity=delta, action='increment')` with an idempotency key, and writing the cursor row + a `METERING_USAGE_EMITTED` audit row in the same SQLAlchemy transaction.
**Repo state:** None of the required artifacts exist on `main`:

- `app/models/subscription.py` carries no `billing_model` column on `Subscription`.
- `app/models/admin_tier_overrides.py` does not exist.
- `app/models/metering_emissions.py` does not exist.
- `app/workers/metering_worker.py` does not exist.
- `app/celeryconfig.py` (or equivalent beat-schedule config) carries no entry for the metering emitter.
- `app/models/admin_audit_log.py` carries no `METERING_USAGE_EMITTED` action constant.
- The Stripe SKU set has no Enterprise hybrid product (only Individual, Team, Company recurring SKUs from Step 30a.1 exist, with the intro-fee one-time Price from Step 30a.2).

**Operational impact today:** Zero customer-visible impact. No Enterprise customer exists; the Enterprise tier is doc-described but not provisionable. Impact escalates immediately at first Enterprise sale: without the emitter, every overage unit goes uninvoiced. The platform-fee Price would still bill (it is a flat recurring Stripe Price), so the customer would not see a billing failure — they would see Luciel under-charging silently, which surfaces as a revenue audit failure rather than a customer-facing one.
**Owning roadmap step:** Arc 5 (schema migration — lands `subscriptions.billing_model`, `admin_tier_overrides`, `metering_emissions`) + Arc 6 (Stripe SKU restructure — lands the Enterprise hybrid Price pair + the metering emitter worker + the Celery beat entry).
**Resolution path:**

1. **Arc 5 Alembic Revision A** — add `subscriptions.billing_model VARCHAR(16) NULL` with in-migration `UPDATE` backfilling pre-existing rows to `'flat'`; create `admin_tier_overrides` table with the eleven columns enumerated in ARCHITECTURE §3.2.14; create `metering_emissions` append-only table with `(admin_id, period, emission_ts)` primary key + `stripe_idempotency_key` + `quantity_emitted` columns.
2. **Arc 5 audit-action constant** — add `METERING_USAGE_EMITTED` to the action enum in `app/models/admin_audit_log.py` with the standard chain-hashed field set (§4.3).
3. **Arc 6 Stripe SKU restructure** — create the Enterprise hybrid product in Stripe: one recurring platform-fee Price + one metered usage Price on the same subscription (Stripe `recurring.usage_type='metered'` + `recurring.aggregate_usage='sum'` on the usage Price). Configure SSM keys `STRIPE_PRICE_ENTERPRISE_PLATFORM_FEE` and `STRIPE_PRICE_ENTERPRISE_USAGE_METERED`.
4. **Arc 6 metering worker** — author `app/workers/metering_worker.py` per the ARCHITECTURE §3.2.14 design (hourly Celery beat schedule entry + the four-step emit + cursor + audit + idempotency flow); wire it into the same `--beat` worker container used by the retention purge worker (§3.2.4).
5. **Arc 6 entitlement-policy extension** — extend `app/policy/entitlements.py` to read `admin_tier_overrides.billing_model` for Enterprise Admins and select the correct gate path (static-map gate for Free/Pro; override-consulted gate for Enterprise).
6. **Unit + integration tests** — cover the four failure modes: (a) Stripe API failure on emit leaves the cursor uncommitted and the next run retries the full delta; (b) idempotency-key collision is treated as success at the cursor level; (c) an Enterprise Admin with `billing_model='flat'` (negotiated flat-rate Enterprise) skips the emitter entirely; (d) the `consumption` enum value is reserved but not actively routed.

**Pattern E:** This is a new capability addition under the established `add → cutover → cleanup` shape: Arc 5 Revision A is the add; Arc 6 Stripe SKU + worker is the cutover; no cleanup pass is required because no prior shape is being replaced (Enterprise hybrid is a net-new product). Rollback path is the reverse Alembic migration + Stripe product archive + worker removal.
**Validation evidence:** None today (design only; no code lands until Arc 5 + Arc 6 ship). Closure evidence will be: (a) `alembic upgrade head` on a clean DB produces the three new artifacts (`subscriptions.billing_model` column, `admin_tier_overrides` table, `metering_emissions` table); (b) a seeded Enterprise Admin with a known usage pattern produces a `metering_emissions` row at the next hourly tick + a Stripe usage record with matching quantity + a `METERING_USAGE_EMITTED` audit row chained correctly; (c) the failure-mode tests above pass.
**Cross-refs:** `D-tenancy-collapse-admin-instance-lead-2026-05-22` (parent umbrella — this drift is one half of the Arc 4 tier-shape revision split-out); `D-free-tier-captcha-missing-2026-05-22` (sibling — the other half); `arc4-out/A-tenancy-collapse-arc-record.md` §3 (Alembic Revision A extended scope), §6 (Stripe SKU restructure), §12 (risk register — sequence row); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.14 (metering hook design); CANONICAL_RECAP §11.7 (public positioning copy) and §14 (entitlement matrix v2 annotation block).

### D-free-tier-captcha-missing-2026-05-22
**Status:** OPEN — P2, abuse-control hygiene. **Partial landing 2026-05-22-late at Arc 8 Work-Unit 5** (code-only commit, no deploy): the `POST /api/v1/billing/signup-free` route shell + `app/services/hcaptcha_service.py` + `settings.hcaptcha_secret_key` / `hcaptcha_verify_url` / `hcaptcha_site_key` field reservations + `tests/api/test_signup_free_shape.py` contract pin are now on `main`. Captcha-fail → HTTP 422 with `error_codes` list, captcha-not-configured → HTTP 501 (boot-safe), captcha-pass → HTTP 200 with `status="pending-arc-5"` (admin-row mint blocked on Arc 5 because the `admins` table does not exist yet). The `admins.last_signup_ip VARCHAR(45)` column folds into Arc 5 Revision A (do not land standalone — table does not exist pre-Arc-5). Remaining work: (a) marketing-site widget wiring; (b) SSM SecureString `HCAPTCHA_SECRET_KEY` provisioning; (c) Arc 5 lands the `admins` row mint + email-send + `last_signup_ip` capture + 1-per-IP soft gate; (d) `ADMIN_FREE_TIER_PROVISIONED` audit row in `app/repositories/audit_chain.py` (post-Arc-5 rename sweep).

Surfaced 2026-05-22 in the Arc 4 tier-shape revision pass. The Free tier ships at $0/month with no Stripe payment-method gate at signup. Email verification exists today (`magic_link_service.py` already enforces a verified email before the cookie session mints), and is **necessary but not sufficient** to bound a Free-tier abuse surface: a bad-faith actor can mint N email aliases on a disposable-email provider and provision N Free Admins, consuming the per-Admin static allowance (1 Instance, 10 leads/month, model-token budget) N times over. The required abuse-control surface is a CAPTCHA at signup + a 1-per-email-domain or 1-per-IP soft gate; neither exists today.
**Section that raised it:** Arc 4 tier-shape revision pass, 2026-05-22-late. Surfaced by the partner's Free-tier acceptance: "All saas products that I see partner have a free tier like openAIs codex and perplexity. It allows people to be able to try out the product and move up tiers as desired." → agent committed Free tier shape with email-verify + CAPTCHA + 1-per-email/IP as the abuse-control composition.
**Raised by:** Agent during the Arc 4 tier-shape revision pass, 2026-05-22-late, in the Free-tier limits acceptance flow.
**Design claim:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2 tier-shape note (2026-05-22-late) commits the Free-tier gate composition: "CAPTCHA-gated signup to bound abuse." ARCHITECTURE §4.7 (2026-05-22-late annotation) commits the gate as one of the two new enforcement gates introduced under this revision, composing with the existing three-layer scope enforcement.
**Repo state (as of Arc 8 Work-Unit 5 partial landing, 2026-05-22-late):**

- ~~No CAPTCHA dependency in `requirements.txt` (e.g. `hcaptcha-client` or a reCAPTCHA verify helper).~~ **Resolved at Arc 8 WU-5:** `httpx` (already in deps) handles the verify call directly — no SDK required. The verify shim lives at `app/services/hcaptcha_service.py`.
- ~~No CAPTCHA verify route on the marketing site's signup form or on `app/api/v1/billing.py`'s `/checkout` (Free does not use Checkout; the Free provisioning path will need its own route, e.g. `POST /api/v1/billing/signup-free`).~~ **Resolved at Arc 8 WU-5:** `POST /api/v1/billing/signup-free` route shell landed; route verifies the captcha and returns `status="pending-arc-5"` until Arc 5 mints the Admin row.
- No SSM key for the CAPTCHA verify secret. (Operator action required; tracked separately.)
- No 1-per-email or 1-per-IP soft gate in `app/services/tier_provisioning_service.py`. (Blocked on Arc 5 — `admins.last_signup_ip` column does not exist yet.)
- No CAPTCHA verify call-site on the website signup form. (Marketing site, not backend; tracked separately.)

**Operational impact today:** Zero customer-visible impact at this moment because no Free tier exists yet (the existing live customer was on Solo, which has a payment-method gate). Impact escalates immediately when Free launches: a single bad-faith actor can multi-account-mint Free Admins until our model-provider bill noticeably moves; the same actor can probe for Free-tier carry-over into Pro/Enterprise via re-parenting (Q5), which would land the same actor's prior model usage into a higher-tier Admin's audit chain in a way the audit chain has no semantic to mark as abusive.
**Owning roadmap step:** Arc 8 (security hardening — the natural home alongside worker-not-root, version endpoint, health endpoint, SES sandbox exit + feedback + suppression). Arc 8 must precede Arc 5 (schema migration) because Arc 8 touches `app/middleware/*.py` and `app/repositories/audit_chain.py` that Arc 5 will rename — running Arc 8 second would force a merge conflict on every security-hardening commit. See `arc4-out/A-tenancy-collapse-arc-record.md` §12 (risk register — sequence row corrected to Arc 8-before-Arc 5).
**Resolution path:**

1. **CAPTCHA provider selection** — hCaptcha (privacy-preserving, GDPR-friendly, free up to 1M requests/month) is the v1 pick; reCAPTCHA is the fallback if hCaptcha's accessibility posture proves a problem in practice. The choice is documented in this drift to lock the dependency-add decision in Arc 8.
2. **Backend verify route** — add `POST /api/v1/billing/signup-free` accepting `{email, display_name, captcha_token}`; verify the captcha token against the hCaptcha verify endpoint; reject with 422 on captcha failure; on success, run the 1-per-email + 1-per-IP soft gate (read `admins.email` and `admins.last_signup_ip` against the new request); on success, mint the Free Admin via `TierProvisioningService.provision_free_admin(email, ip)`.
3. **`admins.last_signup_ip` column** — add a nullable `VARCHAR(45)` column (IPv6-sized) to `admins` to back the 1-per-IP gate; populate it at signup for Free Admins and leave it NULL for Pro/Enterprise Admins (the gate only applies to Free).
4. **Website signup form** — add the hCaptcha widget to the Free signup form (separate flow from the Pro/Enterprise Checkout); wire the captcha token into the `POST /api/v1/billing/signup-free` request body.
5. **SSM key** — `HCAPTCHA_SECRET_KEY` SSM SecureString parameter for the verify-side secret.
6. **Audit hook** — emit an `ADMIN_FREE_TIER_PROVISIONED` audit row (chain-hashed per §4.3) with `{email_domain, ip_subnet}` field set for forensics in case an abuse pattern emerges.
7. **Soft-gate response shape** — a captcha-pass + soft-gate-fail returns 409 with `error.code='free_tier_quota_exceeded'`; the website shows a "You've already created a Free account from this email domain or network. Sign in or upgrade to Pro." message.

**Pattern E:** This is a new capability addition under the standard `add` shape: no prior shape is being replaced; the Free tier is net-new. Rollback path is removing the route + the widget + the SSM key + the column.
**Validation evidence:** None today (design only; no code lands until Arc 8 ships). Closure evidence will be: (a) a synthetic abuse test (mint 10 Free Admins from the same /24 subnet) is rejected by the soft gate after the first; (b) a captcha-failure response is 422 not 500; (c) the audit row carries the expected forensic field set; (d) the `D-stripe-checkout-no-email-validation-2026-05-18` sibling drift is unaffected (it covers a different surface).
**Cross-refs:** `D-tenancy-collapse-admin-instance-lead-2026-05-22` (parent umbrella — this drift is one half of the Arc 4 tier-shape revision split-out); `D-enterprise-metering-not-implemented-2026-05-22` (sibling — the other half); `D-worker-runs-as-root-in-container-2026-05-22` and `D-version-endpoint-hardcoded-not-build-sha-2026-05-22` and `D-health-version-endpoint-gated-by-apikey-auth-2026-05-22` and `D-ses-sandbox-exit-pending-2026-05-22` and `D-ses-feedback-loop-not-wired-2026-05-22` and `D-ses-suppression-app-layer-not-implemented-2026-05-22` (Arc 8 sibling-cohort — all land in the same security-hardening arc); `arc4-out/A-tenancy-collapse-arc-record.md` §12 (risk register — Arc 8-before-Arc 5 sequence); ARCHITECTURE §3.2 tier-shape note (2026-05-22-late) and §4.7 (2026-05-22-late annotation); CANONICAL_RECAP §11.7 (public positioning copy with the Free-tier abuse-control language) and §14 (entitlement matrix v2).

### ~~D-worker-runs-as-root-in-container-2026-05-22~~
**Status:** CLOSED 2026-05-22 at Arc 8 Work-Unit 2 paired deploy ceremony. Dockerfile gained `RUN useradd --create-home --uid 10001 --shell /usr/sbin/nologin luciel && chown -R luciel:luciel /app` followed by `USER luciel` before the final `CMD`. The same image runs both backend (uvicorn) and worker (celery) processes, so non-root posture applies to both services.

**Closure verification (2026-05-22 ≈12:15 EDT, live wire):**
- Code commit (Dockerfile USER directive + build_info wiring): `02e1989`
- Build-script hardening (`--platform linux/amd64 --provenance=false --sbom=false` + paranoid local `docker inspect` Stage 1b gate): `74df825`
- Deployed image digest: `sha256:5983a2af8859ef4be44993a23a91fffa4a4a590623a1c57ba53d19af4931d85a`
- Backend task-def: `luciel-backend:81`; Worker task-def: `luciel-worker:36`
- Worker task ARN: `arn:aws:ecs:ca-central-1:729005488042:task/luciel-cluster/a7dea540222a4f47a3a4beb7a3a7f442`
- `aws ecs execute-command ... -- ps -eo pid,user,uid,gid,comm` returned: `PID 1: celery user=luciel uid=10001 gid=10001` (plus 3 child celery processes also `luciel uid=10001`). The exec session worker (`ssm-session-wor`) and `ps` itself appear as `root` because ECS Exec spawns its session shell as root inside the container — this is documented AWS Exec behaviour and is **not** evidence that the container's main process runs as root. Canonical diagnostic is PID 1 / the application process, not the exec session's own uid.
- `aws ecs execute-command ... -- cat /etc/passwd` confirmed `luciel:x:10001:10001::/home/luciel:/usr/sbin/nologin` is present in the running container's `/etc/passwd`.
- `aws logs tail /ecs/luciel-worker --since 5m | Select-String -Pattern 'SecurityWarning'` returned zero matches (no Celery superuser warning emitted post-deploy).
- IAM dependency added: new inline policy `luciel-worker-ssmmessages-exec` on `luciel-ecs-worker-role` granting `ssmmessages:{CreateControlChannel,CreateDataChannel,OpenControlChannel,OpenDataChannel}` so ECS Exec can establish a session channel against the non-root container (the existing `luciel-worker-inline` policy only covered SQS + SSM Parameter Store, not the SSM messaging API surface).

**Diagnostic-correction note (agent error, recorded honestly):** the first deploy attempt at 2026-05-22 ≈11:34 EDT (image digest `sha256:9414390f...`) was diagnosed mid-ceremony as failing because `aws ecs execute-command ... -- id` reported `uid=0(root)`. This was a **diagnostic-tool error, not a real drift state**. `id` inside an ECS Exec session reports the exec session worker's uid (root, by AWS design), not the container's main process uid. The correct diagnostic is `ps -eo pid,user,uid,gid,comm` and reading PID 1 / the application process row. The wrong diagnostic led the agent to chase a BuildKit attestation-manifest theory (real footgun, but unrelated to the uid signal we were misreading) and ship a second build (`74df825`) with `--platform linux/amd64 --provenance=false --sbom=false`. The second deploy was redundant from a USER-directive correctness standpoint — the first image (`9414390f`) was already running celery as `luciel uid=10001`. However, the build hardening is **kept** because (a) it eliminates BuildKit attestation-blob ambiguity in future Fargate pulls (real defensive value) and (b) Stage 1b paranoid local `docker inspect` gate prevents image-misbuild from ever reaching ECR. Net effect: two deploys instead of one, ~30 min of operator time, but no production state corruption. The Dockerfile change landed correctly on the first build; the agent's diagnostic was wrong.

**Pre-closure body preserved for audit:**

User information: uid=0 euid=0 gid=0 egid=0`. The Dockerfile has no `USER` directive after the `pip install` layer, so the worker process runs as root inside the container.~~

### ~~D-version-endpoint-hardcoded-not-build-sha-2026-05-22~~
**Status:** CLOSED 2026-05-22 at Arc 8 Work-Unit 3 paired deploy ceremony (same ceremony that closed `~~D-worker-runs-as-root-in-container-2026-05-22~~` — these two drifts were always going to ride together because they share the Dockerfile + paired-redeploy ceremony). The Dockerfile now declares `ARG BUILD_GIT_SHA="unknown"` + `ENV BUILD_GIT_SHA=$BUILD_GIT_SHA` before any RUN/COPY layers; `app/core/build_info.py` reads the env at module import via `_read_git_sha()` (defaulting to `"unknown"` on empty/whitespace) and populates a module-level singleton `BUILD_INFO` dict with keys `app`, `version`, `git_sha`, `status`; `app/api/v1/health.py` returns `dict(BUILD_INFO)` (fresh copy per call to prevent mutation-poisoning). The version field reads via `importlib.metadata.version("luciel-backend")`. The image-digest field was deferred (ECS provides it via `ECS_CONTAINER_METADATA_URI_V4` at runtime, which is a separate hook and was not blocking the original drift's payload-superset closure).

### ~~D-buildkit-attestations-poison-fargate-image-selection-2026-05-22~~
**Status:** CLOSED-AT-DETECTION 2026-05-22 at Arc 8 Work-Unit 2 paired deploy ceremony — **filed and resolved in the same commit-pair (`74df825`)**. The drift was surfaced as a hypothesis during mid-ceremony diagnosis when the agent (incorrectly, see paired `~~D-worker-runs-as-root-in-container-2026-05-22~~` diagnostic-correction note) read `aws ecs execute-command ... -- id` returning `uid=0(root)` as evidence that the Dockerfile USER directive had not taken effect. Investigation revealed that Docker Desktop's BuildKit produces a multi-entry manifest list (image + SBOM-attestation + provenance-attestation) **even for single-architecture builds**, and that the manifest digest pushed to ECR can be ambiguously resolved by Fargate's image-pull layer — in principle, Fargate could select a non-image manifest entry (an attestation blob with no `User` config), causing the container to fall back to root. **In our case, this was not the actual cause of the uid signal we observed** (PID 1 was already `luciel uid=10001` on the first build `9414390f`; the `id` diagnostic was reporting the exec session shell's uid, not the application's). However, the BuildKit attestation footgun is a real, low-frequency, high-confusion failure mode worth permanent record so future arcs do not trip on it.
**Section that raised it:** Arc 8 Work-Unit 2 paired deploy ceremony, 2026-05-22 ≈11:50 EDT, during the diagnosis of the (incorrectly-read) uid signal from the first deploy.
**Raised by:** Agent during mid-ceremony diagnosis. Hypothesised first, then mitigated (correctly), then later discovered to have **not been the actual cause** of the originating signal. Recorded honestly because the mitigation is still defensive value.
**Design claim:** Six-pillar contract (reliability + traceability — deploys must produce a single deterministic image identity that Fargate resolves unambiguously). A manifest list with attestation entries adds non-determinism to image resolution; for ECS Fargate, where the runtime cannot fall back to alternate manifests at debug time, the safer posture is single-manifest images with no attestation blobs.
**Repo state at closure:** `scripts/deploy_arc8.ps1` Stage [1/7] now invokes `docker buildx build --platform linux/amd64 --provenance=false --sbom=false --build-arg BUILD_GIT_SHA=$Sha -t $Image --load .`; Stage [1b/7] runs `docker inspect --format='{{.Config.User}}'` and `--format='{{.Architecture}}'` on the built image and hard-fails the script if `User != 'luciel'` or `Architecture != 'amd64'`. Build output for the resulting deploy (`74df825`) shows a single `exporting manifest` line, no `exporting attestation manifest` line, no `exporting manifest list` line, and a smaller and more typical layer count.
**Operational impact today:** None today (the closure landed in the same commit-pair that filed the drift). Going forward, this drift's mitigation prevents an entire class of low-frequency Fargate image-selection ambiguity issues from recurring.
**Owning roadmap step:** Arc 8 Work-Unit 2 (closed in-flight); future deploy scripts (Arc 5 migration deploy, Arc 6 Stripe SKU deploy) should adopt the same build flags.
**Resolution path:** Adopted in `scripts/deploy_arc8.ps1` at commit `74df825`. Future deploy scripts should mirror the three flags (`--platform linux/amd64 --provenance=false --sbom=false`) and the Stage [1b] paranoid local `docker inspect` gate.
**Pattern E:** Build-script defensive hardening. No application code change, no schema change, no IAM change, no SSM change. Customer-visible surface change is zero.
**Validation evidence:** Build output of commit `74df825` shows a single-manifest image (no attestation blobs in the `exporting` lines); Stage [1b] gate passed with `User=luciel` and `Architecture=amd64`; deployed image digest `sha256:5983a2af8859ef4be44993a23a91fffa4a4a590623a1c57ba53d19af4931d85a`. The paired drift's closure also confirms the worker container's PID 1 is `luciel uid=10001` in production.
**Cross-refs:** `~~D-worker-runs-as-root-in-container-2026-05-22~~` (parent diagnostic context — this drift was surfaced as a sibling hypothesis during that drift's closure ceremony); `scripts/deploy_arc8.ps1` (the closure artifact — carries the three build flags and the Stage [1b] gate); commit `74df825` (the closure commit).

### ~~D-health-version-endpoint-gated-by-apikey-auth-2026-05-22~~
**Status:** CLOSED 2026-05-22-late at Arc 8 Work-Unit 4 scoping pass — **misfiled drift, no code change required**. The drift was authored against the path `/api/v1/health/version`, which **does not exist** as a live route. The real version endpoint is mounted at **`/api/v1/version`** (router chain: `app.include_router(api_router, prefix='/api/v1')` in `app/main.py:139` + `api_router.include_router(health.router)` in `app/api/router.py:16` + `@router.get('/version')` in `app/api/v1/health.py:7`). The real path **`/api/v1/version`** is already enumerated in `SKIP_AUTH_PATHS` at `app/middleware/auth.py:63` and was already publicly reachable at the time the drift was filed.
**Closure verification (2026-05-22-late, live wire):**
- `curl -sS -o - -w "\nHTTP %{http_code}\n" https://api.vantagemind.ai/api/v1/version` → `HTTP 200`, body `{"app":"Luciel Backend","version":"0.1.0","status":"ok"}` (public, no JWT).
- `curl -sS -o - -w "\nHTTP %{http_code}\n" https://api.vantagemind.ai/api/v1/health/version` → `HTTP 401`, body `{"detail":"Missing or invalid Authorization header. Use Bearer <api_key>"}` — the 401 is the auth middleware short-circuiting on a path that doesn't exist (middleware runs before FastAPI route dispatch, so a nonexistent path under the v1 prefix returns 401 not 404).
- `curl -sS -o - -w "\nHTTP %{http_code}\n" https://api.vantagemind.ai/health` → `HTTP 200`, body `{"status":"ok","service":"Luciel Backend"}` (public, no JWT).

**Diagnostic-correction note (agent error, recorded honestly):** the Arc 3 Work-Unit C deploy ceremony smoke walk at 2026-05-22 ≈ 02:23 EDT issued a curl against `/api/v1/health/version` (presumed-but-wrong path) and read the 401 response as evidence of an auth gate, when in fact it was evidence that the path itself was wrong. The correct probe path is `/api/v1/version`. The drift filing on 2026-05-22 propagated the path error into both the drift body and the paired drift (`D-version-endpoint-hardcoded-not-build-sha-2026-05-22`), which still has the same path error in its design claim and validation-evidence sentences. That paired drift remains OPEN (the hardcoded-`0.1.0` payload is genuinely a real drift), but its path string is corrected at Arc 8 Work-Unit 3 (the payload-fix work-unit). The deploy ceremony record at `arc3-out/B5-deploy-ceremony-record.md` carries the original (wrong-path) observation verbatim for traceability — corrections live here, not by rewriting the ceremony record.

### D-ses-iam-overgrant-unused-actions-2026-05-22
**Status:** OPEN — P3 IAM hygiene. Surfaced 2026-05-22 in Arc 3 B.3 ledger-correction discovery. The `LucielSESSendEmail` inline policy on `luciel-ecs-web-role` grants `ses:SendBulkEmail` alongside `ses:SendEmail` and `ses:SendRawEmail`, but the application layer (`app/services/email_service.py`) only ever calls `client.send_email` (SESv2 single-recipient path). `SendBulkEmail` is unused.
**Section that raised it:** Arc 3 B.3 SES IAM scout, 2026-05-22 ≈01:05 EDT. The agent inspected the live policy attachment while authoring the B.3 ledger-correction record.
**Raised by:** Agent during the B.3 ledger-correction scout.
**Design claim:** Six pillars: security (least-privilege) and traceability (the IAM policy should mirror the application's send-shape contract). The current overgrant is small but is a category of drift we should not let accrete.
**Repo state:** No repo-side defect; the drift is in AWS infra (IAM inline policy on `luciel-ecs-web-role`). The policy was authored before the SESv2 migration narrowed the send-shape to single-recipient transactional only.
**Operational impact today:** Nil — unused actions cannot be exploited because the app does not call them. The risk is purely audit-shape: a future security scan would flag the overgrant. The widening to `identity/*` planned at the SES sandbox exit (Arc 8) is the natural moment to also drop the unused `SendBulkEmail` action.
**Owning roadmap step:** Arc 8 IAM-hardening sub-arc; paired naturally with the SES sandbox-exit identity-ARN widening so the IAM redeploy is a single touch.
**Resolution path:** Edit the inline policy on `luciel-ecs-web-role` to drop `ses:SendBulkEmail` from the `Action` array while widening `Resource` to `arn:aws:ses:ca-central-1:729005488042:identity/*` per `D-ses-sandbox-exit-pending-2026-05-22`'s post-exit shape. One `iam put-role-policy` call.
**Pattern E:** Pure IAM-layer subtractive change. No application-layer touch, no schema change, no SSM change. The least-privilege win is bounded but real.
**Validation evidence:** Closure evidence will be an `aws iam get-role-policy --role-name luciel-ecs-web-role --policy-name LucielSESSendEmail` that returns an `Action` array containing only `ses:SendEmail` and `ses:SendRawEmail`, plus the next post-exit SES smoke walk continuing to succeed (proves the application's send path is unaffected by the subtraction).
**Cross-refs:** `arc3-out/B3-ses-iam-no-op-record.md` (the ledger-correction record that surfaced this drift); `D-ses-sandbox-exit-pending-2026-05-22` (the natural pairing for the IAM redeploy); `~~D-luciel-ecs-web-role-missing-ses-send-permission-2026-05-18~~` (the parent drift whose closure surfaced this child).

### D-ses-sandbox-exit-pending-2026-05-22
**Status:** OPEN — P2 deliverability runway. Surfaced 2026-05-22 in Arc 3 B.4 ticket-draft work. The SES account in `ca-central-1` is in sandbox mode (`ProductionAccess=false`), meaning only pre-verified identities receive email. Until sandbox exit, every welcome-email send to a non-verified address fails with `AccessDeniedException`. The ticket text is drafted at `arc3-out/B4-ses-sandbox-exit-request.md` (transactional-only, 1:1 opt-in, ca-central-1, vantagemind.ai); operator submits via AWS Console.
**Section that raised it:** Arc 3 B.4 ticket-draft work, 2026-05-22 ≈01:15 EDT. Surfaced as a planned-and-tracked async dependency on AWS Support approval.
**Raised by:** Agent during the B.4 ticket-draft authoring.
**Design claim:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (Auth model — Option B welcome-email mechanic) commits that every redeemable invite ships a welcome email. Under sandbox SES, this contract is conditional on the recipient address being pre-verified; post-exit, the contract becomes unconditional. The exit is a hard prerequisite for the public-launch posture.
**Repo state:** No repo-side defect; the drift is in AWS account-level SES configuration. The ticket text is committed at `arc3-out/B4-ses-sandbox-exit-request.md` (commit `d46caa8`).
**Operational impact today:** Bounded — known-allowlist sends work, non-allowlist sends fail loudly with `AccessDeniedException`. Customer impact today is zero (no non-allowlist customer flow is live). The exit unlocks public-launch onboarding.
**Owning roadmap step:** Async — awaits AWS Support approval (typical 24-72h turnaround). On approval, the SES IAM widening (`D-ses-iam-overgrant-unused-actions-2026-05-22`), feedback-loop wiring (`D-ses-feedback-loop-not-wired-2026-05-22`), suppression-layer (`D-ses-suppression-app-layer-not-implemented-2026-05-22`), and reply-to inbox confirmation (`D-ses-reply-to-monitored-inbox-not-confirmed-2026-05-22`) all open for paired execution.
**Resolution path:** Operator submits the ticket text at `arc3-out/B4-ses-sandbox-exit-request.md` via AWS Console (SES → Account dashboard → Request production access). Track the case ID; on approval, fire the four paired follow-ups above.
**Pattern E:** Pure AWS-account-config change. No code, no schema, no SSM, no IAM (the IAM widening is paired but is its own drift). The approval is the gate.
**Validation evidence:** Closure evidence will be an `aws sesv2 get-account` call in `ca-central-1` that returns `ProductionAccess=true`, plus a post-exit smoke send to a non-allowlist address that returns a `MessageId` rather than `AccessDeniedException`.
**Cross-refs:** `arc3-out/B4-ses-sandbox-exit-request.md` (the ticket text); the four paired Arc-8 follow-up drifts named above.

### D-ses-feedback-loop-not-wired-2026-05-22
**Status:** OPEN — P2 deliverability hygiene. Surfaced 2026-05-22 during the B.4 ticket-draft work. SES bounce/complaint notifications are not yet wired to an SNS topic with a backend handler; today, a bounce or complaint silently degrades sender reputation without any application-layer visibility.
**Section that raised it:** Arc 3 B.4 ticket-draft authoring, 2026-05-22.
**Raised by:** Agent while authoring the ticket text — the AWS approval bar requires a credible bounce/complaint posture, which we promise in the ticket but have not yet implemented.
**Design claim:** The six-pillar contract (reliability + traceability) requires that bounced/complained recipients are captured at the application layer, not just at the SES wire. Without the loop, a single complaint storm could put the domain on a blocklist before we notice.
**Repo state:** No SNS topic configured, no handler in `app/api/v1/`, no `email_send_event` table in the schema.
**Operational impact today:** Bounded — send volume is low; reputation risk is small but real. The risk grows linearly with send volume.
**Owning roadmap step:** Arc 8 deliverability sub-arc, paired with `D-ses-sandbox-exit-pending-2026-05-22` approval (AWS Support reviews bounce/complaint posture as part of the approval).
**Resolution path:** (a) Create SNS topic `luciel-ses-events` in `ca-central-1`; (b) configure SES configuration set `luciel-default` with event-destination pointing at the topic for `Bounce`, `Complaint`, `Reject`, `RenderingFailure`; (c) thread `ConfigurationSetName=luciel-default` into all three `email_service.py` send-call sites (L270, L442, L605); (d) author `app/api/v1/ses_events.py` to receive the SNS HTTPS subscription and write rows into a new `email_send_event` table; (e) Alembic migration for the table; (f) integration test that posts a synthetic bounce JSON and asserts the row lands.
**Pattern E:** Cross-layer additive — SNS topic + SES configuration set + application route + schema migration. No existing surface is mutated. Customer-visible surface change is zero (admin-side observability only).
**Validation evidence:** Closure evidence will be a synthetic bounce post that round-trips into an `email_send_event` row, plus the `ConfigurationSetName` field showing on outbound `send_email` calls in a CloudWatch trace.
**Cross-refs:** `D-ses-sandbox-exit-pending-2026-05-22` (paired); `D-ses-suppression-app-layer-not-implemented-2026-05-22` (the natural consumer of the feedback-loop rows).

### D-ses-suppression-app-layer-not-implemented-2026-05-22
**Status:** OPEN — P2 deliverability hygiene. Surfaced 2026-05-22 during the B.4 ticket-draft work. There is no application-layer suppression list — the backend will happily send to a previously-bounced address again, which is the canonical trigger for SES sender-reputation degradation.
**Section that raised it:** Arc 3 B.4 ticket-draft authoring, 2026-05-22.
**Raised by:** Agent while authoring the ticket text — the AWS approval bar names suppression as a requirement.
**Design claim:** Six-pillar contract (reliability) requires that a bounced address is never sent to again without a manual reset. SES has an account-level suppression list, but it operates at the SES wire; an application-layer mirror is the right place because it lets us short-circuit the send call entirely (cheaper, faster, and decoupled from SES API state).
**Repo state:** No `email_suppression` table, no `_is_suppressed(address)` precheck in `email_service.py` send paths.
**Operational impact today:** Bounded — today's send volume is small and our allowlist is small. The risk grows with send volume.
**Owning roadmap step:** Arc 8 deliverability sub-arc, paired with `D-ses-feedback-loop-not-wired-2026-05-22` (the suppression layer is the natural consumer of the feedback-loop rows).
**Resolution path:** (a) Alembic migration adding `email_suppression` table with `address`, `reason` (`HardBounce` / `Complaint` / `ManualBlock`), `first_suppressed_at`, `last_suppressed_at`; (b) `EmailSuppressionService` with `is_suppressed(address) -> bool` and `record_suppression(address, reason, source_event_id)`; (c) `_is_suppressed` precheck at the top of every `email_service.py` send-call site, returning `SuppressedRecipientError` rather than calling `client.send_email`; (d) the feedback-loop handler from `D-ses-feedback-loop-not-wired-2026-05-22` calls `record_suppression` on every `Bounce` / `Complaint` event; (e) admin endpoint to clear a suppression.
**Pattern E:** Application-layer additive (new service, new table, new precheck) plus a small integration test matrix. No existing surface is mutated.
**Validation evidence:** Closure evidence will be a synthetic bounce → suppression-row write → next send call to that address returning `SuppressedRecipientError` without a wire trip.
**Cross-refs:** `D-ses-feedback-loop-not-wired-2026-05-22` (the upstream signal); `D-ses-sandbox-exit-pending-2026-05-22` (the umbrella deliverability drift).

### D-ses-reply-to-monitored-inbox-not-confirmed-2026-05-22
**Status:** OPEN — P3 deliverability hygiene. Surfaced 2026-05-22 during the B.4 ticket-draft work. SES outbound calls in `app/services/email_service.py` do not set `ReplyToAddresses`; replies (e.g., a customer hitting Reply in Gmail to a magic-link email) bounce against `noreply@vantagemind.ai`, which is not a monitored inbox.
**Section that raised it:** Arc 3 B.4 ticket-draft authoring, 2026-05-22.
**Raised by:** Agent while authoring the ticket text.
**Design claim:** Six-pillar contract (reliability + traceability) requires that a customer-initiated reply to a transactional email lands in a real inbox a human reads, not at a black-hole `noreply` address. AWS deliverability guidance names this as a soft requirement for sandbox exit approval.
**Repo state:** No `ReplyToAddresses` field in any `send_email` call in `app/services/email_service.py` (sites L270, L442, L605).
**Operational impact today:** Bounded — send volume is low; reply volume is lower. The risk is opportunity-cost (a customer trying to engage hits a wall).
**Owning roadmap step:** Arc 8 deliverability sub-arc.
**Resolution path:** (a) Confirm a monitored inbox exists (e.g., `support@vantagemind.ai`) and that DNS forwards it to a real mailbox; (b) thread `ReplyToAddresses=["support@vantagemind.ai"]` into all three `email_service.py` send-call sites; (c) one-time smoke send and reply round-trip evidence.
**Pattern E:** Pure application-layer additive (one parameter on three send calls) plus a DNS confirmation.
**Validation evidence:** Closure evidence will be a smoke email out, a manual reply from a test inbox, and the reply landing in the configured monitored inbox.
**Cross-refs:** `D-ses-sandbox-exit-pending-2026-05-22` (the umbrella deliverability drift); `arc3-out/B4-ses-sandbox-exit-request.md` (the ticket text that promises this posture).

### D-no-internal-smoke-path-for-direct-alb-2026-05-22
**Status:** OPEN — P3 observability hygiene. Surfaced 2026-05-22 in Arc 3 B.1/B.2.5 deploy-smoke work. There is no internal smoke path that hits the ALB directly with a trusted TLS chain; the only path through the ALB to `/health` is via the custom domain `https://www.vantagemind.ai/health`, which works for the customer-facing surface but cannot be used as a deploy-gate (it depends on Amplify DNS + custom-domain TLS chain). The ALB DNS name `luciel-targets-...` does not have a trusted cert, so a direct `Invoke-WebRequest` against it fails the certificate-trust check.
**Section that raised it:** Arc 3 B.1/B.2.5 deploy-smoke walks, 2026-05-22 ≈00:50 EDT and 2026-05-21 evening.
**Raised by:** Agent during the post-rollout ALB-health verification step.
**Design claim:** Six-pillar contract (reliability) requires a deploy-gate smoke path that exercises the ALB target group end-to-end without depending on the Amplify custom-domain chain. Today the deploy-gate falls back to ECS task-state and target-group health-check, which are necessary but not sufficient (they don't prove the application returns a 200 to a real HTTP request).
**Repo state:** No repo defect; the gap is in operational tooling.
**Operational impact today:** Bounded — the customer-domain path works; the deploy-gate is just thinner than it should be.
**Owning roadmap step:** Arc 8 observability sub-arc; paired naturally with the planned `/ready` endpoint work.
**Resolution path:** Option (a) attach a second certificate to the ALB scoped to an internal `alb.luciel.local` name so an internal smoke probe can hit it directly. Option (b) cleaner: introduce an in-cluster probe (a Lambda or a Fargate task with a curl) that hits the ALB private IP path and writes to CloudWatch. Option (b) preferred because it also exercises the VPC routing.
**Pattern E:** Operational-tooling additive. No application-layer touch.
**Validation evidence:** Closure evidence will be a documented smoke path with a CloudWatch metric that pings on every deploy.
**Cross-refs:** `D-health-endpoint-shallow-no-db-readiness-check-2026-05-22` (the sibling /ready-endpoint drift, paired natural-fit closure).
