### D-entitlement-matrix-v1-2026-05-20
**Status:** OPEN — P1 design-truth + monetization-defence. The three-tier monetization story rests on "the tiers exist as separate products and not as seat counts" (CANONICAL_RECAP §14). The Step 30a.1 closure operationalised the product-shape difference as scope-hierarchy depth (Individual=agent, Team=agent+domain, Company=agent+domain+tenant), which the umbrella realignment drift (`D-tier-semantics-realignment-2026-05-20`) retunes to hierarchy-width-plus-cross-cutting-capability. The retuning surfaces a gap: beyond the instance cap (3/10/50), the leads cap (3/100/Unlimited), and the Luciel-shape difference, **the matrix of operational entitlements that distinguishes the three tiers has never been authored as a first-class artifact**. A buyer today reads §14 and sees three prices, three caps, and the one-paragraph product-difference defence — they do not see the rate-limit, conversation-cap, channel-availability, branding, SSO, audit-retention, or SLA differences that operationally distinguish a Team subscription from an Individual one. This drift carves out v1 of the entitlement matrix as a first-class artifact in §14 with a corresponding policy file at `app/policy/entitlements.py`, recording honestly which rows are enforced today (the **Live-Today** matrix) and which rows are committed-to but not yet built (the **Roadmap** matrix). The honest split lets §14 carry the full product-difference defence without overstating what the implementation enforces.
**Section that raised it:** Pre-Journey-1 live-testing pause, 2026-05-20, during the partner's three-concern review. Concern #3 in the partner's framing, with the explicit handoff: "for concern 3 actually I am not fully sure of what the monetization differences should be. I will entrust you with the judgment." The advisor's recommendation (Option B — staged matrix with Live-Today + Roadmap split) was greenlit by the partner alongside the umbrella realignment decision.
**Raised by:** Aryan (partner) on 2026-05-20, with the entitlement-design judgment handed to the advisor. The matrix values authored today are partner-reviewed against the four clarification rounds covering channel availability (all tiers, voice/SMS/email gated on Step 34a), widget concurrent-instances semantics, cross-domain memory semantics, Dedicated Success Manager scope, and Priority Support SLA shape.
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §14 commits the product-difference story; the realignment retunes the operationalisation but leaves the product-difference defence load-bearing. Without a first-class entitlement matrix, the defence is supported only by the price-and-cap rows and the prose paragraph — neither of which an operations engineer or a procurement reviewer can map to a contract surface. ARCHITECTURE §4.1 (scope hierarchy as billing boundary) implicitly commits that every tier-distinguishing knob lives in a single referenceable artifact; the v1 entitlement matrix is that artifact.
**Repo state:** No existing matrix file. The closest existing artifacts are scattered: `app/models/subscription.py` `DOMAIN_COUNT_CAP_BY_TIER` (one row of the matrix), `app/services/admin_service.py` `_enforce_tier_scope` (the allowed-scope-per-tier row), `app/services/tier_provisioning_service.py` (the pre-mint walk encoding the implicit row counts), `app/api/v1/billing.py` `INTRO_FEE_BY_TIER` (one row), and the leads-cap one-liner in the chat path (one row). The v1 matrix consolidates these into a single referenceable artifact and adds the new rows the realignment surfaces.
**Operational impact today:** Critical-but-narrow. One live tenant (`co-354c5056`, being retired today by partner). Impact is design-truth, not customer-blocking: the matrix is the surface a future paying Team customer asks for when comparing tiers, and the surface a future operations engineer asks for when scoping a rate-limit incident. Front-loading the matrix today (before the second paying Team customer exists on the wire) is cheap; back-loading it after multiple tenants have accumulated implicit expectations is expensive.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step **30a.6 sub-bullet B** (Entitlement matrix v1) — the second sub-bullet of the consolidated Step 30a.6 row in CANONICAL_RECAP §12 per partner direction 2026-05-20. The matrix work pairs with Step 30a.6 sub-bullet A (tier-hierarchy realignment) inside the same single-day commit arc. Sub-bullet B lands the matrix file (`app/policy/entitlements.py`), the §14 matrix sub-section in CANONICAL_RECAP, the Live-Today enforcements for the rows that have backend support today (seats, leads cap, widget count, API rate-limit by tier), and the umbrella carve-out drift for the rows that do not have backend support yet.
**Resolution path:** Three-stage. **Stage A (single-day, Pass 3 of the realignment arc):** author `app/policy/entitlements.py` carrying the v1 matrix as a single source-of-truth module. The module exposes `ENTITLEMENTS_BY_TIER: dict[str, TierEntitlements]` where `TierEntitlements` is a frozen dataclass with the 16 rows authored today: `seats`, `leads_cap`, `domains`, `voice_channel`, `sms_channel`, `email_channel`, `widgets`, `conversations_per_day_per_seat`, `api_rate_limit_rpm`, `concurrent_sarah_instances`, `cross_domain_memory`, `audit_retention_days`, `audit_csv_export`, `custom_widget_branding`, `sso`, `priority_support`, `dedicated_success_manager`. Each row carries a `live_today: bool` flag distinguishing the **Live-Today** matrix from the **Roadmap** matrix. **Stage B (same commit):** wire the Live-Today rows into the existing enforcement points — `seats` already wired via `_enforce_tier_scope`, `leads_cap` wired into the chat one-liner, `domains` wired into the route-level cap check on `POST /admin/domains/self-serve`, `widgets` wired into the embed-key issuance route, `api_rate_limit_rpm` wired into the `RateLimitFallback` middleware tier-aware bucket. **Stage C (single umbrella carve-out drift for the Roadmap rows):** per partner direction 2026-05-20 entrusting the carve-out shape to the advisor's judgment, the eight Roadmap rows land as a single umbrella drift `D-entitlement-matrix-v1-roadmap-rows-deferred-2026-05-20` carrying all eight rows in one status table (row name, enforcement-point that doesn't yet exist, natural Step pairing, validation-evidence shape at closure). The eight rows: `conversations_per_day_per_seat` (counter not built, natural pairing Step 34 / Step 31.x), `concurrent_sarah_instances` (counter not built, natural pairing Step 36 / Step 31.x), `cross_domain_memory` (architecture present via Step 24.5c but tier-gating not enforced, natural pairing Step 37), `audit_retention_days` (purge worker is tier-agnostic today, natural pairing next email-service / cron touch), `audit_csv_export` (no route, natural pairing Step 31.x dashboard export), `custom_widget_branding` (Step 30b widget supports a `theme` field but tier-gating not enforced, natural pairing next widget touch), `sso` (no integration today, natural pairing future enterprise step), `priority_support` (no SLA infra today, natural pairing future ops step), and `dedicated_success_manager` (operator-process row, no infra component, natural pairing first Company-tier customer hand-off). Per-row drifts open lazily at the corresponding Step's touch — preserves audit-trail discipline without front-loading eight near-identical stubs today.
**Pattern E:** Additive at the policy-file layer, the §14-doctrine layer, and the carve-out-drift layer. No existing enforcement point is modified other than to **read from** the new matrix instead of from a hard-coded local constant — the values authored in the matrix file mirror the values already encoded in the existing enforcement points, so the diff at every existing call site is a one-line substitution (`if tier == "team": cap = 100` → `cap = ENTITLEMENTS_BY_TIER[tier].leads_cap`). No schema change. No customer-visible regression because the values are unchanged.
**Validation evidence:** Pending. Discovery evidence is the 2026-05-20 partner three-concern review. Closure evidence is (a) `pytest tests/policy/test_entitlements.py` green on the 16 rows × 3 tiers = 48 cell assertions; (b) the existing enforcement-point tests (`test_admin_service_tier_scope.py`, `test_billing_intro_fee.py`, etc.) green against the matrix-read substitution; (c) `CANONICAL_RECAP §14` carries a new matrix sub-section with the Live-Today + Roadmap split and a row-by-row enforcement-point cross-ref to `app/policy/entitlements.py`; (d) the eight carve-out drifts (or one umbrella carve-out) land in §3 alongside this drift; (e) the resumed Journey 1 Individual signup walks through the realigned Pricing copy → Stripe Checkout → set-password → `/app` without encountering a row of the matrix that the implementation does not honour.
**Cross-refs:** CANONICAL_RECAP §14 (the doctrine this drift lifts into a first-class artifact); ARCHITECTURE §4.1 (scope hierarchy as billing boundary — the architectural foundation); `D-tier-semantics-realignment-2026-05-20` (umbrella — the matrix is sub-bullet B of the consolidated Step 30a.6 realignment row); `D-channels-promised-not-built-multi-tier-2026-05-20` (sibling — the channel-availability rows are committed-to on every tier; the backend gate is Step 34a); `D-pricing-page-truth-2026-05-20` (sibling — the Pricing surface inherits the matrix at the headline level); `D-entitlement-matrix-v1-roadmap-rows-deferred-2026-05-20` (the single umbrella carve-out drift authored alongside this one, carrying the eight Roadmap-row deferrals); `~~D-billing-team-company-not-self-serve-2026-05-13~~` and `~~D-trial-policy-mixed-per-tier-2026-05-14~~` (predecessors — the previous monetization-shape commits this drift retunes).

### D-channels-promised-not-built-multi-tier-2026-05-20
**Status:** OPEN — P1 design-truth. The 2026-05-20 partner clarification round locked the channels-availability decision as: **voice, SMS, and email channels are available on ALL tiers** — not as a higher-tier entitlement. Under the Arc 4 three-tier shape (Free / Pro / Enterprise — 2026-05-22-late), the universal-channels doctrine survives unchanged: every tier carries voice / SMS / email at the doctrine layer, and the implementation gate remains Step 34a. The original framing referenced the v1 four-tier noun set (Individual / Team / Company) — preserved verbatim in the next sentence for traceability; under the current tier shape, read "all tiers" as Free / Pro / Enterprise. The partner's framing: "we should have voice, email, SMS for all tiers available. Remember how and why we are designing Luciel." The decision honours the §11 Q7 commitment that channels emerge from configuration, not from a separate product per channel — and the §11 Q8 commitment that cross-channel continuity is the architectural foundation, not a high-tier upsell. The drift is the gap between that decision and the live implementation: today, only the **chat widget** and **programmatic API** legs of Q7 are built (Step 24.5c closure 2026-05-11; Step 30b widget CDN 2026-05-10; Step 30d content safety 2026-05-11). Voice, SMS, and email channel adapters are not built — they are committed-to on the Step 34a roadmap row ("📋 Planned (no current ETA)") and inherit the three Step 24.5c primitives (`conversations` table, `conversation_id` FK, `identity_claims` table) but are not reachable end-to-end today. The drift records the asymmetry honestly: the marketing surface (Pricing, future capability copy) commits channels on every tier; the implementation gate is Step 34a; the entitlement matrix v1 lands the rows with `live_today=False` for voice / SMS / email and a Step 34a natural pairing.
**Section that raised it:** Pre-Journey-1 live-testing pause, 2026-05-20, during the channel-availability clarification round inside the umbrella tier-realignment review. Specific partner exchange: the advisor initially proposed channels as a tier-distinguishing knob (voice on Team-and-up, SMS on Company-only); the partner corrected with "channels available on ALL tiers," which is the core product thesis the advisor had momentarily lost grip on ("Remember how and why we are designing Luciel").
**Raised by:** Aryan (partner) on 2026-05-20, in the channel-availability clarification round. The advisor's mis-proposal is recorded honestly in this drift's discovery-evidence trail because the same mis-proposal could surface again in a future tier-design conversation if the drift does not record it.
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §11 Q7 commits "A channel adapter framework. Inbound webhooks and outbound tool registrations, all bounded by the same scope policy. Channels emerge from configuration, not from a separate product per channel." §11 Q8 commits cross-channel continuity as the architectural foundation. §14 (post-realignment) commits voice / SMS / email as Live-Today=False, Roadmap=True for every tier — the channel availability is a product promise, the implementation gate is Step 34a. ARCHITECTURE §3.2.1 (public endpoint) and §3.3 step 1 (channel ingest) jointly commit the channel-adapter shape; the implementation today serves the widget + API legs only.
**Repo state:** The chat-widget channel is built (`app/api/v1/widget.py`, `Luciel-Website` widget bundle at `https://d1t84i96t71fsi.cloudfront.net/widget.js`, Step 30b CDN closure 2026-05-10, Step 30d content-safety closure 2026-05-11). The programmatic-API channel is built (the existing `/api/v1/chat` surface). The voice channel, SMS channel, and email channel are not built — no `app/channels/voice/`, no `app/channels/sms/`, no `app/channels/email/` directory exists; the email-service module at `app/services/email_service.py` handles transactional sends (magic-link, welcome-set-password, pilot-refund-confirmation) but is not a channel-adapter that ingests inbound emails into a Luciel conversation. The Step 34a roadmap row commits the channel-adapter framework that lands all three; the row is `📋 Planned (no current ETA)`.
**Operational impact today:** Low — the marketing surface today does not actively promise voice / SMS / email to any tier (the §14 entitlement matrix v1 surfaces it for the first time when Step 30a.7 lands), so no customer has been mis-sold. Impact escalates the moment the §14 matrix lands and the Pricing surface inherits the channel-availability headline: every paying customer reads "voice, SMS, email — included" and the only honest delivery shape is Live-Today=False + Roadmap=True at the matrix-cell level, with a customer-visible "channels coming with the Step 34a release" annotation on the Pricing surface or the in-app channel-config screen. Operational defence is to keep the matrix-cell `live_today=False` flag visible in any customer-facing surface that quotes the matrix.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 34a (Channel adapter framework — voice / SMS / email). Existing row in CANONICAL_RECAP §12, status `📋 Planned (no current ETA)`. This drift's closure is paired with Step 34a's closing tag, not with the realignment closing tag — the realignment lands the design-truth claim (channels promised on every tier, gated on Step 34a); Step 34a lands the implementation.
**Resolution path:** Three-stage. **Stage A (lands today, Pass 2 of the realignment arc):** the §14 matrix sub-section authored at `D-entitlement-matrix-v1-2026-05-20` carries the channel rows with `live_today=False` for voice / SMS / email on every tier, and an explicit "gated on Step 34a" footnote. **Stage B (lands today, Pass 3 of the realignment arc):** the `app/policy/entitlements.py` file carries the matrix-cell flags so any customer-facing surface that reads the matrix can render the "Live-Today" affordance honestly. **Stage C (Step 34a closure):** the channel-adapter framework lands, the matrix-cell flags flip to `live_today=True`, and this drift moves to §5 with strikethrough alongside the Step 34a closing tag.
**Pattern E:** Design-truth flag in the matrix at v1 launch, implementation paired with the existing Step 34a roadmap row. No premature implementation. No marketing surface that overpromises (the matrix's `live_today=False` flag is the customer-visible truth-surface). No regression risk because the chat-widget + API channels stay live throughout.
**Validation evidence:** Pending. Discovery evidence is the 2026-05-20 partner clarification message ("channels available on ALL tiers") and the advisor's mis-proposal trail in the prior message exchange. Closure evidence is (a) the §14 matrix sub-section landed with voice / SMS / email rows flagged Live-Today=False on every tier; (b) the `app/policy/entitlements.py` file's matrix-cell flags read the same; (c) any future Pricing-surface copy that quotes the matrix renders the channel rows with a "Step 34a release" footnote or `[Roadmap]` badge; (d) the Step 34a closing tag eventually retires this drift to §5.
**Cross-refs:** CANONICAL_RECAP §11 Q7 (the channel-adapter design claim this drift defends); CANONICAL_RECAP §11 Q8 (the cross-channel continuity claim this drift defends); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 24.5c row (the three-primitive foundation the future channel adapters inherit); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 34a row (the owning roadmap step for the implementation); `D-tier-semantics-realignment-2026-05-20` (umbrella); `D-entitlement-matrix-v1-2026-05-20` (sibling — the matrix is where the channel rows are surfaced with their Live-Today=False flag); `D-channels-only-chat-implemented-2026-05-09` (predecessor — the original "channels other than chat are not built" drift; this drift retunes it for the multi-tier marketing claim that the realignment surfaces); `D-pricing-page-truth-2026-05-20` (sibling — any future Pricing-surface copy that lists channels inherits this drift's `live_today=False` flag).

### ~~D-invite-redeemed-user-sees-no-subscription-on-file-2026-05-18~~
**Status:** CLOSED 2026-05-18. Fix landed in commit `dba6a755` on `main` and deployed to prod as `luciel-backend:72` / `luciel-worker:27` at 2026-05-18 ≈19:08 EDT (image digest `sha256:8b5020d7745c3ae681e1083f2cc2407793e69b9f8250bfba08fef327dfeb4692`). 16 contract tests pinning the fix at `tests/api/test_step30a_5_post_smoke_fixes_shape.py`. OpenAPI on the deployed wire confirms `DomainConfigSelfServeRead` is live with both rollup fields. Pre-closure body preserved below.
**Pre-closure body (preserved for audit):** P0 functional regression caught in the Step 30a.5 live $1,000 smoke walk against tenant `co-354c5056` (owner `aryan+smoke-30a5@yourdomain.com`, invitee `aryans.www@gmail.com`) on 2026-05-18 ≈15:10 EDT. After the invitee redeemed the welcome-set-password JWT, the redemption code in `app/services/invite_service.py` line 483 correctly created a `ScopeAssignment(user_id=<invitee>, tenant_id='co-354c5056', domain_id='general', role='teammate', active=True)`, but the very next step — `_mint_and_set_session(db, user_id)` at `app/api/v1/auth.py` line 277–284 calling `_resolve_tenant_for_user(db, user_id)` at line 132 — returned `""` instead of `co-354c5056`. The cookie was minted with `tenant_id=""`, the frontend's `/dashboard/tenant` reader saw no tenant, and the invitee landed on the **"No subscription on file"** empty state — the same surface a never-paid user sees. CANONICAL_RECAP §12 promised redeemed invitees see their workspace; this drift broke that promise for every non-paying role (teammate / department_lead / tenant_admin).
**Section that raised it:** Step 30a.5 live smoke walk, 2026-05-18 ≈15:10 EDT, after the partner paid $1,000 against the public Company pricing CTA on `https://www.vantagemind.ai/pricing`. The owner-side login worked because owners hold both a Stripe subscription and an owner-role ScopeAssignment (the May-17 fix at `tier_provisioning_service._ensure_owner_scope_assignment`). The invitee-side regression surfaced only on the redemption.
**Raised by:** Aryan (partner) on 2026-05-18 ≈15:14 EDT via screenshot `image-3.jpg` showing the redeemed invitee's empty-state render in incognito Chrome.
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 commits that an invitee who clicks the welcome-set-password email, sets a password, and lands in `/app` sees the workspace scoped to the inviter's tenant. ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (Auth model — Option B welcome-email mechanic) re-locked this on 2026-05-16. Both claims are violated by the resolver short-circuit.
**Repo state:** Defect at `app/api/v1/auth.py` lines 107–118 (pre-fix). The function asked `BillingService.get_active_subscription_for_user(user_id)` for the user's tenant, which is wrong by design — tenant binding is owned by `ScopeAssignment`, not by Stripe billing. The function was correct for owners only because owners happen to satisfy both binding sources. Diagnosis dumps from 2026-05-18 ≈15:30 EDT (`d8-invite_service.txt`, `d12-mint-session.txt`, `d13-resolve.txt`) confirmed the redemption code wrote the ScopeAssignment correctly and the resolver was the locus.
**Operational impact today:** Critical-but-narrow. Only one live Company tenant (`co-354c5056`) existed at discovery, with one redeemed invitee. The invitee's workspace was unreachable until the fix. No cross-tenant leak (the resolver returned `""`, not someone else's tenant). The fix is symmetric to the 2026-05-17 inviter-side fix at `tier_provisioning_service._ensure_owner_scope_assignment` (drift `~~D-step-30a-owner-scopeassignment-missing-self-serve-checkout-2026-05-17~~`); the two together close the ScopeAssignment-as-source-of-truth discipline for tenant binding.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.5 post-smoke. Fix landed in PR #51 (Luciel) merged 2026-05-18 ≈17:50 EDT as commit `dba6a755`, deployed to prod ECS the same evening.
**Resolution path (executed):** Three changes. (a) `_resolve_tenant_for_user` resolves via `ScopeAssignmentRepository.list_for_user(user_id, active_only=True)` first, preferring `role='owner'` (canonical primary scope), else most-recently-started active assignment. (b) `BillingService.get_active_subscription_for_user` retained as a fallback for the mid-checkout race window where a Stripe subscription row exists before `tier_provisioning_service` has written the owner ScopeAssignment. (c) 16 new contract tests at `tests/api/test_step30a_5_post_smoke_fixes_shape.py` pin the resolution order, owner-preference, billing-fallback ordering, empty-string preservation, and a drift-id beacon in the docstring so a future grep on the drift id surfaces this fix. Closure evidence is the second smoke-walk verification (invitee logs back into `/app` and sees the workspace; cookie `tenant_id == "co-354c5056"`).
**Pattern E:** Pure resolver-layer fix — the source-of-truth flip is invisible to every caller. Owner path is bit-identical (owner has both binding sources, the new resolver hits step 1, returns the same `tenant_id`). Invitee path now resolves. No schema change. No route signature change. No customer-visible surface change beyond the fix itself.
**Validation evidence:** 16 contract tests green (`pytest tests/api/test_step30a_5_post_smoke_fixes_shape.py -v` returns 16 passed). Deployment evidence is the ECS service description showing `td: arn:...luciel-backend:72`, `running == desired == 1`, single PRIMARY deployment. OpenAPI on the deployed wire shows `#/components/schemas/DomainConfigSelfServeRead` as the 200 response items ref for `GET /api/v1/admin/domains/self-serve` (proves both this fix and the rollup fix landed in the same image). Live smoke evidence is pending (the second T1 walk after the deploy; queued for the partner's next session segment).
**Cross-refs:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 (the contract this drift broke); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (re-locked 2026-05-16); `~~D-step-30a-owner-scopeassignment-missing-self-serve-checkout-2026-05-17~~` (sibling inviter-side fix; the two together complete the ScopeAssignment-as-source-of-truth discipline); `D-company-tab-domain-rollup-fields-missing-2026-05-18` and `D-team-tab-invite-row-missing-role-and-domain-2026-05-18` (sibling drifts surfaced in the same smoke walk); `docs/designs/step-30a-5-company-self-serve.md` §13.1 (the T1 walk this fix unblocks).

### ~~D-company-tab-domain-rollup-fields-missing-2026-05-18~~
**Status:** CLOSED 2026-05-18. Backend fix in commit `dba6a755` (`DomainConfigSelfServeRead` schema + route handler), frontend in commit `6ac47c0e` (Domain card rollup line render). Both deployed. 5 new contract tests in `tests/api/test_step30a_5_post_smoke_fixes_shape.py` plus 3 frontend vitest cases pin the contract. OpenAPI on the deployed wire confirms the schema is live. Pre-closure body preserved below.
**Pre-closure body (preserved for audit):** UI gap surfaced in the same smoke walk as the critical-resolver drift. The Step 30a.5 design §4.4 promised that `GET /api/v1/admin/domains/self-serve` would surface two route-level rollup fields per Domain — `pending_invites_count` and `active_agents_count` — so the CompanyTab Domain card could render "3 agents · 1 invite pending" without a second N+1 fan-out. PR #50 shipped the route but not the rollup; the route returned plain `DomainConfigRead`. As a result the live `/app/company` Domain cards on tenant `co-354c5056` (Support, General Assistant) rendered with no seat-pressure indicator, exactly matching the bare-card layout shown in screenshot `image.jpg`.
**Section that raised it:** Step 30a.5 live smoke walk, 2026-05-18 ≈15:10 EDT, on the same Company tenant as the critical-resolver drift. Surfaced by direct visual comparison to design §4.4 ("two extra rollup fields injected at the route level — not on the model") which the partner had reviewed earlier in the session.
**Raised by:** Aryan (partner) on 2026-05-18 ≈15:18 EDT via screenshot `image.jpg` after logging into the owner side of the smoke tenant.
**Design claim:** Step 30a.5 design doc §4.4 explicitly commits the two rollup fields and the "route-level injection, not on the model" pattern. CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.5 row commits the success criterion that a Company admin lands on `/app/company` and sees the org chart — the rollup is the load-bearing affordance for seeing seat pressure per Domain.
**Repo state:** Pre-fix, `app/api/v1/admin.py` line 449 declared `response_model=list[DomainConfigRead]` on the `/admin/domains/self-serve` route. The handler called `service.list_domain_configs` and returned the bare configs. `src/lib/admin.ts` `DomainConfig` interface had no rollup fields. `src/pages/Dashboard.tsx` Domain card had no rollup line render block.
**Operational impact today:** Cosmetic-but-load-bearing. A Company admin could still navigate to their Domain cards, but had no way to read seat pressure at a glance — the affordance design §4.4 promised. Impact escalates as soon as a Company tenant has more than three Domains, because the alternative (clicking into each Domain individually) is the friction the design was meant to remove.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.5 post-smoke. Fix landed in PRs #51 (Luciel) and #5 (Luciel-Website), both merged 2026-05-18 ≈17:50–18:00 EDT, deployed the same evening.
**Resolution path (executed):** Three changes across two repos. (a) New `DomainConfigSelfServeRead(DomainConfigRead)` schema at `app/schemas/admin.py` with `pending_invites_count: int = Field(..., ge=0)` and `active_agents_count: int = Field(..., ge=0)`. The two fields are NOT on the `DomainConfig` model — they are joined at the route level per design §4.4. (b) `GET /admin/domains/self-serve` switched to `response_model=list[DomainConfigSelfServeRead]` and computes both rollups via two grouped queries (one over `UserInvite` filtered to `status='pending'`, one over `Agent` filtered to `active=True`), both tenant-scoped via `_resolve_invite_actor`. The two-query shape stays O(1) in roundtrips regardless of the 50-domain Company tier cap. (c) Frontend `DomainConfig` TypeScript interface extended with the two optional ints; `Dashboard.tsx` Domain card renders the rollup line `{N} agents · {M} invites pending` below the description. Defensive: the fields are typed as optional so a stale frontend served against a pre-fix backend renders `0 agents · 0 invites pending` rather than crashing.
**Pattern E:** Additive at every layer. New schema subclass extends the canonical model serializer; new route-level computation does not touch service-layer methods; new UI block sits inside the existing Domain-card render without restructuring. No schema migration. No breaking change to existing callers (older clients ignore the extra fields).
**Validation evidence:** 5 backend contract tests (route response model, group-by columns, PENDING+active filters, tenant-scoping). 3 frontend vitest cases on `listDomainsSelfServe` (wire contract + optional-shape tolerance). Both repos green. Deployed-wire evidence: `Invoke-RestMethod` against `https://api.vantagemind.ai/openapi.json` returns the schema component and the route's 200 response items ref points at `DomainConfigSelfServeRead`. Live smoke evidence is pending alongside the critical-resolver drift's second-walk evidence.
**Cross-refs:** Step 30a.5 design §4.4 (the contract this drift broke); `~~D-invite-redeemed-user-sees-no-subscription-on-file-2026-05-18~~` (sibling P0 surfaced in the same smoke walk; the post-smoke commit closes both at once); `D-team-tab-invite-row-missing-role-and-domain-2026-05-18` (third sibling from the same walk); `D-company-self-serve-incomplete-org-building-ui-missing-2026-05-16` (the parent in-flight drift whose closure this drift's fix unblocks).

### ~~D-team-tab-invite-row-missing-role-and-domain-2026-05-18~~
**Status:** CLOSED 2026-05-18. Frontend fix in commit `6ac47c0e` (Luciel-Website PR #5). 3 vitest cases on `listDomainsSelfServe` pin the wire side. Pre-closure body preserved below.
**Pre-closure body (preserved for audit):** Pure-UI gap surfaced in the same 2026-05-18 smoke walk as the two siblings. The Team tab on `/app` rendered the pending-invite row with only the invitee email and the expiry countdown. The `UserInvite` payload returned by `GET /admin/invites` already carried `role` and `domain_id` (both shipped in PR #50 / Step 30a.5 backend), but the Dashboard render block at `src/pages/Dashboard.tsx` line 825–920 (pre-fix) never read those fields. A Company admin inviting a department lead into `support` and a teammate into `sales` could not tell which row was which.
**Section that raised it:** Step 30a.5 live smoke walk, 2026-05-18 ≈15:10 EDT, while the partner was reviewing the Team tab on the owner side of tenant `co-354c5056`. Screenshot `image-2.jpg` captures the pre-fix render shape (only the email visible, no role or domain badge).
**Raised by:** Aryan (partner) on 2026-05-18 ≈15:22 EDT via direct visual inspection of `/app`.
**Design claim:** Step 30a.5 design §5.1 commits that the Team tab renders role and domain_id on every pending-invite row so admins can distinguish leads, teammates, and tenant-admins targeting different Domains. CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.5 row promises the cascading-invite shape (Company admin invites lead, lead invites agents) is visible end-to-end — the row-level badges are the affordance that makes the cascade legible.
**Repo state:** Pre-fix, `src/pages/Dashboard.tsx` line 825–840 (the pending-invite `<li>` render) showed only `<div>{inv.invited_email}</div>` and the expiry line. The `UserInvite` TypeScript interface at `src/lib/admin.ts` line 341–395 already declared both `role: string` and `domain_id: string` — the wire was correct, the render was incomplete.
**Operational impact today:** Cosmetic. A Company admin could still revoke an unwanted invite by matching the email, but could not see at a glance which role / Domain a pending invite targeted. Impact escalates as a tenant scales to multiple Domains; today bounded by the live-tenant count.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.5 post-smoke. Fix landed in Luciel-Website PR #5 merged 2026-05-18 ≈18:00 EDT as commit `6ac47c0e`.
**Resolution path (executed):** Single change to the Team-tab pending-invite render block in `src/pages/Dashboard.tsx`. Each pending-invite row now renders two inline pill badges next to the invitee email: a role pill (`data-testid={`invite-role-${inv.id}`}`) styled with `uppercase tracking-[0.12em]`, and a domain_id pill (`data-testid={`invite-domain-${inv.id}`}`) styled with `font-mono`. The badges sit before the expiry countdown so admins read role/domain before they read the time remaining.
**Pattern E:** Pure render-layer additive change. No interface extension (the fields were already on the wire). No schema change. No backend touch. No regression risk to the existing revoke-invite control or the expiry render.
**Validation evidence:** Frontend vitest suite stays at 36/36 green (3 new cases on `listDomainsSelfServe` siblings the rollup fix). Deployed-bundle evidence: `Invoke-WebRequest` against the live Vite bundle finds both `invite-role-` and `invite-domain-` `data-testid` markers in the minified JS — proves the new render code is on the wire at `https://www.vantagemind.ai`. Live smoke evidence is pending alongside the two sibling closures.
**Cross-refs:** Step 30a.5 design §5.1 (the contract this drift broke); `~~D-invite-redeemed-user-sees-no-subscription-on-file-2026-05-18~~` and `~~D-company-tab-domain-rollup-fields-missing-2026-05-18~~` (the two P0 / cosmetic siblings from the same walk; the post-smoke commit triad closes all three).

### ~~D-luciel-ecs-web-role-missing-ses-send-permission-2026-05-18~~
**Status:** RESOLVED (ledger correction) on 2026-05-22 in Arc 3 B.3 — discovery proved the `LucielSESSendEmail` inline policy on `luciel-ecs-web-role` was already in place pre-Arc-3, scoped to `arn:aws:ses:ca-central-1:729005488042:identity/vantagemind.ai` with `ses:SendEmail`, `ses:SendRawEmail`, `ses:SendBulkEmail`. The drift was raised on a partial scout; the IAM layer is sound for the current sandboxed-SES posture. The post-sandbox-exit widening of the `Resource` ARN to `identity/*` is now tracked as `D-ses-iam-overgrant-unused-actions-2026-05-22` (Arc 8 follow-up). **Arc 3 hygiene 2026-05-22:** strikethrough applied to §3 heading; matching §5 closure stanza authored in this same arc; closure record at `arc3-out/B3-ses-iam-no-op-record.md`. **Original Status (pre-closure):** OPEN — P2 deliverability/observability. Surfaced during the 2026-05-18 smoke walk when the welcome-set-password email for the placeholder owner address `aryan+smoke-30a5@yourdomain.com` failed in SES with `AccessDeniedException` while the parallel send to `aryans.www@gmail.com` (a verified identity) succeeded. The nuanced shape — some emails go through, others fail with the same task-role principal — points at the SES sandbox's per-identity allowlist combined with insufficient `ses:SendEmail` scoping on the `luciel-ecs-web-role` IAM role.
**Section that raised it:** Step 30a.5 live smoke walk, 2026-05-18 ≈15:08 EDT, while diagnosing why the owner address never received the set-password email. The agent recovered the JWT from the CloudWatch `welcome-set-password-email` warning line (which logs the full URL on the SES failure path; cross-ref `D-set-password-token-logged-plaintext-2026-05-17`).
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-18 ≈15:08 EDT during the recovery dance for the placeholder owner address.
**Design claim:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (Auth model — Option B welcome-email mechanic) commits that every redeemable invite ships a welcome email; the implicit precondition is that the SES principal is authorized to deliver to any RFC-5322-valid address (post-sandbox-exit) or to any pre-verified address (pre-sandbox-exit). The current IAM scoping satisfies neither cleanly.
**Repo state:** No repo-side defect; the drift is in AWS infra (IAM role + SES configuration). The IAM role `luciel-ecs-web-role` is attached to both `luciel-backend-service` task and `luciel-worker-service` task; both inherit the same scoped `ses:SendEmail` permission. The SES account remains in sandbox mode in `ca-central-1`.
**Operational impact today:** Low — bounded by the SES sandbox shape (only verified identities receive). The real risk is the post-sandbox-exit moment: the moment SES sandbox is lifted, the IAM scoping becomes the next layer that can silently fail without anyone noticing. Today's loud `AccessDeniedException` becomes tomorrow's silent delivery gap if the IAM scoping isn't widened in lockstep with the sandbox exit.
**Owning roadmap step:** None today — paired with the SES-sandbox-exit task in the deliverability runway. Natural pairing with the next email-service touch.
**Resolution path:** Three-stage. (a) Audit the current `luciel-ecs-web-role` policy attachment for the `ses:SendEmail` and `ses:SendRawEmail` actions; widen the `Resource` ARN from any per-identity ARN to the account-level `arn:aws:ses:ca-central-1:729005488042:identity/*` so post-sandbox the role can send from any verified identity without an IAM redeploy. (b) Add a request a SES-sandbox-exit ticket with AWS Support; mirror DNS to SPF/DKIM/DMARC for `vantagemind.ai` (already in place per the 2026-05-17 dyn-DNS work) so the exit is approved on first attempt. (c) Add `tests/integration/test_ses_send_smoke.py` (skipped under `CI=true`, runs only on `LIVE_SES=1`) that sends a real email to a configured allowlist address and asserts a `MessageId` is returned — closure evidence for the post-sandbox state.
**Pattern E:** Infra-layer fix paired with an observability test. No code change in the application layer. No schema change. Customer-visible surface change is strictly an improvement (more emails deliver, observability improves).
**Validation evidence:** Discovery evidence is the CloudWatch warning line at 2026-05-18 ≈15:08 EDT showing `AccessDeniedException` for the placeholder address alongside a successful `MessageId` for the verified address (same task, same code path, same IAM role). Closure evidence pending the sandbox-exit milestone.
**Cross-refs:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (the welcome-email contract this drift partially defends); `D-set-password-token-logged-plaintext-2026-05-17` (sibling email-service drift; the failure-path token logging is what enabled the recovery dance that surfaced this drift); `D-welcome-email-subject-mojibake-2026-05-17` (sibling email-service drift surfaced earlier).

### ~~D-billing-webhook-service-stripe-attribute-error-2026-05-18~~
**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-20 in Arc 2 backend-hygiene by extending `BillingWebhookService.__init__` to accept and store `self.stripe: StripeClient` (default-resolved via `get_stripe_client()` when not injected), plus threading the singleton through both route call sites in `app/api/v1/billing.py` (the bad-signature audit path at L194 and the main dispatch at L276). The `_on_checkout_completed`'s `self.stripe.retrieve_subscription(...)` read now resolves a real StripeClient on every webhook; the existing try/except remains in place as defense-in-depth for genuine Stripe-unreachable conditions. **Arc 2 hygiene 2026-05-20:** strikethrough applied to §3 heading; matching §5 closure stanza authored in this same arc. **Original Status (pre-closure):** OPEN — P3 fallback-path observability. Surfaced in CloudWatch during the 2026-05-18 smoke walk's Stripe webhook leg: a `BillingWebhookService` instance raised `'BillingWebhookService' object has no attribute 'stripe'` when attempting to read `self.stripe` on the primary subscription-resolution path. The fallback path (resolving the sub_id directly from `checkout.session` event fields) caught the error and continued cleanly, so the tenant provisioned correctly and no customer-visible failure occurred. The drift is the attribute-access defect itself — it should not exist on a path that runs on every checkout.
**Section that raised it:** Step 30a.5 live smoke walk, 2026-05-18 ≈15:06 EDT, during the post-Stripe-checkout webhook-replay observability sweep.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-18 ≈15:06 EDT during the error-log sweep.
**Design claim:** No CANONICAL_RECAP or ARCHITECTURE claim is directly broken — the fallback path's existence is part of the design. The drift is that the primary path runs into an attribute error before the fallback fires, which means the fallback is the de-facto primary on every checkout. The hot path should not depend on a try-except over an `AttributeError`.
**Repo state:** Defect in `app/services/billing/webhook_service.py` (or wherever the `BillingWebhookService` class is defined). The constructor evidently does not set `self.stripe` on every code path; the resolve method references `self.stripe` unguarded. Need to read the file to pin the exact line numbers (deferred to the resolution commit).
**Operational impact today:** Zero customer-visible impact — every paid tenant from the live $300 and $1,000 walks provisioned correctly. The fallback path is the load-bearing surface. Impact escalates if the fallback ever breaks: today's silent-recovery becomes tomorrow's silent-non-provisioning if no one notices the primary path is dead.
**Owning roadmap step:** None today — a focused billing-service hardening commit on `main`. Natural pairing with the next billing-service touch.
**Resolution path:** Two-stage. (a) Read the `BillingWebhookService` constructor and resolve the missing-attribute init path; either always set `self.stripe = stripe_client` (passing `None` is fine if the resolve method tolerates it) or rename the attribute so the unguarded reference reads off a structurally-present field. (b) Add `tests/services/billing/test_webhook_service_attrs.py` with an AST-style assertion that every method that references `self.stripe` is preceded by an `__init__` write of the same attribute, and a runtime assertion that constructing `BillingWebhookService()` does not leave the attribute unset.
**Pattern E:** Pure constructor-layer fix. No route change. No schema change. The fallback path stays in place as defense-in-depth even after the primary path is fixed.
**Validation evidence:** Discovery evidence is the CloudWatch error line at 2026-05-18 ≈15:06 EDT showing the `AttributeError` traceback. Closure evidence is the AST + runtime test green plus a clean log sweep on the next live checkout.
**Cross-refs:** Step 30a.1 (Stripe checkout primitives — the surface this service backs); Step 30a.4 (the Team-tier $100 paid walk that did not surface this drift, suggesting the missing-attribute path was introduced or aggravated between 30a.4 and 30a.5).

### ~~D-luciel-migrate-pins-raw-digest-fragile-2026-05-18~~
**Status:** CLOSED 2026-05-18 by the deploy hygiene fix in the same evening's Step 30a.5 post-smoke deployment. Pre-closure body preserved below.
**Pre-closure body (preserved for audit):** During the 2026-05-18 post-smoke deploy, the existing `luciel-migrate:14` task definition pointed at image digest `sha256:aca2135c…` which had been pruned from ECR by the lifecycle policy (the 30a.4-era image preceding the 30a.5 build). Attempting to run the migrate task as a pre-deploy schema probe failed with `ImagePull` errors. The workaround — register `luciel-migrate:15` against the fresh 30a.5 image digest — worked the first time but exposes a structural fragility: pinning raw digests in long-lived task definitions ties them to ECR's retention behavior, which can prune mid-deploy.
**Section that raised it:** Step 30a.5 first prod deploy, 2026-05-18 ≈12:35 EDT, when the migrate probe failed to pull its image. Resolved within the same deploy by registering the fresh task-def.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-18 ≈12:36 EDT during the alembic-head probe step.
**Design claim:** No formal claim is broken — the deploy runbook implicitly assumed long-lived task-defs would remain runnable. The drift is the absence of a digest-freshness step in the runbook.
**Repo state:** No repo-side defect; the deploy runbook (today living in the partner's session memory and the design doc §12) implicitly assumed the migrate task-def could be re-run at will. The fix is procedural: every deploy registers a fresh `luciel-migrate:N+1` against the same digest as the backend image, rather than reusing a long-lived task-def revision.
**Operational impact today:** Zero customer-visible impact. The Step 30a.5 deploy completed with the workaround. Impact going forward is bounded by the policy now baked into the runbook (every deploy registers fresh task-defs for all three families: backend, worker, migrate).
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.5 post-smoke deploy hygiene. The 2026-05-18 ≈18:48 EDT post-smoke deploy executed cleanly with `luciel-backend:72` / `luciel-worker:27` / `luciel-migrate:16` all freshly registered against image digest `sha256:8b5020d7745c3ae681e1083f2cc2407793e69b9f8250bfba08fef327dfeb4692` — the procedural fix is in place and proven.
**Resolution path (executed):** Procedural. The post-30a.4 deploy script (today PowerShell, future shell-out) registers fresh task-defs for all three families (backend, worker, migrate) on every deploy, sharing the same image digest. Documentation lives in the design doc's deploy section (`docs/designs/step-30a-5-company-self-serve.md` §12 to be added on the doc-truth pass) and in this drift entry. No source-tree change.
**Pattern E:** Pure procedural fix. No code change. No schema change. The previous-deploy task-defs are not deregistered (so rollback to a prior revision remains possible until ECR prunes the older image), and the new task-defs use the fresh digest.
**Validation evidence:** The 2026-05-18 ≈18:48 EDT deploy registered `luciel-backend:72` / `luciel-worker:27` / `luciel-migrate:16` cleanly, the migrate probe ran to `exitCode: 0`, the backend service rolled to steady state, and the OpenAPI wire check confirmed the new schema is live.
**Cross-refs:** Step 30a.5 design §12 (the deploy section the doc-truth pass updates); `D-ecs-exec-powershell-python-c-quoting-fragile-2026-05-16` (sibling deploy-hygiene drift on the laptop-side quoting).

### D-stripe-checkout-no-email-validation-2026-05-18
**Status:** OPEN — P3 product polish. Surfaced when the partner accidentally completed the Step 30a.5 $1,000 Stripe checkout with the literal placeholder email `aryan+smoke-30a5@yourdomain.com` — a non-deliverable address. The checkout accepted the address and minted a tenant, owner user, and welcome-email send (which failed in SES with `AccessDeniedException`, see sibling drift). A simple deliverability check at the checkout step would have caught this before payment.
**Section that raised it:** Step 30a.5 live smoke walk, 2026-05-18 ≈15:05 EDT, when the partner noticed the welcome email never arrived to a real inbox and traced it back to the typo.
**Raised by:** Aryan (partner) on 2026-05-18 ≈15:05 EDT.
**Design claim:** No CANONICAL_RECAP or ARCHITECTURE claim is directly broken. The Stripe checkout's email field is the customer's responsibility under Stripe's design. The drift is the second-order observation that a typo here cascades into a tenant-minted-without-deliverability state — the customer paid, the tenant exists, the welcome email cannot be delivered, the customer cannot self-serve their workspace.
**Repo state:** No repo-side defect. The Stripe checkout is hosted by Stripe and the email field is whatever the buyer types. The drift is in the absence of a deliverability check downstream of the Stripe webhook — the `BillingWebhookService` accepts the address as-is and hands it to `tier_provisioning_service` which mints the owner user.
**Operational impact today:** Low — the Step 30a.5 smoke was the first occurrence and was self-resolved by extracting the JWT from CloudWatch. Impact escalates with real-customer typos because the customer cannot recover without a support touch (no welcome email, no `/auth/forgot-password` send to a deliverable address).
**Owning roadmap step:** None today — a focused billing-hardening commit on `main` or a separate "checkout deliverability" mini-step. Natural pairing with the SES-sandbox-exit milestone (drift `D-luciel-ecs-web-role-missing-ses-send-permission-2026-05-18`).
**Resolution path:** Two viable shapes. (a) **Pre-mint validation** (cheapest): in `tier_provisioning_service` before creating the owner user, run the buyer email through `email_validator.validate_email(..., check_deliverability=True)` which performs an MX-record lookup; if deliverability fails, surface a `customer.email_invalid` webhook to a slack channel and skip the welcome email (the customer can recover via Stripe's customer-portal email-edit). (b) **Post-mint repair flow**: surface a `customer-email-invalid` warning in the `/dashboard` empty state with an inline "Update your email" form that re-mints the welcome JWT. Default recommendation is (a) for the cost/benefit; (b) is the additive complement for the long tail.
**Pattern E:** Either resolution is additive at the service layer. No schema change. No route signature change beyond the optional new "update email" route in option (b). Customer-visible surface change is strictly an improvement.
**Validation evidence:** Discovery evidence is the 2026-05-18 ≈15:05 EDT smoke walk where the placeholder address minted a tenant and the welcome email failed at SES. Closure evidence is a deliberate typo-injection test in `tests/services/test_tier_provisioning_email_validation.py` plus a clean live smoke against a deliverable but previously-untested address.
**Cross-refs:** `D-luciel-ecs-web-role-missing-ses-send-permission-2026-05-18` (the sibling email-deliverability drift surfaced in the same walk); `D-pilot-account-billing-no-subscription-on-file-2026-05-16` (predecessor billing-hardening drift); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (the Option B welcome-email mechanic this drift defends).

### ~~D-set-password-token-logged-plaintext-2026-05-17~~
**Status:** RESOLVED (ingest-side) on 2026-05-20 in Arc 2 backend-hygiene; the in-flight redaction emitter contract is in place and pinned by `tests/security/test_email_service_redaction.py`. The CloudWatch backlog audit (resolution-path leg c — `aws logs filter-log-events` + idempotent `status='revoked'` flip on any token-bearing row whose `jti` is found in the historical log buffer) is a paired prod-touch deferred to Arc 3. **Arc 2 hygiene 2026-05-20:** strikethrough applied to §3 heading; matching §5 closure stanza authored in this same arc under the Arc 2 banner. **Original Status (pre-closure):** OPEN — P1 security. Every set-password and magic-link delivery in `app/services/email_service.py` logs the full token-bearing URL at INFO level on the success path and at WARNING level on the SES failure path, embedding the unredeemed signed HS256 JWT verbatim in CloudWatch. The success-path emitters are at line 197–204 (`[magic-link-email] ... url=%s ... message_id=%s`), line 365–374 (`[welcome-set-password-email] ... url=%s message_id=%s`), and line 524 (pilot-refund email). The failure-path emitters at line 208–216 and line 376–386 additionally log the full plaintext body alongside the URL. Until the token is consumed (single-use `token_jti`) or expires (24h JWT TTL, 7d row TTL for invites), anyone with `logs:GetLogEvents` on `/aws/ecs/luciel-backend` can lift a usable invite/welcome/reset link from CloudWatch and impersonate the inviter's mint by exchanging it at `/auth/set-password`.
**Section that raised it:** Step 30a.4 doc-truth pass on 2026-05-17, surfaced while reviewing `app/services/email_service.py` for the welcome-email mojibake drift (see `D-welcome-email-subject-mojibake-2026-05-17`). Not surfaced earlier because the Step 30a.3 close (`~~D-magic-link-only-auth-no-password-fallback-2026-05-16~~`) audited the route and webhook surface but not the email-send observability surface.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-17 during the §3.2.13 read-back to verify the Team-invite path closure.
**Design claim:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (Auth model — Option B welcome-email mechanic) commits that the set-password JWT is a single-use bearer credential whose only legitimate carrier is the customer's inbox. The implicit precondition is that the token does not appear in any other persisted store — neither database row (it is hashed to `token_jti`), nor request log, nor SES delivery log, nor application log. CloudWatch is a persisted log store. The implementation violates the precondition.
**Repo state:** Defect at `app/services/email_service.py` lines 197–204, 208–216, 365–374, 376–386, 524, 536 (and any future paired emitters). Current behaviour is uniform across all three send paths (magic-link, welcome-set-password, pilot-refund) since the email-service module was written in one cut. CloudWatch log group is `/aws/ecs/luciel-backend` retention currently `Never Expire` (verified via `aws logs describe-log-groups`).
**Operational impact today:** High-but-narrow exposure window. The privilege bar to lift the token is `logs:GetLogEvents` on the backend log group — today the IAM principals with that permission are the founder's AWS console role and the `luciel-ecs-web-role` (the latter cannot read its own logs). No third-party log shipper is configured. Exposure becomes acute the moment a log-shipping integration (Datadog, Splunk, BetterStack, Loki) is added without a redaction layer, because the token surfaces in any downstream sink. Equally acute if a future operator-shared CloudWatch dashboard ever copies a log line into a Slack channel, support ticket, or Notion page.
**Owning roadmap step:** None today — a focused observability-hardening commit on `main` rather than a roadmap deliverable. Natural pairing with the next email-service touch.
**Resolution path:** Three-stage. (a) **Redact at the emitter** — replace every `url=%s` with `url_token_jti=%s` and pass the JWT's `jti` claim (extracted via the existing `consume_*` helpers' read-only decode path) instead of the full URL; on the failure path, also strip `?token=...` from the URL before logging. (b) **Pin the contract** — add `tests/api/test_email_service_redaction.py` with a `caplog` assertion that no INFO-or-WARNING line emitted from a `send_welcome_set_password_email` call contains the substring `?token=`. (c) **Audit the existing CloudWatch backlog** — one-shot script that scans the last 24h of `/aws/ecs/luciel-backend` for `?token=` occurrences, captures the `token_jti` for each, and force-marks the matching `user_invites` / magic-link rows `status='revoked'` so any token already in the log loses redemption power. The audit script is the closure-side evidence.
**Pattern E:** Pure observability fix at the emitter layer. No schema change. No route signature change. No customer-visible surface change. The `token_jti` substitution is a strict reduction of disclosure (the jti is what already appears in the DB row, which is bounded by the application's existing access control).
**Validation evidence:** Pending. Discovery evidence is direct code read on 2026-05-17 (file `app/services/email_service.py` at the cited line numbers, HEAD commit `0818b9e`); confirmation against CloudWatch is the `diag_tail_backend.ps1` output dump from the same session showing `url=https://vantagemind.ai/auth/set-password?token=eyJ...` in a successful welcome-email INFO row for invite-006.
**Cross-refs:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (the Option B welcome-email mechanic — the design contract this drift breaks); `~~D-magic-link-only-auth-no-password-fallback-2026-05-16~~` (predecessor — the Step 30a.3 closure that introduced the welcome-set-password path; the new emitter inherited the pre-existing magic-link emitter's logging shape, so the defect predates Step 30a.4 but is uniform across all three send paths); `~~D-team-self-serve-incomplete-invite-ui-missing-2026-05-16~~` (the closure under which this drift was discovered); `D-welcome-email-subject-mojibake-2026-05-17` (sibling email-service drift surfaced in the same pass); `D-secret-disclosure-recurrence-2026-05-12` (the structural-pattern sibling — the email-service emitter logs a credential the same way previous incidents logged DSNs; the broader hardening discipline that drift records applies here).

### ~~D-welcome-email-subject-mojibake-2026-05-17~~
**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-20 in Arc 2 backend-hygiene by replacing U+2019 (right-single-quote) and U+2014 (em-dash) with ASCII equivalents in `SUBJECT_WELCOME_SET_PASSWORD`, `SUBJECT_INVITE_SET_PASSWORD`, and `SUBJECT_RESET_PASSWORD` (resolution-path option (a)). Body copy keeps the typographer's quotes / em-dashes because `Body.Text.Data` is wire-carried with explicit `Charset="UTF-8"` which Gmail decodes correctly — only the `Simple.Subject` header path was wire-degraded. **Arc 2 hygiene 2026-05-20:** strikethrough applied to §3 heading; matching §5 closure stanza authored in this same arc. **Original Status (pre-closure):** OPEN — cosmetic + deliverability. The welcome-set-password and invite-set-password subjects render in Gmail as `YouÆve been invited to VantageMind ù set your password` (smart-apostrophe and em-dash mangled to Latin-1 fallback glyphs), not the intended `You've been invited to VantageMind — set your password`. The source string at `app/services/email_service.py` line 54 is valid UTF-8 (`SUBJECT_INVITE_SET_PASSWORD: Final[str] = "You\u2019ve been invited to VantageMind \u2014 set your password"`), and the SES `Subject` content block at line 359 correctly sets `"Charset": "UTF-8"`. The mojibake is therefore introduced at the SES wire layer — SES v2 `send_email` with `Simple.Subject` writes the subject header without RFC 2047 encoded-word wrapping, so any non-ASCII character degrades to `=?` fallback at the receiving MUA when the SMTP `Content-Transfer-Encoding` chain assumes Latin-1.
**Section that raised it:** Step 30a.4 doc-truth pass on 2026-05-17, surfaced from screenshots of the test-clock invite emails Aryan forwarded into the session. Not surfaced earlier because the Step 30a.3 close exercised the welcome-email surface only against the log-only transport (`LUCIEL_EMAIL_TRANSPORT=log`), and the live $100 paid Individual smoke at 2026-05-16 ≈21:06 EDT used the magic-link subject (`Welcome to VantageMind — set your password`) which has the same em-dash but Aryan did not surface a Gmail rendering at that time.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-17 during the §3.2.13 read-back, after Aryan's screenshot showed the rendered subject in his Gmail inbox.
**Design claim:** No CANONICAL_RECAP or ARCHITECTURE claim is directly broken; the subject literal is locked in source but the rendered subject is the customer-facing surface. The closest design hook is the implicit Pattern E contract that the brand presentation is consistent across the marketing site and the transactional inbox.
**Repo state:** Source string correct (UTF-8 codepoints U+2019 and U+2014) at `app/services/email_service.py` line 53–54 and at the invite send-call sites. SES v2 send_email parameterisation at line 354–362 uses `Content.Simple.Subject.Data` with `Charset="UTF-8"`, which the SES v2 docs describe as the supported shape but which in practice does not emit an RFC 2047 `=?UTF-8?B?...?=` encoded-word header — the subject is wire-encoded as the raw UTF-8 byte sequence, which Gmail then decodes per its local fallback table (Latin-1 in the observed case).
**Operational impact today:** Low. The invite link in the body works regardless of subject rendering, so no customer is blocked. Deliverability secondary effect: a subject containing the characters `Æ` and `ù` for a transactional brand email increases Gmail spam-classifier weight, which interacts badly with the broader "transactional from a young domain" signal that Aryan independently observed during the session (invite-006 landed in spam despite SES success).
**Owning roadmap step:** None today — a focused email-hygiene commit on `main`. Natural pairing with the next email-service touch or with the JWT-in-logs sibling drift (`D-set-password-token-logged-plaintext-2026-05-17`).
**Resolution path:** Two viable shapes. **(a) ASCII-only subjects** (simplest): replace `\u2019` with `'` and `\u2014` with `-` in all three subject constants — `SUBJECT_MAGIC_LINK`, `SUBJECT_WELCOME_SET_PASSWORD`, `SUBJECT_INVITE_SET_PASSWORD`. Removes the mojibake entirely with zero infra change. **(b) Switch to `send_raw_email`** (cleaner long-term): assemble the MIME message via `email.message.EmailMessage` which writes `Subject` as `=?UTF-8?B?...?=` automatically, then call `client.send_raw_email(RawMessage={"Data": msg.as_bytes()})`. Preserves the typographer's quote and em-dash but is a larger change footprint touching three send paths. Default recommendation is (a) given the cost/benefit tradeoff; revisit (b) when the brand voice case for proper typography rises (e.g. when a designer joins). Closure evidence is a real-domain SES smoke against a Gmail address where the rendered subject contains the literal ASCII string.
**Pattern E:** Pure copy fix at the emitter layer (option a) or a localised transport-layer swap (option b). No schema change. No customer-visible link-or-flow change. The invite redemption surface is identical pre- and post-fix.
**Validation evidence:** Discovery evidence is Aryan's screenshot of the test-clock invite-006 inbox (Gmail rendering `YouÆve` and `ù`) on 2026-05-17. Source-side evidence is a direct read of `app/services/email_service.py` line 53–54 at HEAD `0818b9e` confirming the UTF-8 codepoints in the source string and `Charset="UTF-8"` in the SES request.
**Cross-refs:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (the Option B welcome-email mechanic — the rendered-subject surface this drift defends); `D-set-password-token-logged-plaintext-2026-05-17` (sibling email-service drift surfaced in the same pass; pairs at the next email-service touch); `~~D-team-self-serve-incomplete-invite-ui-missing-2026-05-16~~` (the closure under which this drift was discovered).

### ~~D-step-30a-owner-scopeassignment-missing-self-serve-checkout-2026-05-17~~
**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-17 — owner `ScopeAssignment` is now minted at every self-serve checkout via `_ensure_owner_scope_assignment` in `app/services/tier_provisioning_service.py` (line 401, invoked from `premint_for_tier` at line 215). Pre-existing self-serve buyers backfilled by Alembic migration `b4d8a2e7c1f3_step30a_owner_scope_backfill.py` (descends from `e7b2c9d4a18f`, head `b4d8a2e7c1f3` as verified via `alembic current`). Audit-preserved in §3 with strikethrough per move-to-§5 doctrine; closure stanza in §5.
**Pre-closure body (preserved for audit):** Owner-scope precondition gap. The Step 30a.4 invite surface's `_resolve_invite_actor` reads the caller's `(tenant_id, domain_id)` off the active `ScopeAssignment` row for the cookied `user_id`. Self-serve checkout at Step 30a.1 minted `User`, `Tenant`, `Domain`, `Agent`, `LucielInstance`, `Subscription`, and `AdminApiKey`, but never minted the owner's own `ScopeAssignment` — the design assumed Step 30a.1's pre-mint walked the scope rows for every primitive, but the buyer's-own-scope row was absent from the walk. The visible failure mode at the time the closure tag cut was that any cookied request hitting `/api/v1/admin/invites` (or any other route gated on `_resolve_invite_actor`) returned 401 with `actor_scope_not_found`, because no row existed in `scope_assignments` for `user_id=<buyer>`. Live-discovered when Aryan attempted to invite a teammate from `/app/team` on the test-clock Team tenant immediately after the Step 30a.4 closing tag.
**Section that raised it:** Step 30a.4 closing-tag verification, 2026-05-17. Surfaced during the first cookied attempt at `POST /api/v1/admin/invites` against the freshly-deployed task-def carrying the four new routes. The route returned 401 with `actor_scope_not_found` rather than the expected 201 invite-row; CloudWatch trace pointed at `_resolve_invite_actor` raising on the empty `scope_assignments` query for the cookied user.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-17, after correlating the 401 response with the `ScopeAssignment` repository's empty-result branch.
**Design claim:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (Auth model — cookie→admin-context bridge) and §4.7 (three-layer scope enforcement) together commit that every cookied caller resolves to a stable `(tenant_id, domain_id?)` tuple via an active `ScopeAssignment` row. The Step 30a.1 closure (`~~D-billing-team-company-not-self-serve-2026-05-13~~`) stated that `TierProvisioningService.pre_mint_for_tier` walks every scope-bearing row at signup. The implicit precondition that the buyer's-own owner `ScopeAssignment` is one of those rows was never spelled out; the implementation skipped it because the Step 30a-era assumption was that the buyer's only relationship to the tenant was through the `Tenant.owner_user_id` FK, which the Step 30a.4 `_resolve_invite_actor` does not consult.
**Repo state:** Fix at commit `8019866` ("D1: mint owner ScopeAssignment at self-serve checkout") on `aryanonline/Luciel` `main`. `app/services/tier_provisioning_service.py` adds `_ensure_owner_scope_assignment(session, user_id, tenant_id, domain_id)` at line 401 — looks up an active `ScopeAssignment` for `(user_id, tenant_id)`, inserts one with `role='owner'`, `domain_id=<the just-minted default Domain>` if absent, idempotent on retries. Called from `premint_for_tier` at line 215, after the `LucielInstance` mint but before the post-mint commit, so the row lands in the same transaction as the rest of the signup pre-mint walk. Backfill at commit `6cb8d4a` ("D2: backfill migration for existing self-serve buyers") — Alembic migration `b4d8a2e7c1f3_step30a_owner_scope_backfill.py` descends from `e7b2c9d4a18f` (the Step 30a.4 `user_invites` migration), walks every `tenants` row with a non-NULL `owner_user_id` that lacks an active `scope_assignments` row for `(owner_user_id, tenant_id)`, and inserts the missing row. Idempotent under re-run because the insert is gated on `WHERE NOT EXISTS`. Migration head verified `b4d8a2e7c1f3` via `alembic current` post-deploy.
**Operational impact today:** Resolved. Pre-resolution impact was total — every cookied admin route that consulted `_resolve_invite_actor` (the four `/admin/invites` lifecycle routes) returned 401 with `actor_scope_not_found` for every self-serve buyer; the test-clock Team tenant Aryan was using to verify the closing tag could not mint a single invite. Post-resolution impact is zero: the live test-clock Team tenant successfully minted three invites, redeemed three set-password tokens, and the audit chain `USER_INVITED×3 → INVITE_REDEEMED×3` is walkable in `admin_audit_logs`.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.4 closing-tag arc. The fix sits inside the same closing-tag arc as the Step 30a.4 invite UI; the closing tag is re-cut as `step-30a-4-team-invite-ui-corrected` to record the two-commit correction on top of the original `step-30a-4-team-invite-ui-complete`.
**Resolution path:** Two-stage (now closed). (1) Mint the owner `ScopeAssignment` at every future self-serve checkout (forward-fix, commit `8019866`). (2) Backfill the missing row for every existing self-serve buyer (one-shot migration, commit `6cb8d4a`). Both landed on `main` and the migration ran cleanly to head `b4d8a2e7c1f3` in production.
**Pattern E:** Additive forward + idempotent backfill. The forward-fix adds one helper function and one call site inside an existing service method; no row mutation on pre-existing data because the helper short-circuits when the row already exists. The backfill migration inserts only missing rows (`WHERE NOT EXISTS` predicate); it never mutates an existing `scope_assignments` row, never deletes, and survives re-run. AdminAuditLog footprint is zero because pre-mint walks do not emit audit rows (the audit chain begins at user-action time).
**Validation evidence:** Direct test-clock Team-tenant evidence on 2026-05-17 — three invites minted via `POST /api/v1/admin/invites`, three redemption round-trips through `/auth/set-password?token=...`, three new agents visible on `/app/team` via `GET /agents?list_all=true`. `alembic current` returns `b4d8a2e7c1f3 (head)` on the deployed container. Pre-fix evidence is the CloudWatch 401-trace from the first invite attempt against the test-clock tenant, captured in the Step 30a.4 verification dump.
**Cross-refs:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (the cookie→admin-context bridge whose `_resolve_invite_actor` precondition this fix honours — updated this same commit to name `_ensure_owner_scope_assignment` in the Team-invite path paragraph); ARCHITECTURE §4.7 (three-layer scope enforcement — the precondition that every cookied caller resolves through an active `ScopeAssignment`); `~~D-team-self-serve-incomplete-invite-ui-missing-2026-05-16~~` (parent closure — the Step 30a.4 closing tag this fix sits inside; closure stanza in §5 names commits `8019866` and `6cb8d4a` in the chain); `~~D-billing-team-company-not-self-serve-2026-05-13~~` (predecessor — the Step 30a.1 closure whose pre-mint walk this drift retroactively extends); `D-cors-delete-method-blocked-2026-05-17` (sibling correction landed in the same Step 30a.4 closing-tag re-cut arc, deploy-only fix); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.4 row (the design home; updated this commit to record the corrected closing tag).

### ~~D-cors-delete-method-blocked-2026-05-17~~
**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-17 — `app/main.py` line 133 widens CORSMiddleware `allow_methods` from `["GET", "POST", "OPTIONS"]` to `["GET", "POST", "PATCH", "DELETE", "OPTIONS"]`, deployed via `scripts/deploy_30a4_hotfix_e1.ps1` to task-def `:69` (commit `4a650c5` for the source change, `0818b9e` for the deploy script). Verified post-deploy by F12 Network capture on 2026-05-17 showing `OPTIONS https://api.vantagemind.ai/api/v1/admin/invites/<id>/revoke` returning **200** with `Access-Control-Allow-Methods` including `DELETE`, immediately followed by the `DELETE` request returning **200** with the revoke success body. Audit-preserved in §3 with strikethrough per move-to-§5 doctrine; closure stanza in §5.
**Pre-closure body (preserved for audit):** CORS preflight gap. The Step 30a.4 website surface inside `src/pages/Dashboard.tsx` TeamTab calls `revokeInvite(id)` from `src/lib/admin.ts`, which issues a cross-origin `DELETE /api/v1/admin/invites/{id}/revoke` against `api.vantagemind.ai` from the `vantagemind.ai` Amplify origin. The browser's CORS preflight (`OPTIONS` with `Access-Control-Request-Method: DELETE`) was rejected by the backend with HTTP 400 because the CORSMiddleware at `app/main.py` line 130–134 declared `allow_methods=["GET", "POST", "OPTIONS"]` only. The `DELETE` request itself never fired (the browser short-circuits on a failed preflight), so the React handler surfaced the non-AdminApiError fallback toast "Couldn't revoke" — which mimicked a network error and sent the diagnostic in the wrong direction for the first hour of the incident. Visible only on the website surface; cookied curl against the same endpoint succeeded because curl does not issue preflight.
**Section that raised it:** Step 30a.4 closing-tag verification continuation, 2026-05-17. Surfaced after the D1+D2 fix unblocked the create+list paths; the revoke path then exhibited a different failure mode (toast vs 401). Discovered when Aryan attempted to revoke an invite from the test-clock TeamTab and the toast read "Couldn't revoke" with no further error context.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-17, after initially mis-attributing the failure to the new revoke route's error path; the F12 Network screenshot from Aryan showing `OPTIONS = 400` on the preflight vindicated the original CORS hypothesis that the advisor had retracted prematurely. Advisor-side lesson: retracting CORS on the basis of `OPTIONS POST = 200` traces in CloudWatch was a confusion of preflight-method vs request-method — POST preflights had always succeeded because POST was in `allow_methods`; the new DELETE method was the regression vector.
**Design claim:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (Auth model — cookie→admin-context bridge) implicitly commits that every cookie-gated admin route is reachable from the website's same-cookie session. The Step 30a.4 closure added two new HTTP methods (PATCH not used today but reserved by the resend route's future signature; DELETE used today by the revoke route) without revising the CORS allowlist. The implicit precondition is that the CORS allowlist is a superset of every HTTP method any cookie-gated admin route serves; the implementation violated the precondition because the original allowlist was authored at Step 30a.2-pilot Commit 3d when only GET and POST routes existed.
**Repo state:** Fix at commit `4a650c5` ("step 30a.4 hotfix E1 (drift D-cors-delete-method-blocked-2026-05-17): widen CORS allow_methods to GET/POST/PATCH/DELETE/OPTIONS") on `aryanonline/Luciel` `main`. `app/main.py` line 133 changed from `allow_methods=["GET", "POST", "OPTIONS"]` to `allow_methods=["GET", "POST", "PATCH", "DELETE", "OPTIONS"]`. New test file `tests/api/test_step30a_4_cors_delete.py` adds two preflight-shape tests that pin the contract: one asserts `OPTIONS /api/v1/admin/invites/<id>/revoke` with `Access-Control-Request-Method: DELETE` returns 200 with `DELETE` in the `Access-Control-Allow-Methods` response header; one mirrors the assertion for `PATCH`. Both green against the in-memory test client. Deploy mechanic at commit `0818b9e` ("step 30a.4 hotfix E1: dedicated deploy script") — `scripts/deploy_30a4_hotfix_e1.ps1` is a minimal ECR-push + task-def-register + force-redeploy script with no Alembic step (no migration in this fix), correct `containerName="luciel-backend"` (avoiding the sibling `D-deploy-script-jq-filter-container-name-mismatch-2026-05-16` defect), and a post-deploy preflight check that hits `OPTIONS https://api.vantagemind.ai/api/v1/admin/invites/<probe-id>/revoke` and asserts 200.
**Operational impact today:** Resolved. Pre-resolution impact was high but narrow — the revoke surface was the only impacted route (resend is POST which had always been in the allowlist; the eventual PATCH-future routes did not yet exist on the website surface). Every Team-tier admin attempting to revoke a pending invite from the website saw the "Couldn't revoke" toast and could not unblock the invite-cap on their tenant. Workaround during the incident window was cookied curl with `-X DELETE` from the founder's terminal. Post-resolution impact is zero; F12 captures show OPTIONS=200 + DELETE=200 on the prod surface.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.4 closing-tag arc. Hotfix carve-out rather than a roadmap-step deliverable; closure is part of the closing-tag re-cut `step-30a-4-team-invite-ui-corrected` alongside D1+D2.
**Resolution path:** One-stage (now closed). Widen `allow_methods` at the CORSMiddleware mount, pin the contract with preflight-shape tests for every method actually served by a cookie-gated admin route, deploy via a dedicated hotfix script that includes a post-deploy preflight assertion. Closed in one round trip.
**Pattern E:** Additive widen of a list constant in middleware configuration. No schema change. No route signature change. No customer-visible surface change other than the previously-blocked revoke flow now succeeding. The CORS contract is strictly more permissive in one dimension (additional methods) and unchanged in the others (origins, headers, credentials). The pinning tests are additive in the test suite.
**Validation evidence:** F12 Network capture from Aryan on 2026-05-17 showing pre-fix preflight returning 400 and post-fix preflight returning 200 against the same endpoint, immediately followed by the DELETE returning 200. CloudWatch trace on the post-deploy task-def shows the revoke flipping the invite row's `status` from `pending` to `revoked` and emitting the `INVITE_REVOKED` audit row. Test-suite evidence: the two new tests in `tests/api/test_step30a_4_cors_delete.py` are green alongside the 28 contract tests in `tests/api/test_step30a_4_invite_shape.py` — 30/30 across the Step 30a.4 surface.
**Cross-refs:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (the cookie→admin-context bridge whose website-side reachability this drift defends — updated this same commit to record that `allow_methods` includes `PATCH` and `DELETE` since 2026-05-17 to support the cookied DELETE on `/admin/invites/{id}/revoke`); `~~D-team-self-serve-incomplete-invite-ui-missing-2026-05-16~~` (parent closure — the Step 30a.4 closing tag this fix sits inside; closure stanza in §5 names commit `4a650c5` and deploy `0818b9e` in the chain); `~~D-step-30a-owner-scopeassignment-missing-self-serve-checkout-2026-05-17~~` (sibling correction landed in the same Step 30a.4 closing-tag re-cut arc; surfaced first, blocked the create+list paths; CORS surfaced second, blocked the revoke path); `D-deploy-script-jq-filter-container-name-mismatch-2026-05-16` (sibling deploy-toolchain drift — `scripts/deploy_30a4_hotfix_e1.ps1` authored fresh with the correct `containerName="luciel-backend"` to avoid the systemic jq-filter defect; the sibling's broader fix on every `scripts/deploy_*.sh` remains OPEN); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.4 row (the design home; updated this commit to record the corrected closing tag).
