Two pieces remain unimplemented and are what this drift carves out: (a) the eighth `POST /pilot-refund` route that the 2026-05-15 canon amendment to CANONICAL_RECAP §14 ¶273 ("Intro refund policy") and ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 ("Eight-route HTTP surface") commit to, and (b) the website intro-offer surface across `aryanonline/Luciel-Website` (Pricing, Signup, Nav, Account, LegalTerms) that translates the locked canon into a customer-facing UX.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-15 during Step 30a.2 website-audit triage. The website concern — "the monetization on our website doesn't reflect our actual monetization" — surfaced that Pricing.tsx, Signup.tsx, Nav.tsx, Account.tsx, and LegalTerms.tsx still describe the pre-Step-30a.2 per-tier trial shape ($30/$300/$2000 CAD/mo with 14d / 7d / 7d trials respectively) rather than the locked paid-intro shape ($100 CAD one-time + uniform 90-day trial, first-time-only, full refund anytime in the trial window). The refund-surface gap surfaced in the same conversation: the partner locked "full refund anytime during the period, first-time only, self-serve" as the customer-facing promise, which the existing seven-route billing surface cannot deliver because (i) Stripe's Customer Portal does not natively expose one-time-charge refunds, (ii) the $100 intro fee is a separate one-time charge from the recurring subscription (Stripe Option A line-item assembly), and (iii) the customer-facing promise is "one-click refund + cancel", not "refund only, trial continues".
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §14 ¶271 commits the paid-intro shape; ¶273 (added 2026-05-15) commits the refund policy. ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 commits the eight-route HTTP surface and the `BillingService.process_pilot_refund` spec, including the eligibility predicate (`is_first_time_customer(email)` + `status=='trialing'` + `trial_end > now()`), the cascade behaviour (refund + tenant deactivation in one transaction), the new `SUBSCRIPTION_PILOT_REFUNDED` audit action with its field set, and the four error codes (`not_first_time_customer` 403, `intro_window_expired` 409, no-active-intro 404, Stripe-not-configured 501). The website surface is implied by the marketing-site contract in §3.2.13 ("the marketing site calls only the Luciel backend") and the Step 30a.2 first-time-gate smoke in `D-stripe-live-account-not-yet-activated-2026-05-13` annotation.
**Repo state:** Backend (`aryanonline/Luciel`): `app/services/billing_service.py` has `INTRO_TRIAL_DAYS=90`, `INTRO_FEE_PRICE_KEY`, `is_first_time_customer`, `resolve_intro_fee_price_id`, and the line-item assembly in `create_checkout_session`; `app/integrations/stripe/client.py` accepts `intro_fee_price_id` and stacks it on the recurring line; `app/core/config.py` defines `stripe_price_intro_fee: str = ""`. The eighth route `POST /pilot-refund` is **not** in `app/api/v1/billing.py`. `BillingService.process_pilot_refund` is **not** in `app/services/billing_service.py`. The `SUBSCRIPTION_PILOT_REFUNDED` action constant is **not** in `app/models/admin_audit_log.py`. No contract test file `tests/api/test_step30a_2_pilot_refund_shape.py` exists. Website (`aryanonline/Luciel-Website`): `src/pages/Pricing.tsx` still hard-codes `monthlyPrice: "$30" | "$300" | "$2,000"` and `annualPrice: "$300" | "$3,000" | "$20,000"` with per-tier trial copy; `src/pages/Signup.tsx` does not call a first-time-customer probe before rendering tier copy; `src/components/Nav.tsx` has no signup CTA (only `Book a demo`); `src/pages/Account.tsx` has no pilot-refund button; `src/pages/LegalTerms.tsx` §6 (Billing) describes monthly billing without the intro-fee and refund mechanics. No `useFirstTimeCustomerStatus` hook or equivalent exists in `src/hooks/`. The website is at commit `811387c` on `main` (Step 30a.2 Commit 2 — best-effort PIPEDA-aligned legal copy); the backend is at commit `76ed23f` on `main` and deployed live as `:50`.
**Operational impact today:** Medium. A first-time prospect landing on the marketing site sees the pre-Step-30a.2 tier pricing as the headline, can sign up via the existing Stripe Checkout flow, and — because the backend already runs Step 30a.2 Stripe Option A logic — will be charged $100 + a 90-day trial _if_ the `stripe_price_intro_fee` SSM parameter is populated with a real Price ID, or will hit the `resolve_intro_fee_price_id` empty-string fallback and the route layer's contact-sales 422 short-circuit otherwise (see `D-stripe-live-account-not-yet-activated-2026-05-13`). Either way, the customer-facing copy does not match what the backend does; refunds can only be processed through operator-mediated Stripe Dashboard action today, not self-serve. No customer who could previously sign up cannot now; the gap is the Step 30a.2 success criterion ("a first-time customer can find Luciel, see the intro offer, pay $100, use the product for 90 days, refund themselves if they want, or convert to recurring on day 91") which is not yet end-to-end demonstrable.
**Resolution path:** Step 30a.2-pilot close (in flight 2026-05-15) lands in three commits. (a) **Backend (Luciel repo):** add `POST /api/v1/billing/pilot-refund` to `app/api/v1/billing.py`; add `BillingService.process_pilot_refund(user)` to `app/services/billing_service.py` with the eligibility, refund-issue, cascade, and audit-emission sequence specified in ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13; add `ACTION_SUBSCRIPTION_PILOT_REFUNDED` to `app/models/admin_audit_log.py`; extend `app/repositories/audit_chain.py` if any new field-set columns are needed (the four-field payload `{stripe_refund_id, intro_charge_id, refunded_amount_cents, currency}` fits inside the existing JSONB `details` column, no schema change needed); add `tests/api/test_step30a_2_pilot_refund_shape.py` covering 200, 403, 404, 409, 501 paths plus the audit-row contract; extend `tests/e2e/step_30a_live_e2e.py` with a `test_pilot_refund_self_serve` harness step. (b) **Backend deploy:** ECR push `:51`, register `td-:51`, force-redeploy, three-flow + pilot-refund smoke against live. (c) **Stripe live + SSM:** create the $100 CAD one-time intro Price in `acct_1TX2BmRytQVRVXw7`, write the Price ID to SSM `/luciel/production/stripe_price_intro_fee` (closes the parallel drift `D-stripe-live-account-not-yet-activated-2026-05-13` for the seventh Price). (d) **Website (Luciel-Website repo):** Pricing.tsx replaces the tier-headline price with `"$100 for 90 days, then $X/mo"` plus footnote (first-time customers, refund anytime in the trial), Signup.tsx detects first-time vs returning and shows the matching copy + invokes the right backend path, Nav.tsx gets a `Start 90-day pilot` CTA pointing to `/pricing`, Account.tsx renders a `Refund my $100 intro fee` button when the cookied user is in an active intro trial and wires it to `POST /pilot-refund`, LegalTerms.tsx §6 (Billing) gets a fourth subsection on the intro fee and refund window. (e) **Amplify rebuild + CloudFront `/*` invalidation.** Acceptance: the GATE 4 rewrite covers pilot purchase, Stripe test-clock day-91 conversion, self-serve refund (one real $100 live smoke), repeat-customer block, magic-link, widget embed, and cancel cascade end-to-end. Closing tag: `step-30a-2-pilot-complete`.
**Cross-refs:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.2 row; CANONICAL_RECAP §14 ¶271 (paid-intro shape) and ¶273 (refund policy); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (eight-route surface and `process_pilot_refund` spec); DRIFTS §3 `D-stripe-live-account-not-yet-activated-2026-05-13` (the parallel deploy gap for the seventh Stripe Price — closes in the same commit arc); DRIFTS §5 `~~D-trial-policy-mixed-per-tier-2026-05-14~~` (the design-side closure that this drift's implementation now delivers end-to-end).

The greppable stable identifier discipline pinned at `D-cross-reference-wiring-asymmetric-no-shared-q-step-tokens-2026-05-13` requires that cross-references into §12 use stable identifiers; when a row merges, the cross-references must be updated to name the merged row (e.g. "Step 32 wave 2") rather than the now-defunct sibling identifier ("Step 32b").
**Repo state at the time of raise:** `docs/CANONICAL_RECAP.md` §12 carries 26 rows after the pass-9 closing commit `a7484b6` (sorted by step number after `496dc2d`), with Step 32 and Step 32b as two adjacent rows describing waves 1 and 2 of the same `/dashboard` → `/app` shell evolution. Both rows cross-reference ARCHITECTURE §3.2.12 (Step 32b's wave-2 stanza) and §3.2.13 (the shared cookie middleware), both rows describe the same Step 31 dashboard backend, and both rows commit to the same `vantagemind.ai` origin (no subdomain split). The merge candidate is unambiguous; the sibling rows under audit (30a.2 + 30a.2-pilot, 30a.4 + 30a.5, 34 + 34a) each carry distinct markers, distinct closing tags, or distinct drift carriers.
**Operational impact at the time of raise:** Zero customer impact and zero behavior impact. The architecture is unchanged; the merge is a doc-truth restatement that names what the rows already describe — a single dashboard-shell concern shipped in two waves. The impact is on **read-cold-ness** and **doctrine consistency** — a cold reviewer reading §12 should see one row per architectural concern, not two rows that read as two independent steps when they are the same concern in two ship windows.

This Option 3 merge follow-up adds a sixth: **merge-vs-split honesty**. Predicate: for every adjacent pair of §12 rows, ask whether they describe (i) two independent architectural concerns (keep as two rows) or (ii) two waves / phases / increments of the same architectural concern (merge into one row with wave markers). The signal is the cross-reference shape: if both rows cross-reference the *same* ARCHITECTURE §3.2.X subsection and *the same* backend services, they almost certainly describe one concern in two ship windows. Future passes reading §12 will see a row that names two waves and can grep this drift to learn why; without this drift, the merge looks like a doctrine breach at first read (one row claiming two markers). This is the same precedent the pass-9 §12 honesty pass already established for the rename + marker re-stating: the meta-drift exists so the next reader of §12 understands the prior decisions without re-deriving them.

### D-scope-assignments-history-table-missing-2026-05-09

**Status:** RESOLVING THIS PASS — closes in commit (b) of this reconciliation
**Raised by:** Architecture §4.3 lists `scope_assignments_history` as one of three append-only tables that matter most.

Two rows in history, never UPDATE in place") using the same `scope_assignments` table as an append-only log. There is no separate `scope_assignments_history` table or migration anywhere in `alembic/versions/` or `app/models/`.

### D-celery-task-surface-thin-2026-05-09

**Status:** OPEN — partially tracked against existing roadmap; retention purge is the load-bearing gap
**Raised by:** Architecture §3.2.4 (background workers handle "ingesting documents the customer uploaded, refreshing search indexes, sending follow-up emails, running scheduled retention purges, and similar")
**Repo state:** `app/worker/tasks/` contains only `memory_extraction.py`. Document ingestion is built but as foreground code (`app/knowledge/ingestion.py`), not a worker task. There is no search-index refresh task, no follow-up-email task, no scheduled retention-purge task. `app/policy/retention.py` defines the policy; the worker that runs it does not exist.
**Owning roadmap mapping:** Document ingestion-as-worker and follow-up emails are subsumed by Step 34 (workflow actions). **Retention purge is not currently on the roadmap** and it is the load-bearing gap because Architecture §4.4's soft-delete + scheduled-purge guarantee depends on it actually running. Without a running purge worker, soft-deleted rows accumulate forever and the storage-cost story in §4.4 ("the retention worker handles that") is fiction.
**Doc-truthing this pass:** Architecture §3.2.4 gets per-responsibility markers (✅ memory extraction, 🔧 document ingestion as foreground, 📋 the rest). The retention-purge gap is escalated to its own drift token below (`D-retention-purge-worker-missing-2026-05-09`) because it has a load-bearing guarantee depending on it.

### D-context-assembler-thin-2026-05-09

**Status:** OPEN — code-quality drift, no owning roadmap step yet
**Raised by:** Architecture §4.2 ("at runtime, both layers are composed in a single foundation-model context, with the Soul layer placed structurally so it cannot be overridden by injected Profession-layer content")
**Repo state:** `app/runtime/context_assembler.py` produces a 6-line prompt: identity + tenant id + domain id + channel + user message + a stock instruction. The actual production prompt assembly happens in `app/services/chat_service.py` and is more substantive than the assembler suggests, but is not consolidated. Specifically missing: per-scope Profession-layer loading as a coherent step, a structural Soul-vs-Profession separation that prevents prompt injection from overriding Soul rules, and an output-side policy check that catches a model attempting to violate Soul-layer rules.
**Owning roadmap mapping:** None today. This is a refactor + a small policy addition, not a feature, so it does not naturally belong to one of the existing roadmap steps. Best fit is as a prerequisite of Step 33 (evaluation framework) since evaluation needs a single observable assembly point. Defer assignment; track as a code-quality drift.
**Doc-truthing this pass:** Architecture §4.2 gets a 🔧 marker. The drift stays open as a known refactor with no scheduled date — flagged for a future roadmap-grooming pass.
