### ~~D-retention-purge-worker-missing-2026-05-09~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-14 by Step 30a.2 — see §5 close entry. §3 body preserved verbatim per §6 doctrine. (Prior status: OPEN — load-bearing; needs a roadmap home.) **Arc 0 hygiene 2026-05-20:** strikethrough applied to §3 heading to match the §5 mirror at L1477; no body or status change.
**Raised by:** Split out from `D-celery-task-surface-thin-2026-05-09` because it has a load-bearing architectural guarantee depending on it.
**Design claim:** Architecture §4.4 ("The retention worker handles that, in batches sized to coexist with live traffic without lock contention"); Architecture §3.2.4 lists "running scheduled retention purges" as a worker responsibility; Architecture §3.4 commits "a retention purge cannot break the audit chain" which presumes a purge worker exists.
**Repo state:** `app/policy/retention.py` defines the retention policy. There is no scheduled task in `app/worker/tasks/` that runs the purge. Soft-deleted rows accumulate without bound today.
**Operational impact:** Storage cost grows with every soft-delete and never shrinks. Customers cannot be told "data is purged after the contracted retention period" with a straight face until this lands. Compliance posture is also weaker than the architecture claims.
**Owning roadmap step:** None today. Recommend adding to roadmap (this pass does not unilaterally add it because retention purge is enough work — schedule, idempotency, lock semantics, audit emission to `deletion_logs`, end-to-end test — that it deserves its own line and operator buy-in before scheduling). For now, flagged here as a known gap requiring a near-term roadmap decision.
**Doc-truthing this pass:** Architecture §3.2.4 and §4.4 receive 📋 markers; the prose stays unchanged because the design is correct, the implementation is missing.


### D-embed-key-issuance-workflow-missing-2026-05-09

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-09 by closing commit `c8b2142` (Step 30b commit (d) of step-30b-embed-key-issuance: canonical-doc updates + DRIFTS close). §3 body **restored verbatim** from `c8b2142^` by Pass 9 doc-truthing on 2026-05-13 per the §6 "do not delete from §3" doctrine that landed in commit `0d9a0c4` on 2026-05-09 — the original closure deleted the §3 body in violation of §6 (the doctrine was 3 hours old; honest mistake). §5 strikethrough closure landed at `c8b2142` and is preserved unchanged.
**Raised by:** Step 30b commit (e) end-of-build review.
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30b row: "A company adds a few lines of code to their site, and within an hour their visitors are having real conversations with the company's Luciel." The within-an-hour clause requires an operator-runnable issuance path that produces an embed key with `key_kind='embed'`, `permissions=['chat']`, a non-empty `allowed_origins`, a `rate_limit_per_minute`, and a populated `widget_config`.
**Repo state at the time of raise:** `app/services/api_key_service.py:create_key` mints rows on the `api_keys` table but does not validate the embed-key invariants (the four columns added in commit (b) are accepted positionally as kwargs and pass through unchecked). No admin endpoint, no CLI, no runbook produces a key in the embed shape today; an operator would have to write the row by hand and read the raw key out of the create_key return value, which is not a workflow we can hand to ourselves let alone a customer.
**Operational impact at the time of raise:** The widget bundle and the gate are both green, but no one can issue the credential they validate. First paying customer cannot self-serve, and the operator's manual path is fragile (hand-rolled SQL, no audit row, no SSM write).
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30b. Closed when the issuance path landed and an operator could mint an embed key in under five minutes against any tenant. Resolution shape (as shipped at `c8b2142`): admin endpoint extension + operator CLI in the embed-shape validation, wrapping `create_key` and writing the four widget columns.
**Pattern E:** New rows only; no mutation of existing keys. Audit emission via the same `AdminAuditRepository.record` path the rest of `api_key_service` uses.
**Pass 9 doctrine note:** This is one of three 2026-05-09 post-doctrine §3 deletions Pass 6 did not catch (its audit predicate walked only recent closures). Pass 9 restores all three in this same commit and raises `D-pass-6-mirror-restoration-incomplete-three-deletions-missed-2026-05-13` to record why the mirror discipline grep needs to walk *every* §5 strikethrough — not just recent ones.

### D-prod-widget-bundle-cdn-unprovisioned-2026-05-09

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-10 by closing commit `ee14e67` (Step 30b chase-up: close D-prod-widget-bundle-cdn-unprovisioned drift, hold Step 30b row at 🔧). §3 body **restored verbatim** from `ee14e67^` by Pass 9 doc-truthing on 2026-05-13 per the §6 "do not delete from §3" doctrine — the original closure deleted the §3 body in violation of §6. §5 strikethrough closure landed at `ee14e67` and is preserved unchanged.
**Raised by:** Step 30b commit (e) end-of-build review.
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30b row: customers add "a few lines of code to their site" and the widget loads. That requires the bundle to be reachable from any customer origin under a stable, cacheable URL.
**Progress on `step-30b-widget-cdn-deploy` at the time of raise (merged 2026-05-10 as `85990c4`):** All four resolution-path items shipped:
  1. Private S3 bucket `luciel-widget-cdn-prod-ca-central-1` with CloudFront OAC, distribution `EU5R6YVX26RPY` at `d1t84i96t71fsi.cloudfront.net`, and GitHub OIDC deploy role `arn:aws:iam::729005488042:role/luciel-widget-cdn-deploy` are provisioned via `cfn/luciel-widget-cdn.yaml` (commit `ae87491`). Stack is in `CREATE_COMPLETE` in account 729005488042 / region ca-central-1.
  2. `scripts/deploy_widget_cdn.sh` (commit `903d39e`, mode 755) uploads the bundle as both a hashed filename (`luciel-chat-widget.<hash>.js`, immutable Cache-Control) and a stable alias (`widget.js`, short Cache-Control), then issues a CloudFront invalidation on `widget.js` only. Idempotent: identical content → identical hash → object-level no-op, but a fresh invalidation still fires.
  3. `.github/workflows/ci.yml` adds a `widget-cdn-deploy` job (commit `0cc2ecb`) gated on `push + refs/heads/main`, gated on the existing `widget-build-and-size` job, and using GitHub OIDC (`id-token: write`, `role-duration-seconds: 900`) to assume the deploy role. The job downloads the artifact the size gate just validated, runs the deploy script, and HEAD-checks the resulting URL with 6 retries × 15s.
  4. The first CI run (`25628334070`, on merge `85990c4`) executed phases 1–4 of the deploy script cleanly: pre-flight passed, content hash `36a25740a60c` computed, all four S3 objects uploaded, invalidation `I39PVZ9FUUP7U3XP6M2I6L9TNE` created. End-to-end reachability is now confirmed independently from outside our network: `curl -I https://d1t84i96t71fsi.cloudfront.net/widget.js` returns `HTTP/2 200`, `content-type: application/javascript; charset=utf-8`, `content-length: 27300` (matches the source bundle exactly), `cache-control: public, max-age=300, must-revalidate`. The hashed alias at `https://d1t84i96t71fsi.cloudfront.net/luciel-chat-widget.36a25740a60c.js` returns the same body with `cache-control: public, max-age=31536000, immutable`.
**Why this drift stayed open until ee14e67:** The first CI run failed at phase 5 (`aws cloudfront wait invalidation-completed`) with `AccessDenied: cloudfront:GetInvalidation`. The CFN deploy role's inline policy granted `CreateInvalidation` and `GetDistribution` but not `GetInvalidation`, so the wait step could not poll. The deploy itself succeeded (the invalidation that the wait step was polling completed normally a few seconds later); only the deploy-job exit code went red. Closing this drift required the next CI run to go green end-to-end after `step-30b-cleanup` landed the IAM fix (`cloudfront:GetInvalidation` added to the role, see commit `ef7cbf7` on that branch) and the operator ran `aws cloudformation deploy --stack-name luciel-widget-cdn ...` to apply the in-place IAM update. After the next merge-to-main triggered a green CI run — both jobs passing — the closing tag `step-30b-widget-cdn-complete` landed on that merge commit and this drift moved to Section 5.
**Pattern E:** No row mutations. CDN artifacts are forward-only; old hashed paths stay reachable for any customer that pinned a specific version. The IAM role identity stays the same across the policy update; only its action list grows by one read-only verb.
**Pass 9 doctrine note:** This is one of three 2026-05-09 post-doctrine §3 deletions Pass 6 did not catch.

### D-confirmation-gate-not-enforced-2026-05-09

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-11 by closing commit `b9d0520` (Step 30c: action-classification gate enforced at the tool broker). §3 body **restored verbatim** from `b9d0520^` by Pass 9 doc-truthing on 2026-05-13 per the §6 "do not delete from §3" doctrine — the original closure deleted the §3 body in violation of §6. §5 strikethrough closure landed at `b9d0520` and is preserved unchanged.
**Raised by:** Architecture §3.3 step 8 ("Policy gate"), §4.9 (synchronous-only invocation rejected); Canonical Recap §4 (behavior contracts: "Luciel does not take consequential action without permission")
**Design claim (revised in the pass that raised this drift):** Tool invocations are classified into three tiers: **routine** (just do it, audited), **notify-and-proceed** (execute and surface visibly to the customer), and **approval-required** (return a confirmation request before executing). Approval is required only when an action is genuinely consequential — irreversible, high-blast-radius, off-pattern relative to the customer's established usage, or where Luciel itself is uncertain. Routine and reversible external-facing actions are not gated, because gating them would make Luciel feel timid and bureaucratic and would violate the senior-advisor voice in Recap §3.
**Repo state at the time of raise:** `app/policy/` did not contain an action-classification module. None of the three tiers existed. No `consequential_action` predicate, no off-pattern detector, no confidence-threshold check, no confirmation-pending state on sessions or messages, no model-side instruction in `LUCIEL_SYSTEM_PROMPT` describing the tiered contract. The escalate tool was the closest existing mechanism but it was voluntary and unstructured.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30c (Action classification — tiered approval discipline). Positioned between Step 30b (embeddable chat widget) and Step 31 (dashboards + validation gate) so the tiered contract holds before the first paying customer arrives. The off-pattern tier leans on the memory layers being correct, so it has a soft dependency on the four-kinds memory architecture being usable.
**Doc-truthing in the pass that raised this drift:** Architecture §3.3 step 8 rewrote from a binary gate to tier-aware classification. Architecture §4.9 softened the synchronous-only rejection to acknowledge the tier split. Recap §4 received a one-sentence clarification of what "consequential" means (irreversible, high-blast-radius, or off-pattern — not merely external-facing). Recap §12 got the new Step 30c line.
**Resolution as shipped at b9d0520 and observed clean post-deploy:** Fail-closed three-tier gate (ROUTINE / NOTIFY_AND_PROCEED / APPROVAL_REQUIRED) shipped as a pluggable provider; `LucielTool.declared_tier` is mandatory and the base default is `None` so a forgotten tier inherits APPROVAL_REQUIRED rather than silently executing. Closing tag `step-30c-action-classification-complete` on doc-truthing commit `99c6eb5` (re-cut forward from code-complete `b216300` per the "code + docs agree here" pattern). Production enforcement first observed clean 2026-05-11 via ECS rolling deploy (`luciel-backend:39` + `luciel-worker:19`, ECR digest `sha256:f0bf303272fb0801eefc4cf0d20d2ddb624f2a5f60c8e845cbe422869739f863` from `main` HEAD `84339a3`, zero ERROR/Traceback/CRITICAL post-deploy, deploymentCircuitBreaker did not fire).
**Pass 9 doctrine note:** This is one of three 2026-05-09 post-doctrine §3 deletions Pass 6 did not catch — and the most consequential of the three because the original Status cell in `CANONICAL_RECAP §12` Step 30c row already named the §5 closure of this drift (so the cross-ref worked); the breach is purely that the §3 design-claim/repo-state context disappeared on closure. Pass 9 restores it.

### D-route-shipped-without-end-to-end-coverage-2026-05-10

**Status:** OPEN (broader-routes slice only) — widget-surface slice CLOSED on 2026-05-11 by Step 30d Deliverable C (PR #16 merged `146f133`); harness at `.github/workflows/widget-e2e.yml` + `ci/e2e/run_widget_e2e.sh` + `ci/e2e/assert_widget_stream.py` + `scripts/bootstrap_platform_admin_ci.py` behind `workflow_dispatch` in v1, with AST contract test `tests/api/test_widget_e2e_harness_shape.py` pinning the cross-file invariants in the existing backend-free CI lane; planned follow-up adds `pull_request` trigger alongside `workflow_dispatch` per Pattern E (never delete). The broader "any route can ship without an E2E gate" process gap stays OPEN beyond Step 30d and still needs a roadmap home
**Raised by:** Step 30b Phase 4 staging E2E. The widget endpoint (`POST /api/v1/chat/widget`) shipped to `main` with three latent first-request bugs, each of which would have been caught by a single end-to-end POST against a deployed instance:
  1. `D-bug-scope-policy-kwarg` — `create_embed_key` called `enforce_agent_scope(agent_id=...)` but the policy method's parameter name is `scope_id`. Mint route 500. Fixed in PR #4 / commit `1aba06a`.
  2. `D-bug-slowapi-limit-provider-signature` — `embed_per_minute_limit_string(request: Request)` did not match either of slowapi's two call shapes (zero-arg or one-arg-keyed). Every widget POST returned a 500 with no CORS headers, surfaced in the browser as a misleading `No 'Access-Control-Allow-Origin' header` error. Fixed in PR #5 / commit `a64cdba` by replacing the broken callable with a static `EMBED_WIDGET_RATE_LIMIT = "30/minute"`.
  3. `D-bug-sessionmodel-attr-name` — widget route read `session.session_id` after `session_service.create_session(...)`. `SessionModel`'s primary key column is `id`, not `session_id`. AttributeError on first widget turn. Fixed in PR #6 / commit `d4720ae`.
**Design claim:** Step 30b's success criterion (CANONICAL_RECAP.md §12) is "customers can drop a script tag and Luciel answers from the customer's content." That criterion was meant to be enforced by CI gating the merge.
**Repo state:** `.github/workflows/ci.yml` runs unit tests, AST checks, widget bundle size gate, and widget CDN deploy. It does **not** spin up the backend image and make a real HTTP POST against `POST /api/v1/chat/widget` with a freshly minted embed key. The widget surface was therefore covered only by Python imports and per-function unit tests, neither of which exercises the slowapi callback, the auth middleware chain, the ScopePolicy kwarg surface, the JSON request parser, or the SessionModel attribute the route reads. Three bugs landed on `main` and reached the staging deploy before any of them fired.
**Owning roadmap step:** Partially owned by **Step 30d (Widget content safety and scope guardrails)** — the CANONICAL_RECAP §12 row for Step 30d explicitly commits to "an automated test [that] proves both behaviors on every change to the widget surface," which is the containerized end-to-end gate this drift requires for the widget slice: on every PR touching `app/api/v1/chat_widget.py`, `app/api/v1/admin.py` (embed-keys handler), `app/api/widget_deps.py`, or `app/middleware/auth.py`, (a) brings up backend + Postgres + Redis, (b) seeds a tenant + domain + embed key, (c) POSTs a widget message, (d) asserts HTTP 200, `text/event-stream` content-type, and a non-empty first SSE frame, plus (e) asserts the scope-refusal and content-safety behaviors land. The non-widget slice of this drift — the general "any route can ship without an E2E gate" process gap — remains OPEN beyond Step 30d and needs a future roadmap home. This drift **partially closes** with Step 30d (widget-surface PRs gated end-to-end); it fully closes only when the gate is extended to all customer-reachable routes.
**Doc-truthing this pass:** No CANONICAL_RECAP or ARCHITECTURE prose change. The Step 30b row in §12 stays 🔧 until the CI gate is in place and the staging widget passes end-to-end (technical green + safety green per the drift below). This drift's widget-surface slice closes when Step 30d closes; the broader-routes slice stays open beyond Step 30d.
**Closeout update 2026-05-11:** Widget-surface slice closed on Step 30d landing as recorded in the Status line above; this entry stays in §3 because the broader-routes slice remains OPEN. Owning roadmap step for the residual slice is still pending. The Step 30b row stays 🔧 against its own success criterion (REMAX-customer visitors exchanging real conversations); the closure here does not flip that row.

### D-widget-no-content-safety-or-scope-guardrail-2026-05-10

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-12 by Step 30d closing PRs #14/#15/#16 (closing PR sequence `3cbd489` → `c7d958e` → `146f133`, closeout commit `f8ac1d4`); §5 mirror lives in the closed-drifts section. Entry **restored to §3 in pass 6 (2026-05-13)** because pass-1 closure in `f8ac1d4` deleted this §3 body in violation of §6 doctrine ("Do not delete the entry from Section 3 — move it"). The audit chain requires the original §3 body to remain readable after closure; this restoration is verbatim from the parent of `f8ac1d4`.
**Raised by:** Step 30b Phase 4 staging E2E. With domain_config 374 (`tenant=luciel-staging-widget-test`, `domain=cloudfront-staging`, `system_prompt_additions=NULL`) bound to embed key 698, the live widget at `https://d1t84i96t71fsi.cloudfront.net/staging-widget-test.html` accepted and answered an off-topic request ("how are you doing") and engaged substantively with a sensitive-content request ("I need help making a sex toy"). The widget is generally helpful; it is not customer-deployable.
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §4 commits Luciel to a behavior contract — staying in scope of what the customer site is for, declining requests outside that scope politely, and refusing sensitive-content engagement that would damage the customer's reputation. ARCHITECTURE §3.3 step 8 (action classification) covers tool-call gating but says nothing about message-content gating. Neither doc currently commits to a content-safety layer or a per-domain on-topic guardrail.
**Repo state:** No content-safety check exists in the request path. `app/policy/` has no moderation module. The chat service threads `domain_config.system_prompt_additions` into the system prompt — that column is the only existing knob — but the staging row was created with `NULL` and the issuance path does not require it to be non-null before a widget goes live. No provider-side moderation API call (OpenAI moderation, Anthropic content filters) is wired into the chat pipeline. The only existing constraint that touches content is `EMBED_REQUIRED_PERMISSIONS = frozenset(['chat'])`, which gates surfaces (no tool calls from widget) but not the content of conversational turns.
**Two distinct gaps inside this drift:**
  - **Gap A — on-topic scoping.** Per-domain prompt that constrains the widget to the customer's vertical. Mitigation today is operational (write `system_prompt_additions` correctly before going live). Real fix is a (1) preflight validator that refuses to mint an embed key against a domain with NULL or empty `system_prompt_additions`, (2) a template library of vetted scope prompts (real estate, support, sales) operators can pick from, and (3) a CI test that asserts an out-of-scope question receives a decline-with-redirect.
  - **Gap B — content safety.** Sensitive/adult/illegal-content refusal, independent of vertical. Cannot be done with prompt alone — needs a moderation gate (provider API or in-process classifier) before the LLM call, and a sanitized refusal response that does not leak the offending text into traces.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30d (Widget content safety and scope guardrails) — adopted into CANONICAL_RECAP §12 on 2026-05-10 (commit `d2b05c46`), sitting between Step 30c (action classification — tool gating) and Step 31 (dashboards + validation gate). Step 30c gates *what Luciel does*; Step 30d gates *what Luciel says and what it engages with*. They are sibling problems, not parent/child, and folding 30d into 30c would dilute both. Step 30d's success criterion: with a real REMAX-style domain config, the widget (1) declines an off-topic question with a graceful redirect to the customer's vertical and (2) refuses sensitive-content engagement with a fixed, sanitized response that never reaches the LLM provider's traces in raw form. This drift closes when Step 30d closes.
**Immediate mitigation (Step 30b tail, not Step 30d):** Populate `domain_configs.id=374` with a real-estate scoping and refusal prompt via `PATCH /api/v1/admin/domains/luciel-staging-widget-test/cloudfront-staging` so the staging widget refuses both the off-topic test and the sex-toy test. This raises the floor for the REMAX demo without closing the drift. The drift stays OPEN until Step 30d's preflight validator, provider-side moderation gate, and CI tests land.
**Doc-truthing this pass:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 carries the Step 30d row (committed `d2b05c46`) that explicitly names this drift as one of its two closing conditions. No ARCHITECTURE prose change yet — Step 30d's design-shape edits (moderation gate in §3.3 and issuance-time preflight in §3.2.2) land surgically when the build lands, per DRIFTS §6 doctrine that a new roadmap step on its own is not a reason to grow the design docs.

### D-widget-chat-no-application-level-audit-log-2026-05-10

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-12 by Step 31 sub-branch 1 (PR #30, closeout commit `fa876ce`); §5 mirror lives in the closed-drifts section. Entry **restored to §3 in pass 6 (2026-05-13)** because pass-1 closure in `fa876ce` deleted this §3 body in violation of §6 doctrine ("Do not delete the entry from Section 3 — move it"). The audit chain requires the original §3 body to remain readable after closure; this restoration is verbatim from the parent of `fa876ce`.
**Raised by:** Step 30b Phase 5 staging audit-log spot check. Four `POST /api/v1/chat/widget` calls were sent through the live widget at 02:09:42, 02:09:53, 02:10:44, 02:11:08 UTC on 2026-05-11. CloudWatch log group `/ecs/luciel-backend` carries only uvicorn access lines (HTTP method, path, source IP, status code) for those four turns. A targeted CloudWatch `filter-log-events` against the same time window with pattern `?tenant_id ?domain_id ?embed_key ?session_id ?widget_chat ?chat_completion` returned **zero** events. The widget chat request path emits no application-level structured log lines — no per-turn record carrying `tenant_id`, `domain_id`, `embed_key_prefix`, `session_id`, message length, latency, or model used.
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §13 (end-to-end product acceptance) implies per-tenant observability for any customer-facing surface — "we can answer is Luciel earning its keep here in under a minute." ARCHITECTURE §3.2.7 (Audit trail) states that every consequential action produces an immutable audit record across three channels, one of which is the application log stream where the application emits audit events in human-readable form. The widget chat path emits none of these for a chat turn — only uvicorn access lines.
**Repo state:** `app/api/v1/chat_widget.py` does not emit explicit `logger.info(...)` records at request entry, after dependency resolution, or after the LLM response is streamed. The chat service does not appear to emit per-turn audit records either (no `audit_logs` table write, no structured log line). The only application-level evidence today that a widget conversation happened is the `messages` and `sessions` row writes — which are state, not observability — plus uvicorn's HTTP access line, which carries only path and status.
**Operational impact today:** For the REMAX preview, we have HTTP-level monitoring only. We cannot: (a) attribute a tenant-specific widget 500 to a specific tenant from logs alone (we would have to correlate source IP against CloudFront access logs and then DB rows); (b) build a usage-by-tenant chart for Step 31 from log data; (c) prove from logs that a sensitive-content refusal happened versus a generic 200 with empty SSE; (d) target a retention-purge sweep on widget audit records (none exist). For a single controlled demo customer this is tolerable. For a paying-customer cohort it is not.
**Owning roadmap step:** **Step 31 (dashboards + validation gate).** Step 31 already commits to a five-part pre-launch validation gate including operations and compliance categories — both of those require the structured logs this drift identifies as missing. Folding this into Step 31 rather than spawning a Step 30e because (1) the fix shape — structured loggers, audit-log table write, dashboard ingest — is the same fix that Step 31 needs anyway, (2) splitting it would force Step 31 to inherit a half-built audit pipeline, (3) the widget surface can ship to a single demo customer (REMAX) without it as long as we are honest with REMAX that detailed per-conversation metrics arrive in the next milestone. This drift closes when Step 31's validation gate exercises a widget turn and verifies the structured record landed with the documented field set.
**Doc-truthing this pass:** Step 30b row in CANONICAL_RECAP §12 updated to record stage-1 (Luciel-owned staging E2E) observed clean on 2026-05-10, with the three bugs found-and-fixed and the three open drifts (this one, route-coverage, content-safety) called out by id. Marker stays 🔧 — the row's literal success criterion is REMAX-customer visitors exchanging real conversations, which has not happened yet. ARCHITECTURE §3.2.7 receives a 📋 marker on the "Application log stream" bullet pointing to Step 31; the prose stays unchanged because the design is correct, the implementation for the widget surface is incomplete.

### D-celery-worker-runs-as-root-2026-05-11

**Status:** OPEN — pre-existing security hygiene gap surfaced (not introduced) during the Step 30c prod deploy of 2026-05-11.
**Raised by:** Post-deploy log review of the new `luciel-worker:19` task on `luciel-worker-service` after rolling out the action-classification gate. The `/ecs/luciel-worker` log group shows Celery emitting its standard `SecurityWarning: You're running the worker with superuser privileges: this is absolutely not recommended! Please specify a different user using the --uid option. User information: uid=0 euid=0 gid=0 egid=0` at process startup. This warning has been firing on every worker boot since at least rev 14 — it is not new to rev 19. Step 30c happens to be the first time we noticed and recorded it.
**Design claim:** ARCHITECTURE §6 (security) and the broader principle of least privilege in CANONICAL_RECAP §3 (senior-advisor voice extends to operational discipline) both imply the worker should not run as root. Containers should run as a least-privileged non-root user wherever the workload does not require root.
**Repo state:** `Dockerfile` does not contain a `USER` directive after the install steps; the image therefore runs as `root` (uid=0). The task definitions `td-backend-rev39.json` and `td-worker-rev19.json` do not override this via a `user` field in the container definition. The worker's actual workload (Celery against SQS, `/tmp/celery_alive` mtime heartbeat for the ECS health check) requires no root privilege.
**Operational impact today:** Low. The worker container is sandboxed by Fargate, talks only to SQS, RDS, and Redis via IAM-bound endpoints, and has no inbound network surface. A root-inside-the-container compromise still has to escape Fargate to do anything meaningful. But the warning is a hygiene-and-audit finding: it is the first thing a security reviewer screenshots, and we want a clean log on a customer-facing security questionnaire.
**Resolution path:** Add a non-root user to the `Dockerfile` (e.g. `RUN groupadd -r luciel && useradd -r -g luciel luciel` then `USER luciel` before the `CMD`), confirm `/tmp/celery_alive` is writable by that user (it is, since `/tmp` is world-writable in the base image), rebuild + redeploy both `luciel-backend` and `luciel-worker` through the same digest-pinned task-def revision pattern used for Step 30c. Owning roadmap step: not currently assigned — candidates are folding it into Step 31's compliance pillar or opening a small `Step 30e` hardening step. Decision deferred to a future planning pass.
**Cross-refs:** Surfaced in DRIFTS §5 `~~D-confirmation-gate-not-enforced-2026-05-09~~` (the Prod observed-clean stanza records where this was first noticed). `docs/runbooks/step-30c-action-classification-deploy.md` is the runbook whose post-deploy log review exposed it.

### D-step-24-5c-impl-backlog-2026-05-11

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-12 by Step 24.5c sub-branch 5 (PR #28, closeout commit `55e4db9`); §5 mirror lives in the closed-drifts section. Entry **restored to §3 in pass 6 (2026-05-13)** because pass-1 closure in `55e4db9` deleted this §3 body in violation of §6 doctrine ("Do not delete the entry from Section 3 — move it"). The audit chain requires the original §3 body to remain readable after closure; this restoration is verbatim from the parent of `55e4db9`.
**Raised by:** Step 24.5c design-lock pass on 2026-05-11. The design is committed (ARCHITECTURE §3.2.11 — new subsection landing this commit; §3.3 step 5 marker; §4.9 rejected-alternative bullets). The implementation does not exist on `main` at the time this drift is opened (grep against the working tree returns zero hits for `conversation_id`, `identity_claims`, `CrossSessionRetriever`).
**Design claim:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.11 (Identity & conversation continuity) commits three primitives: (a) a `conversations` table (`id` UUID PK, `tenant_id`, `domain_id`, `created_at`, `last_activity_at`, `active`); (b) a nullable `conversation_id` FK on `sessions` pointing at `conversations.id` (session-linking, never session-merging — §4.9 rejected alternative); (c) an `identity_claims` table (`id`, `user_id` FK to `users.id`, `claim_type` ∈ {`email`, `phone`, `sso_subject`}, `claim_value` case-folded for email / E.164-normalised for phone, `issuing_scope_id`, `issuing_adapter`, `verified_at` nullable, `active`, `created_at`) with uniqueness on (`claim_type`, normalised `claim_value`, `issuing_scope_id`). Runtime surface: a `CrossSessionRetriever` in `app/memory/` (sibling to the per-session retriever) that, given the active session's `(conversation_id, tenant_id, domain_id)`, returns the N most recent messages from sibling sessions under the same `conversation_id`, scope-filtered inside the retriever, capped by a per-call budget, returning ranked passages with provenance metadata (`source_session_id`, `source_channel`, `timestamp`). Request resolution: at §3.3 step 4 (scope policy check), after the requesting key resolves to its `(tenant, domain, agent)` scope, the runtime asks the identity resolver whether a `User` exists in this scope whose `identity_claims` include the channel-specific identifier the ingress adapter just asserted; if yes the session is bound to that `User` and a `conversation_id` is resolved by walking the `User`'s other recent active sessions under the same scope (most recent active conversation wins, configurable per scope); if no, a synthetic `User` and a new `conversation_id` are minted in the same transaction. v1 trust model is **adapter-asserted**: the phone gateway swears the call came from a particular E.164 number, the widget swears the embed-key request came from a particular logged-in `User`, the programmatic API caller swears the message belongs to a particular email known out-of-band. End-user-driven verification (email-confirm link, SMS one-time code, SSO subject match) is **deferred to Step 34a + Step 31** by design.
**Repo state:** None of the three primitives exists. `app/models/session.py` has no `conversation_id` column; there is no `app/models/conversation.py`, no `app/models/identity_claim.py`, no migration in `alembic/versions/` that creates either table; `app/memory/` exists (sibling layout is correct) but has no `CrossSessionRetriever`. The identity-resolver hook at §3.3 step 4 is also absent — `ScopePolicy` resolves the request to a scope today but does not bind the resolved session to a `User` via channel-asserted claims. The 24.5b primitives that this step builds on (`users` table, `scope_assignments`) are in place and unchanged by this drift.
**v1 success criterion** (what closes this drift, copied from CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 24.5c row): two distinct channels (the embeddable chat widget and the programmatic API) exchange messages on two sessions joined by **one** `conversation_id` and **one** `identity_claims` row, with the `CrossSessionRetriever` surfacing the sibling session's recent turns inside the foundation-model context of the second turn. The voice/SMS/email legs of the Recap §13.1 T8 demonstration (widget Monday → phone Wednesday) inherit the same primitives but require Step 34a's channel adapter framework to be reachable end-to-end and stay scoped there per the T8 footnote in §13.1 and per `D-channels-only-chat-implemented-2026-05-09`.
**Deliberate non-goals at v1** (carried forward, **not regressions** — recorded here so a future review does not mistake them for missing work that should have been in 24.5c):
  - End-user-driven claim verification (email-confirm link, SMS one-time code, SSO assertion). v1 records claims as asserted with `verified_at=NULL` and the cross-session retriever treats asserted-but-unverified claims as sufficient *within the issuing scope*. Verification primitives land with Step 34a (the adapters that consume them) and Step 31 (the onboarding/dashboard surface that prompts for them).
  - Cross-tenant identity federation (a `User` recognised across Brokerage A and Brokerage B as the same person). Rejected for v1 in ARCHITECTURE §4.9. Step 38 (bottom-up expansion) carries the explicit operator-approved re-parenting transaction; until then, every `identity_claim` is scoped to its `issuing_scope_id` and the same number/email under two scopes are two independent facts.
  - A per-`User` inbox view spanning all channels. Step 31 dashboards territory.
  - The voice / SMS / email channel adapters themselves. Step 34a. The §3.2.11 primitives are framework-ready for them; the adapters are not part of this step.
**Closing tag** (planned, when impl lands): `step-24-5c-cross-channel-identity-complete`, cut on the doc-truthing commit of the implementation arc — same shape as Step 30c's `99c6eb5` tag-on-doc-truthing pattern, so that the tag reads "code + docs agree here."
**Implementation arc** (sketch, not a contract — final shape decided when the work starts): (1) Alembic migration adds `conversations` table + nullable `sessions.conversation_id` FK + `identity_claims` table with the documented unique index; (2) `app/models/conversation.py` and `app/models/identity_claim.py` mirror the §4.1 scope-bearing model shape (FKs to scope, audit timestamps); (3) `app/memory/cross_session_retriever.py` lands as a sibling of the per-session retriever with the documented signature; (4) identity resolver hook in `app/runtime/` (or `app/services/`, decided at impl time) binds the session to a `User` at §3.3 step 4 and resolves `conversation_id`; (5) widget + programmatic adapters assert their respective claim types into the resolver; (6) the v1 success-criterion end-to-end test lives alongside the widget E2E harness landed in `D-route-shipped-without-end-to-end-coverage-2026-05-10` (now closed for the widget surface); (7) doc-truthing commit re-cuts the closing tag forward onto the all-three-docs-agree state per the §6 doctrine. This list is illustrative — it is not the spec; the spec lives in ARCHITECTURE §3.2.11 and CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 24.5c.
**Doc-truthing this pass:** All three canonical docs change in one commit (triangular cross-reference pattern, same shape as Step 30c's `99c6eb5` doc-truthing commit). CANONICAL_RECAP §11 Q8 answer expanded to name the three primitives and the adapter-asserted v1 trust model (status row's marker stays `📋` but the answer cell is no longer thin); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 24.5c row flips `📋 Candidate` → `📋 Planned` with the full closeout-style stanza naming primitives + non-goals + planned closing tag + this drift id; ARCHITECTURE adds new §3.2.11 (Identity & conversation continuity) between §3.2.10 (Monitoring) and §3.3 (request flow), updates §3.3 step 5 to name the cross-session retriever as a sibling of the per-session retriever, and adds two §4.9 rejected-alternative bullets (session-merging across channels; cross-tenant identity federation in v1). No code change. The §6 doctrine is honoured because this **is** an architectural-shape change (three new primitives, a new runtime retriever, a new identity resolution hook in the request flow) — not a roadmap detail that belongs in commit messages.
**Cross-refs:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.11 (new subsection, primary spec), ARCHITECTURE §3.3 step 5 (cross-session retriever sibling marker), ARCHITECTURE §4.9 (two new rejected alternatives), CANONICAL_RECAP §11 Q8 (strategic answer expanded), CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 24.5c row (the row this drift backs), DRIFTS §3 `D-channels-only-chat-implemented-2026-05-09` (Step 34a-owned drift that gates voice/SMS/email being reachable end-to-end; the 24.5c primitives are designed to be framework-ready for those adapters when they land), DRIFTS §3 `D-context-assembler-thin-2026-05-09` (cross-session retriever output joins per-session memory at context-assembly time; assembler consolidation work in that drift is adjacent territory but does not block 24.5c impl).

### D-step-31-impl-backlog-2026-05-11

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-12 by Step 31 sub-branch 5 (PR #34, closeout commit `fa876ce`); §5 mirror lives in the closed-drifts section. Entry **restored to §3 in pass 6 (2026-05-13)** because pass-1 closure in `fa876ce` deleted this §3 body in violation of §6 doctrine ("Do not delete the entry from Section 3 — move it"). The audit chain requires the original §3 body to remain readable after closure; this restoration is verbatim from the parent of `fa876ce`.
**Raised by:** Roadmap planning on 2026-05-11. Step 31 is the gate the first paying customer (REMAX Crossroads) drives through; it is also the named closing step for three existing drifts (`D-widget-chat-no-application-level-audit-log-2026-05-10`, the broader-routes slice of `D-route-shipped-without-end-to-end-coverage-2026-05-10`, and the Step 24.5c carried-forward route-wiring/per-`User`-inbox non-goal).
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 row commits to (a) three scope-respecting dashboard views (tenant, domain, agent) that each answer "is Luciel earning its keep here?" in under a minute, and (b) a five-part pre-launch validation gate — **isolation, customer journey, memory quality, operations, compliance** — that must be all-green before a new customer goes live. ARCHITECTURE picks this up as a new §3.2.12 (Hierarchical dashboards & validation gate) landing in the design-lock commit on `step-31-design-lock`, citing §4.1 (scope hierarchy as the billing boundary) and §4.7 (three-layer scope enforcement) as the load-bearing primitives the dashboard service builds on.
**Repo state at design-lock:** Per-turn DB observability already exists — `app/models/trace.py` and `app/services/trace_service.py` write a `Trace` row keyed to `tenant_id` / `domain_id` / `agent_id` / `luciel_instance_id` after every chat turn (both the streaming and non-streaming paths in `app/services/chat_service.py`). What does NOT exist: (1) **application log stream emission** on the widget chat path — `app/api/v1/chat_widget.py` emits `logger.warning` only on moderation blocks and `logger.exception` on the catch-all error, no structured `logger.info` at request entry, after auth/scope resolution, or after a successful stream; (2) the **`SessionService.create_session_with_identity` route wiring** carried forward from Step 24.5c PR #27 (widget today calls the legacy `session_service.create_session(...)` with `user_id=None`, see `app/api/v1/chat_widget.py` line 181, so the §3.3 step 4 identity-resolver hook is built and proven end-to-end against real Postgres but the routes still take the legacy path); (3) any **dashboard query layer or HTTP surface** (`app/services/dashboard_service.py` and `app/api/v1/dashboard.py` do not exist); (4) the **five-part validation gate harness** (`tests/e2e/step_31_validation_gate.py` does not exist).
**Implementation arc (planned, in order — same five-sub-branch shape as Step 24.5c):**
  - **Sub-branch 1 — application-level audit log on the widget chat path + route wiring of `create_session_with_identity`.** Closes `D-widget-chat-no-application-level-audit-log-2026-05-10` end-to-end (the design-doc half flips ARCHITECTURE §3.2.7's `Application log stream` bullet 📋 → ✅ for the widget surface). Structured `logger.info` emission at three points in `app/api/v1/chat_widget.py`: (a) `widget_chat_turn_received` at request entry with `tenant_id`, `domain_id`, `embed_key_prefix`, `agent_id`, `luciel_instance_id`, message length; (b) `widget_chat_session_resolved` after lazy session creation with `session_id`, `user_id`, `conversation_id`, `is_new_user`, `is_new_conversation`; (c) `widget_chat_turn_completed` after the stream finishes with `session_id`, `latency_ms`, `model`, `provider`, `tokens_emitted`, `blocked_by_moderation`. The lazy-session path swaps from `session_service.create_session(...user_id=None...)` to `session_service.create_session_with_identity(...)` when the embed-key request carries a `client_claim` field (`email` or `phone` asserted by the customer's own site), falling back to the anonymous path when it does not. Schema gains a nullable `client_claim` on `ChatWidgetRequest` so this is a backward-compatible widget-bundle bump. Backend-free contract test `tests/api/test_step31_chat_audit_shape.py` pins (1) all three emission sites exist by AST search, (2) each carries the documented field set, (3) `create_session_with_identity` is reachable from the widget route when `client_claim` is present, and (4) no `logger.info` from this module ever carries a raw message body (defense against accidentally writing PII to the log stream).
  - **Sub-branch 2 — dashboard query layer.** `app/services/dashboard_service.py` with three methods (`get_tenant_dashboard`, `get_domain_dashboard`, `get_agent_dashboard`). Each method respects the three-layer scope enforcement from §4.7: the caller's resolved scope is the **upper bound** of what the method can read, not a hint. Aggregates surfaced: turn count, unique-user count, escalation count, moderation-block count, latency p50/p95, top-N most-active Luciel instances, top-N busiest domains/agents (only at the level above), seven-day trend lines. All aggregates query the existing `traces` table + the existing scope tables. No new DB writes. Backend-free contract tests pin scope-bound output (a tenant-scoped call cannot return rows for another tenant; a domain-scoped call cannot return rows for another domain under the same tenant; an agent-scoped call cannot return rows for another agent under the same domain).
  - **Sub-branch 3 — dashboard HTTP surface.** `GET /api/v1/dashboard/tenant`, `GET /api/v1/dashboard/domain/{domain_id}`, `GET /api/v1/dashboard/agent/{agent_id}` under `app/api/v1/dashboard.py`, each calling the service from sub-branch 2 and enforcing scope via the existing `ScopePolicy` chain. Response shape is a stable JSON envelope so a future frontend (Step 32) can render against it without breaking when fields are added. Contract test asserts: an embed key cannot reach any of the three endpoints (they require an admin or scope-admin key); a tenant-admin key calling the domain endpoint for a domain in a different tenant gets 403; a domain-admin key calling the tenant endpoint for its own tenant gets 403 (cannot escalate upward).
  - **Sub-branch 4 — five-part validation gate harness.** `tests/e2e/step_31_validation_gate.py` is the Postgres-required, runnable-script live e2e in the Step 30c / Step 24.5c precedent. Five claim groups, one per pillar of the gate: (i) **isolation** — two tenants seeded with overlapping shapes, every dashboard call from one cannot see the other's data; (ii) **customer journey** — widget turn through `create_session_with_identity` → audit row emitted → trace row written → dashboard reflects the turn; (iii) **memory quality** — memory extraction worker runs on the seeded turn, the resulting memory item is scope-bound and recoverable on the next session under the same `conversation_id`; (iv) **operations** — alarms exist for the three load-bearing signals (error rate, queue depth, DB saturation — placeholder assertions today against `cfn/luciel-prod-alarms.yaml`; the live verification is `[PROD-PHASE-2B]`); (v) **compliance** — `admin_audit_logs` hash chain is intact across the seeded run, `deletion_logs` shape exists, retention purge worker is on the roadmap (cross-ref `D-retention-purge-worker-missing-2026-05-09`). Backend-free harness-shape pin in `tests/api/test_step_31_validation_gate_shape.py`.
  - **Sub-branch 5 — live e2e + doc-truthing commit.** Closes the three drifts named at the top of this entry, flips the §12 row 📋 → ✅, flips ARCHITECTURE §3.2.7 widget-application-log marker 📋 → ✅, and cuts closing tag `step-31-dashboards-validation-gate-complete` on the doc-truthing commit per the Step 30c / Step 24.5c precedent (so the tag reads "code + docs agree here"). The broader-routes slice of `D-route-shipped-without-end-to-end-coverage-2026-05-10` closes here when the validation-gate harness in sub-branch 4 is extended in a Pattern E follow-up to the `pull_request` trigger on the same allowlist shape as the widget-e2e harness.
**Deliberate non-goals at v1, carried forward as not-regressions:** dashboard frontend UI (Step 32 — backend API + harness is enough for the §12 row's "under a minute" criterion); the off-pattern detector for action classification (soft-dep on `D-context-assembler-thin-2026-05-09`); WAF / Multi-AZ / autoscaling verification (those are `[PROD-PHASE-2B]` operator-side drifts, not Step 31); end-user-driven claim verification (Step 34a — adapter-asserted stays the v1 trust model); per-tenant tier overrides for the action-classification gate (out of scope at v1).
**Cross-refs:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.7 (widget-application-log bullet, flips ✅ at sub-branch 1); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.12 (new subsection landing at design-lock); ARCHITECTURE §4.1 (scope hierarchy as billing boundary — load-bearing for the dashboard service); ARCHITECTURE §4.7 (three-layer scope enforcement — load-bearing for the dashboard HTTP surface); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 31 row (flips ✅ at sub-branch 5); CANONICAL_RECAP §11 Q2 (the strategic answer this step is the practical demonstration of); `D-widget-chat-no-application-level-audit-log-2026-05-10` (closes with sub-branch 1); `D-route-shipped-without-end-to-end-coverage-2026-05-10` broader-routes slice (closes with sub-branch 5 + Pattern E follow-up); Step 24.5c PR #27 carried-forward route-wiring item (closes with sub-branch 1).

### D-secret-disclosure-recurrence-2026-05-12

**Status:** OPEN — 🔥 Hot. Pattern, not single event; no further ad-hoc rotation until Step 32 lands per the resolution path below.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) self-flagged during the 2026-05-12 rotation arc. Cross-ref incident `docs/incidents/2026-05-12-dsn-disclosed-in-chat.md`.
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §3 senior-advisor voice ("we cannot make any compromises in our security and programmatic errors") and ARCHITECTURE §3.2.8 (secrets discipline, Pattern E retention) jointly imply secrets do not traverse chat or unauthorized channels. The 2026-05-05 incident already established the lesson; the 2026-05-12 events demonstrate that the *procedure* designed to enforce the lesson itself produces disclosure pathways under load.
**Repo state:** Four disclosure events in seven days. 2026-05-05: admin DSN paste-back during P3-S Half 1 (`docs/incidents/2026-05-05-admin-dsn-disclosed-in-chat.md`). 2026-05-12 ~20:30 EDT: operator paste-back of full `aws ssm get-parameter-history` for both `/luciel/database-url` and `/luciel/production/worker_database_url`, both with `--with-decryption`, both with passwords in plaintext, as pre-flight survey before rotation. 2026-05-12 ~21:28 EDT: rotation script's `print(f"FAIL: {type(e).__name__}: {e}")` formatted the full psycopg `ProgrammingError` into chat, including the post-Phase-1 admin DSN (with password v2) that the script had just received from `os.environ['DATABASE_URL']` and failed to parse because of the SQLAlchemy `postgresql+psycopg://` scheme.
**Operational impact today:** Low likelihood of exploitation (RDS in private subnet, no bastion, no VPN to VPC), high impact on integrity of the audit story for any future security review. Per stated business principle, the integrity-of-audit dimension is load-bearing on its own even when the realistic exploitation likelihood is low.
**Resolution path:** No further rotation attempts on either currently-disclosed password until Step 32 ("Secret rotation runbook, AWS-side, audit-logged") lands. The two currently-acknowledged-exposure passwords stay active in production with this drift's status as the canonical record. Step 32 rotates both as part of its own acceptance criteria. The rotation is **not** an emergency tonight because the exploitation path is gated by VPC-internal network access; the rotation is critical *before* any external trust posture (customer onboarding, security questionnaire response, SOC2 audit). Owning roadmap step: Step 32 candidate (see `D-rotation-procedure-laptop-dependent-2026-05-12` for the scope of that step).
**Cross-refs:** `docs/incidents/2026-05-12-dsn-disclosed-in-chat.md`; `docs/incidents/2026-05-05-admin-dsn-disclosed-in-chat.md`; sibling drifts `D-rotation-procedure-laptop-dependent-2026-05-12`, `D-rotation-exception-handlers-leak-dsn-2026-05-12`, `D-ssm-readonly-access-broad-2026-05-12`; ARCHITECTURE §3.2.8 (secrets discipline, Pattern E retention — the design promise this drift records four breaches of).

### D-rotation-procedure-laptop-dependent-2026-05-12

**Status:** OPEN — 🔥 Hot. BLOCKING any external trust posture (customer onboarding, security questionnaire, SOC2 audit).
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) during the 2026-05-12 Phase 2 worker-rotation attempt. The Phase 1 admin rotation succeeded by good luck (AMSI did not yet have the pattern signature in cache); Phase 2 hit the same construct three different ways and was blocked at every turn.
**Design claim:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.8 (secrets, Pattern E) and the broader senior-advisor discipline in CANONICAL_RECAP §3 imply secret rotation is a routine operational discipline, not an ad-hoc ceremony. A routine discipline cannot depend on the operator's local laptop satisfying multiple unstated preconditions.
**Repo state:** The 2026-05-12 Phase 2 attempt accumulated multiple PowerShell pitfalls now logged into the cumulative-pitfalls list: (#12) AMSI/Defender blocks any PowerShell script that contains both `[System.Convert]::ToBase64String` and `aws ecs execute-command` in the same parsed unit, even when the payload is benign — the signature is on the construct combination, not on content; signature-based detection persists across `Unblock-File` and across saving to disk vs inline. (#13) The Windows → AWS-CLI → SSM-agent argv chain strips all quote characters from any argv element, because the SSM agent on the container side runs the `--command` value via `execvp` directly (no intermediate shell). Quoted Python `-c` payloads must therefore use **zero quote characters** — practically this means encoding the entire script as a comma-separated integer list wrapped in `exec(bytes([…]).decode())`. No general-purpose rotation script can rely on this transport. (#14) The relay-bucket approach (upload script to a private S3 bucket, container fetches via presigned URL) fails on the backend image because it has neither `aws` CLI nor `curl`. (#15) Stdin pipe via `aws ecs execute-command --interactive | tee /tmp/file` creates the destination file but does not deliver content; the SSM session's interactive stdin path does not pump bytes through to the agent for the operator-pipe pattern.
**Operational impact today:** Routine rotation is effectively impossible. The 2026-05-12 attempt produced disclosure event #2 of the evening (the exception-leak) specifically because it forced the rotation script through five different transport iterations under time pressure with multiple ad-hoc payload reshapes. A laptop-bound rotation procedure does not survive contact with production.
**Resolution path:** Open a new roadmap step (current candidate: **Step 32, "Secret rotation runbook — AWS-side, audit-logged"**) with the following acceptance criteria: (a) rotation logic baked into a versioned container image (not a shell script the operator pastes); (b) execution triggered by EventBridge schedule **or** a manual button (CLI / console click) that invokes the runtime, never by a paste-back ceremony; (c) new password generated inside the runtime container using `secrets.choice` against an explicit alphabet, written directly to SSM via the runtime's task-role permission, **never returned to the caller**; (d) CloudTrail-audited end-to-end with the rotated parameter version retained per Pattern E; (e) exception handlers MUST NOT format the connection string into any log line — see sibling `D-rotation-exception-handlers-leak-dsn-2026-05-12` for the explicit contract. The runbook's first execution rotates both currently-disclosed passwords (admin v2 → v3, worker v1 → v2), thereby closing `D-secret-disclosure-recurrence-2026-05-12`. Owning roadmap step: not yet assigned — proposed as Step 32. Decision deferred to operator + advisor planning pass.
**Cross-refs:** `docs/incidents/2026-05-12-dsn-disclosed-in-chat.md`; `D-secret-disclosure-recurrence-2026-05-12`; `D-rotation-exception-handlers-leak-dsn-2026-05-12`; `D-ssm-readonly-access-broad-2026-05-12`; ARCHITECTURE §3.2.8 (secrets discipline — the rotation runbook in Step 32 lands the operational discipline this subsection currently asserts only at the design layer).

### D-rotation-exception-handlers-leak-dsn-2026-05-12

**Status:** OPEN — ⚠️ Warm. Contract item; codifies into the Step 32 design but stands on its own as a code-discipline drift.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on direct observation of the failure mode that produced disclosure event #3 of the 2026-05-12 incident. The rotation script's `try / except Exception as e: print(f"FAIL: {type(e).__name__}: {e}")` produced `FAIL: ProgrammingError: missing "=" after "postgresql+psycopg://luciel_admin:<password-v2>@luciel-db.…/luciel" in connection info string` — the full DSN including the just-rotated admin password.
**Design claim:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.8 (secrets discipline) and the senior-advisor voice on integrity-of-audit imply that no log line, audit row, or operator-visible output ever contains a connection string with a password. The rotation code path is the path where this is most likely to happen and most damaging when it does.
**Repo state:** The Phase 2 rotation script (`_rot.py`, reconstructable from the incident timeline; not committed to the repo, gitignored at the operator's clone) used `print(f"FAIL: {type(e).__name__}: {e}")` against the psycopg `ProgrammingError`. psycopg, SQLAlchemy, and botocore all put the connection string in `__str__` for connection-related exceptions; this is library behavior, not script behavior. The script was written without a contract against that library behavior.
**Operational impact today:** Tonight, one disclosure event of the post-Phase-1 admin password. Going forward, every future rotation attempt is at risk for the same failure mode unless the contract is codified.
**Resolution path:** Step 32's rotation-runbook design contract pins the exception-handler shape to **never format the exception's `__str__`** — only `type(e).__name__` plus a hand-curated message. The contract reads (proposed wording for the Step 32 design doc): "In any rotation, migration, or DSN-touching code path, exception handlers must follow `print(f\"FAIL: {type(e).__name__}\")` (or equivalent logger call) and a hand-curated message that names the failed operation. Direct interpolation of the exception value, the exception args, or any object that holds the connection string is forbidden. Test discipline: every rotation script's contract test exercises a forced-failure path and asserts no `://` substring appears anywhere in the captured output." Owning roadmap step: Step 32 (proposed).
**Cross-refs:** `docs/incidents/2026-05-12-dsn-disclosed-in-chat.md`; `D-secret-disclosure-recurrence-2026-05-12`; `D-rotation-procedure-laptop-dependent-2026-05-12`; ARCHITECTURE §3.2.8 (secrets discipline — the no-DSN-in-logs invariant this drift codifies as a code-discipline contract).

### ~~D-cluster-name-luciel-cluster-not-luciel-prod-2026-05-12~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-13 by pass-6 doc-truthing audit (one runbook class-(a) violation fixed at `docs/runbooks/step-28-p3-h-rotate-and-purge.md:292`; §5 mirror at L1648). **Arc 0 hygiene 2026-05-20:** the body-internal Closeout update at L779 already records the close, but the §3 heading and Status line were never updated to match the §5 mirror — strikethrough + Status realignment applied this pass. **Original Status (pre-closure):** OPEN — 🔧 Partial. Pure doc drift; no infra change.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) during the 2026-05-12 Phase 1 admin-rotation pre-flight. The `aws ecs describe-services --cluster luciel-prod ...` form returned `ClusterNotFoundException`; `aws ecs list-clusters` revealed the actual cluster name is `luciel-cluster`. The recap-summary state at the start of the session had referenced `luciel-prod` as the cluster name. The Phase 1 work pivoted to `luciel-cluster` without further incident.
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP and ARCHITECTURE reference the production ECS cluster by name in multiple operational stanzas. The name used in docs must match the name registered in AWS, or every runbook command fails on the first execution.
**Repo state:** Need to grep `docs/` for `luciel-prod` (the cluster reference, not the SSM parameter prefix `/luciel/production/…` which is a different name and is correct) and replace with `luciel-cluster` everywhere the reference is to the ECS cluster specifically. The SSM parameter prefix `/luciel/production/…` is correct and stays unchanged. The CloudFormation stack `luciel-prod` (if it exists) is also a separate name from the ECS cluster and stays unchanged.
**Operational impact today:** Low — operator and advisor both know the correct name now. But the next operator (future hire, security reviewer, future-self-six-months-from-now) reading the docs cold would hit `ClusterNotFoundException` on the first command and have to re-derive the actual name.
**Resolution path:** Doc-truthing pass to update CANONICAL_RECAP and any runbook prose that references the cluster name. The Step 24.5c and Step 31 prod-deploy runbook (`docs/runbooks/`, see `D-step-24-5c-and-31-schema-and-code-undeployed-to-prod-2026-05-12`) needs the same audit. Combine with the next routine doc-truthing pass; not load-bearing enough to warrant a standalone commit.
**Three-name-class clarification (added in pass 6, 2026-05-13 — prevents a future re-grep from panicking over legitimate name-collisions):** Three different AWS resource classes all happen to start with the string `luciel-prod`, and only the first is the failure mode this drift tracks. (a) **ECS cluster argument** — the bare string `luciel-prod` handed to `--cluster ...` or assigned to a `$cluster` variable: WRONG, the actual cluster name is `luciel-cluster`, this is the failure mode. (b) **SSM parameter prefix** `/luciel/production/...`: CORRECT, stays unchanged. (c) **CloudFormation stack names and SNS topics** — `luciel-prod-alarms`, `luciel-prod-alerts`, `luciel-prod-worker-autoscaling`, `cfn/luciel-prod-alarms.yaml`, `cfn/luciel-prod-worker-autoscaling.yaml`: CORRECT, these are distinct AWS resources from the ECS cluster and their names are registered in AWS as written. A grep for `luciel-prod` in `docs/` returns many hits across all three classes; only class-(a) hits are bugs.
**Audit at pass 6 (2026-05-13) — what was found and fixed:** Grep across `docs/CANONICAL_RECAP.md`, `docs/ARCHITECTURE.md`, `docs/DRIFTS.md`, and `docs/runbooks/` for every `luciel-prod` occurrence. Every hit in the three canonical docs is class-(b) or class-(c) and stays unchanged (`cfn/luciel-prod-alarms.yaml` references in CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 31 row and ARCHITECTURE §3.2.12 §3.2.10 stanzas, the YAML filenames in DRIFTS §3 production-pending entries). Runbook hits are mostly class-(c) (`luciel-prod-alarms` stack name, `luciel-prod-alerts` SNS topic, `luciel-prod-worker-autoscaling` stack) and stay unchanged. **One class-(a) violation found:** `docs/runbooks/step-28-p3-h-rotate-and-purge.md:292` assigns `$cluster = "luciel-prod"` — the exact failure mode this drift was raised to track. Fixed in pass 6 (`$cluster = "luciel-cluster"`).
**Closeout update 2026-05-13 (pass 6):** All class-(a) violations across `docs/` corrected (one runbook fix). The three-name-class clarification above is the canonical reference for any future operator who greps `luciel-prod` and panics. This drift closes in this DRIFTS update; §5 mirror lands in this same commit per §6 doctrine.
**Cross-refs:** `docs/incidents/2026-05-12-dsn-disclosed-in-chat.md` (where the cluster name was first observed correctly during the rotation pre-flight); `docs/runbooks/step-28-p3-h-rotate-and-purge.md:292` (the one class-(a) violation found and fixed in pass 6).

### D-ssm-readonly-access-broad-2026-05-12

**Status:** OPEN — ⚠️ Warm. Hardening item, not blocking; surfaces as a finding any security reviewer flags.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) during the 2026-05-12 Phase 2 worker-rotation pre-flight, while surveying the backend container's IAM surface to determine whether the container could write to SSM directly (it cannot — write isn't granted). The execution role `luciel-ecs-execution-role` carries the AWS-managed policy `AmazonSSMReadOnlyAccess`, which grants `ssm:Get*`, `ssm:Describe*`, `ssm:List*` on `Resource: "*"` — every SSM parameter in the account, not scoped to `/luciel/*` or `/luciel/production/*`.
**Design claim:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.8 (secrets discipline) and the principle of least privilege in CANONICAL_RECAP §3 (senior-advisor voice extends to operational discipline) jointly imply that the backend's SSM access should be the narrowest path that delivers `/luciel/database-url`, `/luciel/production/worker_database_url`, and any other `/luciel/*` parameters the container actually reads at startup, and nothing else.
**Repo state:** `luciel-ecs-execution-role` has zero inline policies and two attached managed policies: `AmazonECSTaskExecutionRolePolicy` (correct, required for ECR pull and log emission) and `AmazonSSMReadOnlyAccess` (over-grants account-wide read). The task role `luciel-ecs-web-role` has one inline policy (`luciel-web-sqs-readonly`) and zero attached managed policies — that one is correctly scoped. The over-grant is on the execution role specifically.
**Operational impact today:** Low — the container is not compromised, and the parameters in the account that aren't `/luciel/*` are mostly other infrastructure that isn't itself sensitive. But the blast radius of a backend compromise is wider than it needs to be by exactly the size of the SSM parameter store.
**Resolution path:** Replace `AmazonSSMReadOnlyAccess` with an inline policy on `luciel-ecs-execution-role` that grants `ssm:GetParameters` and `ssm:GetParameter` on `Resource: arn:aws:ssm:ca-central-1:<account-id>:parameter/luciel/*` only, plus the KMS `Decrypt` permission on the key actually used by `/luciel/*` SecureString parameters (currently AWS-managed `alias/aws/ssm` — see `D-prod-kms-customer-managed-unverified-2026-05-09`). Owning roadmap step: not yet assigned — natural candidate is folding into Step 32's runbook so the scope-tightening lands in the same operational pass as the rotation-runbook design.
**Cross-refs:** `docs/incidents/2026-05-12-dsn-disclosed-in-chat.md`; `D-prod-kms-customer-managed-unverified-2026-05-09`; `D-rotation-procedure-laptop-dependent-2026-05-12`; ARCHITECTURE §3.2.8 (secrets discipline — the principle of least privilege on SSM access surfaces here as a hardening item).

### D-pillar-4d-audit-row-field-verify-deferred-2026-05-13

**Status:** OPEN — 📋 Deferred. Step 31 closed on Pillars 1, 2, 3, 4a/b/c-structural, and 5. The Pillar 4 sub-pillars 4d and 4e were not executed live before the closing tag; they are split out here as a separate piece of work.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-13 during the post-rotation-deferral recap. Originally, Pillar 4 of the Step 31 validation gate was claimed GREEN end-to-end based on a synthetic widget turn at ~18:21 EDT on 2026-05-12 producing audit activity in `/ecs/luciel-backend`. The CloudWatch search on 2026-05-12 ~22:20 EDT found the widget-chat traffic itself (`widget_chat_turn_received` / `widget_chat_session_resolved` / `widget_chat_turn_completed` INFO lines from `app.api.v1.chat_widget` at 22:17–22:21 UTC = 18:17–18:21 EDT, matching the recap's stated time window) but did **not** find structured audit lines carrying the §3.2.7 field set (`tenant_id`, `domain_id`, `embed_key_prefix`, `session_id`, and explicit absence of raw message body). A repo grep of `app/repositories/audit_chain.py` and `app/db/session.py` resolves the ambiguity: the audit chain emits to a **database table** (the `admin_audit_log` table, populated by the SQLAlchemy `before_flush` listener `install_audit_chain_event()` that runs on every transaction commit), not to CloudWatch Logs. The `audit_chain: before_flush handler installed.` CloudWatch line is startup confirmation, not the audit emission itself. The recap-summary phrase "6 audit lines confirmed in `/ecs/luciel-backend`" was lossy summarization of what was actually a DB-row count from a synthetic-turn psql query, not a CloudWatch line count. The Pillar 4c structural claim survives this reinterpretation (the synthetic turn did produce DB rows); the Pillar 4d field-set verify needs to happen against the DB rows, not against CloudWatch.
**Design claim:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.7 (application log stream) and the Step 31 five-pillar validation gate (CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 31 row, customer-journey pillar) jointly commit to a structured audit trail with a redaction contract: the audit row carries identity context (tenant, domain, embed-key prefix, session) and never the raw message body.
**Repo state:** `app/repositories/audit_chain.py` registers the `before_flush` listener that populates `row_hash` and `prev_row_hash` on `admin_audit_log` table rows; the canonical chain content is the `_CHAIN_FIELDS` list inside that module. `app/api/v1/chat_widget.py` emits three `logger.info` markers (`widget_chat_turn_received`, `widget_chat_session_resolved`, `widget_chat_turn_completed`) to CloudWatch and writes the structured audit rows to `admin_audit_log` via the existing repository pattern. The widget-surface audit-log claim closed `D-widget-chat-no-application-level-audit-log-2026-05-10` in Step 31 sub-branch 1 (PR #30). The CloudWatch markers and the DB rows are two separate emission paths; the field-set redaction contract attaches to the DB rows (the auditable artifact), not to the CloudWatch markers (which are operational telemetry).
**Operational impact today:** None — the audit-chain code is live in production (Phase 1 force-new-deployment of 2026-05-12 confirmed `luciel-backend:41` healthy with the Step 31 code path), and the synthetic widget turns at 18:17–18:21 EDT exercised it. The structural claim (rows written, hash chain advances) was verified at sub-branch 5 live-run time (run stamp `20260512-144847-068362`, 40/40 claims green in the harness against dev RDS). What's deferred is the standalone DB-row field-verify against tonight's specific synthetic-turn rows in production — a read-only check, no production state change.
**Resolution path:** Read-only DB query against production RDS via the `python -c "exec(bytes([…]).decode())"` transport proven on 2026-05-12, against the post-Phase-1 admin DSN already live in SSM v2. The script selects from `admin_audit_log` filtered by the widget turn timestamps (22:17–22:21 UTC = 18:17–18:21 EDT on 2026-05-12) and the relevant tenant/embed-key, then asserts: each row carries `tenant_id`, `domain_id`, `embed_key_prefix`, `session_id` populated and non-null; no row carries a message-body field, a `message_text` field, or any column whose name suggests raw widget chat content; the chain advances correctly (`prev_row_hash` of row N matches `row_hash` of row N-1). Acceptance: harness exits 0 with the 4 assertions named explicitly. Owning roadmap step: not currently assigned — natural pickup is a small follow-up commit (call it Step 31.1) **after** Step 32 (rotation runbook) lands, so the DB-read is done with a freshly-rotated admin password rather than the currently-disclosed-but-acknowledged v2.
**Cross-refs:** `D-pillar-4e-cross-table-row-verify-deferred-2026-05-13`; `D-pillar-4c-evidence-location-recap-ambiguous-2026-05-13`; CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 31 row caveat addendum; CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Q2 row (✅ Implemented marker depends on this and 4e closing for fully-green Pillar 4 against production rows); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.7 (the field-set redaction contract this drift will verify against production `admin_audit_log` rows); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.12 closure caveats (the post-hoc addendum that names this deferral as Step 31.1 follow-up shape).
