### D-pillar-4c-evidence-location-recap-ambiguous-2026-05-13

**Status:** OPEN — 🔧 Partial. Doc-truthing finding; not a code drift, not a state drift. Self-correction recorded for audit per the §6 honesty doctrine.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-13 during the post-rotation-deferral recap, while attempting to execute the deferred Pillar 4d verification. The session-summary state at the start of the 2026-05-13 conversation phrased the Step 31 Pillar 4c result as "6 audit lines confirmed in `/ecs/luciel-backend` from synthetic widget turn at 18:21 EDT." CloudWatch search across the cited time window found the widget-chat traffic INFO lines but not structured audit lines with the §3.2.7 field set; a repo grep then established that the audit chain emits to the `admin_audit_log` database table, not to CloudWatch (the `audit_chain: before_flush handler installed.` startup line is the only audit-chain string that appears in CloudWatch, and it's a registration confirmation, not an audit emission). The substantive claim survives this re-reading (synthetic widget turns at 18:17–18:21 EDT did produce DB rows in `admin_audit_log` via the `before_flush` listener), but the recap's phrasing conflated CloudWatch markers with audit-row emission. Two surface artifacts can each be "audit evidence" without being the same artifact, and the recap should distinguish them.
**Design claim:** §6 honesty doctrine in `docs/DRIFTS.md` and the senior-advisor voice in CANONICAL_RECAP §3 jointly require that when an internal phrasing turns out to be lossy or misleading on re-reading, it gets a doc-truthing pass. Lossy summarization is fine in real time; it gets corrected when the imprecision is caught.
**Repo state:** The Step 31 row in CANONICAL_RECAP §12 itself does not contain the ambiguous phrasing — that was an artifact of inter-session state-summary, not the canonical doc. The §12 row correctly references the harness's pillar-by-pillar claim counts (40/40 across five pillars at run stamp `20260512-144847-068362`) and the structured-audit emission paths (three `logger.info` markers in CloudWatch + audit-row writes via the existing repository pattern). The doc-truthing in this drift is therefore additive: add a caveat addendum to the Step 31 §12 row that names the Pillar 4d/4e production-row verifications explicitly as deferred-but-tracked, and that names the two emission paths (CloudWatch markers vs `admin_audit_log` rows) explicitly so the next reader does not re-introduce the conflation.
**Operational impact today:** None — the integrity of Pillar 4c is intact (DB rows did get written), and the integrity of Pillars 1, 2, 3, 4a/b, and 5 is also intact. The drift is about the audit story being precise enough that a future security reviewer cannot reasonably challenge it.
**Resolution path:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 31 row gains a caveat addendum naming (a) the two distinct emission paths, (b) the Pillar 4d/4e production-row verifications as deferred and tracked by `D-pillar-4d-audit-row-field-verify-deferred-2026-05-13` and `D-pillar-4e-cross-table-row-verify-deferred-2026-05-13`, (c) the unchanged closing-tag claim (Step 31 closed on Pillars 1/2/3/4a/b/c-structural/5; the deferred 4d/4e are post-closure follow-ups, not re-openings). This drift closes when the addendum lands in the same commit as this DRIFTS update.
**Cross-refs:** `D-pillar-4d-audit-row-field-verify-deferred-2026-05-13`; `D-pillar-4e-cross-table-row-verify-deferred-2026-05-13`; CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 31 row caveat addendum (which names the two distinct emission paths explicitly to prevent this conflation from recurring); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.7 (post-hoc note added in pass-2 that distinguishes CloudWatch markers from `admin_audit_log` rows at the contract level); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.12 closure caveats.

### D-doc-truthing-pass-3-overstep-and-recap-last-updated-sediment-2026-05-13

**Status:** OPEN (self-correction, moved to Section 5 in this commit — same-pass-self-correction shape, precedent `D-canonical-recap-q1-q8-roadmap-genericized-2026-05-08`).
**Raised by:** Operator (partner) on 2026-05-13, on review of `main` after PR #40 (`step-31-doc-truthing-pass-3-triangulation-doctrine`, merged `09c6ddd`) and the cumulative "Last updated" paragraph that had grown across PRs #36 (`d843812`) → #38 (`f359d5f`) → #39 (`c5aec38`) at `CANONICAL_RECAP.md` line 9. Two doctrine breaches, both with explicit precedent in the docs' own maintenance protocols:

  - **Breach 1 — top-of-file changelog sediment in `CANONICAL_RECAP.md`.** A "Last updated: 2026-05-13 ..." paragraph had accreted at the head of the recap across three commits, summarizing what each one did. CANONICAL_RECAP §17 forbids this by name ("No version-history sediment. The document reflects current state. Past state is in git and in `DRIFTS.md`.") and ARCHITECTURE.md line 17 calls out the exact failure mode ("This document does not carry a top-of-file changelog"). The substantive facts the paragraph mentioned were already in their proper homes — §11 (Q2 flip), §12 (Step 31 row + caveat addendum), DRIFTS §3 (the 8 new drifts from `f359d5f`). The paragraph duplicated all of them at the top of the recap and gave the doc the texture of a project agenda rather than the comprehensive business overview it is.
  - **Breach 2 — doctrine restated as a parallel top-level section in all three docs.** PR #40 introduced `## Section 18 — Triangulation discipline` in `CANONICAL_RECAP.md`, `## Section 8 — Triangulation discipline` in `ARCHITECTURE.md`, and `## Section 8 — Triangulation discipline (canonical home of the doctrine)` in `DRIFTS.md`. The cross-document doctrine those sections restate was **already canonical** in `DRIFTS.md` §1 line 30 ("When this document, the architecture document, the canonical recap, the repository, or production disagree, the resolution is recorded here as a drift. The four artifacts converge by closing drifts, not by editing one and hoping the others catch up.") and `DRIFTS.md` §6 line 495 ("the canonical docs grow only when the architectural shape changes ... A new roadmap step, on its own, is not a reason to grow the docs"). Adding three new top-level sections to restate doctrine each doc already encoded violated the intra-doc "one source of truth per fact" rule each maintenance section states in its own voice (`CANONICAL_RECAP.md` §17, `ARCHITECTURE.md` §6). It also made how-we-maintain-the-docs a top-level section parallel to the substantive business / system / integrity sections — the failure mode the operator named as "the docs are not a mere agenda."

**Design claim:** The three documents are independent substantive views of the same business (CANONICAL_RECAP = business view; ARCHITECTURE = system view; DRIFTS = integrity / audit view), each readable cold on its own, **and that property comes from each doc carrying only its substantive content plus one short maintenance section.** Top-of-file changelogs and parallel "discipline of the discipline" sections both undermine the readable-cold property: the first by pushing the substantive content below a project log, the second by elevating process to a parallel substantive section.
**Repo state at the time of the breach:** `CANONICAL_RECAP.md` carried the "Last updated: 2026-05-13 ..." paragraph at line 9, grown across PRs #36/#38/#39. `CANONICAL_RECAP.md` §18 (PR #40), `ARCHITECTURE.md` §8 (PR #40), and `DRIFTS.md` §8 (PR #40) restated doctrine already canonical in `DRIFTS.md` §1 + §6. Both breaches were within the doc-truthing arc itself — the same arc that was supposed to be enforcing the doctrine — which is precisely the situation §6 honesty doctrine asks the audit ledger to record.
**Resolution path:** Both breaches corrected on 2026-05-13 by PR #41 (`step-31-doc-truthing-pass-4-remove-sediment-and-doctrine-section`, merged `40b2acf`):

  - The "Last updated" paragraph was removed entirely from `CANONICAL_RECAP.md`. The substantive facts remain in their proper homes (§11, §12, DRIFTS §3), exactly as the doctrine requires.
  - The §18 / §8 / §8 "Triangulation discipline" sections were removed from all three docs (revert of PR #40). The cross-document clarification (that "one source of truth per fact" is intra-doc; cross-doc redundancy is the triangulation working correctly) survives as one folded clarifying line inside each existing maintenance section (`CANONICAL_RECAP.md` §17, `ARCHITECTURE.md` §6), pointing at `DRIFTS.md` §1 + §6 as the canonical home of the cross-document lifecycle rules.

This drift closes in this DRIFTS update — the doctrine breach was already corrected in PR #41; this entry records it for audit per §6 honesty doctrine, and the §5 closure mirror lands in this same commit.
**Cross-refs:** PR #36 (`d843812`), PR #38 (`f359d5f`), PR #39 (`c5aec38`) — the three commits that grew the "Last updated" paragraph; PR #40 (`09c6ddd`) — the parallel-section over-step; PR #41 (`40b2acf`) — the correction; CANONICAL_RECAP §17 (maintenance protocol, intra-doc one-source rule + cross-doc triangulation pointer); ARCHITECTURE §6 (same shape); DRIFTS §1 line 30 (cross-document source-of-truth, canonical home of doctrine); DRIFTS §6 line 495 (no-bloat rule, also part of canonical home).

### D-doc-truthing-pass-6-section-3-deletion-on-closure-and-orphan-cross-ref-2026-05-13

**Status:** OPEN (self-correction, moved to Section 5 in this commit — same-pass-self-correction shape, precedent `D-canonical-recap-q1-q8-roadmap-genericized-2026-05-08` and `D-doc-truthing-pass-3-overstep-and-recap-last-updated-sediment-2026-05-13`).
**Raised by:** Operator (partner) on 2026-05-13, asking on review of pass 5: *"have all the drifts that properly need to close been closed and has everything now been properly referenced between the docs and our agreement been properly maintained"*. The honest answer required a full audit of the §3/§5 mirror discipline against the §6 rule ("closing a drift = move-to-§5 with strikethrough; **do not delete from §3**") since that rule first landed in commit `0d9a0c4` on 2026-05-09. Three doctrine breaches surfaced, all sitting in the audit ledger unrecorded:

  - **Breach 1 — four §3 entries deleted on closure in violation of §6, post-doctrine.** The four drifts `D-widget-no-content-safety-or-scope-guardrail-2026-05-10`, `D-widget-chat-no-application-level-audit-log-2026-05-10`, `D-step-24-5c-impl-backlog-2026-05-11`, and `D-step-31-impl-backlog-2026-05-11` were all raised after the §6 "do not delete" rule landed (2026-05-09 in commit `0d9a0c4`) and were closed in subsequent commits (`f8ac1d4` Step 30d closeout, `fa876ce` Step 31 sub-branch 5, `55e4db9` Step 24.5c sub-branch 5) that deleted the §3 body and added the §5 strikethrough heading. The §6 rule requires both: §3 entry preserved verbatim with closeout update line, §5 strikethrough mirror added in the same commit. The audit chain depends on the body of each drift remaining readable in §3 after closure so the design-claim/repo-state context is available alongside the resolution line in §5. Pass 6 restores all four §3 entries **verbatim from the parent of their closure commit**, with a Status line that names the resolution commit and the pass-6 restoration so the audit chain reads honestly cold.
  - **Breach 2 — orphan cross-reference in `ARCHITECTURE.md` §3.3.** Line 334 references the drift token `D-widget-no-content-safety-2026-05-09` — a slug that has never existed in `DRIFTS.md`. The actual slug raised on 2026-05-10 by Step 30b Phase 4 staging E2E is `D-widget-no-content-safety-or-scope-guardrail-2026-05-10` (longer form, different date). The reference resolves to nothing; a future reader searching `DRIFTS.md` for the cited token finds zero hits and has to re-derive the actual drift by topic match. Pass 6 corrects the token in place to the canonical slug. No surrounding prose change.
  - **Breach 3 — `D-cluster-name-luciel-cluster-not-luciel-prod-2026-05-12` left open with one runbook-level violation un-fixed.** The drift's resolution path committed to a doc-truthing audit covering `CANONICAL_RECAP`, `ARCHITECTURE`, and the runbooks; the audit found that all three canonical docs and most runbooks reference legitimate class-(b)/class-(c) `luciel-prod-*` resources (SSM prefix, CloudFormation stacks, SNS topics) that are correctly named and stay unchanged, but `docs/runbooks/step-28-p3-h-rotate-and-purge.md:292` assigned `$cluster = "luciel-prod"` — the exact failure mode the drift was raised to track. Pass 6 fixes the one violation, augments the §3 entry with a three-name-class clarification (so a future grep does not panic over `luciel-prod-alarms`), and closes the drift with a §5 mirror in the same commit.

**Design claim:** The §6 doctrine "closing a drift = move-to-§5, do not delete from §3" is load-bearing for the audit chain — the original §3 body (raised-by / design-claim / repo-state / resolution-path) carries the context a future security reviewer or new operator needs alongside the §5 resolution line, and that context is exactly what a verbatim delete loses. The orphan cross-ref breach is the converse failure mode of the same property: even when a drift is correctly preserved, a stale token elsewhere in the docs makes it unfindable. The cluster-name follow-through breach is the third shape: a drift can be open with a half-executed resolution path long enough that the unfixed half becomes invisible until directly asked.
**Repo state at the time of breach detection:** §3 contains the four restorations above (all marked with `RESOLVED on <date> by <commit>; restored to §3 in pass 6` Status lines). `ARCHITECTURE.md` line 334 carries the orphan token. `docs/runbooks/step-28-p3-h-rotate-and-purge.md:292` carries the bad `$cluster = "luciel-prod"` assignment. All three breaches existed silently across passes 1–5; pass 5 (`c3a976c`, PR #42) added the two honesty closures for `D-pillar-4c` and the PR-#40 over-step but did not catch the broader pattern of post-doctrine §3 deletions.
**Resolution path:** Three fixes land in pass 6, all in one commit:

  1. **Four §3 restorations**, verbatim from the parent of each drift's closure commit, with one new Status line per restored entry naming the resolution commit and the pass-6 restoration reason. The §5 strikethrough entries for those four drifts already exist (correctly written from their respective closure commits) and are unchanged.
  2. **One ARCHITECTURE §3.3 line-334 cross-ref fix**: `D-widget-no-content-safety-2026-05-09` → `D-widget-no-content-safety-or-scope-guardrail-2026-05-10`. No surrounding prose change.
  3. **One runbook fix + close `D-cluster-name-luciel-cluster-not-luciel-prod-2026-05-12`**: `docs/runbooks/step-28-p3-h-rotate-and-purge.md:292` `$cluster = "luciel-prod"` → `$cluster = "luciel-cluster"`; §3 entry receives a three-name-class clarification + closeout update; §5 mirror added in the same commit per §6 doctrine.

This drift's §5 closure mirror lands in this same commit per the same-pass-self-correction precedent.
**Doctrine reflection (recorded for future passes):** The pattern from pass 5 holds — doctrine breaches inside the audit ledger itself are the ones most worth recording, because they are the ones that *would otherwise sit silently*. The three breaches here had been sitting in the ledger across multiple passes; only a direct "is everything clean" question surfaced them. The lesson is that an honest *post-merge audit* against the docs' own rules belongs in the doc-truthing protocol, not just verification that the current pass followed the rules. Pass 6 is the first pass to do that explicitly; future closing passes should include a quick §3 vs §5 mirror-discipline grep against the doctrine date floor before being declared complete.
**Cross-refs:** Closure commits that deleted §3 bodies in violation of §6: `f8ac1d4` (Step 30d closeout, Pass-30d), `fa876ce` (Step 31 sub-branch 5, Pass-31), `55e4db9` (Step 24.5c sub-branch 5, Pass-24.5c); commit that introduced §6 "do not delete" rule: `0d9a0c4` (2026-05-09); the four restored §3 entries: `D-widget-no-content-safety-or-scope-guardrail-2026-05-10`, `D-widget-chat-no-application-level-audit-log-2026-05-10`, `D-step-24-5c-impl-backlog-2026-05-11`, `D-step-31-impl-backlog-2026-05-11`; `D-cluster-name-luciel-cluster-not-luciel-prod-2026-05-12` (closes in this same commit); precedent `D-doc-truthing-pass-3-overstep-and-recap-last-updated-sediment-2026-05-13` (pass 5, same self-correction shape).

### D-canonical-recap-status-cell-bloat-violates-triangulation-2026-05-13

**Status:** OPEN (self-correction, moved to Section 5 in this commit — same-pass-self-correction shape, precedent `D-canonical-recap-q1-q8-roadmap-genericized-2026-05-08`, `D-doc-truthing-pass-3-overstep-and-recap-last-updated-sediment-2026-05-13` (pass 5), `D-doc-truthing-pass-6-section-3-deletion-on-closure-and-orphan-cross-ref-2026-05-13` (pass 6)).
**Raised by:** Operator (partner) on 2026-05-13 in the conversation that produced this pass: *"like our docs (e.g Canonical recap) have huge paragraph in the tables (e.g the strategic questions table and roadmap table). Are all markers reflected properly and are these huge paragraphs needed if we are performing triangulation and is this discipline preserved for all of our docs?"* The honest audit answered in three parts: (a) yes, every marker (✅ / 🔧 / 📋 / 🔬) reflects current reality; (b) no, the huge paragraphs are not needed under triangulation — they are a discipline breach; (c) no, the discipline is not uniformly preserved — the breach is concentrated in `CANONICAL_RECAP.md` Section 11 (Q-row Status cells) and Section 12 (Step-row Status cells), while `ARCHITECTURE.md` (12 tables, none bloated) and `DRIFTS.md` (zero tables, all prose) hold their respective shapes correctly.
**Design claim:** Triangulation doctrine pinned in PR #40 / commit `dfab55e` (`docs/CANONICAL_RECAP.md` §16 / `docs/ARCHITECTURE.md` §6 / `docs/DRIFTS.md` §1) says the three canonical docs hold three independent substantive views — `CANONICAL_RECAP` is the business view, `ARCHITECTURE` is the system view, `DRIFTS` is the integrity view — and each must be readable cold. Each doc's job is its own angle on the same facts, not a superset of the other two. A `CANONICAL_RECAP` Status cell that re-explains the architecture in 5,000–10,000 characters is the business view impersonating the system view: it duplicates ARCHITECTURE content inline, and the duplication degrades every time one side updates without the other. The correct shape of a closed-step Status cell is: marker + date + one-sentence what-shipped + ARCHITECTURE § cross-ref + closing tag + drift-slug closures + any production-facing caveat (deploy gap, deferred verify, stage-gate). Implementation specifics — file paths, function signatures, line-by-line code behavior, harness internals, table column lists — belong in ARCHITECTURE where they are the load-bearing content, and stay in `git log` for the per-commit detail. The business reader, the security reviewer, and the future operator each get a cleaner read when each doc honors its own scope.
**Repo state at the time of breach detection:** Eight Status cells in `CANONICAL_RECAP.md` were 800–9000+ characters: Q2 (2,569 chars), Q8 (2,449 chars), Step 24.5c (3,027 chars), Step 30b (3,264 chars), Step 30c (5,797 chars), Step 30d (3,811 chars), Step 31 (8,985 chars), plus smaller residual bloat in Q-rows. The drift extends back at least to Step 30c closeout (2026-05-11, commit `99c6eb5`) which set the precedent of writing the full deploy stanza into the Status cell. Subsequent steps inherited the pattern (30d, 31). Six prior doc-truthing passes (1–6) on `step-31` did not catch the pattern because each pass focused on factual correctness of the close-out rather than the triangulation shape of the document.
**Resolution path:** Pass 7 (this commit) compresses every bloated Status cell to the triangulation-correct shape:

  1. **Q-row Status cells in Section 11** — Q2 and Q8 compressed; all other Q-rows already correctly shaped. Each compressed cell preserves: marker, implementing-step pointer, one-sentence what-shipped, ARCHITECTURE § cross-ref, operational-record pointer (§12 row below), closing tag, every drift slug touched, every production caveat (Prod-deploy gap, Pillar-4d/4e deferred).
  2. **Step-row Status cells in Section 12** — Step 24.5c, 30b, 30c, 30d, 31 compressed. Each cell preserves: marker, date range, sub-branch / PR list, one-sentence what-shipped, ARCHITECTURE § cross-ref(s), closing tag, every commit SHA that is referenced elsewhere (`99c6eb5`, `b216300`, `84339a3`, the ECR digest, deploy run IDs, etc.), every drift slug closed or referenced, production-facing caveats (Prod-deploy gap, closure caveats, observed-clean stanzas reduced to the load-bearing fact + DRIFTS §5 pointer for the full stanza, deliberate v1 non-goals).
  3. **No content destroyed** — the architectural detail removed from `CANONICAL_RECAP` already lives in `ARCHITECTURE.md` (§3.2.11, §3.2.12, §3.3 step 6.5, §3.3 step 8, §4.9), the production-rollout detail already lives in DRIFTS §5 closure stanzas (`~~D-confirmation-gate-not-enforced-2026-05-09~~` carries the full Step 30c prod observed-clean stanza; `~~D-widget-no-content-safety-or-scope-guardrail-2026-05-10~~` carries the Step 30d harness-gap follow-up detail; `~~D-step-31-impl-backlog-2026-05-11~~` carries the Step 31 five-pillar harness detail), and the commit-level detail lives in `git log` against the closing tags. Triangulation now holds: each doc covers its own angle, redundancy across docs is at the cross-reference level (drift slug, ARCHITECTURE § number, closing tag, commit SHA), not at the prose level.

This drift's §5 closure mirror lands in this same commit per the same-pass-self-correction precedent.
**Doctrine reflection (recorded for future passes):** Pass 6's lesson was *audit historical mirror discipline*. Pass 7's lesson is *audit the shape of the docs themselves against the triangulation doctrine they declare*. Six doc-truthing passes verified close-out factual correctness but did not look at the macro question "does each doc still read as its own view, or has CANONICAL_RECAP grown into a superset?" The breach is invisible at any single closure (each Status cell looked thorough; thoroughness was the wrong virtue) and only surfaces in a triangulation-shape audit. Future closing passes should include, alongside the §3/§5 mirror-discipline grep that pass 6 added, a Status-cell length grep against the bloat threshold (anything over ~1,500 chars deserves a triangulation-shape review). The pattern to watch for is: when you find yourself writing implementation detail in a Status cell, that detail belongs in ARCHITECTURE; the Status cell takes a one-sentence summary and a cross-ref.
**Cross-refs:** Triangulation doctrine pin: PR #40, commit `dfab55e`, doctrine block at `CANONICAL_RECAP.md` §16 + `ARCHITECTURE.md` §6 + `DRIFTS.md` §1. Closing commits whose Status cells were bloated and are compressed in this pass: `99c6eb5` (Step 30c), Step 24.5c doc-truthing commit, `f8ac1d4` and downstream (Step 30d), `fa876ce` (Step 31 sub-branch 5 doc-truthing), and the four pass-6 follow-up commits (the Status-cell bloat predates pass 6 but pass 6 did not address it). Same-pass-self-correction precedents: `D-canonical-recap-q1-q8-roadmap-genericized-2026-05-08`, `D-doc-truthing-pass-3-overstep-and-recap-last-updated-sediment-2026-05-13` (pass 5), `D-doc-truthing-pass-6-section-3-deletion-on-closure-and-orphan-cross-ref-2026-05-13` (pass 6). No-bloat doctrine for the canonical docs: §6 "What does NOT belong in the design docs" (also the canonical home of the build-detail-stays-in-commit-messages rule).

### D-cross-reference-wiring-asymmetric-no-shared-q-step-tokens-2026-05-13

**Status:** OPEN (self-correction, moved to Section 5 in this commit — same-pass-self-correction shape, precedents `D-canonical-recap-q1-q8-roadmap-genericized-2026-05-08`, `D-doc-truthing-pass-3-overstep-and-recap-last-updated-sediment-2026-05-13` (pass 5), `D-doc-truthing-pass-6-section-3-deletion-on-closure-and-orphan-cross-ref-2026-05-13` (pass 6), `D-canonical-recap-status-cell-bloat-violates-triangulation-2026-05-13` (pass 7)).
**Raised by:** Operator (partner) on 2026-05-13 in the conversation that produced this pass: *"I hope now that we have made these edits the cross references through our docs is properly preserved as well. Like canonical references the other two docs wherever needed. Same for Architecture and drifts. There should [be] proper linkages at all points like maybe architecture the roadmap steps or the strategic questions?"* and the follow-up sharpening the shape: *"I was thinking one way you reference is by adding the roadmap step and strategic question."* The pre-Pass-8 audit found a real asymmetry across the three docs: DRIFTS → ARCHITECTURE = 46 refs, DRIFTS → CANONICAL_RECAP = 78 refs (well-wired), but **CANONICAL_RECAP → ARCHITECTURE = 7 refs** and **ARCHITECTURE → CANONICAL_RECAP = 4 refs** (under-wired). Six of eight Q-rows in §11 carried no ARCH § pointer (Q1, Q3, Q4, Q5, Q6, Q7); every §3.2.1–§3.2.10 subsection in ARCHITECTURE carried no back-link to the Q-row or Step-row that justified it; every §4.1–§4.9 subsection likewise; §3.3's eleven numbered steps carried no Q/Step token map.
**Design claim:** Triangulation doctrine (pinned PR #40 / commit `dfab55e`) requires each of the three canonical docs to read *cold* as its own substantive view of the business. Cross-doc redundancy belongs at the **cross-reference** level (the same fact reached from three angles, each angle pointed at the other two by a shared identifier), not at the **prose** level (one doc reproducing another doc's load-bearing content). The shared identifiers that make triangulation greppable are the **Q-tokens** (Q1–Q8 in Recap §11) and **Step-tokens** (Step 24.5c, Step 28–38 in Recap §12), plus the closing-tag identifiers (`step-<n>-...-complete`). These tokens are stable, opinionated, and unique — a future grep across the three docs can confirm that every Q-row in Recap has an ARCH § that names it back by Q-token, every ARCH subsection has a Q-token + Step-token tying it to a business answer, and every DRIFTS §3 entry names both the Q-token and Step-token of the question whose integrity it tracks. Where a section honours a broader Recap section (Section 4 never-do contract, Section 2 two layers, Section 15 deliberate non-goals) rather than a single Q, the back-link uses the Section number instead of a Q-token — same shape, broader scope.
**Repo state at the time of breach detection:** raw cross-doc reference counts as listed above; concrete row-level gaps as enumerated above (6 Q-rows, 10+ ARCH §3.2 subsections, 9 §4 subsections, all §3.3 numbered steps). The breach predates the entire doc-truthing pass series (passes 1–7 walked over it without addressing it; passes 1–6 verified close-out factual correctness, pass 7 verified Status-cell triangulation shape, but none of the seven verified the cross-reference graph between the three docs).
**Resolution path:** Pass 8 (this commit) wires the three docs together at every load-bearing point using Q/Step tokens as the shared vocabulary:

  1. **CANONICAL_RECAP §11 Q-rows** — six previously un-linked Q-rows (Q1, Q3, Q4, Q5, Q6, Q7) gain an `Architecture: ARCHITECTURE §...` cell suffix naming the ARCH subsections that hold the system view, plus an operational-record pointer naming the implementing or candidate Step. Q2 and Q8 were already wired (§3.2.12 / §3.2.11) and stay unchanged.
  2. **CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step-rows** — every Step row gains an explicit Q-token tail naming the Q (or Recap Section) it operationalises, hardens, validates, or decides. Implemented Steps (24.5c, 28, 29, 30b, 30c, 30d, 31) already carried ARCH § cross-refs in their Status cells; the Q-token tail is the new addition. Planned/Candidate Steps (30a, 32, 32a, 33, 33b, 34, 34a, 35, 36, 37, 38) gain both the Q-token and the ARCH § in the same cell tail.
  3. **ARCHITECTURE §3.2.1–§3.2.12** — every subsection gains a `**Triangulation:**` opening line immediately after the heading, naming the Q-token(s) it answers, the Step-token(s) it implements, the closing tag(s) if any, and the DRIFTS §3 integrity questions if any. §3.2.11 and §3.2.12 (already partially wired in their prose bodies) gain the same opener-line shape for symmetry.
  4. **ARCHITECTURE §4.1–§4.9** — every cross-cutting property subsection gains the same `**Triangulation:**` opening line.
  5. **ARCHITECTURE §3.3** — a single `**Triangulation per step (Q/Step token map):**` paragraph is inserted at the section opening, mapping each of the eleven numbered steps to its Q-token and Step-token. The numbered step prose is unchanged — the per-step token map sits above it so a reader reaches the prose with the tokens in mind.
  6. **DRIFTS §3 entries** — the Q-tokens are implicit in the slug for the historically Q-anchored drifts; this pass adds explicit Q-token mention to the doctrine reflection below rather than re-stamping every entry (the Step-token is already present in every entry's name or body).
  7. **No prose destroyed.** Every existing line in all three docs is preserved verbatim except where pass 7's Status-cell tails were already-being-edited; the new cross-references are *additive* (one line per Q-row, one line per ARCH subsection, one tail clause per Step-row, one paragraph at §3.3 head).

This drift's §5 closure mirror lands in this same commit per the same-pass-self-correction precedent now established across passes 5, 6, 7, and this pass.
**Doctrine reflection (recorded for future passes):** Pass 7's lesson was *audit triangulation shape — each doc must hold its own scope*. Pass 8's lesson is *audit the triangulation graph — the three docs must be greppably wired together by stable identifiers*. The Q-tokens (Q1–Q8), Step-tokens (Step 24.5c, Step 28–38, plus 30a/b/c/d, 32a, 33b, 34a, 31.1), and closing-tag identifiers (`step-<n>-...-complete`) form the shared vocabulary. The pattern to watch for: when a section of any of the three docs has no Q-token, no Step-token, and no closing-tag identifier in its opening line, ask whether the section is actually load-bearing for the business — if it is, the linkage is missing; if it isn't, the section may not belong in a canonical doc at all. Future closing-pass checklists should include a third grep alongside pass 6's mirror-discipline grep and pass 7's Status-cell length grep: a Q/Step token-coverage grep that confirms every Q-row in Recap is named back by at least one ARCH subsection, every §3.2 / §4 subsection in ARCH names a Q-token or a Section number, and every DRIFTS §3 entry names at least one Q-token or Step-token in its design-claim or cross-refs block.
**Cross-refs:** Triangulation doctrine pin: PR #40, commit `dfab55e`. Pass 7 (the immediately preceding self-correction): `D-canonical-recap-status-cell-bloat-violates-triangulation-2026-05-13`. Same-pass-self-correction precedents: `D-canonical-recap-q1-q8-roadmap-genericized-2026-05-08`, `D-doc-truthing-pass-3-overstep-and-recap-last-updated-sediment-2026-05-13`, `D-doc-truthing-pass-6-section-3-deletion-on-closure-and-orphan-cross-ref-2026-05-13`, `D-canonical-recap-status-cell-bloat-violates-triangulation-2026-05-13`. Pass-8 commit closes this drift in §5 in the same commit.
### D-pass-6-mirror-restoration-incomplete-three-deletions-missed-2026-05-13

**Status:** OPEN (self-correction, moved to Section 5 in this commit — same-pass-self-correction shape, precedents `D-canonical-recap-q1-q8-roadmap-genericized-2026-05-08`, `D-doc-truthing-pass-3-overstep-and-recap-last-updated-sediment-2026-05-13` (pass 5), `D-doc-truthing-pass-6-section-3-deletion-on-closure-and-orphan-cross-ref-2026-05-13` (pass 6), `D-canonical-recap-status-cell-bloat-violates-triangulation-2026-05-13` (pass 7), `D-cross-reference-wiring-asymmetric-no-shared-q-step-tokens-2026-05-13` (pass 8)).
**Raised by:** Operator (partner) on 2026-05-13 after Pass 8 merged, asking: *"okay I hope that all throughout our docs, all discipline and symmetry has been maintained properly?"* The Pass-9 audit ran three closing-pass greps — Q/Step token coverage (pass 8's lesson), Status-cell length (pass 7), and §3/§5 mirror discipline (pass 6) — and found the first two clean but the third revealed nine §5 strikethrough closures with no surviving §3 entry. Classification: **5** were born §5-only inside commit `0d9a0c4` (2026-05-09 18:27 UTC), the very commit that established the §6 "do not delete from §3" doctrine — pre-doctrine, not violations. **1** (`D-ci-ast-job-red-on-main-2026-05-08`) was born §5-only post-doctrine in commit `8ad59e4` whose parent also lacked a §3 body — minor procedural irregularity, no restoration possible (annotated with a Pass-9 doctrine note in §5). **3** were genuine post-doctrine §6 violations Pass 6 did not catch: `D-embed-key-issuance-workflow-missing-2026-05-09` (closed `c8b2142`, ~3 hours after the doctrine landed), `D-prod-widget-bundle-cdn-unprovisioned-2026-05-09` (closed `ee14e67`), and `D-confirmation-gate-not-enforced-2026-05-09` (closed `b9d0520`). In each of the three, the closure commit's parent contained the §3 body; the closure commit deleted it instead of moving-with-strikethrough.
**Design claim:** The §6 "do not delete from §3 on closure" doctrine and the §3/§5 mirror discipline derived from it require **every §5 strikethrough closure** to have a corresponding §3 entry — preserved verbatim from raise time, augmented with a Status line naming the closure commit and tag if any. Pass 6's audit predicate was narrower than the doctrine itself: it walked only the four post-doctrine closures it found in the four most recent close-out commits, and missed three earlier post-doctrine closures sitting between the doctrine commit (`0d9a0c4`, 2026-05-09 18:27) and the four it caught (Step 30d close, Step 31 sub-branch 5 close, Step 24.5c sub-branch 5 close — all later). The correct audit predicate is *every §5 strikethrough entry, paired with the timestamp of its closure commit relative to `0d9a0c4`*, not *the four most recent close-outs*. Pass 9 establishes that predicate and applies it.
**Repo state at the time of breach detection:** 26 §3 entries, 20 §5 strikethrough closures, 9 orphan §5 entries (no §3 mirror). Of the 9, 5 pre-doctrine (born in `0d9a0c4`), 1 post-doctrine-but-never-had-§3 (`D-ci-ast-job-red-on-main-2026-05-08`, closure `8ad59e4`), 3 post-doctrine §6 violations Pass 6 missed (the three named in **Raised by** above).
**Resolution path:** Pass 9 (this commit) does four things in one commit:

  1. **Restore the 3 post-doctrine §6-violation §3 bodies verbatim** from each closure commit's parent (`c8b2142^` for embed-key-issuance, `ee14e67^` for prod-widget-bundle-cdn, `b9d0520^` for confirmation-gate). Each restoration is byte-identical to the parent commit's §3 body, with two additions: a new Status line at the top naming the closure commit + tag (if any) + this Pass-9 restoration with date, and a Pass-9 doctrine note at the bottom explaining that this is one of three deletions Pass 6 did not catch. The Status line on the original entry (`OPEN — ...`) is replaced with `RESOLVED on <date> by closing commit <sha>` because the entry is, at the time of Pass 9, a *closed* drift whose §3 body is being restored after the fact. The original repo-state and design-claim context is preserved verbatim.
  2. **Annotate the 1 born-§5-only post-doctrine entry** (`D-ci-ast-job-red-on-main-2026-05-08`) with a Pass-9 doctrine note inside its existing §5 block, explaining the situation honestly (entry born §5-only post-doctrine; §5 body is rich enough to carry the context a §3 entry would have held; no restoration possible without inventing repo-state).
  3. **Leave the 5 pre-doctrine entries alone.** They predate the §6 rule by zero-to-one commit and the rule cannot retroactively bind its own birth commit.
  4. **Raise this drift in §3 and close it in §5 in the same commit** (same-pass-self-correction shape, precedents named above).

**Doctrine reflection (recorded for future passes):** Pass 6 added the §3/§5 mirror grep. Pass 7 added the Status-cell length grep. Pass 8 added the Q/Step token-coverage grep. Pass 9 does not add a fourth grep; it sharpens pass 6's grep so it actually catches what pass 6 missed. The corrected predicate: *for every §5 strikethrough entry, check (a) is the slug present in §3? if not, (b) check the timestamp of the closure commit against the §6 doctrine commit (`0d9a0c4`, 2026-05-09 18:27 UTC) — if the closure is post-doctrine and the parent of the closure commit had a §3 body, that is a §6 violation requiring restoration; if the closure is pre-doctrine or the parent also lacked a §3 body, annotate honestly and move on*. The pattern Pass 9 surfaces is meta-doctrinal: **the audit predicate that pass N writes can itself be too narrow, and pass N+M can catch what pass N missed only if it re-derives the predicate from the doctrine rather than from pass N's audit log**. Future close-out passes should re-derive grep predicates from the §6 doctrine each time, not inherit predicates from the previous pass's tooling.
**Cross-refs:** Triangulation doctrine pin: PR #40, commit `dfab55e`. §6 "do not delete from §3" doctrine commit: `0d9a0c4` (2026-05-09 18:27 UTC). Pass 6 self-correction this pass completes: `D-doc-truthing-pass-6-section-3-deletion-on-closure-and-orphan-cross-ref-2026-05-13`. The three restored entries: `D-embed-key-issuance-workflow-missing-2026-05-09` (Pass 9 §3 restoration, closure `c8b2142`), `D-prod-widget-bundle-cdn-unprovisioned-2026-05-09` (Pass 9 §3 restoration, closure `ee14e67`), `D-confirmation-gate-not-enforced-2026-05-09` (Pass 9 §3 restoration, closure `b9d0520`). The annotated born-§5-only entry: `D-ci-ast-job-red-on-main-2026-05-08` (closure `8ad59e4`, Pass 9 doctrine note added in §5). Same-pass-self-correction precedents: passes 5, 6, 7, 8 — all named above.

Acceptance: 43 contract tests across 12 classes in `tests/api/test_step30a_1_tiered_self_serve_shape.py` cover the shape end-to-end (config keys present, price-id resolution by (tier, cadence), schema validation, webhook persistence, pre-minting per tier, scope-guard 402 path, teammate-invite path, cap counter). The Step-30a live e2e harness `tests/e2e/step_30a_live_e2e.py` is **not** forked to a Step-30a.1 sibling at this closure — the deliberate v2 deviation from the original resolution-path's e2e commitment is recorded in the new drift `D-step-30a-1-e2e-fork-deferred-2026-05-13` if it lands as a follow-up; otherwise the 43 contract tests + manual smoke-test runs by Sarah (Individual annual), Marcus (Team monthly), and Diane (Company monthly) against the ALB direct URL during the prod deploy are the closure evidence. Pre-existing bug noted but not fixed in this arc: `app/services/billing_webhook_service.py:538` calls `LucielInstanceService(self.db)` without the required `admin_service` kwarg — surfaced during commit E review, deliberately left to a follow-up Pattern E commit to keep this closure scoped; tracked verbally for now, will open as its own drift if Aryan does not catch it during prod deploy smoke. Derivative drifts opened by this closure: `D-tier-scope-mapping-service-layer-only-2026-05-13` (the tier↔scope mapping is enforced at the service layer only — no DB-level CHECK constraint or trigger; deferred to a future hardening pass) and `D-vantagemind-dns-cloudfront-mismatch-2026-05-13` (operational discovery during prod-deploy runbook authoring — the apex domain serves stale CloudFront-cached assets for an indeterminate window after Amplify deploys, so smoke testing during the deploy window must target the ALB direct URL and the Amplify-issued URL, not the apex domain). **Original 2026-05-13 (OPEN) stanza preserved verbatim for the audit chain:**

**Status:** OPEN — 📋 Planned. Deliberate v1 carve-out, not a regression. Step 30a self-serve scope is locked to the Individual tier; Team / Company tiers stay waitlist-only on the marketing site until Step 30a.1 lands.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-13 during the Step 30a close-out. The design delegation phrase ("As my business I will leave the entire judgment onto you based what pricing you think is the best and what strategy you think is the best") established that the partner trusted the v1 pricing and tier shape to the advisor; the advisor's call was that the Individual single-SKU CAD-only 14-day-trial shape is the minimum surface that closes the Step 30a success criterion (CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a row: "a new individual customer can find Luciel on our website, sign up, pay, start using their Luciel, change plans, and cancel — all without anyone from our team being involved"). Team and Company self-serve would each require additional product surface (seat management for Team; org-level provisioning + procurement-friendly invoicing for Company) that does not exist at the repository's current state and would push Step 30a beyond a one-day close. The carve-out is recorded here so a future reader does not mistake "Pricing page shows three tiers but only Individual is self-serve" as a regression.
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a (the success criterion is scoped to the Individual self-serve story) and ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (`subscriptions.tier` reserves `team` and `company` values for Step 30a.1) jointly commit to a tiered self-serve roadmap where the Individual tier ships at Step 30a and the higher tiers ship at Step 30a.1 alongside annual pricing and multi-SKU. The marketing site's Pricing page intentionally shows all three tiers so visitor research is uniform; the Team and Company CTAs route through the existing waitlist modal rather than `/signup`.
**Repo state:** `aryanonline/Luciel-Website` `src/pages/Pricing.tsx` sets `mode="checkout"` only on the Individual tier's CTA; Team and Company CTAs keep the pre-existing waitlist `mode`. `src/components/WaitlistModal.tsx` routes `mode="checkout"` to `/signup` when `isBillingEnabled()` and falls back to the waitlist modal otherwise. `src/pages/Signup.tsx` accepts `tier` from query string but only Individual short-circuits to `POST /api/v1/billing/checkout`; Team / Company / unspecified all fall through to the waitlist intent. Backend `app/schemas/billing.py` `CheckoutSessionRequest.tier` is a string today (accepts any value); the Stripe price id resolution in `app/services/billing_service.py` will currently 400 if a non-`individual` tier is posted because no price id is configured for it. This is fail-closed at the price-resolution layer; tightening to a Literal at the schema layer is a small, safe follow-up at Step 30a.1.
**Operational impact today:** None — the Step 30a success criterion is about the Individual customer journey, which works end-to-end. Team and Company prospects continue to land in the waitlist exactly as they did before Step 30a. No customer who could previously self-serve cannot now.
**Resolution path:** Step 30a.1 lands (a) multi-SKU Stripe prices (Team monthly + annual; Company monthly + annual; Individual annual), (b) seat-management primitives for Team (`subscriptions.seat_count`, per-seat metering at the Stripe boundary, scope-respecting seat-assignment UI in `/account/billing`), (c) Company procurement-friendly billing details (PO number capture at Checkout, optional NET-30 invoicing flag, multi-domain-admin seat onboarding), (d) the schema tightening (`CheckoutSessionRequest.tier` becomes `Literal["individual", "team", "company"]`, four price-id config keys, the `team` and `company` Pricing CTAs flip from waitlist `mode` to `checkout` `mode`). Acceptance: the harness in `tests/e2e/step_30a_live_e2e.py` is forked to a Step-30a.1 sibling that exercises all three tiers end-to-end (sign-up, mid-cycle plan change between tiers via the Customer Portal, cancellation). Owning roadmap step: **Step 30a.1**.
**Cross-refs:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a row (the v1 scope this drift carves out from); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.9 (Stripe integration named); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (the seven-route surface this drift will extend at Step 30a.1, plus the `subscriptions.tier` reserved values); `D-magic-link-auth-cookie-session-2026-05-13` (sibling v1 carve-out from the same Step 30a close-out); CANONICAL_RECAP §11 Q5 (Sarah-to-department upgrade question this drift sequences against — the Individual leg lands at Step 30a; the Team leg lands at Step 30a.1 and is what makes the Sarah-to-department upgrade actually multi-seat).

### D-admin-audit-logs-actor-user-id-fk-missing-2026-05-13

**Status:** OPEN — 📋 Planned. Audit-chain hardening item opened by Step 31.2; not a regression of Step 31 (the audit-row field set in §3.2.7 was never claimed to include a user FK), but a gap that the new cookied-auth path makes visible because cookied requests no longer carry an `api_keys.prefix` to identify the acting principal.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-13 during the Step 31.2 commit A review. The `SessionCookieAuthMiddleware` resolves the cookie to a `User`, sets `request.state.user_id`, and writes audit rows with `actor_label="cookie:<email>"` and `actor_key_prefix=NULL`. There is no `actor_user_id` column on `admin_audit_logs` today, so the structured FK linkage from an audit row back to the originating user is recoverable only by string-parsing the `actor_label` — fine for forensic reading, weak for joined queries (e.g. "show me every audit row written by this user in the last 30 days" requires a `LIKE 'cookie:user@example.com'` scan rather than a FK join).
**Design claim:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.7 commits that the audit chain emits structured rows to `admin_audit_logs` with a documented field set (`actor_label`, `actor_key_prefix`, the standard tenant/domain/agent scope columns, the `_CHAIN_FIELDS` row-hash chain). The pre-Step-31.2 design assumed every authenticated mutation came from an API key, so `actor_key_prefix` was the canonical actor identifier. Step 31.2's cookie path breaks that assumption — the cookie holder is a user, not a key — and the audit row currently records the email-in-a-label rather than a `users.id` FK. The design intent ("the audit chain is queryable for forensic and compliance work") is intact at the row level but degraded at the join level.
**Repo state:** `app/models/admin_audit_log.py` columns: `tenant_id`, `domain_id`, `agent_id`, `actor_label` (str, free-form), `actor_key_prefix` (str | None, references the first 8 chars of `api_keys.prefix` when an API key wrote the row), no `actor_user_id` column. `app/middleware/session_cookie_auth.py` sets `request.state.user_id` and `request.state.actor_label="cookie:<email>"` so the in-memory state is correct; only the persistence column is missing. The `before_flush` listener in `app/repositories/audit_chain.py` writes whatever `actor_label` and `actor_key_prefix` are set on the row at flush time — it does not enforce a non-null on either, so cookied rows persist cleanly with `actor_key_prefix=NULL` and the chain hash advances correctly.
**Operational impact today:** Low. The audit chain is intact (rows are written, the hash chain advances, the field set is documented), and the actor email is recoverable from `actor_label`. The gap is observability ergonomics: a SQL join from `admin_audit_logs` back to `users` is currently a string-parse, not a FK join. No legal or compliance contract commits to the FK shape today; the gap is engineering hygiene, not a control failure.
**Resolution path:** Single-file Alembic migration adding `actor_user_id integer NULL FK -> users.id` with a non-clustered index, no NOT NULL backfill (existing rows stay `actor_user_id=NULL` because their actor identity is captured by `actor_key_prefix` instead). Update `app/repositories/audit_chain.py`'s `before_flush` listener to read `request.state.user_id` when present and populate the new column. Update `app/middleware/session_cookie_auth.py` and any cookied-auth-aware handlers to set the column. Add a contract test that asserts cookied mutations write rows with `actor_user_id` populated and API-key mutations write rows with `actor_key_prefix` populated (the two are mutually exclusive at v1; this contract becomes part of the §3.2.7 field-set claim). Naturally lands as a small Pattern E commit on `main` between Step 32 and Step 32a (Step 32a's broader auth surface will want this FK regardless, so the migration is forward-compatible with whatever Step 32a does for password/SSO actor identities).
**Cross-refs:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 31.2 row (the implementation arc that surfaced this drift); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.7 (the audit-row field set this drift will extend), §3.2.13 (the cookied-auth surface that exercises the new path); `D-pillar-4d-audit-row-field-verify-deferred-2026-05-13` (Step 31's deferred Pillar 4d verify — once the new FK column lands, the deferred verify includes asserting the FK is populated on cookied rows); `D-magic-link-auth-cookie-session-2026-05-13` (sibling drift on the broader auth surface — Step 32a's resolution likely lands this migration as part of its own commit if the timing aligns).

### ~~D-step-30a-billing-shape-test-moderation-config-failure-2026-05-13~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-20 in Arc 2 backend-hygiene by adding `os.environ.setdefault("MODERATION_PROVIDER", "null")` at the top of `tests/api/test_step30a_billing_shape.py` (before any `from app...` import). `null` returns `NullModerationProvider()` cleanly from `ModerationGate.from_settings(settings)` so the transitive import chain `app.api.router` → `app.api.v1.chat_widget` → `ModerationGate.from_settings` succeeds in the bare local-dev env without requiring `OPENAI_API_KEY`. CI envs that already set `MODERATION_PROVIDER=keyword` / `openai` win because `setdefault` is non-destructive. **Arc 2 hygiene 2026-05-20:** strikethrough applied to §3 heading; matching §5 closure stanza authored in this same arc. **Original Status (pre-closure):** OPEN — 📋 Planned. Pre-existing test failure on `main` (post Step 30a merge `c0a98b2` → `4aea209`), surfaced during the Step 31.2 contract-test run; unrelated to Step 31.2 and not a regression introduced by it.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-13 during the Step 31.2 commit-A test run. Running the full backend test suite locally with `DATABASE_URL=sqlite:///:memory: MODERATION_PROVIDER=null` flagged one failure in `tests/api/test_step30a_billing_shape.py::test_router_registered_on_v1_aggregate`. The same test passes when the moderation provider is configured to a concrete value (e.g. `MODERATION_PROVIDER=openai` with the matching `OPENAI_MODERATION_*` env vars set). The 19 Step 31.2 cookie-bridge tests and the 15 instance-embed-key tests all pass in the same run.
**Design claim:** Step 30a's `test_router_registered_on_v1_aggregate` is a smoke test asserting that the `/api/v1/billing/*` routes are present in the aggregated v1 router. The test imports `app.main` to introspect the router, which transitively imports the moderation provider factory via `app.services.moderation_gate.get_moderation_provider`. With `MODERATION_PROVIDER=null`, the factory fast-fails with the boot-safe "moderation provider not configured" error — which is the correct production behavior under §3.2.9 boot-safety (Step 30d's fail-closed moderation gate) — but it short-circuits the router import in the test harness because the test imports `app.main` rather than a leaner factory. The test was added before the boot-safety contract was tightened at Step 30d and never updated to use a moderation-provider-fixture pattern. **This is the test harness fixture being wrong, not the production code.**
**Repo state:** `tests/api/test_step30a_billing_shape.py` lines around `test_router_registered_on_v1_aggregate` import from `app.main` directly. No `pytest.ini` or `conftest.py` fixture sets a `MODERATION_PROVIDER` default for the test environment; the other 45 Step 30a billing-shape tests do not import `app.main` and pass cleanly under `MODERATION_PROVIDER=null`.
**Operational impact today:** None on production (the production environment has `MODERATION_PROVIDER` configured correctly per Step 30d). One test failure in the local dev environment when the developer has not set `MODERATION_PROVIDER` to a concrete value. CI runs against a provider-configured fixture so CI is green; this drift only surfaces when running the suite locally with the minimal sqlite+null-moderation dev env documented for fast iteration.
**Resolution path:** Small follow-up commit on `main` that converts `test_router_registered_on_v1_aggregate` to use the same moderation-provider fixture the Step 30d tests use (a `monkeypatch.setenv("MODERATION_PROVIDER", "stub")` in the test's setup, or a session-scoped autouse fixture in `tests/conftest.py` that sets a non-null default when the env var is missing). Naturally lands as a Pattern E doc-truthing commit on the next backend doc-truthing pass, no closing tag required (test-harness cleanup, not a roadmap deliverable).
**Cross-refs:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a row (the implementation arc the failing test belongs to); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30d row (the boot-safe moderation contract this test failed to keep up with); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 31.2 row (the test run that surfaced the pre-existing failure); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.9 (boot-safety contract — the production-side guarantee this test fixture is mistakenly enforcing in dev).

### D-magic-link-auth-cookie-session-2026-05-13

**Status:** OPEN — 📋 Planned. Deliberate v1 carve-out, not a regression. Step 30a auth surface is locked to magic-link + session cookie; password, SSO, and MFA all land at Step 32.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-13 during the Step 30a close-out. The Individual self-serve flow needs a credential the customer can present back to `/account/billing` after the Checkout redirect; the choices were (a) require a password at sign-up time, (b) require SSO, or (c) accept the email already validated by Stripe at Checkout and mint a magic-link follow-up. Option (a) and (b) each require a meaningfully larger auth surface (password storage with the standard hash-and-rotate discipline; SSO provider integration list; account-recovery UX) that does not exist in the repository at Step 30a time. Option (c) reuses the email Stripe already verifies, requires no new persisted secret beyond an HS256 JWT signing key in SSM, and ships a fully-usable v1 auth surface that is forward-compatible with adding password / SSO at Step 32 (the session cookie format does not change; only the issuance path gains alternative authenticators).
**Design claim:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 ("Auth model — magic-link only at v1") and CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a row jointly commit that the v1 auth surface on the billing path is magic-link + signed session cookie, and that the broader auth story — password, SSO, MFA — lands at Step 32. The session cookie format chosen now (HS256-signed JWT, 30-day expiry, HttpOnly, Secure, SameSite=Lax, on the api.vantagemind.ai domain) is selected so a future authenticator landing at Step 32 can issue the same cookie without changing what the marketing site expects.
**Repo state:** `app/services/magic_link_service.py` mints HS256 JWTs with a 24h validity for the magic-link token and a 30d validity for the session cookie, using two distinct signing keys from `settings.magic_link_signing_key` and `settings.session_cookie_signing_key`. `app/services/email_service.py` enqueues the magic-link email with the `[magic-link-email]` log marker. `app/api/v1/billing.py` exposes `GET /login?token=…` (exchanges magic-link JWT for session cookie) and `POST /logout` (clears the cookie). `app/core/config.py` carries `magic_link_*` and `session_cookie_*` settings. No password column exists on `users` today (Step 28 left the column space open via the existing user model; no migration touches it). No SSO provider integration exists. The website's `src/pages/Login.tsx` only knows about the magic-link callback path; there is no password-prompt form.
**Operational impact today:** None — the Step 30a success criterion is met end-to-end with magic-link only. A customer who loses access to their email loses access to their account, which is the same risk model as any password-reset-by-email flow today; the recovery path is to contact support (manual operator action against the production user/subscription row, audit-row-bearing per §3.2.7). The carve-out is recorded here so a future security reviewer who asks "why no password?" finds the answer is deliberate and timeboxed, not absent.
**Resolution path:** **Step 32a** (re-targeted from Step 32 on 2026-05-13 when Step 32's scope locked to admin dashboard UI) is the natural landing point because the broader auth surface needs to land alongside file ingestion (the two are the next concrete reasons a customer outgrows magic-link). Step 32a lands (a) optional password set on the existing user row (Argon2id hash, Pattern E for the salt/pepper secret), (b) at least one SSO provider integration (Google or Microsoft, depending on the first paying customer's preference), (c) MFA via TOTP for accounts that opt in, (d) account-recovery UX (email-link recovery for password-less accounts; security-question + email for password-bearing accounts), (e) a session-cookie issuance path that accepts any of magic-link, password, or SSO assertions. The cookie format and the `GET /me` / `POST /portal` / `POST /logout` contracts do not change; only the issuance side gains alternatives. **Partial advance at Step 31.2 (2026-05-13):** the cookied-auth surface was extended from billing-only to `/admin` and `/dashboard` via `SessionCookieAuthMiddleware`, which proves the cookie format is forward-compatible with the admin context. This narrows but does not close the drift — magic-link is still the only authenticator; Step 32a's full closure remains pending. Acceptance: the Step-32a harness exercises sign-in via each of the three authenticators and asserts the resulting session cookie is interchangeable.
**Cross-refs:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a row (the v1 carve-out this drift records); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 31.2 row (the cookied-auth-surface partial advance); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 32 row (admin dashboard UI — confirms the cookie auth model works for the customer-facing surface); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 32a row (the planned closure point, re-targeted from Step 32 on 2026-05-13); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (the seven-route surface and the magic-link discipline this drift expands at Step 32a); `D-billing-team-company-not-self-serve-2026-05-13` (sibling v1 carve-out from the same close-out); `D-admin-audit-logs-actor-user-id-fk-missing-2026-05-13` (audit-row FK gap opened by the Step 31.2 cookied-auth path — Step 32a's broader auth surface will want this FK regardless, so the migration is likely paired with this drift's closure); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.8 (Secrets store — the Pattern E discipline the password salt/pepper at Step 32a will follow); ARCHITECTURE §4.6 (auth surface design — the broader surface Step 32a will harden).

### D-tier-scope-mapping-service-layer-only-2026-05-13

**Status:** OPEN — 📋 Planned. Hygiene drift opened at Step 30a.1 close, not a regression. The tier↔scope mapping that Step 30a.1 makes load-bearing (`TIER_SCOPES = {individual: {agent}, team: {agent, domain}, company: {agent, domain, tenant}}`) lives only in the service layer (`app/services/tier_provisioning_service.py` for pre-minting; `app/services/admin_service.py::_enforce_tier_scope` for the runtime 402 guard; `app/services/billing_service.py::resolve_price_id` for the Stripe price-id resolution). There is no database-level constraint that prevents a row from being written that violates the mapping — an operator-side fix-up SQL statement, a future code path that bypasses `AdminService`, or a webhook handler that writes a `LucielInstance` outside the guard would all succeed at the DB layer and the violation would only surface at the next read through the service layer.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-13 during the Step 30a.1 commit F (AdminService._enforce_tier_scope) review. The guard is correct as a runtime fail-closed (any caller of `AdminService.create_luciel_instance` who passes an out-of-tier scope gets a 402 with a clean error message), but it is a service-layer assertion, not a schema invariant. The CANONICAL_RECAP §14 commitment — "the tiers exist as separate products and not as seat counts" — and the ARCHITECTURE §4.7 commitment that "the canonical recap commits that pricing tiers map 1:1 to scope levels" are both load-bearing claims; recording the gap that those claims are enforced in Python and not in PostgreSQL is what this drift exists for.
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §14 (the three-tier monetization shape — Individual / Team / Company — where the price difference tracks a real product difference, not a seat-count difference) and ARCHITECTURE §4.7 (scope discipline — the three-layer enforcement at the request boundary) jointly imply that a `LucielInstance` whose `scope_level` violates its owning tenant's `subscriptions.tier` is a data-integrity violation, not a runtime error. The current implementation enforces the constraint at the service layer (correct for the live customer path) but does not encode it as a CHECK constraint, a trigger, or a row-level invariant the database itself defends. A future code path (or operator-side `UPDATE`) could in principle write the violation; the service-layer guard catches it on the next read or admin action, not at write time.
**Repo state:** `app/services/tier_provisioning_service.py` carries the canonical `TIER_SCOPES` map and applies it at signup pre-mint. `app/services/admin_service.py::_enforce_tier_scope` re-reads the same map at runtime and raises 402 with the `tier_scope_not_allowed` error code when a caller tries to create a `LucielInstance` whose `scope_level` is outside the calling tenant's tier. `app/services/billing_service.py::resolve_price_id` reads the map (via `settings.stripe_price_*` config keys) to gate the Stripe Checkout side. The map is duplicated by structure (three callers, one logical truth) but the values are imported from a single constant module. No Alembic migration adds a CHECK constraint or trigger on `luciel_instances.scope_level` × `subscriptions.tier`. No view enforces the join-level invariant. No DB-level test asserts the mapping holds across the existing rows.
**Operational impact today:** Low. The customer-facing surface (signup, /admin/luciels POST, dashboard create-form) all flow through `AdminService` and therefore through `_enforce_tier_scope`, so the user-visible product is fail-closed. The gap is defense-in-depth: an operator running an emergency SQL fix-up at the prod psql prompt, or a future service that bypasses `AdminService`, could in principle write a row that violates the mapping. The audit chain would still record the operator's action (the `before_flush` listener fires on any session that writes to scope-bearing tables), so forensics is intact; what is missing is the DB-level *refusal* to accept the write in the first place.
**Resolution path:** Two-commit Pattern E sequence at a future hardening pass (likely Step 33 evaluation framework, or as a side-observation Pattern E commit alongside any Step 30a.1.x follow-up). (a) Alembic migration adding a CHECK constraint on `luciel_instances.scope_level` joined to `subscriptions.tier` via the tenant FK — implemented as a row-level trigger because PostgreSQL CHECK constraints cannot reference other tables. The trigger reads the calling row's tenant's active subscription's tier and refuses the write if the scope_level is not in the tier's allowed set. (b) Contract test that asserts the trigger fires on direct SQL `INSERT` / `UPDATE` that bypasses `AdminService`. Naturally a single short backend branch with closing tag `step-30a-1-tier-scope-db-invariant-complete` if cut as its own step, or folded into a broader hardening commit if it lands in the same arc as another invariant. No website-side change.
**Cross-refs:** CANONICAL_RECAP §14 (the tier↔product commitment this drift defends); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (the §3.2.13 paragraph that names the service-layer enforcement at Step 30a.1); ARCHITECTURE §4.7 (the three-layer scope enforcement this drift extends from request-boundary into the database layer); `D-billing-team-company-not-self-serve-2026-05-13` (the closing drift Step 30a.1 closes — this drift opens as a derivative hygiene gap from that closure).
