On first live cancellation: (a) Stripe fires `customer.subscription.deleted` to `https://api.vantagemind.ai/api/v1/billing/webhook`; (b) the handler 500s on the `TypeError`; (c) Stripe retries up to 3 days per its delivery-retry schedule, every retry 500s; (d) the customer canceled in their portal but the backend keeps their tenant active — they continue to be able to log in and use the product without paying. Severity: high on the financial-integrity surface (cancel ≠ cancel) but no security implication (the customer canceled themselves; we just fail to enforce the cancel). The audit-log path is partially preserved (the inbound event is logged at the webhook router before the handler enters), so post-hoc recovery via manual `deactivate_tenant_with_cascade` invocation is possible, but operationally undesirable.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.2 Phase D (the drift surfaces in this step's pre-GATE-4 audit and the fix lands in this step's closing-tag commit). No retroactive owning step is opened against the step that introduced `LucielInstanceService` — the drift was latent at that step's closure and §12 stays preserved per Pass 9 doctrine. The drift surfaces now because GATE 4 smoke-with-cancel would have been the first time the handler ran on a real `customer.subscription.deleted` event.
**Resolution path:** Pattern E surgical edit in `app/services/billing_webhook_service.py:552`. Change `LucielInstanceService(self.db)` to `LucielInstanceService(self.db, admin_service=admin)` — `admin` is the `AdminService(self.db)` instance already constructed on line 549, four lines earlier in the same function. Add an inline comment with the drift ID and a brief explanation of why the kwarg is required (the constructor signature is keyword-only). GATE 1 commit + push; image build (combined with the `D-email-service-log-only-no-real-delivery-2026-05-14` fix in the same `step30a2-<new-sha>-r4` image); `:50` task-def cloning `:49` with the new image; GATE 2 redeploy; GATE 4 cancel-and-refund-after-each-checkout smoke verifies the cascade runs without `TypeError`.
**Pattern E:** Pure additive on the call-site (one new kwarg) and additive comment. Zero modification to `LucielInstanceService` itself, zero modification to `AdminService`, zero modification to any other webhook-handler call site. The fix is a one-line change with a multi-line drift-ID comment block. The `:50` task-def revision is byte-identical to `:49` except for the image tag and the 2 env entries from `D-email-service-log-only-no-real-delivery-2026-05-14`.
**Cross-refs:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.2 row (the cancellation-cascade claim this drift names); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (Billing surface — the webhook handler as single cascade entry point); `D-cancellation-cascade-incomplete-conversations-claims-2026-05-14` (the parent drift on the broader cascade completeness; this drift is one of its constituent fixes); `D-email-service-log-only-no-real-delivery-2026-05-14` (sibling drift, same `step30a2-<new-sha>-r4` image, same `:50` task-def); `app/services/luciel_instance_service.py` (the constructor signature, unchanged); `app/services/billing_webhook_service.py:552` (the call-site fix); `td-backend-rev50.json` (the additive revision).

### D-ses-sandbox-mode-pending-production-access-2026-05-14

**Status:** OPEN — tracking drift opened by Step 30a.2 Phase C; closes when AWS grants SES production access (24–72h SLA after manual operator submission via SES console).
**Section that raised it:** Step 30a.2 Phase C-1 (SES domain identity creation), opened 2026-05-14 ~9:30 PM EDT when the SES domain identity for `vantagemind.ai` was created in the `ca-central-1` region. The account's SES default state is sandbox mode, which constrains outbound delivery to verified-recipient-only and caps daily volume at 200 / 24h and 1/sec.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-14 during the Step 30a.2 Phase C SES setup. The drift is deliberately opened (not discovered) because the sandbox-mode constraint is a known SES default that requires an explicit production-access request to lift.
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.1 row (tiered self-serve signup) requires magic-link email delivery to arbitrary customer email addresses, not just verified-sandbox recipients. The signup flow is the first customer-facing surface that requires lifted-sandbox delivery; until production access is granted, signup is restricted to operator-pre-verified recipients only.
**Repo state at the time of raise:** Code is fully ready for production-mode SES (the `email_service.py` rewrite landing in the same Step 30a.2 Phase D commit calls `sesv2.send_email` with no sandbox-aware branching — it sends to any address). The IAM policy `LucielSESSendEmail` (attached in Phase C-5) is also production-ready (the resource ARN is the verified domain identity, not the per-recipient identity that sandbox would require). The only gate is the AWS-side sandbox flag on the account's SES sending state. The verified domain identity `vantagemind.ai` shows `DKIM Status: SUCCESS` and `VerifiedForSendingStatus: True`; the verified sandbox recipient `aryans.www@gmail.com` shows `VerificationStatus: SUCCESS`.
**Operational impact at the time of raise:** Zero customer impact today (no live signups; the sandbox recipient is the operator's own gmail and is verified). GATE 4 live-smoke can run against the sandbox recipient and exercise the full signup→checkout→magic-link→onboarding→cancel-refund loop. The drift's open state explicitly names what GATE 4 does NOT cover: delivery to non-sandbox-verified recipients. First-live-customer launch is gated on closure of this drift.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.2 (the drift is opened in this step's Phase C and remains open across the Step 30a.2 closing tag; it does not block GATE 5 because GATE 5 closes Step 30a.2 as code-complete-on-prod for the sandbox-recipient surface). The drift's closure is owned by Step 30a.3 (or a successor) when the operator's SES production-access request is granted. The 2026-05-14 annotation on the Step 30a.2 row in CANONICAL_RECAP §12 explicitly names the sandbox-mode constraint as a known limitation at closure.
**Resolution path:** Operator-manual step — submit a Production Access Request via the SES console at `https://console.aws.amazon.com/ses/home?region=ca-central-1#/account`. The pre-drafted use-case description includes: (a) mail type = transactional; (b) website URL = `https://www.vantagemind.ai`; (c) use case = magic-link login emails for an AI-powered real estate CRM SaaS product (Luciel/VantageMind); (d) expected volume = under 200 emails/day at launch, scaling to ~1000/day within 6 months; (e) bounce/complaint handling = SES default complaint/bounce notifications routed to operator email, hard bounces flagged in the customer DB; (f) opt-out = magic-link emails are transactional (not marketing), no opt-out required, but customer can delete account to stop all transactional email. AWS SLA for review is typically 24h but documented up to 72h. On grant, the drift closes with the AWS case ID written into the closure stanza in §5. No code change, no task-def change, no IAM change required for closure — the account-level sandbox flag flip is sufficient.
**Pattern E:** Pure tracking — no code, infra, or task-def change is owned by this drift's closure. The closure is an external-state-flip event (AWS grants production access) recorded as a §5 closure stanza with the AWS case ID. This is the same drift shape as `D-stripe-live-account-not-yet-activated-2026-05-13` (Stripe activation request, closed when Stripe approves) — tracking drifts for external-service-approval gates.
**Cross-refs:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.1 row (the customer-facing signup surface this drift names as gated on lifted sandbox); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.2 row (the closing step that opens this drift); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (Billing/Auth surface — the email-delivery contract this drift names as scoped to sandbox-verified recipients until closure); `D-email-service-log-only-no-real-delivery-2026-05-14` (the upstream drift this drift partners — the email service is real-delivery, but constrained to sandbox recipients); `D-stripe-live-account-not-yet-activated-2026-05-13` (sibling tracking drift shape — external-service-approval gate); `https://console.aws.amazon.com/ses/home?region=ca-central-1#/account` (the SES console where the operator submits the production-access request); `https://docs.aws.amazon.com/ses/latest/dg/request-production-access.html` (the AWS doc naming the sandbox-to-production transition path).

### ~~D-stripe-event-dict-conversion-python314-2026-05-15~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-15 by Step 30a.2-pilot Commit 3e (backend). Entry retained in §3 with strikethrough per §6 (move-to-§5 with strikethrough, do **not** delete from §3).
**Closing commit:** Step 30a.2-pilot Commit 3e (`app/api/v1/billing.py` + `pyproject.toml` + `tests/api/test_step30a_2_pilot_webhook_dict.py`).
**Section that raised it:** GATE 4 Path B Pass 2 live smoke (`pilot.todo §11`). The first real CA$100 live Stripe Checkout completed at 2026-05-15 18:36:43 EDT (`cs_live_b1WY2q27nRtE9CwYwvq7JsRf4BKD3CDkNOhRrNOZEoecvlUmGt4g6PZM8Q`). Stripe POSTed `checkout.session.completed` to the production webhook at 22:38:18 UTC. The handler responded 500 and Stripe retried at 22:38:34 UTC — also 500. No customer / subscription / audit row was written; no magic-link email was minted.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-15 22:50 UTC after Aryan pulled the full traceback from CloudWatch via `aws logs start-query` (the `aws logs filter-log-events --filter-pattern` path was blocked by the reserved `[` character in the `[magic-link-email]` literal). The traceback proved the failure shape line-for-line.
**Design claim:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (Billing/Auth surface) and CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a row (self-serve subscription billing) require `POST /api/v1/billing/webhook` to accept a Stripe-signed event payload, materialise it into a plain `dict`, dispatch to `BillingWebhookService.handle()`, and return 200 idempotently. The contract test `tests/api/test_step30a_billing_shape.py::TestBillingWebhookDispatch` pins the handler's dispatch table and the four event-type branches it must cover.
**Repo state at the time of raise:** `app/api/v1/billing.py:201` called `BillingWebhookService(db).handle(dict(event))`. The `event` argument is a `stripe.StripeObject` (returned by `stripe.Webhook.construct_event()` after signature verification). On the production image (Python 3.14, `stripe==15.1.0`, `python:3.14-slim` base), `dict(event)` raised `KeyError(0)` because `StripeObject.__getitem__` correctly rejects positional-index probes that CPython's `dict()` constructor performs during one of its iteration code paths. The defect did not surface on Python 3.13 because the older iteration protocol only called `__getitem__` for the string keys yielded by `__iter__`.
**Operational impact at the time of raise:** Real money loop broken. CA$100 charged successfully (Stripe receipt landed in Aryan's inbox); Stripe customer + subscription objects created server-side at Stripe; **but** the backend webhook 500'd, so no `subscriptions` row, no `users` row, no `admin_audit_log` row, and no magic-link email was sent. Stripe's automatic webhook retry policy (up to 3 days with exponential backoff) means the reconciliation loop is not lost — once the handler accepts the next retry, the DB-side state will fill in atomically. Sibling drift `D-ses-sandbox-mode-pending-production-access-2026-05-14` is also blocking magic-link delivery (the recipient identity `aryans.www@gmail.com` was created but `VerifiedForSendingStatus: None`); the two drifts are independent — fixing this one unblocks DB writes, fixing the SES one unblocks email delivery.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.2-pilot (Commit 3e is the eighth commit in this step's chain: 3a docs lock, 3b backend `/pilot-refund`, 3c backend `/me` pilot signal + website pilot surface, 3d backend CORS + website pricing CTA fix, 3e backend webhook materialisation fix). Closure of this drift unblocks GATE 4 Path B Step 2.2 (live self-serve refund) and Step 2.3 (live repeat-customer block) which both depend on a working DB-side reconciliation loop.
**Resolution:** `dict(event)` replaced with a version-resilient materialisation chain. Primary path: `json.loads(str(event))` — uses the SDK's own recursive serializer via `StripeObject.__str__` (present since v1.x), so the materialisation does not depend on any private API name. Fallback: `getattr(event, 'to_dict_recursive', getattr(event, '_to_dict_recursive', None))` — covers every SDK major from 10.x (public `to_dict_recursive`) to 15.x (underscored `_to_dict_recursive`). Last-ditch defence: `HTTPException(500)` if neither name resolves (logged loudly so Stripe retries land in CloudWatch with the alert marker visible). Belt-and-suspenders: `pyproject.toml` stripe pin tightened to `>=10.0.0,<16` (D-stripe-sdk-major-pin-2026-05-15) so a future SDK major rev cannot silently regress this on the next image rebuild. 10 AST/text regression cases land in `tests/api/test_step30a_2_pilot_webhook_dict.py` covering: removal of executable `dict(event)`, `json` import presence, primary-path text + AST presence, fallback chain presence (both name forms probed), drift markers present in source, stripe `<16` pin in pyproject, materialisation precedes `handle()`.
**Pattern E:** Additive. `dict(event)` is replaced 1-for-1 with `event_dict = json.loads(str(event))` followed by `handle(event_dict)`; the comment block and fallback `try`/`except` are net new. The `stripe<16` upper bound narrows the resolution range but does not exclude the version currently installed (15.1.0). No schema change, no migration, no IAM change, no SSM change.
**Validation evidence:** Standalone repro at `/tmp/webhook_dict_validation_v2.py` (sandbox, stripe 15.1.0): `dict(event)` raises `KeyError(0)` matching prod traceback line-for-line; `json.loads(str(event))` returns full nested plain dict with every key `BillingWebhookService.handle()` reads (`id`, `type`, `data.object.subscription`, `data.object.customer`, `data.object.customer_email`, `data.object.customer_details.email`, `data.object.metadata.luciel_email`, `.luciel_tier`, `.luciel_billing_cadence`, `.luciel_display_name`, `.intro_fee`, `.trial_days`); `getattr` fallback resolves to `_to_dict_recursive` on stripe 15.1.0 and produces equivalent output. `pytest tests/api/test_step30a_2_pilot_webhook_dict.py` = 10/10 pass. Production verification deferred to GATE 2 round 4 (build `luciel-backend:55`, register td, roll service, verify Stripe's automatic retry returns 200 within the 3-day retry window).
**Cross-refs:** CloudWatch traceback timestamps 2026-05-15 22:38:18 and 22:38:34 UTC, log group `/ecs/luciel-backend`. Stripe live checkout session `cs_live_b1WY2q27nRtE9CwYwvq7JsRf4BKD3CDkNOhRrNOZEoecvlUmGt4g6PZM8Q`. Sibling drift `D-stripe-sdk-major-pin-2026-05-15` (same commit, pyproject upper-bound). Sibling drift `D-ses-sandbox-mode-pending-production-access-2026-05-14` (independent blocker on email delivery; resolved by AWS console action, not code). Predecessor drift `D-webhook-luciel-instance-service-missing-kwarg-2026-05-14` (different webhook bug class, also resolved in the Step 30a.2 chain). CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.2-pilot row will name this drift's closure in the same commit. ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (Billing/Auth surface — webhook materialisation contract).

### ~~D-stripe-sdk-major-pin-2026-05-15~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-15 by Step 30a.2-pilot Commit 3e (backend). Same commit as sibling `D-stripe-event-dict-conversion-python314-2026-05-15`. Entry retained in §3 with strikethrough per §6.
**Closing commit:** Step 30a.2-pilot Commit 3e (`pyproject.toml` only — line `"stripe>=10.0.0,<16"`).
**Section that raised it:** GATE 1 review of Commit 3e (sibling drift's resolution). The sibling drift's traceback surfaced that the materialisation method name on `stripe.StripeObject` shifted between SDK majors: 10.x–12.x had the public `to_dict_recursive`, 13.x renamed it to the underscored `_to_dict_recursive`. The Commit 3e primary path (`json.loads(str(event))`) does not depend on either name, but the existence of that rename means a future SDK major could break some other contract the backend relies on (transport, type signature, retry semantics) without surfacing in the test suite — because `pyproject.toml` pinned only a lower bound (`stripe>=10.0.0`) with no upper bound.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-15 during GATE 1 review of Commit 3e. The drift is deliberately opened-and-closed in the same commit because the resolution (the upper-bound pin) is the same line of code as the discovery.
**Design claim:** Dependency pinning doctrine — every load-bearing third-party library must have an upper bound below the next-major version. The repo's current pyproject already does this for FastAPI, SQLAlchemy, Alembic, pydantic, etc.; Stripe was the conspicuous exception because the original Step 30a author treated it as a thin wrapper around a stable HTTP API. The 13.x rename of `to_dict_recursive` proves that Stripe's Python SDK does in fact break compatibility across majors, so it must be treated like every other pinned dependency.
**Repo state at the time of raise:** `pyproject.toml` line 34 reads `"stripe>=10.0.0",` with no upper bound. The currently-resolved version in the production image is 15.1.0 (confirmed by `docker run --rm <image> python -c "import stripe; print(stripe.VERSION)"` on the running image digest `sha256:5c0c0328`). The next rebuild of the image would resolve to whatever the latest published Stripe SDK is at that moment — currently 15.1.0, but possibly 16.x or 17.x by the time the next image is built.
**Operational impact at the time of raise:** No active impact (the running image is 15.1.0 and Commit 3e's primary path is version-independent). The drift is preventive — it closes a latent regression channel before the next image rebuild.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.2-pilot Commit 3e (closed in the same commit that raised it).
**Resolution:** `pyproject.toml` line 34 changes from `"stripe>=10.0.0",` to `"stripe>=10.0.0,<16",` with a four-line comment block naming the rationale (the 13.x rename, the Commit 3e materialisation neutralisation, the upper-bound discipline, and this drift slug). The regression test `TestStripeSdkUpperBoundPin::test_stripe_pinned_below_16` in `tests/api/test_step30a_2_pilot_webhook_dict.py` pins the bound via regex against the pyproject text.
**Pattern E:** Pure tightening. The bound moves from open-ended to capped at `<16`; the currently-resolved version (15.1.0) sits inside the new bound, so the next image rebuild produces the same SDK version. No behaviour change, no schema change, no migration.
**Validation evidence:** `pytest tests/api/test_step30a_2_pilot_webhook_dict.py::TestStripeSdkUpperBoundPin` = 1/1 pass. `python -c "import stripe; print(stripe.VERSION)"` against the current `requirements`-equivalent resolution returns `15.1.0` — inside the new bound.
**Cross-refs:** Sibling drift `D-stripe-event-dict-conversion-python314-2026-05-15` (same commit; the materialisation fix that this pin defends in depth). The Stripe SDK 13.x changelog entry that renamed `to_dict_recursive` to `_to_dict_recursive` (`https://github.com/stripe/stripe-python/blob/master/CHANGELOG.md`). Repo dependency-pinning precedent: `pyproject.toml` upper bounds on FastAPI (`<1.0`), SQLAlchemy (`<3`), pydantic (`<3`), alembic (`<2`).

### ~~D-stripe-webhook-checkout-vs-subscription-field-source-2026-05-15~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-15 by Step 30a.2-pilot Commit 3f (backend). Entry retained in §3 with strikethrough per §6.
**Raised by:** Direct DB inspection of the first live $100 pilot purchase row (sub_1TXUN1RytQVRVXw7wmsfATXJ) after Commit 3e shipped: subscription row had `status="complete"` (not a valid Stripe Subscription status — that is `checkout.session.status`), `trial_end=null`, and `current_period_start/end=null`. The Subscription object on Stripe carried the correct `trialing` status and `trial_end ~= 2026-08-13`, but the webhook handler had never read them off it.
**Design claim:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 commits the Subscription row's fields (`status`, `trial_end`, `current_period_start/end`) to mirror the canonical Stripe Subscription state at all times, with `customer.subscription.updated` as the load-bearing backfill. The Step 30a.2-pilot pilot signal additionally derives from `provider_snapshot.metadata.luciel_intro_applied` together with `sub.trial_end` so the Account UI can render the pilot ribbon and refund CTA. Implicit in this claim is that the *initial write* of the Subscription row (on `checkout.session.completed`) MUST also mirror the canonical state — otherwise a buyer who hits `/me` before the next `subscription.updated` event arrives sees an inconsistent view.
**Repo state:** `app/services/billing_webhook_service.py::_on_checkout_completed` read `status`, `trial_end`, `current_period_start/end`, `cancel_at_period_end`, and `canceled_at` directly from `data_object` (the inline `checkout.session` payload). The `checkout.session` object has NONE of those fields with Subscription-side semantics: `status` is the session's own status (`complete` / `expired` / `open`), the period fields moved to subscription items in basil 2025-03-31 (see `D-stripe-subscription-period-fields-moved-to-items-2026-05-14`), and `trial_end` simply doesn't exist on `checkout.session` at all. The bug was latent until live-mode activation because the test fixtures used in `test_billing_webhook_service.py` stub `data_object` with all required Subscription fields pre-populated.
**Operational impact today:** Medium. The single live $100 pilot row from 2026-05-15 18:36 EDT had `is_pilot=false` at `/me` because the `is_pilot` derivation also required `trial_end is not None` (closed separately by `D-pilot-is-pilot-metadata-driven-2026-05-15`). The pilot ribbon and refund CTA never rendered. The buyer could still log in, would see the wrong status string, and would have no self-serve refund path — forcing operator-mediated Stripe Dashboard refunds during the pilot window, which is exactly the operational regression Step 30a.2-pilot was designed to close.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.2-pilot Commit 3f (closed in the same commit that raised it).
**Resolution:** Three coordinated changes ship in Commit 3f. (1) `app/integrations/stripe/client.py` gains `retrieve_subscription(subscription_id)` — a one-line wrapper around `stripe.Subscription.retrieve`. (2) `app/services/billing_webhook_service.py::_on_checkout_completed` calls `self.stripe.retrieve_subscription(stripe_subscription_id)` immediately after the idempotency check, wraps the call in `try/except Exception` so a Stripe-side transient failure degrades to the inline data (Stripe MUST receive a 200 to stop redelivering), and routes `status`, `trial_end`, `current_period_start/end`, `cancel_at_period_end`, and `canceled_at` through a `_from_sub` helper that prefers the Subscription object's value with `data_object` as fallback. (3) The existing live row (`sub_1TXUN1...`) is left in place — the Step 2.2 live refund test exercises its `/pilot-refund` cascade end-to-end, and the subsequent Step 2.1 redo (a fresh $100 purchase against Commit 3f) is the on-the-wire validation that `trial_end` now lands. 12 AST/text regression cases land in `tests/api/test_step30a_2_pilot_commit3f.py` covering: `retrieve_subscription` method presence and signature, `retrieve_subscription` invocation in webhook, `_from_sub` helper presence and that the four migrated fields all flow through it, `try`-wrapped fetch, no-direct-`data_object.get("status")` regression pin, and the cross-file Commit-3f marker invariant.
**Pattern E:** Pure widening of the field-source set. The handler still falls back to `data_object` exactly as before when the Stripe fetch fails (which is the only path that exercised this code on every prior test run). The new live-Subscription path is preferred over the fallback, so prior tests continue to pass without modification — confirmed by the 58/58 green run across all four Step 30a.2-pilot test files in the Commit 3f sandbox.
**Validation evidence:** `pytest tests/api/test_step30a_2_pilot_commit3f.py -v` = 12/12 pass. `pytest tests/api/test_step30a_2_pilot_*.py tests/api/test_step30a_2_first_time_gate.py -v` (with stub `DATABASE_URL` and `OPENAI_API_KEY`) = 58/58 pass, zero regressions on Commit 3e tests. AST parse of all three modified files clean. The on-the-wire validation runs at Step 2.1 redo after Commit 3f deploys: a fresh $100 live purchase will produce a Subscription row with `status="trialing"` and `trial_end ~= 2026-08-13` instead of `status="complete"` and `trial_end=null`.
**Cross-refs:** Sibling drift `D-pilot-is-pilot-metadata-driven-2026-05-15` (same Commit 3f; the read-path companion that no longer requires `trial_end is not None`). Predecessor drift `D-stripe-event-dict-conversion-python314-2026-05-15` (Commit 3e — fixed the webhook 500 that masked this field-source bug). Direct DB inspection evidence: Subscription row id=1, `created_at=2026-05-15 23:34:53.844457+00:00`, `status="complete"`, `trial_end=null`, `provider_snapshot.metadata.luciel_intro_applied="true"`. CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.2-pilot row will name this drift's closure in the same commit. ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (Billing surface — the canonical-Subscription-mirroring contract this drift defends).

### ~~D-pilot-is-pilot-metadata-driven-2026-05-15~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-15 by Step 30a.2-pilot Commit 3f (backend). Same commit as sibling `D-stripe-webhook-checkout-vs-subscription-field-source-2026-05-15`. Entry retained in §3 with strikethrough per §6.
**Raised by:** Direct DB inspection during the Step 2.1 closeout audit (2026-05-15 ≈19:46 EDT) revealed that the `/me`-equivalent endpoint's `is_pilot` derivation conjoined the metadata flag (`luciel_intro_applied == "true"`) with a structural Stripe-side detail (`sub.trial_end is not None`). The latter depends on the webhook handler having read the canonical Subscription's `trial_end`, which it was not doing pre-Commit 3f, so `is_pilot` collapsed to `false` for a row that was unambiguously sold on the pilot path.
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §14 ¶271 and ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 commit the pilot signal as a *semantic* claim: "this subscription was sold on the 90-day pilot path." The semantic source of truth is the Stripe metadata field `luciel_intro_applied` (set at checkout creation in `BillingService.create_checkout`), not the structural Subscription-side `trial_end` field. The two should agree when both are present, but `is_pilot` should not become `false` simply because Stripe didn't stamp a `trial_end` (e.g. because the webhook handler historically didn't read it — see sibling drift).
**Repo state:** `app/api/v1/billing.py::get_subscription_status` (the `/me` endpoint's load-bearing function) computed `is_pilot = (str(snapshot_meta.get("luciel_intro_applied", "")).lower() == "true" and sub.trial_end is not None)`. The conjunction with `sub.trial_end is not None` was an over-tight defence: the metadata is already a deliberate, write-time-authored signal; requiring an additional structural witness conflated *"sold as a pilot"* with *"Stripe-side trial state is populated"*.
**Operational impact today:** Medium. Same surface as the sibling drift — the Account UI did not render the pilot ribbon or the self-serve refund CTA for the live $100 buyer, forcing operator-mediated refunds during the pilot window. Resolution shipped in the same commit as the webhook field-source fix so a fresh purchase will set both signals simultaneously.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.2-pilot Commit 3f (closed in the same commit that raised it).
**Resolution:** `is_pilot` is now driven by `luciel_intro_applied` alone: `is_pilot = str(snapshot_meta.get("luciel_intro_applied", "")).lower() == "true"`. `pilot_window_end` prefers `sub.trial_end` when populated (canonical, set by the new Commit 3f webhook path), and falls back to `sub.created_at + timedelta(days=90)` when `trial_end` is null so older Commit-3e rows (the existing 2026-05-15 live row in particular) display the correct deadline. `app/api/v1/billing.py` adds `from datetime import timedelta` at the top. Regression tests `test_is_pilot_no_longer_requires_trial_end`, `test_pilot_window_end_falls_back_to_created_at`, and `test_is_pilot_drives_solely_from_metadata` in `tests/api/test_step30a_2_pilot_commit3f.py` pin the new shape via AST/text assertions.
**Pattern E:** Pure relaxation of a conjunction. The new derivation accepts a strict superset of inputs as `is_pilot=true` (any row where `luciel_intro_applied=="true"`); rows where the metadata flag is false or missing still resolve to `is_pilot=false`, preserving the prior behaviour on that branch. Confirmed by `test_me_derives_is_pilot_from_snapshot_metadata` and `test_me_returns_is_pilot_false_for_regular_trial` in the Commit 3c-era `test_step30a_2_pilot_refund_shape.py` still passing 2/2 against Commit 3f code.
**Validation evidence:** `pytest tests/api/test_step30a_2_pilot_commit3f.py -v` = 12/12 pass (3 cases specifically pin this drift's resolution). `pytest tests/api/test_step30a_2_pilot_refund_shape.py::TestMePilotSignal` = 4/4 pass (no regression in the Commit 3c-era pilot-signal contract).
**Cross-refs:** Sibling drift `D-stripe-webhook-checkout-vs-subscription-field-source-2026-05-15` (same Commit 3f; the write-path companion that populates `trial_end` going forward). Step 30a.2-pilot Commit 3c original `/me` patch (introduced the conjunctive form this drift relaxes). CANONICAL_RECAP §14 ¶271 (pilot offer commitment). ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (Billing surface — the read-path semantics this drift codifies).

### ~~D-pilot-refund-write-path-trial-end-asymmetry-2026-05-15~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-15 by Step 30a.2-pilot Commit 3g (backend). Sibling of `D-pilot-is-pilot-metadata-driven-2026-05-15` (Commit 3f closed the *read* path; this drift closes the *write* path with symmetric semantics).
**Raised by:** Live click-test of `/account/billing` immediately after the Commit 3f roll to `:56` (2026-05-15 ≈21:13 EDT). The pilot ribbon rendered correctly (proving the read path), and the buyer clicked the "Refund my pilot ($100 CAD)" button. The backend rejected with HTTP error code `not_first_time_customer` and the website surfaced toast "This pilot offer is for first-time customers only." The rejection was wrong: this *was* the first-time customer.
**Design claim:** Pilot eligibility — both the read-path "can the UI render the refund CTA?" and the write-path "can the service process the refund?" — must be driven by the same canonical signal: the metadata flag `luciel_intro_applied`. The read path is the prediction; the write path must accept everything the read path renders, or every degraded row becomes a UX cul-de-sac where the user clicks a button that always 403s. Repeat-customer protection is enforced upstream at `BillingService.is_first_time_customer` (guards `create_checkout`); it is not the write path's job to re-litigate first-time-ness, only to confirm the intro path was followed at purchase time.
**Repo state:** `app/services/billing_service.py::process_pilot_refund` had a belt-and-suspenders eligibility predicate: `if not intro_applied or sub.trial_end is None: raise NotFirstTimePilotError(...)`. The `or sub.trial_end is None` clause was the asymmetric over-tightening — it rejected exactly the rows the read path (post-Commit 3f) now renders the refund CTA on. Secondarily, the 90-day window check on line 545 also used `sub.trial_end` exclusively, with no fallback to `created_at + 90 days`.
**Operational impact today:** Critical (would have been). With Commit 3f shipped but Commit 3g not, the read path renders the refund button on degraded rows, the user clicks it, and the write path 403s. The visible UX regression is worse than no button at all because the user has been told they can refund and then told they can't. Mitigation pre-fix: operator-mediated refunds via Stripe Dashboard plus a manual DB row update — exactly the path Step 30a.2-pilot was designed to retire.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.2-pilot Commit 3g (closed in the same commit that raised it).
**Resolution:** Drop the `or sub.trial_end is None` clause; eligibility (2) is now `if not intro_applied: raise NotFirstTimePilotError(...)`. Eligibility (3) (90-day window) gains a fallback: `effective_window_end = sub.trial_end if sub.trial_end is not None else sub.created_at + timedelta(days=90)`, with the same tz-coercion defence as before. Both changes mirror Commit 3f's read-path doctrine line-by-line. `app/services/billing_service.py` adds `from datetime import timedelta` to the import line. Regression tests in `tests/api/test_step30a_2_pilot_commit3g.py` pin the new shape via AST/text assertions and a unit test of the eligibility predicates against an in-memory `Subscription` fixture with `trial_end=None` and `luciel_intro_applied="true"`.
**Pattern E:** Pure relaxation of a conjunction (mirroring Commit 3f). The new derivation accepts a strict superset of inputs as refund-eligible (any row where `luciel_intro_applied=="true"` AND the computed effective_window_end has not passed); rows where the metadata flag is false or missing still raise `NotFirstTimePilotError`, preserving the prior behaviour on that branch. The 90-day window check still raises `PilotWindowExpiredError` for windows that have passed — but now correctly computes the window end from `created_at + 90 days` when `trial_end` is null, so the rejection reason is honest.
**Validation evidence:** `pytest tests/api/test_step30a_2_pilot_commit3g.py -v` = N/N pass (final count recorded in the commit message). `pytest tests/api/test_step30a_2_pilot_commit3f.py` still 12/12 pass (no regression on the read path). Live evidence to be appended after the post-roll Step 2.2 click test succeeds: the buyer (`sub_1TXUN1RytQVRVXw7wmsfATXJ`) executes a self-serve refund, the cascade fires, the Stripe Dashboard shows `Refunded` and `Cancelled`, and the audit chain link is written.
**Cross-refs:** Sibling drift `D-pilot-is-pilot-metadata-driven-2026-05-15` (Commit 3f — the read-path companion this drift mirrors). Predecessor drift `D-stripe-webhook-checkout-vs-subscription-field-source-2026-05-15` (Commit 3f — the underlying webhook field-source bug that created the degraded rows this drift's resolution unblocks refunds for). CANONICAL_RECAP §14 ¶271 (pilot offer commitment). ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (Billing surface — the write-path semantics this drift codifies).

### ~~D-stripe-basil-2025-invoice-charge-traversal-2026-05-15~~
**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-15 by Step 30a.2-pilot Commit 3h (backend). Third commit in the post-roll Step-2.2 corrective sequence (`3f` closed the read-path field-source bug, `3g` closed the write-path eligibility asymmetry, `3h` closes the Stripe SDK basil 2025+ invoice→charge traversal gap that `BillingService.process_pilot_refund` eligibility step (4) hit when it tried to call `find_intro_charge_id` on a live subscription whose invoice had been created under Stripe API version `2026-04-22.dahlia`).
**Section that raised it:** GATE 2 round 6 post-roll Step 2.2 attempt 2 (`pilot.todo §14`). After Commit 3g rolled live at task-def `:57` (image `step30a2-pilot-014dab2-r1`, digest sha256:…), the buyer (`sub_1TXUN1RytQVRVXw7wmsfATXJ`, customer `cus_UWXRMGP6ocrwsS`, invoice `in_1TXUMwRytQVRVXw7wLCDYpwS`, paid CA$100 at 2026-05-15 18:36:43 EDT) re-clicked the `Refund my $100 intro fee` button on `account/billing`. The ribbon rendered correctly (Commit 3f read-path proof preserved) and the click no longer 403'd `not_first_time_customer` (Commit 3g write-path fix preserved), but a new surface error appeared: toast "We couldn't find the pilot charge to refund. Contact support." The corresponding error code is `PilotChargeNotFoundError`, raised by `BillingService.process_pilot_refund` when `StripeClient.find_intro_charge_id(subscription_id)` returns `None`.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-15 22:00–22:05 EDT during the Step 2.2 attempt-2 diagnostic walk. Aryan executed four successive ECS-exec one-liners against the live `luciel-backend-service` task (`7f53432743e14c5eab28e6dbf7ae7e50`) with `STRIPE_SECRET_KEY` loaded from `settings.stripe_secret_key`. v1 confirmed `sub.status=trialing`, `trial_end=1786660690` (2026-08-13), `latest_invoice=in_1TXUMwRytQVRVXw7wLCDYpwS`, invoice `status=paid`, `amount_paid=10000`, but `invoice.payment_intent=None` and `invoice.charge=None` — both fields that the pre-3h primary path in `find_intro_charge_id` relied on. v2 attempted to walk via `Charge.invoice` reverse-lookup but the field returned `AttributeError`. v3 dumped the full top-level `Invoice` payload and confirmed by inspection that the SDK's invoice object exposed every standard field (`amount_paid`, `customer`, `currency`, `lines`, `period_start`, `period_end`, `subscription`, `status`) **but no `payment_intent` or `charge`** — the linkage had moved off the Invoice resource entirely. v4 (decisive) listed `stripe.InvoicePayment.list(invoice='in_1TXUMwRytQVRVXw7wLCDYpwS')` and found one row `inpay_1TXUN2RytQVRVXw7f8CrCTjq` with `status=paid`, `amount_paid=10000`, and a `payment={'payment_intent': 'pi_3TXUMwRytQVRVXw70IEdoC7k', 'type': 'payment_intent'}` mapping that resolved via `PaymentIntent.retrieve` to a `latest_charge='py_3TXUMwRytQVRVXw70A1iOPs5'` ($100 CAD, `status=succeeded`). The traversal that worked on every previous Stripe SDK major (`Invoice.payment_intent` direct field, plus `Charge.invoice` reverse-lookup) was therefore officially deprecated and replaced with the new `InvoicePayment` resource as of Stripe API version `2026-04-22.dahlia` (basil), which the live account is pinned to.
**Design claim:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 commits the eight-route HTTP surface and the four-step eligibility predicate inside `BillingService.process_pilot_refund(user)`. Step (4) — "locate the original `$100 CAD` intro charge so it can be refunded" — is a pure delegation to `StripeClient.find_intro_charge_id(subscription_id)`. The design claim never specified which Stripe resource traversal the client uses; it just promised the function returns a `ch_…` or `py_…` charge id (or `None`). The traversal is therefore the client's implementation detail to keep current with Stripe SDK behaviour — and basil 2025+ moved the field linkage off `Invoice` to the new `InvoicePayment` resource, which the pre-3h primary path did not know about.
**Detection asymmetry — why this was hidden until live click:** The pre-3h primary path (`invoice.payment_intent.latest_charge`) succeeded on every Stripe **test-mode** subscription created under API version `2025-…` and earlier. The live account (`acct_1TX2BmRytQVRVXw7`) auto-upgraded to `2026-04-22.dahlia` (basil) when it was activated 2026-05-14, and the live `$100` smoke purchase on 2026-05-15 created the first invoice under the new API version. The CI suite's mocked stripe responses encoded the pre-basil shape; no test held a pinned schema fixture against a live `2026-04-22` response. The gap was therefore live-evidence-only — the very kind that GATE 4 live smoke is designed to catch.
**Operational impact today:** Critical (would have been). With Commits 3f + 3g shipped but Commit 3h not, the read path renders the refund button on `is_pilot=true` rows, the user clicks it, eligibility steps (1)(2)(3) pass, and step (4) returns `None` because `find_intro_charge_id` cannot walk the basil 2025+ invoice. The visible UX regression is now "the button works but the refund fails on an internal-sounding error", which (a) is functionally identical to a broken refund flow from the customer's perspective, and (b) breaks the partner-locked customer-facing promise "full refund anytime during the period, first-time only, self-serve". Pre-fix mitigation was operator-mediated refunds via Stripe Dashboard plus a manual DB cascade — exactly the path Step 30a.2-pilot was designed to retire.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.2-pilot Commit 3h (closed in the same commit that raised it).
**Resolution:** Rewrite `StripeClient.find_intro_charge_id(subscription_id)` in `app/integrations/stripe/client.py` with a three-tier traversal that puts the basil 2025+ path **first** so live and test-mode-on-the-new-API-version both work, then keeps the pre-basil paths as fallbacks so any older test fixture or test-mode subscription on a pinned older API version still resolves. **Tier 1 (basil 2025+, primary):** `stripe.InvoicePayment.list(invoice=invoice_id, limit=10)` → walk `ips.data`, on each row read `ip.payment.payment_intent` (string id), call `stripe.PaymentIntent.retrieve(pi_id)`, return `pi_obj.latest_charge` (handles both string-form and expanded-object-form return shapes). **Tier 2 (pre-basil modern, fallback):** `invoice.payment_intent` (if set) → `PaymentIntent.retrieve` → `.latest_charge`. **Tier 3 (pre-modern legacy, fallback):** `invoice.charge` (if set, string or object). All three tiers wrapped in `try/except stripe.error.StripeError` so a network blip or permission error on the new resource does not block the legacy paths. The docstring records the basil 2025+ shift and the traversal order. Regression tests in `tests/api/test_step30a_2_pilot_commit3h.py` (12 AST/text cases) pin every element of the new shape: `InvoicePayment.list` invocation present, `invoice=` keyword filter present, `payment.payment_intent` read present, `PaymentIntent.retrieve` call present, both legacy fallback paths preserved, traversal order matches design (basil first), return-`None` terminator present, try/except wrapping present, invoice_id is captured from the subscription's `latest_invoice`, `Subscription.retrieve` uses `expand=['latest_invoice']`, docstring records the basil 2025+ contract.
**Pattern E:** Pure addition of a new traversal tier ahead of the existing ones. The new derivation accepts a strict superset of invoice shapes as charge-resolvable (any invoice whose `InvoicePayment` row has a `payment.payment_intent` mapping, in addition to any invoice whose top-level `payment_intent` or `charge` field is set); invoices where none of the three traversal tiers yields a charge id still return `None` from the function, preserving the prior contract on that branch. No existing call site changes. No DB schema change. No webhook handler change. No new env var, no new SDK version pin (the existing `stripe>=10.0.0,<16` window from `D-stripe-sdk-major-pin-2026-05-15` already includes `15.1.0` which exposes `InvoicePayment`).
**Validation evidence:** `pytest tests/api/test_step30a_2_pilot_commit3h.py -v` = 12/12 pass (recorded in the commit message). `pytest tests/api/test_step30a_2_pilot_commit3f.py tests/api/test_step30a_2_pilot_commit3g.py tests/api/test_step30a_2_pilot_refund_shape.py tests/api/test_step30a_2_first_time_gate.py` still all pass (no regression on read path, write-path eligibility, refund-route shape, or first-time gate). Live evidence to be appended after the post-roll Step 2.2 attempt 3 click test succeeds: the buyer (`sub_1TXUN1RytQVRVXw7wmsfATXJ`, charge `py_3TXUMwRytQVRVXw70A1iOPs5`) executes a self-serve refund, `StripeClient.find_intro_charge_id` resolves to `py_3TXUMwRytQVRVXw70A1iOPs5`, the cascade fires (refund + subscription cancel + audit row + magic-link email), and the Stripe Dashboard shows `Refunded` and `Cancelled`.
**Cross-refs:** Sibling drifts `D-pilot-is-pilot-metadata-driven-2026-05-15` (Commit 3f — read-path field-source companion), `D-pilot-refund-write-path-trial-end-asymmetry-2026-05-15` (Commit 3g — write-path eligibility companion). Predecessor drift `D-stripe-subscription-period-fields-moved-to-items-2026-05-14` (the first basil-era field-shift drift on the same account; same root cause family, different field). Adjacent drift `D-stripe-sdk-major-pin-2026-05-15` (the `stripe>=10.0.0,<16` pin that gives this resolution its room to land without a separate SDK bump). CANONICAL_RECAP §14 ¶271 (pilot offer commitment), ¶273 (refund policy). ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (Billing surface — eligibility step (4)).

### D-pricing-channels-bullet-team-only-placement-2026-05-20
**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-20 (resolved-in-same-commit; closure stanza in §5 below).
**Original status (would have been):** OPEN — P3 marketing-truth. The live Pricing surface at `https://www.vantagemind.ai/pricing` rendered the "Voice, SMS, and email channels (roadmap, all tiers)" bullet only on the Team tier card. The parenthetical "all tiers" is technically honest, but the visual asymmetry — bullet present on the middle (highlighted) card and absent on the two flanking cards — created the impression that voice/SMS/email channels are a Team-and-up entitlement, contradicting the universal-channels doctrine locked in `D-channels-promised-not-built-multi-tier-2026-05-20`.
**Section that raised it:** Pre-Journey-1 live-testing pause, 2026-05-20, during the Block 0.A visual verification step of the E2E replay arc. Partner exchange: "Why does the team card only say Voice, SMS, email channels (roadmap, all tiers)".
**Raised by:** Aryan (partner) on 2026-05-20, in the same Block 0.A response that surfaced the unresolved annual-cadence drift. Both drifts witnessed in the same screenshot of the live Pricing page.
**Design claim:** `D-channels-promised-not-built-multi-tier-2026-05-20` locks channels as a universal commitment across Individual / Team / Company. The Pricing surface inherits that doctrine at the card-bullet level: every tier card must either carry the channels bullet identically or none should (with the parenthetical covering the all-tier scope from a single placement). Visual asymmetry between cards is the defect.
**Repo state at discovery:** `Luciel-Website/src/pages/Pricing.tsx`. The `tiers: TierCard[]` array had the channels bullet only inside the Team entry's `bullets` field (line 68). Individual and Company entries did not carry the bullet at all.
**Operational impact at discovery:** Low at the conversion-funnel level — no annual SKUs or channels-gated SKUs sold today; the screen reads the same to a buyer who only cares about the chat widget. Impact is design-truth alignment: the first prospect who reads the Pricing page top-to-bottom and asks "why does my tier not get voice channels" creates a sales conversation where the answer has to backfill the doctrine that the page should already have made obvious.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.7 Pricing-surface catch-up (resolved-in-same-commit). Pair-closure with `D-annual-cadence-two-months-free-framing-2026-05-20`.
**Resolution path:** Single edit to the `tiers` array in `Pricing.tsx`. Add the bullet `"Voice, SMS, and email channels (roadmap, all tiers)"` to the Individual entry's `bullets` field (between "Configurable per role and workflow" and "90-day pilot…") and to the Company entry's `bullets` field (between "Immutable audit trail…" and "90-day pilot…"). The Team entry's bullet stays as-is. Result: every tier card now carries the channels bullet at the same vertical position relative to the pilot footer, with the same wording. The parenthetical "all tiers" continues to read honestly because the bullet is now present on all tiers.
**Pattern E:** Additive copy fix in the website surface. No backend touch. No schema change. No price change. No regression risk to the highlighted-Team treatment. The placement is now visually symmetric across the three cards.
**Validation evidence:** Closure-evidence shape: (a) `grep -c "Voice, SMS, and email channels" src/pages/Pricing.tsx` returns ≥ 3 (one per tier card; a fourth match inside the closing-tag comment block is expected and intentional); (b) post-Amplify-build, `Invoke-WebRequest https://www.vantagemind.ai/pricing` HTML contains the bullet text three times in the rendered tier cards; (c) visual diff of the live `/pricing` shows the channels bullet present on all three cards at the same vertical position. The vitest contract test is deferred (the frontend repo has no `src/pages/__tests__/` directory yet; authoring one is out of scope for a copy-fix and is captured as a follow-up under `D-annual-cadence-two-months-free-framing-2026-05-20`'s validation-evidence note).
**Cross-refs:** `D-channels-promised-not-built-multi-tier-2026-05-20` (the parent doctrine — channels are an all-tier commitment); `~~D-annual-cadence-two-months-free-framing-2026-05-20~~` (sibling Pricing-surface drift closed in the same commit); `D-pricing-page-truth-2026-05-20` (umbrella Pricing-surface truth drift); `D-tier-semantics-realignment-2026-05-20` (grandparent umbrella).

## Section 4 — Drifts pending production confirmation [PROD-PHASE-2B]

These are claims in `ARCHITECTURE.md` whose verification requires operator-side access to the AWS account. Each will be walked together with the operator step by step in Phase 2B. The repository alone cannot confirm or deny any of them.

**Status:** OPEN [PROD-PHASE-2B]
**Raised by:** Architecture §3.2.1 and §3.6 diagram (WAF in front of ALB)
**Repo state:** No CFN template in `cfn/` provisions a WAF Web ACL. No infra-as-code claim of a WAF.
**Resolution path:** Operator confirms whether a WAF Web ACL is associated with the production ALB. If yes, capture its arn and the rule set. If no, mark §3.2.1's WAF claim as 📋 Planned and open a roadmap item.

### D-prod-multi-az-rds-unverified-2026-05-09

**Status:** OPEN [PROD-PHASE-2B]
**Raised by:** Architecture §3.2.5 ("hot standby in a second availability zone"), §3.6 diagram (PG_PRIMARY ↔ PG_STANDBY)
**Repo state:** No CFN template provisions the RDS instance. The repo cannot confirm Multi-AZ.
**Resolution path:** Operator runs `aws rds describe-db-instances` (read-only) and confirms `MultiAZ: true` and the standby AZ. If single-AZ, mark §3.2.5's standby claim as 📋 Planned.

### D-prod-app-tier-pool-unverified-2026-05-09

**Status:** OPEN [PROD-PHASE-2B]
**Raised by:** Architecture §3.2.3 ("a pool of application servers"), §3.5 ("application server crash" recovery story)
**Repo state:** Task definitions exist (`td-backend-rev39.json` as of the Step 30c prod deploy on 2026-05-11; previously `td-backend-rev34.json`) but desired-count and minimum-pool size are an ECS service property, not a task-def property.
**Resolution path:** Operator confirms desired count and minimum healthy count of the backend ECS service. If desired count is 1, mark §3.2.3's pool claim as 🔧 Partial and open a roadmap item to raise the floor.

### D-prod-worker-autoscaling-unverified-2026-05-09

### D-prod-kms-customer-managed-unverified-2026-05-09

**Status:** OPEN [PROD-PHASE-2B]
**Raised by:** Architecture §3.2.8 ("encrypted with a customer-managed KMS key")
**Repo state:** Verify task role (`cfn/luciel-verify-task-role.yaml`) references KMS Decrypt via SSM service principal but does not name the key. Cannot confirm whether the key in use is AWS-managed (`aws/ssm`) or customer-managed.
**Resolution path:** Operator runs `aws ssm describe-parameters` for one of the SecureString parameters, captures the `KeyId`, then `aws kms describe-key` on it. Confirm `KeyManager: CUSTOMER`. If `AWS`, mark as 🔧 Partial — works the same operationally but rotation control is AWS's, not ours.

### D-prod-secrets-pattern-e-unverified-2026-05-09

**Status:** OPEN [PROD-PHASE-2B]
**Raised by:** Architecture §3.2.8 ("Pattern E: secrets are deactivated, never deleted")
**Repo state:** SSM Parameter Store does not natively support Pattern E (deactivated flag) — it supports versioning. The current implementation pattern needs documentation.
**Resolution path:** Operator inventories SSM parameters with `aws ssm describe-parameters` and confirms the operational pattern: are old versions retained (relying on SSM history) or are deactivated rotated parameters retained as separate parameter names with a `-deactivated-YYYY-MM-DD` suffix? The doc should reflect what we actually do; right now §3.2.8 implies a discipline the implementation may not have.

### D-prod-celery-broker-sqs-vs-redis-2026-05-09

**Status:** OPEN [PROD-PHASE-2B]
**Raised by:** Architecture §3.6 diagram (`Job queue Redis/SQS`); §3.2.4 prose does not name SQS.
**Repo state:** `app/worker/celery_app.py` lines 116-138 explicitly document a two-mode broker design: SQS in production, Redis in development. Production task definitions inject `REDIS_URL` from SSM. The architecture document does not commit clearly to SQS-in-prod.
**Resolution path:** Update Architecture §3.2.4 to state SQS as the production broker explicitly, with the rationale already in `app/worker/celery_app.py` lines 132-138 (ElastiCache cluster mode incompatible with kombu's MULTI/EXEC). Confirm with operator that production is in fact running SQS-mode (not Redis broker via SSM `REDIS_URL`). If REDIS_URL is the actual broker, the architecture is wrong; otherwise the architecture is incomplete and we tighten it.

### D-prod-sqs-stale-messages-2026-05-09

**Status:** OPEN [PROD-PHASE-2B] (operator-flagged, symptom description pending)
**Raised by:** Operator on 2026-05-09 ("SQS stale messages drift"); not yet captured in either design doc.
**Repo state:** Pending operator description.
**Resolution path:** Operator describes the symptom — what is stale, how it manifests, what was observed in CloudWatch or in queue inspection. Drift will be expanded with the description, then we decide whether the cause is a design gap (e.g., visibility timeout vs job duration), a code bug (idempotency or ack handling), or an operational incident (poison messages stuck redelivering).

### D-memory-truncation-2026-05-09

Drift will be expanded with the description, then we decide whether the truncation is a column-length cap, a retrieval-window heuristic, or a model-context budget cap.

### D-step-24-5c-and-31-schema-and-code-undeployed-to-prod-2026-05-12

**Status:** OPEN — active risk window; blocks any code deploy from `main` until closed.
**Raised by:** Partner (Aryan) on 2026-05-12 during Step 31 close-out review, after correctly challenging the agent's incorrect framing that "no prod deploy was needed." The agent had assessed Step 31's PRs in isolation without walking the Alembic migration graph forward from the last known production-deployed revision — a sloppy review that this entry exists to correct.
**Design claim:** Two ARCHITECTURE sections describe a feature surface that, on the current `main` HEAD `fa876ce`, has live application code but no live database schema on production RDS: §3.2.11 (Identity & conversation continuity — Step 24.5c) and §3.2.12 (Hierarchical dashboards & validation gate — Step 31). Both subsections are marked ✅ Implemented and the corresponding CANONICAL_RECAP rows are marked ✅. The implementation claim is correct at the code-and-local-Postgres level; the production-deployment claim is **not asserted by either row today, but the absence of a `[PROD-PHASE-2B]` marker or a Prod observed-clean stanza is itself misleading without this entry** — a reader could reasonably infer the surfaces are live in production, and they are not.
**Repo state:**
  - **Alembic head on `main`:** `3dbbc70d0105` (`alembic/versions/3dbbc70d0105_step24_5c_conversations_and_identity_claims.py`) introduces the `conversations` table, the `identity_claim_type` Postgres enum, the `identity_claims` table (with composite uniqueness on `(claim_type, claim_value, tenant_id, domain_id)` and two partial indexes filtered on `active=true`), and the nullable `conversation_id` FK column on `sessions`. The migration chain prior to head is `a7c1f4e92b85` (Step 30b widget columns on `api_keys`) → `d8e2c4b1a0f3` (Step 29.y Cluster 4 worker rejection-audit idempotency index) → `c5d8a1e7b3f9` (Step 29.y Cluster 3 `admin_audit_logs.row_hash NOT NULL`).
  - **Last production-deployed revision (inferred from the Step 30c prod observed-clean stanza):** ECR digest `sha256:f0bf303272fb0801eefc4cf0d20d2ddb624f2a5f60c8e845cbe422869739f863` built from `main` HEAD `84339a3`, registered as `luciel-backend:39` and `luciel-worker:19` on 2026-05-11. That image predates merge `1e761a6` (Step 24.5c sub-branch 1 — the only commit since Step 30c that touches `alembic/versions/`), so production RDS is presumed to be at `a7c1f4e92b85` (one revision behind head); production application code is presumed to be at `84339a3` (does not contain Step 24.5c models, `CrossSessionRetriever`, `IdentityResolver`, adapter claims wiring, the Step 31 widget audit log emissions, the `create_session_with_identity` route wiring in `app/api/v1/chat_widget.py`, the `DashboardService`, or the `app/api/v1/dashboard.py` HTTP surface). "Presumed" is the correct word — closing this drift includes running `alembic current` against production RDS to confirm the actual revision before the deploy.
  - **Why the gap is currently latent, not active:** production code and production schema are *both* older than the missing pieces and are internally consistent at the older state. The widget chat path on production today calls into the pre-Step-24.5c code path that does not touch `identity_claims` or `conversations`. The first deploy of any code from current `main` to production breaks this consistency: new code will execute `SessionService.create_session_with_identity()` on every widget turn (PR #30 wired it into the route), which inserts into `identity_claims` and `conversations` — tables that do not exist on production RDS — and the widget chat surface will start returning errors on every call. This is the exact failure mode the harness caught locally on 2026-05-12 before the local `alembic upgrade head` (`psycopg.errors.UndefinedTable: relation "identity_claims" does not exist`).
**Operational impact:** Zero today; high tomorrow if any code deploy is taken from `main` without first running the Alembic migration on production RDS. The risk surface is the widget chat path — i.e., the surface customers actually exercise. This entry exists specifically so no future deploy can happen without seeing this warning first.
**Owning roadmap step:** None today — this is a deploy gap, not a design or implementation gap. The work to close it is a prod-deploy event in the Step 30c precedent shape (runbook + ordered execution + observed-clean stanza), executed as a stand-alone piece of scope. It does not earn a new roadmap row because the implementation work for both Step 24.5c and Step 31 is complete on `main`; what remains is operational delivery of work already shipped.
**Resolution path (canonical ordering):**
  1. **Pre-deploy verification:** `alembic current` against production RDS to confirm the actual head revision matches the inferred `a7c1f4e92b85`. If it does not, the runbook plan is revised before any forward migration is run.
  2. **Schema first:** run `alembic upgrade head` against production RDS to advance from `a7c1f4e92b85` to `3dbbc70d0105`. This is additive only (one enum, two tables, one nullable FK column, two partial indexes) — no destructive operations, no column type changes, no NOT NULL backfills required on existing rows. Existing `sessions` rows keep `conversation_id IS NULL` which is the Step 24.5c design contract per ARCHITECTURE §3.2.11. Run inside a transaction (Alembic default for PostgreSQL); if any step fails the partial state is rolled back.
  3. **Code second:** build ECR image from `main` HEAD `fa876ce`, push under a Step-24.5c/31-naming ECR tag, register new `luciel-backend` and `luciel-worker` task-definition revisions (likely `:40` and `:20`, succeeding `:39` and `:19`), update the in-repo manifests in the same doc-truthing commit (`td-backend-rev39.json` → `td-backend-rev40.json`, `td-worker-rev19.json` → `td-worker-rev20.json`) per the precedent set by Step 30c.
  4. **Observed-clean verification:** post-deploy log review of `/ecs/luciel-backend` and `/ecs/luciel-worker` for the canonical clean-startup sequence (`Started server process [1]` → `Application startup complete.` → steady `GET /health → 200 OK`; worker `celery@... ready.` and old-worker `Warm shutdown`); zero `ERROR` / `Traceback` / `CRITICAL` hits across the post-deploy log window; deploymentCircuitBreaker did not fire on either service. Then exercise the widget chat path against the production embed key from the Stage 1 staging E2E (`luc_sk_xwij1...`, id 698, on `domain_configs.id=374`) for one end-to-end turn through `POST /api/v1/chat/widget`, watching for the three new audit log lines (`widget_chat_turn_received`, `widget_chat_session_resolved`, `widget_chat_turn_completed`) in `/ecs/luciel-backend` and the expected three new row writes (`identity_claims`, `conversations`, `sessions` with `conversation_id` populated) via a scoped read query.
  5. **Doc-truthing close:** add a **Prod observed-clean** stanza to both CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 24.5c and Step 31 rows in the Step 30c precedent shape (ECR digest, task-definition revisions, log evidence, runbook of record), append a CLOSED note to this drift entry, move this entry from §3 to §5 with strikethrough heading per §6 doctrine, and re-cut the closing tags `step-24-5c-cross-channel-identity-complete` and `step-31-dashboards-validation-gate-complete` forward onto the doc-truthing commit so the tags continue to read "code + docs + prod all agree here." Runbook of record will live at `docs/runbooks/step-24-5c-and-31-prod-deploy.md`.
**Doc-truthing this pass:** This entry is the first half of closing the honesty gap. The second half is two parenthetical notes appended in CANONICAL_RECAP §12 — one on the Step 24.5c row, one on the Step 31 row — pointing readers to this drift. The ✅ markers stay (the implementation is implemented), but the parentheticals make the deploy gap unmissable. ARCHITECTURE §3.2.11 and §3.2.12 do not need a marker change because they describe design state, which is correct; the gap is operational.
**Extended scope (2026-05-13, Step 31.2 + Step 30a doc-truthing pass):** This drift now also covers Step 30a's migration `b8e74a3c1d52` (down_revision `3dbbc70d0105`, introduces the `subscriptions` table) and Step 31.2's code (no additional migration — Step 31.2 is code-only). The migration chain prod RDS must reach is now `a7c1f4e92b85 → 3dbbc70d0105 (Step 24.5c) → b8e74a3c1d52 (Step 30a)`; Step 31.2 carries no schema change because `api_keys.luciel_instance_id` was already a nullable FK before Step 31.2 (the carve-out was at the issuance API surface, not at the column). Prod ECS task-definition revisions advance from `luciel-backend:39` + `luciel-worker:19` to a new revision pair (likely `:40` + `:20`) carrying the combined Step 24.5c + Step 30a + Step 31.2 code surface. Runbook of record for this combined deploy: `docs/runbooks/step-30a-and-31-2-prod-deploy.md`. The Step 30a-specific operational risk to verify post-deploy: the magic-link email path (SES sender domain verification, `[magic-link-email]` log marker present), the webhook signature verification path (no `SignatureVerificationError` log lines during the synthetic Stripe webhook test), and the `subscriptions.last_event_id` idempotency cursor (one Stripe `evt_test_*` event id appears at most once across the post-deploy log window). The Step 31.2-specific operational risk to verify post-deploy: the `SessionCookieAuthMiddleware` is mounted (a startup log line confirms it; or a cookied curl walk against `GET /api/v1/dashboard/tenant` returns 200 with a valid cookie and 401 without), and the instance-pinned embed-key path validates the four guards (the live e2e harness `tests/e2e/step_31_2_live_e2e.py` is the canonical post-deploy check when run against the production embed key from the Step 30b stage-1 staging E2E).
**Cross-refs:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 24.5c row (parenthetical pointer added this pass); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 31 row (parenthetical pointer added this pass); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a row (extended scope, 2026-05-13); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 31.2 row (extended scope, 2026-05-13); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.11 (Identity & conversation continuity — design state correct); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.12 (Hierarchical dashboards & validation gate — design state correct); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (Billing surface — design state correct); `alembic/versions/3dbbc70d0105_step24_5c_conversations_and_identity_claims.py` (Step 24.5c migration); `alembic/versions/b8e74a3c1d52_step30a_subscriptions_table.py` (Step 30a migration); merge `fa876ce` (Step 31 sub-branch 5 doc-truthing); merge `1e761a6` (Step 24.5c sub-branch 1); merge `4aea209` (Step 30a, current `main` HEAD pre-31.2-merge); branch `step-31-2-cookie-bridge-and-instance-embed-keys` HEAD `c88dfec` (Step 31.2 code awaiting merge); precedent `~~D-confirmation-gate-not-enforced-2026-05-09~~` in §5 (the Step 30c Prod observed-clean stanza is the shape this drift's close will follow); operational siblings `D-prod-alarms-deployed-unverified-2026-05-09` and `D-prod-multi-az-rds-unverified-2026-05-09` (different gaps, same `[PROD-PHASE-2B]` family).

## Section 5 — Resolved drifts (kept for audit)

Closed drifts are kept here permanently with a strikethrough heading. The closing commit, the closing tag (if applicable), and a one-line resolution note are recorded. This makes the audit chain of design decisions walkable backwards; nothing is rewritten or deleted.

### Arc 0 — Drift Hygiene Strikethrough Sweep 2026-05-20

The seven stanzas immediately below close drifts whose code/infrastructure resolution had already shipped to production in earlier arcs but whose §3 headings had not yet been strikethrough'd and whose §5 closure stanzas had not yet been authored. Arc 0 is a doc-only sweep — no code, no task-def, no SSM, no Stripe Dashboard work — that brings DRIFTS.md into mirror-discipline with the shipped backend (`luciel-backend:76` task-def rev49, HEAD `01f0149`). The twelve §3 strikethroughs applied in this arc cover both these seven (which previously had no §5 mirror) and five drifts that already had §5 mirrors but whose §3 headings had not yet been strikethrough'd; the latter five carry their existing §5 stanzas (`D-retention-purge-job-not-scheduled-2026-05-14` L1477, `D-cluster-name-luciel-cluster-not-luciel-prod-2026-05-12` L1648, `D-cascade-integrity-incomplete-on-tier-9-leg-7-2026-05-14` L1450, `D-trial-policy-mixed-per-tier-2026-05-14` L1459, `D-recap-section-12-overflow-2026-05-14` L1468) and are not re-authored here.

### ~~D-tier-9-leg-7-cascade-integrity-fix-2026-05-13~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-14 (shipped in the Step 30a.2 cascade-integrity arc; §3 strikethrough applied 2026-05-20 in the Arc 0 doc-hygiene sweep).
**Closing tag:** `arc-0-drift-hygiene-strikethrough-sweep` (doc-only §3 strikethrough + §5 stanza authoring); the original code resolution shipped under the Step 30a.2 cascade-integrity arc closing-tag chain.
**Closing commits, in order:** the Step 30a.2 Phase B cascade-integrity commit landed the Tier-9 Leg-7 hook in `app/services/cancellation_service.py` and `app/services/billing_webhook_service.py` (the cascade now fans out from the `subscription_pilot_refunded` and `subscription_cancelled` audit events through to the dependent `LucielInstance` deactivation and the `AdminAuditLog` cascade marker row); the Arc 0 doc-only commit on `docs/DRIFTS.md` carries the §3 strikethrough + this §5 stanza.
**Resolution:** Tier-9 Leg-7 (the cascade leg from `SUBSCRIPTION_PILOT_REFUNDED` → `LucielInstance.is_active = False` + cascade-marker `AdminAuditLog` row) was the load-bearing leg that the `~~D-cascade-integrity-incomplete-on-tier-9-leg-7-2026-05-14~~` (§5 L1450) umbrella drift originally identified as missing. The Step 30a.2 Phase B commit wired the hook; the parent umbrella drift was closed at the same time, but this child drift's §3 heading was left un-strikethrough'd until Arc 0. The fix is identical to the parent's resolution — they are mirror entries of the same underlying gap and the same underlying commit.
**Pattern E:** Additive — the cascade hook is a new method call on the existing `CancellationService` and `BillingWebhookService` paths; no existing leg was rewritten. The audit-row schema is unchanged (the cascade marker uses the existing `AdminAuditLog` shape with action `cascade_marker`).
**Validation evidence:** (a) `grep -n "cascade_marker" Luciel/app/services/` returns matches in both `cancellation_service.py` and `billing_webhook_service.py`; (b) the Step 30a.2 contract test `tests/services/test_cascade_integrity.py::test_tier_9_leg_7_pilot_refund_deactivates_instance` passes in CI and against `luciel-backend:76`; (c) live verification on the partner's pilot account confirmed that a `SUBSCRIPTION_PILOT_REFUNDED` audit row produces a paired `LucielInstance.is_active = False` flip + a `cascade_marker` `AdminAuditLog` row within the same DB transaction.
**Cross-refs:** `~~D-cascade-integrity-incomplete-on-tier-9-leg-7-2026-05-14~~` (§5 L1450, parent umbrella drift closed by the same Step 30a.2 Phase B commit); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.11 "Cascade integrity" paragraph (the doctrine home for the Tier-9 Leg matrix); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 "Cascade integrity" row (the doctrine-home cross-ref).

### ~~D-billing-webhook-stripe-period-fields-attribute-error-2026-05-15~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-15 (shipped in the Step 30a.2 Phase D Stripe-webhook hardening commit; §3 strikethrough applied 2026-05-20 in the Arc 0 doc-hygiene sweep).
**Closing tag:** `arc-0-drift-hygiene-strikethrough-sweep` (doc-only §3 strikethrough + §5 stanza authoring); the original code resolution shipped under the Step 30a.2 Phase D closing-tag chain.
**Closing commits, in order:** the Step 30a.2 Phase D commit added the `_extract_period_fields(subscription)` helper at the top of `app/services/billing_webhook_service.py` (the helper reads `current_period_start` / `current_period_end` defensively from `subscription.get(...)` on the dict path and `getattr(subscription, ...)` on the Stripe-object path, returning a typed tuple with `None` fallbacks rather than raising `AttributeError`); the call sites in `_handle_subscription_created`, `_handle_subscription_updated`, and `_handle_subscription_deleted` were rewritten to call the helper instead of doing direct attribute access. The Arc 0 doc-only commit on `docs/DRIFTS.md` carries the §3 strikethrough + this §5 stanza.
**Resolution:** The original failure mode (a Stripe webhook payload arriving as a `dict` rather than a `stripe.Subscription` object, which happens on certain `customer.subscription.*` event shapes when the webhook payload predates the resource-expand layer) caused `AttributeError: 'dict' object has no attribute 'current_period_start'` in `billing_webhook_service.py`. The `_extract_period_fields` helper normalises both shapes into a single typed return path; the call sites carry no shape-branching of their own.
**Pattern E:** Additive — the helper is new; the original attribute-access call sites are rewritten to use it, but no existing webhook handler logic was removed. The defensive `None`-fallback on missing period fields preserves the prior behaviour of recording the audit row even when Stripe omits period dates on certain event shapes (e.g. immediate cancellations).
**Validation evidence:** (a) `grep -n "_extract_period_fields" Luciel/app/services/billing_webhook_service.py` returns matches at the helper definition + three call sites; (b) the Step 30a.2 Phase D contract tests `tests/services/test_billing_webhook_service.py::test_extract_period_fields_dict_path` and `test_extract_period_fields_object_path` both pass; (c) live verification on the partner's pilot account confirmed that the `customer.subscription.updated` webhook on a Team-tier subscription no longer raises `AttributeError` in the worker logs (CloudWatch log group `/ecs/luciel-backend-worker` shows clean processing for the past 5 days).
**Cross-refs:** `D-billing-webhook-service-stripe-attribute-error` (Arc 2 follow-up — there is a related but distinct attribute-error class on the `subscription_schedule.*` event family that is not covered by this fix and will be addressed in Arc 2 backend hygiene); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.10 "Stripe webhook ingestion" paragraph (the doctrine home for the dict-vs-object shape normalisation contract); CANONICAL_RECAP §14 "Billing webhook resilience" row.

### ~~D-magic-link-secret-env-vs-ssm-drift-2026-05-15~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-15 (shipped in task-def rev47 → rev49 SSM-wiring arc; §3 strikethrough applied 2026-05-20 in the Arc 0 doc-hygiene sweep).
**Closing tag:** `arc-0-drift-hygiene-strikethrough-sweep` (doc-only §3 strikethrough + §5 stanza authoring); the original infra resolution shipped under the task-def rev47/48/49 SSM-wiring arc.
**Closing commits, in order:** the task-def rev47 update added `MAGIC_LINK_SECRET` to the `secrets[]` array sourced from SSM parameter `/luciel/production/magic_link_secret` (the parameter itself was created via `aws ssm put-parameter --type SecureString` in the same arc); rev48 corrected the IAM task-execution-role policy to grant `ssm:GetParameters` on the new ARN; rev49 is the current live revision. The Arc 0 doc-only commit on `docs/DRIFTS.md` carries the §3 strikethrough + this §5 stanza.
**Resolution:** Prior to rev47, `MAGIC_LINK_SECRET` was sourced from the task-def `environment[]` array as a plaintext string — a P2 security drift (secret material visible in task-def JSON, ECS console, and CloudFormation drift output). The SSM-wiring arc moved the secret into the `secrets[]` array, which causes ECS to resolve the value at task-start time and inject it into the container env without ever materialising the plaintext in any AWS-console-visible surface. The `auth_service.py` consumer code is unchanged — it still reads `os.environ["MAGIC_LINK_SECRET"]` — the move is a pure infra-layer hardening.
**Pattern E:** Additive — the new SSM parameter and the new IAM policy statement are pure adds; the task-def `environment[]` entry was removed in the same revision that added the `secrets[]` entry, so there is no window during which the secret was sourced from both places. The auth_service consumer signature is unchanged.
**Validation evidence:** (a) `td-backend-rev49.json` `secrets[]` array contains `{"name": "MAGIC_LINK_SECRET", "valueFrom": "arn:aws:ssm:ca-central-1:729005488042:parameter/luciel/production/magic_link_secret"}`; (b) `td-backend-rev49.json` `environment[]` array does NOT contain a `MAGIC_LINK_SECRET` entry (verified by `grep -n MAGIC_LINK_SECRET td-backend-rev49.json` returning only the `secrets[]` match); (c) `aws ssm get-parameter --name /luciel/production/magic_link_secret --with-decryption` returns the value (gated by the task-execution-role IAM policy); (d) live verification: a magic-link send-and-consume cycle on the partner's pilot account succeeds end-to-end against `luciel-backend:76`.
**Cross-refs:** `D-step-32-magic-link-auth-cookie-session` (parent Step 32 auth-arc drift — this rev47 secret-wiring was a prerequisite leg of that larger arc, which itself remains open as a genuine blocker per Phase 5 census); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.5 "Magic-link authentication" paragraph (the doctrine home for the secret-rotation contract); CANONICAL_RECAP §6 "Auth secrets" row.

### ~~D-session-cookie-domain-prod-misalignment-2026-05-15~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-15 (shipped in task-def rev47 env-wiring arc; §3 strikethrough applied 2026-05-20 in the Arc 0 doc-hygiene sweep).
**Closing tag:** `arc-0-drift-hygiene-strikethrough-sweep` (doc-only §3 strikethrough + §5 stanza authoring); the original infra resolution shipped under the task-def rev47 env-wiring arc.
**Closing commits, in order:** the task-def rev47 update set `SESSION_COOKIE_DOMAIN=vantagemind.ai` in the `environment[]` array (the prior value was `luciel.ai`, a stale carry-over from the pre-rebrand auth-cookie contract); rev49 is the current live revision and carries the same value. The Arc 0 doc-only commit on `docs/DRIFTS.md` carries the §3 strikethrough + this §5 stanza.
**Resolution:** The session-cookie domain was previously set to `luciel.ai`, which meant that after the VantageMind rebrand the magic-link-auth cookie set on `www.vantagemind.ai` would not be sent on subsequent same-origin requests (because the cookie's `Domain` attribute did not match the request host). The rev47 env-wiring corrected the value to `vantagemind.ai`, which is the apex domain that covers both `www.vantagemind.ai` (the marketing site) and `app.vantagemind.ai` (the future product subdomain — pre-provisioned). The `auth_service.py` consumer code is unchanged — it still reads `settings.session_cookie_domain` — the fix is a pure env-value correction.
**Pattern E:** Pure env-value correction — the task-def `environment[]` entry was replaced in-place with the corrected value; no new env var was added and no consumer code was rewritten. The fix lands cleanly because the prior cookie shape on `luciel.ai` was never reached by any production traffic (the rebrand cut over before any pilot customer hit the magic-link path).
**Validation evidence:** (a) `td-backend-rev49.json` `environment[]` array contains `{"name": "SESSION_COOKIE_DOMAIN", "value": "vantagemind.ai"}`; (b) live verification: a magic-link consume on `https://www.vantagemind.ai/auth/magic` sets the session cookie with `Domain=vantagemind.ai; Path=/; Secure; HttpOnly; SameSite=Lax`, confirmed via the Network tab response-header inspection on the partner's pilot login on 2026-05-20.
**Cross-refs:** `D-step-32-magic-link-auth-cookie-session` (parent Step 32 auth-arc drift — remains open as a genuine blocker per Phase 5 census); `~~D-magic-link-secret-env-vs-ssm-drift-2026-05-15~~` (sibling task-def rev47 wiring leg); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.5 "Magic-link authentication" paragraph (the doctrine home for the cookie-domain contract); CANONICAL_RECAP §6 "Auth cookie shape" row.

The consumer code in `billing_service.py` and `email_service.py` is unchanged — they still read `settings.marketing_site_url`, `settings.billing_success_url`, `settings.billing_cancel_url` — the fix is a pure env-value correction.
