### ~~D-email-service-transport-log-only-vs-sesv2-drift-2026-05-15~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-15 (shipped in the Step 30a.2 Phase D email-service hardening commit + task-def rev47 env-wiring; §3 strikethrough applied 2026-05-20 in the Arc 0 doc-hygiene sweep).
**Closing tag:** `arc-0-drift-hygiene-strikethrough-sweep` (doc-only §3 strikethrough + §5 stanza authoring); the original code + infra resolution shipped under the Step 30a.2 Phase D + task-def rev47 closing-tag chain.
**Closing commits, in order:** the Step 30a.2 Phase D commit added the `_transport()` method at L102 of `app/services/email_service.py` (the method reads the `LUCIEL_EMAIL_TRANSPORT` env var and returns either a `boto3.client('sesv2')` live transport or a log-only no-op transport, with the live path being the default and the log-only path being the explicit opt-out for local dev); the `EmailService.send(...)` call site was rewritten to dispatch via `self._transport()` rather than a direct `boto3.client('sesv2').send_email(...)` call. Task-def rev47 set `LUCIEL_EMAIL_TRANSPORT=sesv2` explicitly (the default is also `sesv2`, but the explicit value documents the production intent and makes the value visible in the task-def env-array audit surface). The Arc 0 doc-only commit on `docs/DRIFTS.md` carries the §3 strikethrough + this §5 stanza.
**Resolution:** Prior to the Step 30a.2 Phase D fix, the `email_service.py` shipped with a log-only transport hard-coded as the only path — transactional emails (magic-link, welcome, billing receipts) were logged to CloudWatch but never delivered to recipients. The `_transport()` method introduces a switch with `sesv2` as the production-default path; the log-only path is retained for local dev (where SES credentials are not present) and is selected by setting `LUCIEL_EMAIL_TRANSPORT=log_only`. The `MagicLinkError` exception class in the same file is unchanged — it covers the SES delivery-error case that the live transport can raise.
**Pattern E:** Additive — the `_transport()` method is new; the `EmailService.send(...)` call site is rewritten to use it, but the log-only path is preserved as a switch-arm rather than removed (which keeps the local-dev workflow functional). The task-def env-var addition is also additive (the prior absence of the var resulted in the hard-coded log-only path; the new explicit `sesv2` value selects the live path).
**Validation evidence:** (a) `grep -n "_transport" Luciel/app/services/email_service.py` returns matches at the method definition (L102) and the call site; (b) `grep -n "boto3.client('sesv2')" Luciel/app/services/email_service.py` returns a match inside the `_transport()` method body; (c) `td-backend-rev49.json` `environment[]` contains `{"name": "LUCIEL_EMAIL_TRANSPORT", "value": "sesv2"}`; (d) live verification: a magic-link request on the partner's pilot account on 2026-05-20 produced an SES `MessageId` log line in CloudWatch (log group `/ecs/luciel-backend`) and a delivered email in the partner's inbox within ~3 seconds.
**Cross-refs:** `D-welcome-email-subject-mojibake` (Arc 2 follow-up — the SES live path is now in use, but the welcome-email subject line carries a mojibake'd em-dash that will be scrubbed in Arc 2 backend hygiene); `D-rotation-exception-handlers-leak-dsn` (Arc 2 follow-up — sibling email-service exception-handler hardening); SES IAM (Arc 3 paired prod-touch — the production SES sandbox-removal request and the IAM-policy tighten will land in the Arc 3 paired arc); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.6 "Transactional email" paragraph (the doctrine home for the transport-switch contract); CANONICAL_RECAP §6 "Email delivery" row.

### ~~D-billing-webhook-luciel-instance-service-kwarg-mismatch-2026-05-15~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-15 (shipped in the Step 30a.2 Phase B cascade-integrity commit; §3 strikethrough applied 2026-05-20 in the Arc 0 doc-hygiene sweep).
**Closing tag:** `arc-0-drift-hygiene-strikethrough-sweep` (doc-only §3 strikethrough + §5 stanza authoring); the original code resolution shipped under the Step 30a.2 Phase B closing-tag chain.
**Closing commits, in order:** the Step 30a.2 Phase B commit corrected the `LucielInstanceService(...)` constructor call inside `app/services/billing_webhook_service.py` to pass the `admin_service=` kwarg explicitly (the prior call was `LucielInstanceService(self.db, self.admin_service)` positional, which silently bound the admin_service to the wrong parameter slot when the `LucielInstanceService.__init__` signature was extended to accept an audit-context kwarg in the Step 30a.1 audit-row enrichment arc); the new call shape is `LucielInstanceService(self.db, admin_service=self.admin_service)`. The Arc 0 doc-only commit on `docs/DRIFTS.md` carries the §3 strikethrough + this §5 stanza.
**Resolution:** The kwarg-mismatch surfaced as a subtle bug where the Tier-9 Leg-7 cascade hook (the `LucielInstance.is_active = False` flip on `SUBSCRIPTION_PILOT_REFUNDED`) was creating an `AdminAuditLog` row with the wrong `actor_admin_id` — the positional binding was passing the audit-context object into the `admin_service` slot, which meant `AdminAuditLog.actor_admin_id` was being populated from an unrelated context attribute. The kwarg-explicit call shape eliminates the binding ambiguity and the audit rows now carry the correct `actor_admin_id` (the system-actor sentinel for webhook-driven cascades). The Step 30a.1 `LucielInstanceService.__init__` signature itself is unchanged — the fix is purely on the call-site shape.
**Pattern E:** Pure call-site correction — the positional call was rewritten as a kwarg-explicit call; no new parameter was added and no consumer code beyond the single call site was rewritten. The audit-row contract is unchanged on the schema level — only the `actor_admin_id` value populated by this specific cascade path is corrected.
**Validation evidence:** (a) `grep -n "LucielInstanceService(self.db, admin_service=" Luciel/app/services/billing_webhook_service.py` returns a match at the corrected call site; (b) `grep -n "LucielInstanceService(self.db, self.admin_service)" Luciel/app/services/billing_webhook_service.py` returns zero matches (the old positional shape is fully replaced); (c) the Step 30a.2 Phase B contract test `tests/services/test_billing_webhook_service.py::test_pilot_refund_cascade_audit_row_actor` passes (it asserts `actor_admin_id == SYSTEM_ACTOR_ADMIN_ID` on the cascade-marker row); (d) live verification on the partner's pilot account confirmed that the most recent cascade-marker `AdminAuditLog` row carries `actor_admin_id = SYSTEM_ACTOR_ADMIN_ID` (the integer sentinel value defined in `app/policy/audit_actors.py`).
**Cross-refs:** `~~D-tier-9-leg-7-cascade-integrity-fix-2026-05-13~~` (sibling Step 30a.2 Phase B leg — the cascade-hook wiring this kwarg-correction made audit-correct); `~~D-cascade-integrity-incomplete-on-tier-9-leg-7-2026-05-14~~` (parent umbrella drift §5 L1450); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.11 "Cascade integrity" paragraph (the doctrine home for the cascade-marker audit-row contract); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 "Cascade integrity" row.

The `links` array addition and the primary-button label swap are both surgical edits with no regression risk to the existing Pricing nav-link, Logo home-link, or any other Nav element. The mobile-menu render loop is unchanged in structure — it inherits the new `/login` link automatically via the `links.map(...)` pattern.
**Validation evidence:** (a) `grep -n "to: \"/login\"" Luciel-Website/src/components/Nav.tsx` returns a match at the `links: NavLink[]` array entry (the `/login` link is between `/pricing` and `/about`); (b) `grep -n "Book a demo" Luciel-Website/src/components/Nav.tsx` returns matches only at the L83 + L115 retirement-comment annotations — zero rendered occurrences; (c) `grep -n "Start 90-day pilot" Luciel-Website/src/components/Nav.tsx` returns matches at the desktop primary-button (around L88-92) and the mobile primary-button (around L118-122); (d) live verification: opening `https://www.vantagemind.ai/` in a fresh browser session on 2026-05-20 22:55 EDT shows "Log in" as a peer nav-link between "Pricing" and "Company" on desktop and as a row in the mobile menu, with the primary action button reading "Start 90-day pilot" on both desktop and mobile, routing to `/pricing`; the live bundle grep for `Book a demo` returns 15 occurrences but all 15 are on Index/Luciel/Platform/Trust/Contact/Signup page bodies (the deferred §2 leg of `D-marketing-product-boundary-soft-2026-05-16`), not in the Nav region.
**Cross-refs:** `~~D-pricing-page-truth-2026-05-20~~` (sibling Arc 1 closure on the Pricing surface — the same `step-30a-6-tier-hierarchy-realignment` arc closed both, with this Nav-surface closure being the second occurrence of the same defect class on the website surface that `D-pricing-page-truth-2026-05-20` closed on the Pricing surface); `D-tier-semantics-realignment-2026-05-20` (umbrella tier-realignment drift); `D-marketing-product-boundary-soft-2026-05-16` (predecessor — the broader "marketing surface is out of step with the product surface" pattern; the Nav-surface leg is fully closed here, the broader Index/About copy-refresh leg remains deferred to a future marketing pass per L423); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.3 closure stanza (the password-auth + `/login` surface this closure defends); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.6 closure stanza (the tier-hierarchy realignment arc this closure landed in).

### Arc 2 — Backend Code Hygiene 2026-05-20

This arc lands the four backend code-layer closures surfaced across the Step 30a.3 → Step 30a.5 close-out (the welcome-email observability surface, the welcome-email subject rendering surface, the billing-webhook constructor surface, and the local-dev billing-shape test harness), all on `main` under the single closing tag `arc-2-backend-code-hygiene`. The arc ships four §3 strikethroughs + four §5 closure stanzas + six modified source files + one new contract-test file (`tests/security/test_email_service_redaction.py`). Two adjacent drifts were deferred deliberately rather than closed in this arc: (a) `D-stripe-checkout-no-email-validation-2026-05-18` was deferred to Arc 3 because adding `email_validator.validate_email(check_deliverability=True)` introduces a DNS MX-lookup dependency that pairs naturally with the SES sandbox exit milestone (`D-luciel-ecs-web-role-missing-ses-send-permission-2026-05-18`) and both touch the same `tier_provisioning_service` + `BillingWebhookService` boundary; (b) `D-cascade-marker-doc-claim-vs-active-flag-primary-2026-05-16` was deferred to Arc 7 because it is a pure doc-truthing correction whose right home is the cross-doc consistency sweep, not the code-layer arc. One genuine blocker remained in §3 untouched: `D-rotation-exception-handlers-leak-dsn-2026-05-12` stays open under the Step 32 secret-rotation runbook because the `_rot.py` script it targets is not yet in the repo — the drift is forward-referenced to that step, not deferrable into a hygiene arc. The closures land in this order: P1-security (`D-set-password-token-logged-plaintext-2026-05-17`, with the CloudWatch backlog-audit leg explicitly deferred to Arc 3 as a paired prod-touch), cosmetic-deliverability (`D-welcome-email-subject-mojibake-2026-05-17`, option (a) ASCII-subjects), P3-observability (`D-billing-webhook-service-stripe-attribute-error-2026-05-18`), and test-harness (`D-step-30a-billing-shape-test-moderation-config-failure-2026-05-13`).

### ~~D-set-password-token-logged-plaintext-2026-05-17~~

**Status:** RESOLVED (ingest-side) on 2026-05-20 in Arc 2 backend-hygiene. The token-bearing URL is now redacted at the emitter for every `INFO` success-path line and every `WARNING` SES-failure-path line across all three send paths (magic-link, welcome-set-password, pilot-refund); the in-flight emitter contract is pinned by `tests/security/test_email_service_redaction.py`. The historical CloudWatch backlog-audit leg of resolution-path step (c) — `aws logs filter-log-events --filter-pattern '?token='` against `/aws/ecs/luciel-backend` for the discovery-window 2026-05-13 → 2026-05-20, followed by an idempotent `status='revoked'` flip on any `user_invites`/`magic_link_tokens` row whose `jti` is found — is a paired prod-touch deliberately deferred to Arc 3 (where the partner drives the AWS-CLI side and the agent preps the PowerShell + SQL idempotency block). All future emissions from this point forward are safe; the open exposure window narrows to whatever tokens were minted between 2026-05-13 (the drift discovery date) and 2026-05-20 23:00 EDT (the Arc 2 commit landing time).
**Closing tag:** `arc-2-backend-code-hygiene` (this arc's single closing tag carrying all four backend-code closures and the four §3 strikethroughs).
**Closing commits, in order:** (1) `app/services/email_service.py` — added `urllib.parse` (`urlsplit`, `urlunsplit`, `parse_qsl`, `urlencode`) + `re` imports at the top of the module; defined `_redact_token_url(url: str) -> str` (~L60-90) that parses the URL, walks the query-string with `parse_qsl(keep_blank_values=True)`, replaces the value of any param whose key is `token`/`jti`/`signature` with the literal `<redacted>`, and re-emits via `urlencode` + `urlunsplit` (the urlencode pass renders `<redacted>` as `%3Credacted%3E` which is the intended cosmetic side effect — the JWT itself is gone); defined `_TOKEN_URL_PATTERN` (a compiled regex matching `https?://\S*?[?&](?:token|jti|signature)=\S+`) + `_redact_body(body: str) -> str` (~L102-120) that applies `_TOKEN_URL_PATTERN.sub` with a lambda calling `_redact_token_url` on each match; patched the six emitters in `send_magic_link_email` (success INFO + SES-fail WARNING) and `send_welcome_set_password_email` (success INFO + SES-fail WARNING, plus the two pilot-refund variants) to wrap every `url=%s` interpolation in `_redact_token_url(url)` and every `body=%s` interpolation in `_redact_body(body)`. (2) `tests/security/test_email_service_redaction.py` (NEW, 244 lines) — hybrid source-grep + functional `caplog` contract test with five source-grep families (helpers defined; no bare `magic_link_url` in `send_magic_link_email` logger.* calls; no bare `set_password_url` in `send_welcome_set_password_email` logger.* calls; every SES-fail `except` block in both methods wraps its `body=` in `_redact_body`; subject constants are ASCII-only) plus three `caplog`-based functional tests under `pytest.mark.skipif(not _IMPORT_OK, ...)` that import a stubbed `email_service`, send a magic-link with a known JWT, and assert no `?token=<JWT>` substring appears in any captured INFO/WARNING record. The source-grep coverage runs unconditionally so the contract holds even in sandbox environments without `pydantic_settings`. Both files land in the same `arc-2-backend-code-hygiene` commit alongside the §3 strikethrough on this drift's heading and this §5 stanza.
**Resolution:** The drift was a uniform observability defect across all three email-send paths in `app/services/email_service.py`. The fix applies the redaction at the lowest layer — the helper functions live in the same module and are called from inside the `f`-string / `%`-format interpolation passed to `logger.info` / `logger.warning`, so every code path that emits an email log line gets the redaction for free. The `token_jti` substitution recommended in resolution-path step (a) is implicit in the redaction shape: the surviving log line carries `url_token_redacted=...` (the URL with the JWT-bearing query param replaced by `<redacted>`), and the row-bound `jti` is recoverable through the operational `magic_link_tokens` table when an operator legitimately needs to trace a delivery to a specific token-mint. The `_redact_token_url` helper is intentionally narrow: it only redacts query-string values for `token`/`jti`/`signature`; path-bound tokens (none today) and fragment-bound tokens (none today) are out of scope by design, with the regex in `_redact_body` providing belt-and-braces coverage for any future code path that constructs a URL outside `_redact_token_url`'s parser. The CloudWatch-backlog audit (resolution-path step c) is the only piece deliberately not landed in this arc; it requires AWS-CLI access on the partner's laptop, an `aws logs filter-log-events` walk of the relevant log streams (the dispatcher's outermost stream and any worker streams that proxied an email task), and the matching SQL idempotency block. That work is queued for Arc 3 alongside the SES-sandbox exit and the Stripe checkout email-validation drift it pairs with.
**Pattern E:** Pure observability fix at the emitter layer. No schema change. No route change. No customer-visible surface change. The `_redact_token_url` helper is additive at the source-string level (a strict reduction of the disclosed log payload); the SES request payload is untouched (the customer-facing email still carries the live URL). The test file is additive; no existing test is changed.
**Validation evidence:** (a) standalone Python smoke of `_redact_token_url` + `_redact_body` against 8 test cases (magic-link URLs with bare JWT, with multi-param query, with no token, with token in second position, etc.) — all 8 pass with the JWT removed; (b) inline source-grep against `app/services/email_service.py` confirms all five contract families: helpers defined (`grep -n "def _redact_token_url\|def _redact_body" app/services/email_service.py` returns two matches), no bare `magic_link_url` in `send_magic_link_email`'s logger calls (`grep -n "magic_link_url" app/services/email_service.py` returns only inside `_redact_token_url(magic_link_url)` wrappers), no bare `set_password_url` in welcome-set-password logger calls (same pattern), every SES-fail `except` block in both methods wraps its `body=` in `_redact_body(...)`, and subject constants `SUBJECT_WELCOME_SET_PASSWORD` / `SUBJECT_INVITE_SET_PASSWORD` / `SUBJECT_RESET_PASSWORD` are ASCII-only after the mojibake fix lands in the same commit; (c) the new test file's source-grep coverage runs unconditionally and gates the contract on every future change to `email_service.py`. Pending validation: the post-deploy live smoke against a freshly-issued magic-link in CloudWatch confirming the rendered log line carries `url=...%3Credacted%3E...` not the live JWT (queued for the Arc 3 deploy, not load-bearing on Arc 2 closure).
**Cross-refs:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (the Option B welcome-email mechanic — the design contract this closure restores); `~~D-magic-link-only-auth-no-password-fallback-2026-05-16~~` (predecessor — the Step 30a.3 closure that introduced the welcome-set-password path; this closure now hardens the observability layer of that path); `~~D-team-self-serve-incomplete-invite-ui-missing-2026-05-16~~` (the closure under which this drift was discovered); `~~D-welcome-email-subject-mojibake-2026-05-17~~` (sibling §5 Arc 2 closure landing in the same commit — the two email-service drifts were targeted together because both touch the same module and benefit from a single test-file landing); `D-secret-disclosure-recurrence-2026-05-12` (structural-pattern sibling — the hardening discipline that drift records now applies to the email-service emitters); `D-stripe-checkout-no-email-validation-2026-05-18` (Arc 3 sibling — the CloudWatch backlog-audit leg deferred to Arc 3 pairs with the SES sandbox exit which pairs with the email-deliverability drift); `D-rotation-exception-handlers-leak-dsn-2026-05-12` (structural-pattern sibling that stays open in §3 because it targets the `_rot.py` script not yet in the repo — Step 32 secret-rotation runbook is the proper closure home).

### ~~D-welcome-email-subject-mojibake-2026-05-17~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-20 in Arc 2 backend-hygiene via resolution-path option (a) — ASCII-only subjects. The three subject constants `SUBJECT_WELCOME_SET_PASSWORD`, `SUBJECT_INVITE_SET_PASSWORD`, and `SUBJECT_RESET_PASSWORD` now contain only ASCII characters: U+2019 (right-single-quote) was replaced with `'` (U+0027) and U+2014 (em-dash) was replaced with `-` (U+002D). Body copy continues to use typographer's quotes and em-dashes because the SES `Body.Text.Data` and `Body.Html.Data` payloads are wire-carried with explicit `Charset="UTF-8"` in a Content-Type header that Gmail decodes correctly — only the `Simple.Subject` header path was wire-degraded and only that path needed the ASCII narrowing. Option (b) (`send_raw_email` with `email.message.EmailMessage` to emit `=?UTF-8?B?...?=` encoded-word subjects) is the cleaner long-term shape but its larger change footprint did not justify the cost given today's brand-voice case — revisit when a designer joins or the rendered-subject typography becomes a deliberate brand-voice surface.
**Closing tag:** `arc-2-backend-code-hygiene` (shared with the three sibling Arc 2 closures).
**Closing commits, in order:** Single edit on `app/services/email_service.py` — the three subject-constant assignments were rewritten in place (the `Final[str]` annotation and the assignment-target name are unchanged; only the right-hand-side literal is narrowed to ASCII). `SUBJECT_MAGIC_LINK` already carried an ASCII-safe value (`Welcome to VantageMind - set your password`) after a prior edit and was not touched in this arc. The §3 strikethrough on this drift's heading and this §5 stanza land in the same commit.
**Resolution:** The mojibake observation was a Gmail rendering of the SES wire layer's lossy handling of `Simple.Subject` with non-ASCII bytes — Gmail's MIME decoder fell back to a Latin-1 table because the SMTP `Content-Transfer-Encoding` chain did not declare UTF-8 at the header level (only at the body level, which Gmail honoured correctly). Option (a) is the cheapest and most predictable fix because it removes the failure mode entirely at the source: an ASCII subject cannot be wire-degraded. The brand voice on the Pricing surface, the marketing site, and the body of every transactional email continues to use typographer's quotes and em-dashes — only the eight-or-so characters of the rendered subject line revert to ASCII, which is a defensible brand-voice tradeoff for a young domain where deliverability hardening is more valuable than typography fidelity (Gmail's spam classifier weights non-ASCII subjects on transactional brand emails as a mild negative signal, especially when the SES wire layer mis-renders them).
**Pattern E:** Pure copy fix at the emitter layer. No schema change. No route change. No customer-visible flow change. The invite-redemption surface, the welcome-email link target, and the SES request shape are all unchanged.
**Validation evidence:** (a) `grep -nP "\\\\u2019|\\\\u2014" app/services/email_service.py` returns matches only inside body-string literals, not inside any subject-constant assignment; (b) `grep -n "SUBJECT_WELCOME_SET_PASSWORD\\|SUBJECT_INVITE_SET_PASSWORD\\|SUBJECT_RESET_PASSWORD" app/services/email_service.py` shows all three RHS values are ASCII-only; (c) the new `tests/security/test_email_service_redaction.py` source-grep family asserts subject constants contain no U+2019 or U+2014 codepoints, gating the contract on every future change. Pending validation: a post-deploy live smoke against a Gmail address showing the rendered subject reads `You've been invited to VantageMind - set your password` literally (no `Æ` or `ù` fallback glyphs).
**Cross-refs:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (the Option B welcome-email mechanic — the rendered-subject surface this closure defends); `~~D-set-password-token-logged-plaintext-2026-05-17~~` (sibling §5 Arc 2 closure landing in the same commit — paired naturally because both touch the same email-service module); `~~D-team-self-serve-incomplete-invite-ui-missing-2026-05-16~~` (the closure under which this drift was discovered); `D-marketing-product-boundary-soft-2026-05-16` (sibling marketing-surface drift — the brand-voice tradeoff this closure makes for deliverability is consistent with the broader "young domain, ship pragmatically" posture that drift records).

### ~~D-billing-webhook-service-stripe-attribute-error-2026-05-18~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-20 in Arc 2 backend-hygiene by extending `BillingWebhookService.__init__` to accept an optional `stripe_client: StripeClient | None = None` parameter, with a default-resolution path that calls `get_stripe_client()` when the caller does not inject one, and always sets `self.stripe` on the instance. Both call sites in `app/api/v1/billing.py` (the bad-signature audit path at L194 and the main dispatch at L276) were updated to thread the same `stripe_client` singleton through to the constructor. The pre-existing try/except around `self.stripe.retrieve_subscription(...)` on the primary subscription-resolution path remains in place as defense-in-depth for genuine Stripe-unreachable conditions (network blips, 5xx from Stripe), but the attribute-access defect that previously short-circuited the try-block on every invocation is gone.
**Closing tag:** `arc-2-backend-code-hygiene` (shared with the three sibling Arc 2 closures).
**Closing commits, in order:** (1) `app/services/billing_webhook_service.py` — added `from app.integrations.stripe import StripeClient, get_stripe_client` import; extended `__init__(self, db: Session, stripe_client: StripeClient | None = None)` signature; the body always sets `self.stripe = stripe_client if stripe_client is not None else get_stripe_client()` so the attribute is structurally-present on every constructed instance. (2) `app/api/v1/billing.py` at L124 — comment-only edit: `luciel.ai` → `vantagemind.ai` (rebrand residue caught while editing the file). (3) `app/api/v1/billing.py` at L194 — the bad-signature audit path's instantiation now reads `BillingWebhookService(db, stripe_client=stripe_client)._record_unknown_event(...)`. (4) `app/api/v1/billing.py` at L276 — the main webhook dispatch now reads `BillingWebhookService(db, stripe_client=stripe_client).handle(event_dict)`. The §3 strikethrough on this drift's heading and this §5 stanza land in the same commit.
**Resolution:** The defect was a constructor-layer omission: the resolve method's `self.stripe.retrieve_subscription(...)` call assumed an attribute that `__init__` never set on any path. The fix takes the recommended shape from resolution-path step (a) ("always set `self.stripe = stripe_client`") and adds the default-resolution branch so existing call sites that did not previously pass a `stripe_client` keyword still get a working instance — the route handler in `billing.py` already resolves the singleton via `get_stripe_client()` at the top of the request scope, so the keyword-forwarding pattern is the natural shape and avoids a second singleton lookup inside the constructor. The optional AST-style assertion test from resolution-path step (b) was not added in this arc because the constructor-level fix is structurally type-checked (the `StripeClient | None` annotation plus the unconditional `self.stripe = ...` assignment makes the attribute provably-present on every instance under any static-analysis pass); a future Pillar 4 audit-coverage commit can land the AST assertion if the broader pattern surfaces elsewhere.
**Pattern E:** Pure constructor-layer fix plus two surgical call-site edits. No route signature change. No schema change. No customer-visible behaviour change (live behaviour is improved because the primary subscription-resolution path now works as designed instead of falling through the try-except to the fallback path on every checkout). The fallback path remains in place as defense-in-depth.
**Validation evidence:** (a) `grep -n "self\\.stripe" app/services/billing_webhook_service.py` returns the unconditional `__init__` write at the constructor + the `_on_checkout_completed` read site, with no other writes — the attribute is structurally-present on every instance; (b) `grep -n "BillingWebhookService(" app/api/v1/billing.py` returns both call sites at L194 and L276, both passing `stripe_client=stripe_client`; (c) `grep -n "from app.integrations.stripe import" app/services/billing_webhook_service.py` confirms the `StripeClient` + `get_stripe_client` imports landed at the top of the module. Pending validation: a post-deploy live webhook replay (e.g. the next Stripe Checkout Completed event from a real or test-clock checkout) showing the CloudWatch trace no longer contains the `AttributeError: 'BillingWebhookService' object has no attribute 'stripe'` line — the primary path should resolve cleanly via `self.stripe.retrieve_subscription(...)` and the fallback path should not fire (queued for the Arc 3 deploy).
**Cross-refs:** Step 30a.1 (Stripe checkout primitives — the surface this service backs); Step 30a.4 (the Team-tier $100 paid walk that did not surface this drift, confirming the defect's introduction window is 30a.4 → 30a.5); `~~D-step-30a-billing-shape-test-moderation-config-failure-2026-05-13~~` (sibling §5 Arc 2 closure on the same billing-test surface — the moderation-fixture fix in the same arc lets the billing-shape test suite run cleanly in the local-dev env, which is the natural verification harness for this closure); `D-stripe-checkout-no-email-validation-2026-05-18` (Arc 3 sibling deferred to the SES-sandbox-exit pairing); `~~D-team-self-serve-incomplete-invite-ui-missing-2026-05-16~~` (the broader Step 30a.5 closure under which this drift was originally surfaced).

### ~~D-step-30a-billing-shape-test-moderation-config-failure-2026-05-13~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-20 in Arc 2 backend-hygiene by adding `import os` + `os.environ.setdefault("MODERATION_PROVIDER", "null")` at the top of `tests/api/test_step30a_billing_shape.py` before any `from app...` import. The `null` provider value returns a `NullModerationProvider()` cleanly from `ModerationGate.from_settings(settings)` so the transitive import chain `app.api.router` → `app.api.v1.chat_widget` → `ModerationGate.from_settings` resolves a structurally-valid provider in the bare local-dev env without requiring `OPENAI_API_KEY` or `OPENAI_MODERATION_*`. CI environments that already set `MODERATION_PROVIDER=keyword` or `MODERATION_PROVIDER=openai` win because `setdefault` is non-destructive — the existing value is preserved.
**Closing tag:** `arc-2-backend-code-hygiene` (shared with the three sibling Arc 2 closures).
**Closing commits, in order:** Single edit on `tests/api/test_step30a_billing_shape.py` — added `import os` immediately after the module docstring and added `os.environ.setdefault("MODERATION_PROVIDER", "null")` as the next executable statement, before any `from app...` import. The `setdefault` semantics match the same pattern already used at the top of several Step 30 / Step 31 test modules for `DATABASE_URL`, so the convention is consistent across the test tree. The §3 strikethrough on this drift's heading and this §5 stanza land in the same commit.
**Resolution:** The drift was a test-harness-fixture defect, not a production-code defect — `app.services.moderation_gate.ModerationGate.from_settings` correctly fast-fails under `MODERATION_PROVIDER=null` per the Step 30d boot-safety contract, but the `test_router_registered_on_v1_aggregate` smoke test imports `app.main` (which transitively imports the moderation factory) without setting any provider-default. The right-shape fix is to set the default at the test module's top so the harness picks a structurally-valid provider whenever the developer runs the local-dev `sqlite+null-moderation` env, while leaving CI's explicit provider configuration untouched via `setdefault`'s non-destructive semantics. The alternative shape (a session-scoped `autouse=True` fixture in `tests/conftest.py` setting the default) was considered but rejected for this arc because the per-module `setdefault` is more discoverable (the test file declares its own env requirements at the top) and matches the existing convention for `DATABASE_URL` defaults already scattered through the test tree. A future test-infrastructure consolidation commit could lift this into `conftest.py` if the pattern grows beyond three or four modules.
**Pattern E:** Pure test-harness fix at the test-module's top. No source-tree change. No schema change. No fixture-tree restructuring. The change is strictly additive (the `import os` and `setdefault` line execute before any `app.*` import; they cannot affect any other test module's behaviour, and they cannot affect production code because production never imports the test tree).
**Validation evidence:** (a) `grep -n "MODERATION_PROVIDER" tests/api/test_step30a_billing_shape.py` returns the new `setdefault` line at the top of the module; (b) the bare local-dev invocation `DATABASE_URL=sqlite:///:memory: pytest tests/api/test_step30a_billing_shape.py::test_router_registered_on_v1_aggregate` now resolves the import chain without `MODERATION_PROVIDER` set explicitly; (c) the existing CI invocation patterns (which set `MODERATION_PROVIDER=keyword` explicitly) are unchanged in behaviour because `setdefault` is a no-op when the key is already present. Pending validation: a clean run of the full backend test suite against the post-Arc-2 HEAD with no provider env-var explicit, confirming the smoke test passes without any other regression.
**Cross-refs:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a row (the implementation arc the failing test belongs to); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30d row (the boot-safe moderation contract this fixture closure aligns with); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 31.2 row (the test run that originally surfaced the pre-existing failure); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.9 (boot-safety contract — the production-side guarantee this test fixture is no longer mistakenly enforcing in dev); `~~D-billing-webhook-service-stripe-attribute-error-2026-05-18~~` (sibling §5 Arc 2 closure on the same billing-test surface — the billing-shape test suite is the natural verification harness for the webhook-service closure); `D-rotation-exception-handlers-leak-dsn-2026-05-12` (sibling §3 entry that stays open as a genuine blocker because it targets the `_rot.py` script not yet in the repo — Step 32 secret-rotation runbook is its proper closure home).

### ~~D-intro-fee-scaling-to-per-tier-2026-05-16~~

**Status:** REJECTED on 2026-05-20 (Step 30a.7 diligence pass).
**Closing tag (cut and pushed on the doc-truthing commit):** none yet — folded into the broader `step-30a-7-cascade-integrity-hardening-complete` arc as a diligence-pass doctrine revert rather than a new tag.
**Closing commits, in order:** `Luciel` doc-truthing commit reverting (a) CANONICAL_RECAP §14 "Intro offer" paragraph to flat-$100-across-all-tiers (with the per-tier scaling rationale preserved as an audit-trail sentence pointing to this stanza); (b) CANONICAL_RECAP §14 "Annual cadence shape" paragraph to remove the "$100 / $300 / $1,000" enumeration from the same-paid-intro-fee callout; (c) CANONICAL_RECAP §14 "Intro refund policy" paragraph to remove the per-tier refund-amount enumeration; (d) ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 "Paid-intro trial mechanics" paragraph to revert to the Step 30a.2-base shape (single `stripe_price_intro_fee` SSM key, `INTRO_FEE_CENTS = 10000` constant, no `INTRO_FEE_BY_TIER` map); (e) DRIFTS §3 "D-intro-fee-scaling-to-per-tier-2026-05-16" entry strikethrough + forward pointer to this stanza. `Luciel-Website` paired commit on `src/pages/Pricing.tsx`: the three tier cards each carry the same `"90-day pilot for $100 CAD — fully refundable"` bullet (no per-tier $100/$300/$1000 enumeration); the Step 30a.7 closing-tag comment block above the `tiers` array records this rejection alongside the four resolved Pricing-surface drifts in this arc.
**Rejection rationale (partner direction 2026-05-20, verbatim short form):** "keep flat 100 intro fee for all tiers revert the doctorine." Long form (agent recommendation accepted by partner): the per-tier scaling complexity ($300 Team Price + $1,000 Company Price + 2 new SSM keys + `INTRO_FEE_BY_TIER` map in `BillingService` + tier-scaled `refunded_amount_cents` in the `SUBSCRIPTION_PILOT_REFUNDED` audit row + extended contract tests) is not justified by current evidence — no Team or Company customer has yet asked for a higher pilot commitment, and the strategic argument that "a Company paying $1,000 intro is a different buyer than one toe-dipping at $100" is a hypothesis without market evidence. The doctrine returns to the Step 30a.2-base uniform $100 shape that was always the live code reality; the simpler shape preserves the marketing-page narrative ("$100 to try Luciel for 90 days, fully refundable") that has been the consistent buyer-facing story across the Pricing surface from 2026-05-15 onward. Revisit gate: if Company-tier buyers ask for a higher pilot commitment (e.g. as a signal of seriousness to their procurement), reopen this drift with a new id and the same closure path the original carried.
**Resolution:** Live behaviour is unchanged — the backend has carried the flat-$100 shape continuously since Step 30a.2 base on 2026-05-14. What this rejection closes is a four-day drift between the doc-truth (per-tier scaling locked in CANONICAL_RECAP and ARCHITECTURE on 2026-05-16) and the code-truth (flat $100 in `BillingService`). The doctrine now matches the code; the three-way alignment between CANONICAL_RECAP §14, ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13, and `app/services/billing_service.py` is restored. No Stripe Dashboard work, no SSM puts, no code change, no audit-row schema change, no contract-test change required.
**Pattern E:** Pure doc revert. Surgical paragraph-level edits in three places (CANONICAL_RECAP §14 three paragraphs, ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 one paragraph, DRIFTS §3 strikethrough + forward pointer). The marketing surface (`Pricing.tsx`) is updated in the paired commit to remove any per-tier intro-fee enumeration; the Step 30a.5 commit message that mentioned "Start 90-day pilot for $1,000" on the Company CTA is preserved in git history (and is incorrect against the post-rejection shape — the live CTA from Step 30a.7 onward reads "Start 90-day pilot" with no per-tier dollar amount).
**Validation evidence:** (a) `grep -n "INTRO_FEE_BY_TIER" Luciel/app/` returns zero matches — the constant was never implemented; (b) `grep -n "intro_fee_team\|intro_fee_company" Luciel/app/` returns zero matches — the per-tier SSM keys were never wired; (c) the Step 30a.7 doc-truthing commit removes all per-tier scaling language from CANONICAL_RECAP and ARCHITECTURE; (d) the paired `Luciel-Website` commit updates Pricing.tsx to show the same `$100 CAD` intro across all three tier cards; (e) live verification: a Team-tier Checkout in Stripe Live mode produces a session with a single `$100.00 CAD` one-time line item alongside the Team recurring Price, not `$300.00`.

The owner opens `/app`, lands on `/app/company` (CompanyTab gated by `subscription.tier == 'company' AND scope_assignment.role IN ('tenant_admin', 'owner')` per design §11 Q5), creates Domains via the inline form (`POST /api/v1/admin/domains/self-serve`, capped at 50 per `DOMAIN_COUNT_CAP_BY_TIER`, slug regex `^[a-z0-9][a-z0-9-]*[a-z0-9]$` enforced at the Pydantic layer, free-text `display_name` up to 64 chars carried alongside), and invites one department lead per Domain via the per-Domain affordance — the invite carries `role='department_lead'` + `domain_id=<that Domain>` honoured by `InviteService.create_invite` and stamped onto the redeemed `ScopeAssignment.role` by `redeem_invite`. Each department lead clicks their welcome-set-password email, lands on `/auth/set-password?token=…`, sets a password, mints a `luciel_session` cookie that resolves through the new scope-first `_resolve_tenant_for_user` (the post-smoke P0 fix) to `tenant_id=<Company tenant>`, and lands on `/app/team` scoped to their Domain — where TeamTab now also renders for `role='department_lead'` callers per the same Q5 gate. Each lead invites their own agents via the same `POST /api/v1/admin/invites` surface from Step 30a.4, this time with `role='teammate'` and `domain_id=<lead's Domain>`. Each agent's redemption mints a `ScopeAssignment(role='teammate', domain_id=<lead's Domain>)`, and the agent lands on `/app` scoped to that Domain only. The Company admin's CompanyTab Domain cards render the route-level rollup line `{N} agents · {M} invites pending` (the post-smoke F2 sibling fix), and the Team-tab pending-invite rows render role + domain_id pill badges (the post-smoke F3 sibling fix), so the cascading invite shape is legible at a glance from the owner side. **Live evidence (2026-05-18, captured this commit):** Aryan completed a real $1,000 paid Company-tier signup on the prod wire against tenant `co-354c5056` (Stripe Checkout against the live Company-tier intro Price, owner user_id `6fa8a037-fcb4-4d71-a71f-cf7a71f54d02` cookied through to `/app/company`), the post-smoke fix arc closed the three sibling drifts the walk surfaced, and the re-smoke walk against the same tenant with a fresh invitee redemption is queued for the next session segment as the final closure observation. **Smoke probe proof:** the deployed OpenAPI schema and Vite bundle markers (above) confirm both the core Step 30a.5 shape and the post-smoke fix shape are on the live wire. The CompanyTab tier-AND-role gate is the design's load-bearing decision that prevents a department-lead cookie under a Company tenant from seeing every Domain in the tenant (design §11 Q5).
**Pattern E:** Additive at every layer. The `users.password_hash` column from Step 30a.3 and the `user_invites` table from Step 30a.4 are unchanged. The Step 30a.5 migration adds one column on `user_invites` (`role`) with a server-side default so existing rows backfill consistently, and appends two action constants to the audit whitelist. The cookie shape, the route signatures (except for the additive `role` + `domain_id` fields on `POST /admin/invites`), the audit-row schema, and the Step 31.2 middleware contract are all unchanged. No row mutation on pre-existing data beyond the column-default backfill on the new migration.

**Resolution:** A Team-tier customer who has paid the $300 intro fee can now invite teammates end-to-end without founder involvement. The admin opens `/app`, lands on the Team tab inside `src/pages/Dashboard.tsx`, types a teammate email + display name, clicks Send — the website POSTs to `/api/v1/admin/invites`, the cookie-gated route resolves the admin's tenant+domain via `_resolve_invite_actor`, the service mints an HS256 JWT with `purpose='invite'` 24h TTL via `mint_set_password_token`, persists a `user_invites` row with 7-day `expires_at` (row is the source of truth on expiry; JWT TTL stays 24h and resend rotates `token_jti`), and SES delivers the welcome-set-password email with the invite link. The teammate clicks the link, lands on `/auth/set-password?token=…` reusing the existing Step 30a.3 `SetPassword.tsx` page, sets a password ≥ 8 chars, and the `/auth/set-password` route's invite branch consumes the token, marks the invite redeemed, provisions a User + Agent + ScopeAssignment under the inviter's tenant + domain, emits `INVITE_REDEEMED` audit row, mints a session cookie, and redirects to `/dashboard` where the new teammate sees their Team-scope view. The admin's Team tab refreshes via `listAgents(true) + listInvites()` and shows the new agent under "Active agents" and the invite under "Pending invites" flipped to redeemed (or the pending row disappears, depending on filter). Resend and Revoke work end-to-end: resend rotates `token_jti`, re-emits SES, leaves `status='pending'`; revoke flips `status='revoked'` and blocks any subsequent redemption attempt with 401. Instance-cap gate (TIER_INSTANCE_CAPS[TIER_TEAM]=10) enforced at create-time; scope-isolation gate enforced via `_resolve_invite_actor` returning the caller's tenant_id+domain_id from the active ScopeAssignment; replay-prevention enforced via single-use `token_jti` UNIQUE constraint + `status='pending'` predicate in the redemption SQL. **Live $300 paid Team-tier evidence is carved out as `D-step-30a-4-live-300-paid-evidence-pending-intro-fee-scaling-2026-05-17`** per the locked Option-1 closure shape: today's closure rests on 28 backend contract tests + dev-Postgres e2e harness + 7 website contract tests + 33/33 website-suite green + clean build + clean typecheck. The live $300 paid round-trip catches up at the very-end Stripe-Prices sweep, per Aryan's directive "we can start with step 30a.4 we dont need to change our prices we can do that at the very end."
**Pattern E:** Additive end-to-end — new `user_invites` table, new service module, four new cookie-gated routes, new `/auth/set-password` invite-purpose branch, new audit action constants, new website API client functions, new TeamTab pending-invites section. The existing `teammate_email` overload on `POST /admin/luciel-instances` is retained with `DeprecationWarning` (removal scheduled Step 30a.5). The cookie shape and Step 31.2 middleware contract are unchanged. No row mutation on pre-existing data; the migration only adds a new table and indexes.

**Resolution:** Password authentication is now the daily-login primitive across all three tiers (Individual $100, Team $300, Company $1,000); magic-link is retired as a daily-login primitive and survives only as the bootstrap and recovery primitive. Password is mandatory at signup — not opt-in — gated by the Option B welcome-email mechanic that issues the set-password link **after** `checkout.session.completed` commits the `User` row, eliminating the Stripe-Checkout → webhook race window that Option A URL-exchange would have surfaced. The Stripe Checkout success page (`/onboarding`) is passive ("Check your email") and grants no cookied `/app` session; the buyer must redeem the welcome email's `/auth/set-password?token=…` link, set a ≥8-char password, and auto-route to `/dashboard`. The cookie shape and Step 31.2 middleware contract are unchanged. **Live E2E proof (2026-05-16 ≈21:06 EDT, captured this commit):** Aryan completed a real $100 paid Individual signup in incognito on `vantagemind.ai` end-to-end — Pricing → Stripe Checkout → `/onboarding` landing → welcome-set-password email delivered → `/auth/set-password?token=…` accepted password → auto-route to `/dashboard` → sign-out → `/login` with email+password → back on `/dashboard`. All four gates green on the prod surface. **Smoke probe proof:** `POST https://api.vantagemind.ai/api/v1/auth/forgot-password` with valid-TLD payload returns `HTTP/1.1 200` with neutral body `{"ok":true,"message":"If an account exists, a reset link has been sent."}` — confirms the route is mounted, the `SKIP_AUTH_PATHS` exemption works, argon2id + JWT init did not crash the container, and the no-enumeration contract holds. **Smoke deploy lesson (closed in `cfe51fd`):** Pydantic `EmailStr` (`email-validator`) rejects reserved TLDs per RFC 2606 (`.invalid`, `.test`, `.example`, `.localhost`); both deploy scripts (`scripts/deploy_30a3.ps1`, `scripts/deploy_30a3_rollforward.ps1`) now use a real-domain smoke email (response is neutral 200 either way, so this does not hit a real inbox).
**Pattern E:** Additive end-to-end — new column (nullable), new service surface, new routes, new pages. The existing magic-link flow is unchanged structurally; only the post-checkout `_on_checkout_completed` mint path was retargeted from magic-link to welcome-set-password (the helper itself remains for forgot-password use). The cookie shape is identical, so Step 31.2's middleware contract holds without modification. No row mutation on pre-existing data: existing users carry `password_hash IS NULL` until they next pass through the forgot-password recovery surface.
**Cross-refs:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.3 row (the design home this drift closes against); CANONICAL_RECAP §13.1 T1 / T5 (the acceptance scenarios this closure underwrites for the Team and Company tiers — invite-acceptance is the first password-set event using the same `/auth/set-password` route with `purpose=invite`); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 “Auth model” (the implementation home — Option B welcome-email mechanic locked there); `D-magic-link-auth-cookie-session-2026-05-13` (the predecessor drift on cookie session shape — stays OPEN through Step 32a's broader auth story; this closure carves out the password-fallback + mandatory-at-signup slice only); `D-team-self-serve-incomplete-invite-ui-missing-2026-05-16` and `D-company-self-serve-incomplete-org-building-ui-missing-2026-05-16` (strict dependents this closure unblocks — both invite flows now re-use the `/auth/set-password` route with `purpose=invite`); `D-deploy-script-jq-filter-container-name-mismatch-2026-05-16` (sibling deploy-toolchain drift — `cf1ba2c` hardened the C8 script against the container-rename failure mode by dynamically verifying `ContainerName="luciel-backend"` and asserting pre/post-rewrite image swap; the sibling drift's broader fix on every `scripts/deploy_*.sh` remains OPEN).

**Pattern E:** Three additive columns + one additive index; no destructive operations; existing rows backfill as `deactivated_at IS NULL` (active state). No row mutation on pre-existing data — the cascade extension writes timestamps it never wrote before, and pre-existing soft-deleted rows are not retroactively touched.

### ~~D-trial-policy-mixed-per-tier-2026-05-14~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-14 (code-side closure; Stripe-side operational close follows at GATE 3 — see `D-stripe-live-account-not-yet-activated-2026-05-13` §3 annotation)
**Closing tag (planned):** `step-30a-2-trial-and-purge-complete` on the doc-truthing commit that follows the Stripe-activation operational close.
**Closing commits, in order:** `3afc866` (step 30a.2 — `billing_service.py` `TRIAL_DAYS` map replaced with `INTRO_TRIAL_DAYS = 90` constant + `intro_fee_price_id` resolution + `is_first_time_customer(email)` gate via `func.lower(User.email)` + Stripe Option A line-item assembly for first-time signups; `app/core/config.py` adds `stripe_price_intro_fee` setting; new `tests/api/test_first_time_gate.py` + updated `tests/api/test_step30a_1_tiered_self_serve_shape.py`) → this doc-truthing commit.
**Resolution:** Trial policy is uniform across all six (tier, cadence) primitives: $100 CAD one-time intro + 90-day trial on the recurring price, gated to first-time-ever customers by case-insensitive email lookup against the historical customers table. Cancel + rejoin = standard plan rate with no second intro (Pattern E for customer history: the `is_first_time_customer` predicate is a read against persisted customer rows, never a write). The seven-Price Stripe design (six recurring + one intro_fee) is locked in code; the seven live Prices + seven SSM puts land at GATE 3 when Stripe activation completes.
**Pattern E:** Internal-only application-state replacement (no audit-row footprint, no live customer rows touched). The `is_first_time_customer` gate reads existing customer rows; it does not write to them. The pre-30a.2 `TRIAL_DAYS` constant is replaced because the audit chain begins at the Stripe webhook event, not at the trial-policy decision.
**Cross-refs:** CANONICAL_RECAP §14 (Monetization — intro-offer bullet added in this same commit), CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.2 row, ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (Billing surface — extended in this same commit with the intro_fee + 90d trial mechanics), `D-stripe-live-account-not-yet-activated-2026-05-13` (upstream operational gate — the seven-Price design lands in code first, then the Stripe activation form lands the seven live Prices), `~~D-cancellation-cascade-incomplete-conversations-claims-2026-05-14~~` (sibling Step 30a.2 closure — the cascade half of the same step).

### ~~D-retention-purge-worker-missing-2026-05-09~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-14 by Step 30a.2

**Closing commits:** `3afc866` (step 30a.2 — `app/worker/tasks/retention.py::run_retention_purge` Celery task; `AdminService.hard_delete_tenant_after_retention` method walks `deactivated_at < now() - 90 days` and hard-deletes leaf-first; `app/worker/celery_app.py` beat schedule `retention-purge-nightly` at `crontab(hour=8, minute=0)` UTC; `Dockerfile.worker` injects `--beat` so the embedded beat scheduler enqueues the nightly tick) → this doc-truthing commit.
**Resolution:** The scheduled retention purge worker exists. The policy in `app/policy/retention.py` is now enforced by a 08:00 UTC nightly Celery beat schedule that walks tenants with `deactivated_at < now() - INTERVAL '90 days'` and hard-deletes them leaf-first through the cascade-complete soft-delete graph that `~~D-cancellation-cascade-incomplete-conversations-claims-2026-05-14~~` closed in this same commit. The retention worker is therefore load-bearing on the cascade extension; the two drifts closed as a single Step 30a.2 deliverable, in the order (cascade first, then the worker that depends on it). AdminAuditLog rows survive the purge per the audit-chain integrity contract in §3.4. New open drift `D-celery-beat-single-replica-coupling-2026-05-14` records the embedded-beat single-replica constraint as known future-debt.
**Pattern E:** The retention worker is additive (a new Celery task + a new beat schedule entry + a `--beat` flag on the worker container). Hard-delete on tenants past the retention window is the explicit §4.4 exception to soft-delete-by-default — the design always commit to this; the implementation finally honours it. AdminAuditLog rows are intentionally preserved across the hard-delete because the audit chain must remain walkable after a tenant departs the platform.

### ~~D-ci-ast-job-red-on-main-2026-05-08~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-10 (this commit on `step-30b-cleanup`)
**Closing commit:** `9e9cb9e` (this branch's commit (b): `.github/workflows/ci.yml` step "run http_client params + health pytest tests" gains a step-scoped `env: DATABASE_URL: "sqlite:///:memory:"`)
**Closing verification:** Next CI run on the merge of `step-30b-cleanup` into `main` must show the AST job green.
**Raised by:** Discovery on 2026-05-10 while watching the first widget-cdn-deploy run end-to-end. The `gh run list --branch main` history showed the `ast-and-unit-tests` job had been silently red on every push to `main` for at least nine consecutive merges (2026-05-08 `5f297b73` through 2026-05-10 `85990c4`), in every case interrupted by the same collection error: `tests/api/test_health.py` imports `app.main`, which transitively imports `app.core.config` and instantiates `settings = Settings()` at module-load time; `Settings.database_url: str` has no default, so a CI runner with no `DATABASE_URL` exported fails the Pydantic field validator before any test runs.
**Why it persisted unseen:** The CI gate landed in Step 29 D (`89afbae`) at the same time `tests/api/test_health.py` was added. Both pieces work locally because development environments export `DATABASE_URL` from `.env`. The first push to `main` after Step 29 D was the first run with a bare-runner environment, and the failure was already in place. Subsequent merges all failed for the same reason and no one watched the run output. This is the doctrine "red signals stop being signals when ignored" failure mode — visible only because the widget-cdn-deploy run brought the Actions tab back under daily attention.
**Resolution:** `tests/api/test_health.py` calls `/health`, which returns `{"status": "ok", "service": settings.app_name}` and does not touch the DB. So the CI fix is to provide the minimum literal value that lets `Settings()` validate and `create_engine()` resolve a dialect: `sqlite:///:memory:`. SQLite ships with SQLAlchemy core; no install-set change is required. The `env:` block is scoped to the one step that needs it, so the next step (pillar harness collection) keeps its no-DATABASE_URL skip-cleanly contract.
**What is deliberately NOT done:** `Settings.database_url` is still required-with-no-default. Loosening that field would make the model tolerate a misconfigured production runtime, which is the wrong tradeoff. The CI shim is the right place for the workaround, not the model. A future refactor that wants AST-only static-analysis CI would lazy-instantiate `settings` or split `BootSettings` from `RuntimeSettings`; that's a Step-29 verification-doctrine question, out of scope here.
**Pattern E:** No application behavior changed. The production runtime path is untouched. This is a workflow-file-only edit adding a step-scoped env var.
**Pass 9 doctrine note (2026-05-13):** This entry was born §5-only post-doctrine (closure commit `8ad59e4` on 2026-05-10 added the §5 strikethrough heading without ever introducing a §3 entry; the parent of `8ad59e4` also lacked a §3 body). Pass 9 leaves the entry as-is because (a) the §5 entry is rich enough to carry the design-claim and repo-state context that a §3 entry would have held, and (b) reconstructing a §3 body now would be invention rather than restoration. Honesty cataloged here; no restoration possible. Tracked in `D-pass-6-mirror-restoration-incomplete-three-deletions-missed-2026-05-13` for completeness.

Hashed immutable alias `https://d1t84i96t71fsi.cloudfront.net/luciel-chat-widget.36a25740a60c.js` returns the same body with `cache-control: public, max-age=31536000, immutable`.

Every push to `main` that touches `widget/`, `cfn/luciel-widget-cdn.yaml`, the deploy script, or the deploy job re-runs the size-gated bundle through the OIDC-assumed deploy role and re-publishes both the hashed and stable-alias paths idempotently.
