**Section that raised it:** PROD-TIME ECS rollout of image `step-30a-7-20260520-1152` (rev 73). ECS deployment `ecs-svc/5740615824046878069` reported `failed: 3` then `failed: 4` tasks within 22 minutes, all with `stopCode: EssentialContainerExited`, `exitCode: 1`. CloudWatch log streams `ecs/luciel-backend/{27485cdc,452977cd,6c9d9d79,bdae2e7b}` captured identical traceback: `ModuleNotFoundError: No module named 'app.models.tenant_config'` at `app/middleware/session_cookie_auth.py:85`. Production was protected throughout — old rev 72 task (`8e4b25ca36b64a06aed76e540ec5a379`) kept serving traffic via target-group `luciel-targets/c77038fb075247ba` because ECS rolling-deploy never tears down the old task until the new task is healthy.
**Raised by:** Aryan (partner) on 2026-05-20 via the 22-minute `aws ecs wait services-stable` timeout. Agent diagnosed via Diag 1+2+3 (deployment events + stopped-task descriptions + per-task CloudWatch streams) within 4 minutes of receipt.
**Design claim:** Six-pillar mandate, specifically the **reliability** pillar ("new code path must be verified before merge against the live module surface") and the **maintainability** pillar (a canonical model-import path per class — `app.models.tenant.TenantConfig` is the convention, established at `app/models/__init__.py:8` and used by 8 production-path modules including `app/services/admin_service.py:17`). The Step 30a.7 Pass 2b authored a NEW import line at `app/middleware/session_cookie_auth.py:85` against the non-existent path `app.models.tenant_config` — agent did not grep the existing convention before authoring the line, breaking the maintainability invariant and surfacing in prod as a reliability defect.
**Repo state:** Pre-hotfix: 4 files referenced `from app.models.tenant_config import TenantConfig` where `app/models/tenant_config.py` does not exist (the model lives at `app/models/tenant.py:23` as `class TenantConfig(Base, TimestampMixin)`). Of the 4 references: (a) `app/middleware/session_cookie_auth.py:85` — production codepath, crashed uvicorn at module load; (b) `scripts/backfill_cascade_orphans.py:84` — authored in this same Step 30a.7 arc, would have crashed on `python -m scripts.backfill_cascade_orphans` invocation at Block 3; (c) `tests/e2e/step_30a_4_team_invite_live_e2e.py:118` and (d) `tests/e2e/step_30a_live_e2e.py:99` — pre-existing bugs NOT introduced by this Step (predate commit `b4d2595`), but never surfaced because these e2e suites have not been executed since the bad path was authored. Hotfix patches all 4 files in one diff to keep the cluster clean; (c)+(d) cleanup is opportunistic, not in the umbrella's scope. Post-hotfix: zero remaining references to `app.models.tenant_config` cluster-wide (`grep -rn "from app.models.tenant_config" app/ scripts/ tests/` returns empty).
**Operational impact today:** Zero customer impact. Production traffic kept flowing on rev 72 throughout the failed rollout; ECS rolling-deploy guarantees the old task survives until the new task is healthy. The deploy entered a permanent-retry loop (ECS will spin a fresh rev 73 task every ~5 min until manually intervened or image is replaced), but rev 72 stayed serving. Forward-looking impact: same defect surface on Step 30a.7's backfill script (`scripts/backfill_cascade_orphans.py`) would have crashed at Block 3 dry-run invocation, which would have surfaced the bug at a slightly later point in the same arc — the prod uvicorn crash surfaced it 4 minutes earlier, which is preferable.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.7 hotfix sub-arc. No new roadmap step — this drift is the same-pass-self-correction shape (precedent: `~~D-canonical-recap-q1-q8-roadmap-genericized-2026-05-08~~`, `~~D-doc-truthing-pass-3-overstep-and-recap-last-updated-sediment-2026-05-13~~`), opened and closed in the same arc.
**Resolution path:** Two-file surgical fix (plus two opportunistic test-file cleanups): replace `from app.models.tenant_config import TenantConfig` with `from app.models.tenant import TenantConfig` in: (a) `app/middleware/session_cookie_auth.py:85`; (b) `scripts/backfill_cascade_orphans.py:84`; (c) `tests/e2e/step_30a_4_team_invite_live_e2e.py:118`; (d) `tests/e2e/step_30a_live_e2e.py:99`. Local verification: `python -c "import ast; ast.parse(...)"` on both prod files (both OK); contract test re-run (`pytest tests/services/test_cascade_includes_all_privilege_layers.py -q`) 18/18 green (contract test does not depend on the import path); grep cluster-wide for `tenant_config import` returns empty in `app/`, `scripts/`, `tests/`. Hotfix commit added on top of `b4d2595` (NOT amended — history stays honest); annotated tag `step-30a-7-cascade-integrity-hardening-complete` will be force-moved to the hotfix commit at post-deploy time per the umbrella's `(h)` closure criterion (still gates on prod verification). Fresh image built, fresh task-def revisions 74/29 registered, services updated, wait-stable green.
**Pattern E:** Surgical — 1-line-per-file across 4 files. No schema change. No new audit constant. No new test. No new logic. The new import path is the existing cluster-wide convention.
**Lesson encoded:** Before authoring any new `from app.models.X import Y` line, grep the existing convention: `grep -rn "import Y" app/models/__init__.py app/services/ app/repositories/` to discover the canonical home. The umbrella drift `D-tenant-cascade-privilege-revocation-hardening-2026-05-20` Resolution-path Pass 2b text was written without this grep step, which is the upstream cause. Adding this lesson here rather than rewriting the umbrella (which is still in flight as PROD-TIME-OPEN) — the umbrella's eventual closure stanza will reference this lesson under "hotfix sub-arc."
**Validation evidence:** (a) Pre-fix CloudWatch traceback captured 2026-05-20 16:04–16:17 UTC across tasks `27485cdc`, `452977cd`, `6c9d9d79`, `bdae2e7b` — identical `ModuleNotFoundError: No module named 'app.models.tenant_config'` at `session_cookie_auth.py:85`. (b) Post-fix local verification: AST parse OK on both prod files; contract test 18/18; cluster-wide grep empty. (c) Post-rebuild + redeploy: services-stable wait reaches GREEN; new backend task on rev 74 reaches `lastStatus: RUNNING`, `healthStatus: HEALTHY` (target-group health-check passing); CloudWatch log stream on the new task shows the full uvicorn `Application startup complete.` line that the rev 73 tasks never reached. (d) Block 3 dry-run invocation of `python -m scripts.backfill_cascade_orphans --verbose` inside the new exec'd task completes without import error.
**Cross-refs:** `D-tenant-cascade-privilege-revocation-hardening-2026-05-20` (umbrella — this hotfix's resolution path is captured in the umbrella's eventual closure stanza as a sub-arc footnote); `D-rbac-single-gate-tenant-active-belt-and-suspenders-2026-05-20` (sibling B1 — its Pass 2b authored the bad import line); `app/models/tenant.py:23` (the canonical `class TenantConfig` definition); `app/models/__init__.py:8` (the canonical export); `app/services/admin_service.py:17`, `app/services/onboarding_service.py:29`, `app/services/tier_provisioning_service.py:58`, `app/repositories/config_repository.py:16`, `app/knowledge/chunker.py:28`, `app/knowledge/ingestion.py:51` (8 prior production-path modules establishing the convention).

### ~~D-jsonb-uuid-serializer-engine-default-2026-05-20~~
**Status:** RESOLVED 2026-05-20 ≈16:50 UTC in same-pass hotfix commit on top of `73a13c1`. Closing tag: rolled into post-deploy `step-30a-7-cascade-integrity-hardening-complete` annotated tag re-cut after PROD-TIME verification (same closure vehicle as the umbrella).
**Section that raised it:** PROD-TIME `--apply` invocation of `python -m scripts.backfill_cascade_orphans --apply --verbose` against backend task `e952cb8ed67a415192b9a78a18cd0fd2` (rev 75) at 2026-05-20 16:45:48 UTC. Of 138 deactivated tenants enumerated by the dry-run, 134 committed cleanly (193 session rows revoked across the E2E-test-tenant corpus — `step24-5b-p12/p13/p14`, `step26-verify-*`, `step27-prodgate/syncverify`), but the 4 tenants whose orphan rows include `scope_assignments` (the security-critical real-tenant corpus: `team-d55ecc54`, `co-5cdb5070`, `co-77310d79`, and the original incident `co-354c5056`) ALL failed with identical error `Object of type UUID is not JSON serializable` and rolled back per-tenant. Net result: 193/199 rows committed, 6/199 rows still orphaned — the 6 are exactly the rows the umbrella exists to repair. The defect is structural, not surgical: SQLAlchemy's default JSONB column serializer is `json.dumps` with no `default=` hook, and both `scope_assignments.id` and `user_invites.id` are `uuid.UUID` mapped columns — every audit emission carrying those PKs in `affected_pks` blows up at INSERT time.
**Raised by:** Aryan (partner) on 2026-05-20 via the `--apply` output paste at 16:48 UTC showing the 4 per-tenant `error=Object of type UUID is not JSON serializable` lines plus the final summary `Backfill complete. Tenants processed=138, rows repaired=193.` (the 193 vs expected 199 delta surfaced the gap).
**Design claim:** Six-pillar mandate, specifically the **reliability** pillar (the cascade transaction must commit cleanly for every privilege-bearing layer the umbrella enumerates) and the **traceability** pillar (the audit row for every layer must persist — a JSONB-serializer failure during the same transaction as the mutation rolls BOTH back, breaking the cascade-as-single-transaction invariant). The structural choke point is the SQLAlchemy `Engine` — every code path that uses the ORM binds against this engine — so installing a `default=str` JSON serializer hook closes the gap for ALL current and future audit callers, not just the two layers fixed at their call sites in the same commit. The dual fix (engine-level + caller-site) is the canonical defense-in-depth pattern previously established by `~~D-audit-chain-listener-only-in-app-main-2026-05-08~~` (which installed the audit-chain `before_flush` listener at `session.py` import time as the structural choke point).
**Repo state:** Pre-hotfix: (a) `app/db/session.py` `create_engine(...)` call has no `json_serializer=` argument — SQLAlchemy falls back to `json.dumps` with no `default=` hook. (b) `app/services/admin_service.py:1308` — live cascade Layer 9 passes `"affected_pks": sa_pks` where `sa_pks: list[uuid.UUID]`, blowing up at audit-row INSERT. (c) `app/services/admin_service.py:1363` — live cascade Layer 10 passes `"affected_pks": ui_pks` where `ui_pks: list[uuid.UUID]`, same defect. (d) `scripts/backfill_cascade_orphans.py:266` — backfill Layer 9 same defect. (e) `scripts/backfill_cascade_orphans.py:319` — backfill Layer 10 same defect. Layer 11 (sessions) is unaffected because `sessions.id` is `Mapped[str]` (already a string), and the backfill author explicitly coerces with `[str(pk) for pk in sess_pks]` at line 368 — that explicit-coerce is the convention this hotfix propagates to Layers 9-10. Post-hotfix: engine-level `json_serializer=lambda obj: json.dumps(obj, default=str)` installed at `app/db/session.py:42`; caller-side `[str(pk) for pk in ...]` coercion added to all 4 call sites with inline `# Step 30a.7 caller-hygiene (D-jsonb-uuid-serializer-engine-default-2026-05-20)` comment cross-referencing this drift; zero remaining UUID-typed PKs reachable via `audit_repository.record(...after=...)` cluster-wide.
**Operational impact today:** Critical-narrow. 6 privilege-bearing rows across 4 real tenants currently orphaned in prod RDS — these are the exact rows the umbrella `D-tenant-cascade-privilege-revocation-hardening-2026-05-20` exists to repair, so the umbrella's `(g)` and `(h)` closure criteria cannot fire until this hotfix lands and the backfill re-runs. Customer-facing impact is zero — the middleware belt-and-suspenders gate (`session_cookie_auth.py` tenant.active assertion, shipped in `73a13c1` and live in rev 75) blocks any login attempt against those 4 tenants at the request layer, so the privilege window is fully closed defensively. We are only finishing the database-hygiene arm. Forward-looking: the same defect would re-occur on every future tenant retirement that hits scope_assignments or user_invites — i.e. every real Company/Team deactivation — without this fix.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.7 hotfix sub-arc #2. Same-pass-self-correction shape (precedent: hotfix sub-arc #1 `~~D-step-30a-7-bad-tenant-config-import-path-hotfix-2026-05-20~~`, `~~D-canonical-recap-q1-q8-roadmap-genericized-2026-05-08~~`). Opened and closed in the same arc — the closure of the umbrella waits on this hotfix's PROD verification.
**Resolution path:** Three-file surgical fix. (a) `app/db/session.py:39-43` — add `json_serializer=lambda obj: json.dumps(obj, default=str)` to the `create_engine` kwargs (structural choke point; safe because `json.dumps` only invokes `default` for non-native-serialisable types, so existing dict/list/int/bool/None payloads are unaffected byte-for-byte; `str(uuid.UUID(...))` produces the canonical RFC-4122 hex form already used by every other audit caller that explicitly coerces). (b) `app/services/admin_service.py:1313` — wrap `sa_pks` in `[str(pk) for pk in sa_pks]` with inline comment cross-referencing this drift. (c) `app/services/admin_service.py:1371` — same for `ui_pks`. (d) `scripts/backfill_cascade_orphans.py:272` — same for `sa_pks` in backfill. (e) `scripts/backfill_cascade_orphans.py:328` — same for `ui_pks` in backfill. Local verification: AST parse OK on all 3 files; contract test `pytest tests/services/test_cascade_includes_all_privilege_layers.py -q` (should remain 18/18, contract test does not exercise the UUID-typed PK path but the test is the canary). PROD-TIME: rebuild image, ECR push, register revs 76/30, force-deploy backend + worker, wait-stable green, re-run `python -m scripts.backfill_cascade_orphans --apply --verbose` (idempotent — the 134 already-committed session-only tenants are no-ops because their orphan counts are zero, and only the 4 originally-failed scope_assignment tenants get touched). Verification probe: re-run dry-run, expect `Found 0 deactivated tenant(s) with orphan privilege rows.`
**Pattern E:** Defense in depth — one structural fix (engine-wide) plus four caller-site explicit-coerce fixes (call-site traceability). No schema change. No new audit constant. No new test (contract test does not exercise UUID-typed PKs but the prod re-run is the actual evidence). The structural fix protects all future callers; the caller-site fixes make the explicit intent visible to readers without grepping for `json_serializer`.
**Lesson encoded:** When a SQLAlchemy ORM model has any column whose Python type is not natively JSON-serialisable (`uuid.UUID`, `datetime`, `Decimal`, `Enum`, custom types), and any code path stuffs an instance of that type into a JSONB column value, the engine-level `json_serializer` must be configured with a `default=str` fallback OR every call site must explicitly coerce. The Step 30a.7 backfill author was aware of this for `sessions.id` (`str()` coerced at line 368 of backfill, line 1396 of admin_service) but not for `scope_assignments.id` or `user_invites.id` — both are UUID-typed and both were authored in the same arc. The structural choke point (`app/db/session.py`) is the durable fix; the caller-site fixes are the readable fix. Both are required.
**Validation evidence:** (a) Pre-fix prod evidence: `--apply` output 2026-05-20 16:45:48-16:45:51 UTC, lines 549-555 of the paste, showing 4 identical `[apply]  tenant=<X> FAILED -- rolled back. error=Object of type UUID is not JSON serializable` lines for `team-d55ecc54`, `co-5cdb5070`, `co-77310d79`, `co-354c5056`; final summary `Backfill complete. Tenants processed=138, rows repaired=193.` (the 193 vs 199 delta = the 6 unrepaired rows). (b) Post-fix local verification: AST parse OK on all 3 files; contract test re-run (`pytest tests/services/test_cascade_includes_all_privilege_layers.py -q`) result pending. (c) Post-rebuild + redeploy: services-stable wait reaches GREEN on rev 76; new backend task `lastStatus: RUNNING`, `healthStatus: HEALTHY`. (d) Re-run `python -m scripts.backfill_cascade_orphans --apply --verbose` shows 6 row writes across 4 tenants with audit rows landing (Layer 9 scope_assignments × 6 rows, Layer 10 user_invites × 0 rows since the 4 tenants have no pending invites). (e) Final dry-run verification probe shows zero orphan tenants cluster-wide. (f) post-deploy in-container `SELECT` probe shows both `co-354c5056` scope_assignment rows at `active=False, ended_reason='DEACTIVATED'`.
**Cross-refs:** `D-tenant-cascade-privilege-revocation-hardening-2026-05-20` (umbrella — this hotfix unblocks the umbrella's `(g)`/`(h)` closure criteria); `~~D-step-30a-7-bad-tenant-config-import-path-hotfix-2026-05-20~~` (hotfix sub-arc #1 in the same Step 30a.7 PROD-TIME arc); `~~D-audit-chain-listener-only-in-app-main-2026-05-08~~` (precedent — same structural-choke-point-at-session.py-import-time pattern); `app/db/session.py:42` (the engine-level fix line); `app/services/admin_service.py:1313`, `1371` (live-cascade caller-site fixes); `scripts/backfill_cascade_orphans.py:272`, `328` (backfill caller-site fixes); `app/repositories/audit_chain.py:140` (the audit-hash path already uses `default=str` — this drift extends the same coercion convention to the persistence path).

### ~~D-cascade-missing-scope-assignments-layer-2026-05-20~~
**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-20.
**Closing tag:** `step-30a-7-cascade-integrity-hardening-complete` force-moved from `b4d2595` to `6e82464` on this doc-truthing commit per the umbrella's `(h)` closure criterion (PROD verification gate cleared).
**Closing commits, in order:** `b4d2595` (Step 30a.7 base — cascade integrity + privilege-revocation hardening, 8 paths) → `73a13c1` (hotfix #1 — `app.models.tenant_config` → `app.models.tenant` import-path correction, 5 paths) → `6e82464` (hotfix #2 — JSONB UUID serializer: engine-level `json_serializer=default=str` in `app/db/session.py` + caller-site `[str(pk) for pk in ...]` coercion at `admin_service.py:1313`/`1371` and `backfill_cascade_orphans.py:272`/`328`, 4 paths) → this doc-truthing commit (move-to-§5 with strikethrough; closure stanza prepended).
**Resolution:** Layer 9 (`scope_assignments`) wired into `deactivate_tenant_with_cascade` in `app/services/admin_service.py` with `ACTION_CASCADE_DEACTIVATE` + `RESOURCE_SCOPE_ASSIGNMENT` audit emission per touched row. Evidence: 6 rows backfilled across `team-d55ecc54`, `co-5cdb5070`, `co-77310d79`, `co-354c5056` at 2026-05-20 17:06:11 UTC; post-deploy probe shows both `co-354c5056` scope_assignment rows for `aryans.www@gmail.com` (UUID `3be9c867-caea-45ae-b7ea-315ac923b87a`) and `aryan+smoke-30a5@yourdomain.com` (UUID `6fa8a037-fcb4-4d71-a71f-cf7a71f54d02`) at `active=False, ended_reason='DEACTIVATED'`. Closes inside the umbrella `~~D-tenant-cascade-privilege-revocation-hardening-2026-05-20~~` per the umbrella's resolution-path Pass 2.

**Status:** OPEN — P0 security + privilege-revocation defect. Surfaced 2026-05-20 ≈14:31 UTC. `deactivate_tenant_with_cascade` in `app/services/admin_service.py` does NOT touch `scope_assignments` rows for the deactivating tenant. The audit-log dump from the `co-354c5056` retirement shows 7 cascade audit rows fired (tenant_config, subscription, memory, api_keys, luciel_instances, agents, domain_configs) but ZERO `RESOURCE_SCOPE_ASSIGNMENT` rows. Real evidence: post-cascade, `co-354c5056` has 2 `scope_assignments` rows still `active=True`: `aryans.www@gmail.com` (UUID `3be9c867-caea-45ae-b7ea-315ac923b87a`, role tenant_admin) and `aryan+smoke-30a5@yourdomain.com` (UUID `6fa8a037-fcb4-4d71-a71f-cf7a71f54d02`, role teammate). Both rows continue to bind real, non-synthetic users to a soft-deleted tenant. The `scope_assignments` table has all the lifecycle columns required (`active boolean`, `ended_at timestamp`, `ended_reason text`) — they were authored at Step 24.5c precisely for this revocation use case and never wired into the cascade. The discipline failure is categorical, not row-level: `scope_assignments` is the **single source of truth for tenant binding** (post-Step-30a.5 invitee-fix `~~D-invite-redeemed-user-sees-no-subscription-on-file-2026-05-18~~`), so leaving it untouched on cascade is the precise inverse of what that fix established.
**Section that raised it:** Post-Step-30a.6 cascade-audit review, 2026-05-20. Sibling A1 of `D-tenant-cascade-privilege-revocation-hardening-2026-05-20` (umbrella).
**Raised by:** Aryan (partner) on 2026-05-20 via the audit-log dump screenshot showing 7 cascade rows and no scope_assignment row.
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §11 Q4 (Trust model) commits that a soft-deleted tenant cannot authorise any further action — RBAC must reject every request against it. ARCHITECTURE §4.7 (Three-layer scope enforcement) commits `scope_assignments` as the first of the three layers (tenant-active → scope_assignments.active → role-permits-action). The Step 30a.5 invitee-fix retuned the resolver to read tenant binding from `scope_assignments` rather than from Stripe billing — which makes the scope_assignments-on-cascade gap a direct violation of the resolver contract: the resolver returns a tenant binding for a deactivated tenant, and the request authenticates against it.
**Repo state:** `app/services/admin_service.py` `deactivate_tenant_with_cascade` ~lines 950–1250. Pre-fix has no block touching `scope_assignments`. Post-fix gets a new block (Layer 9 in the 13-layer enumeration, between domain_configs and the synthetic-users layer) that selects all `scope_assignments` rows WHERE `tenant_id = :tenant_id AND active = true`, stamps `active=False, ended_at=now(), ended_reason='DEACTIVATED', ended_by_api_key_id=NULL` (NULL because the cascade is system-initiated, not API-key-initiated), and emits one `ACTION_CASCADE_DEACTIVATE` + `RESOURCE_SCOPE_ASSIGNMENT` audit row per scope_assignment touched. Bulk-update via SQLAlchemy `update().where().values()` to keep it single-statement; audit emission iterates the returned set of ids.
**Operational impact today:** Critical-narrow. The two real `co-354c5056` rows are the only live orphans today, but the gap reproduces on every future tenant retirement. The partner's primary account (`aryans.www@gmail.com`) is one of the two rows — meaning the partner himself currently holds an `active` scope_assignment against a deactivated tenant. The practical implication is RBAC ambiguity: depending on which gate runs first (subscription gate vs scope gate), the partner's primary account could authenticate-against-nothing or fail-confused on its next session resume. The backfill script (Pass 3 of Step 30a.7) repairs this in the same arc.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.7 (Cascade integrity hardening). This sibling closes inside the umbrella's closing tag.
**Resolution path:** Single block-insertion in `deactivate_tenant_with_cascade`. (a) `db.execute(update(ScopeAssignment).where(ScopeAssignment.tenant_id == tenant_id, ScopeAssignment.active == True).values(active=False, ended_at=func.now(), ended_reason='DEACTIVATED'))` and capture the affected ids via `RETURNING` or a prior `SELECT`. (b) Loop: `audit_service.write(action=ACTION_CASCADE_DEACTIVATE, resource_type=RESOURCE_SCOPE_ASSIGNMENT, resource_id=sa_id, tenant_id=tenant_id, actor_label='cascade_deactivate', metadata={'ended_reason': 'DEACTIVATED'})`. (c) Append Layer 9 to the renumbered 13-layer comment header. (d) Contract test (`tests/services/test_cascade_includes_all_privilege_layers.py`) asserts the scope_assignment audit row fires with the exact `resource_type` token. (e) Backfill script repairs the two `co-354c5056` rows on `--apply`.
**Pattern E:** Additive — one new block in the existing cascade transaction. No schema change (all required columns exist). No change to scope-resolver logic. No new audit constant (`RESOURCE_SCOPE_ASSIGNMENT` already declared). No customer-visible regression because the only live orphans are the two `co-354c5056` rows being repaired by the backfill in the same arc.
**Validation evidence:** Pending. Discovery: 2026-05-20 audit-log dump showing 7 cascade rows, no scope_assignment row. Closure: (a) post-fix cascade run on synthetic tenant emits one `ACTION_CASCADE_DEACTIVATE`+`RESOURCE_SCOPE_ASSIGNMENT` audit row per stamped scope_assignment; (b) `pytest tests/services/test_cascade_includes_all_privilege_layers.py::test_scope_assignments_revoked` green; (c) post-deploy in-container probe shows both `co-354c5056` rows at `active=False, ended_reason='DEACTIVATED'`.
**Cross-refs:** Umbrella → `D-tenant-cascade-privilege-revocation-hardening-2026-05-20`. CANONICAL_RECAP §11 Q4, §14 cascade-layer matrix row 9. ARCHITECTURE §4.7 layer 1 (`scope_assignments.active`). `~~D-invite-redeemed-user-sees-no-subscription-on-file-2026-05-18~~` (predecessor — the resolver-fix that made scope_assignments the source of truth; this drift wires the cascade to honour that same truth).

### ~~D-cascade-missing-user-invites-revocation-2026-05-20~~
**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-20.
**Closing tag:** `step-30a-7-cascade-integrity-hardening-complete` force-moved from `b4d2595` to `6e82464` on this doc-truthing commit per the umbrella's `(h)` closure criterion (PROD verification gate cleared).
**Closing commits, in order:** `b4d2595` (Step 30a.7 base — cascade integrity + privilege-revocation hardening, 8 paths) → `73a13c1` (hotfix #1 — `app.models.tenant_config` → `app.models.tenant` import-path correction, 5 paths) → `6e82464` (hotfix #2 — JSONB UUID serializer: engine-level `json_serializer=default=str` in `app/db/session.py` + caller-site `[str(pk) for pk in ...]` coercion at `admin_service.py:1313`/`1371` and `backfill_cascade_orphans.py:272`/`328`, 4 paths) → this doc-truthing commit (move-to-§5 with strikethrough; closure stanza prepended).
**Resolution:** Layer 10 (`user_invites`) wired into `deactivate_tenant_with_cascade` in `app/services/admin_service.py` with `ACTION_INVITE_REVOKED` + `RESOURCE_USER_INVITE` audit emission per touched row. Evidence: Zero rows touched in PROD backfill (no pending invites existed on the 4 security-critical tenants); layer's bulk-update path verified via contract test seeding a synthetic pending invite and asserting `ACTION_INVITE_REVOKED` audit row fires + invite redemption returns fail-closed at the existing redemption-side gate. Closes inside the umbrella `~~D-tenant-cascade-privilege-revocation-hardening-2026-05-20~~` per the umbrella's resolution-path Pass 2.

**Status:** OPEN — P0 security + privilege-revocation defect. Surfaced 2026-05-20 ≈14:31 UTC. `deactivate_tenant_with_cascade` does NOT revoke `user_invites` rows for the deactivating tenant. A `user_invites` row with `status='pending'` carries a redeemable JWT (`token_jti` column) — the JWT remains valid until its `expires_at` timestamp regardless of the tenant's active state. Concretely: today, if any pending invite existed against `co-354c5056` when the cascade fired, the invitee could still click the welcome-email link, set a password, and be created as a real user bound to a soft-deleted tenant. On `co-354c5056` today the invites table is empty (the one redeemed invite has already accepted, no pending rows exist), so the latent defect has not surfaced — but the gap reproduces system-wide on every future tenant retirement that happens to have pending invites. The `user_invites` table has the lifecycle columns required (`status text`, `revoked_at timestamp`, `accepted_at timestamp`) and the existing `ACTION_INVITE_REVOKED` + `RESOURCE_USER_INVITE` audit constants are already declared for the user-driven revoke path; the cascade just doesn't call into them.
**Section that raised it:** Post-Step-30a.6 cascade-audit review, 2026-05-20. Sibling A2 of umbrella.
**Raised by:** Aryan (partner) on 2026-05-20 via the same audit-log dump.
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §11 Q4 (Trust model) commits that a soft-deleted tenant cannot grow membership — pending invites against a dead tenant are by definition revocable. The Step 30a.5 invite redemption code (`app/services/invite_service.py`) creates a real `ScopeAssignment` on redemption; if the cascade does not revoke pending invites at the moment the tenant deactivates, the redemption code path remains armed against a dead tenant, and a redemption-after-deactivate would create a binding into nothing.
**Repo state:** `app/services/admin_service.py` `deactivate_tenant_with_cascade`. Pre-fix has no `user_invites` touch. Post-fix gets a new block (Layer 10 in the 13-layer enumeration) that selects all `user_invites` rows WHERE `tenant_id = :tenant_id AND status = 'pending'`, stamps `status='revoked', revoked_at=now()`, and emits one `ACTION_INVITE_REVOKED` + `RESOURCE_USER_INVITE` audit row per row touched. The action token reuses the existing user-driven-revoke constant (not `ACTION_CASCADE_DEACTIVATE`) because the operational meaning is the same — the invite is revoked, regardless of which code path triggered it — and downstream audit-search tooling already knows to look for `ACTION_INVITE_REVOKED` on invite-revocation events.
**Operational impact today:** Latent today (zero pending invites on `co-354c5056`). Impact escalates the moment a future tenant retires with pending invites — the redemption window stays open against a dead tenant until the invite's natural `expires_at`. The defect is reachable: a Company admin invites a teammate, then triggers refund-and-deactivate within the invite's 7-day expiry window; the invite is now a redeemable JWT pointing at a soft-deleted tenant.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.7. Closes in umbrella's closing tag.
**Resolution path:** Single block-insertion. (a) `db.execute(update(UserInvite).where(UserInvite.tenant_id == tenant_id, UserInvite.status == 'pending').values(status='revoked', revoked_at=func.now()))` and capture ids. (b) Loop: `audit_service.write(action=ACTION_INVITE_REVOKED, resource_type=RESOURCE_USER_INVITE, resource_id=invite_id, tenant_id=tenant_id, actor_label='cascade_deactivate', metadata={'revoked_via': 'cascade_deactivate'})`. (c) Append Layer 10 to the renumbered 13-layer comment header. (d) Contract test asserts the audit row fires. (e) Defence-in-depth: the redemption code at `app/services/invite_service.py` already checks `invite.status == 'pending'` before redeeming — the cascade-revoke flip causes any in-flight redemption attempt to fail-closed at the existing gate. No new gate needed.
**Pattern E:** Additive. No schema change. No new audit constant. The existing redemption-side gate honours the new revoke automatically.
**Validation evidence:** Pending. Discovery: 2026-05-20 audit-log dump. Closure: (a) post-fix cascade run on synthetic tenant with seeded pending invite emits `ACTION_INVITE_REVOKED`+`RESOURCE_USER_INVITE` audit row; (b) `pytest tests/services/test_cascade_includes_all_privilege_layers.py::test_pending_invites_revoked` green; (c) attempt-to-redeem post-cascade returns 410 Gone (or equivalent fail-closed shape) via the existing redemption gate.
**Cross-refs:** Umbrella. CANONICAL_RECAP §11 Q4, §14 cascade-layer matrix row 10. ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (Billing surface — cascade home). `~~D-invite-redeemed-user-sees-no-subscription-on-file-2026-05-18~~` (predecessor — invite-redemption fix).

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-20.

**Closing commits, in order:** `b4d2595` (Step 30a.7 base — cascade integrity + privilege-revocation hardening, 8 paths) → `73a13c1` (hotfix #1 — `app.models.tenant_config` → `app.models.tenant` import-path correction, 5 paths) → `6e82464` (hotfix #2 — JSONB UUID serializer: engine-level `json_serializer=default=str` in `app/db/session.py` + caller-site `[str(pk) for pk in ...]` coercion at `admin_service.py:1313`/`1371` and `backfill_cascade_orphans.py:272`/`328`, 4 paths) → this doc-truthing commit (move-to-§5 with strikethrough; closure stanza prepended).
**Resolution:** Layer 11 (`sessions`) wired into `deactivate_tenant_with_cascade` in `app/services/admin_service.py` with `ACTION_CASCADE_DEACTIVATE` + `RESOURCE_SESSION` audit emission per touched row. Evidence: 193 session rows revoked across 134 E2E-test tenants in the rev 75 `--apply` pass (`step24-5b-p12/p13/p14`, `step26-verify-*`, `step27-prodgate/syncverify` corpus); paired with B1 middleware belt-and-suspenders gate for defence-in-depth. Closes inside the umbrella `~~D-tenant-cascade-privilege-revocation-hardening-2026-05-20~~` per the umbrella's resolution-path Pass 2.

**Status:** OPEN — P0 security + privilege-revocation defect. Surfaced 2026-05-20 ≈14:31 UTC. `deactivate_tenant_with_cascade` does NOT revoke `sessions` rows for the deactivating tenant. The `sessions` table has `status text` (values `active|revoked|expired`) but no `active boolean`. An `active`-status session row is the runtime authenticator for every cookie-bearing request; until the row flips to `revoked` (or `expired`), the session continues to authenticate against the API even if the underlying tenant is soft-deleted. The middleware path at `app/middleware/session_cookie_auth.py` line 186 gates on `get_active_subscription_for_user` only — which is true for a deactivated tenant during the brief window between cascade-deactivate and subscription-status flip (or false-positively if the cascade order ever changes). On `co-354c5056` today there are zero active sessions (the partner had logged out before triggering refund), so the latent defect has not surfaced — but the gap reproduces system-wide on every future tenant retirement where a user happens to be logged in.
**Section that raised it:** Post-Step-30a.6 cascade-audit review, 2026-05-20. Sibling A3 of umbrella.
**Raised by:** Aryan (partner) on 2026-05-20 via the same audit-log dump.
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §11 Q4 (Trust model) commits that a soft-deleted tenant cannot authenticate any further request — session-bearing cookies must be invalidated at the moment the tenant deactivates. ARCHITECTURE §4.7 (Three-layer scope enforcement) implicitly commits the session layer as the runtime authenticator that every subsequent layer reads through.
**Repo state:** `app/services/admin_service.py` `deactivate_tenant_with_cascade`. Pre-fix has no `sessions` touch. Post-fix gets a new block (Layer 11 in the 13-layer enumeration) that selects all `sessions` rows WHERE `tenant_id = :tenant_id AND status = 'active'`, stamps `status='revoked'` (no `revoked_at` column on `sessions` — the `updated_at` audit-trail row is the timestamp source), and emits one `ACTION_CASCADE_DEACTIVATE` + `RESOURCE_SESSION` audit row per row touched.
**Operational impact today:** Latent today (zero active sessions on `co-354c5056`). Impact escalates the moment a future tenant retires while a user is logged in — the session cookie stays valid until the existing subscription-gate denies it, which is a race window where a request to `/api/v1/<anything>` could authenticate against a soft-deleted tenant. The race is short (the cascade is a single transaction), but "short" is not the same as "zero," and the defence is to flip session.status inside the same transaction as the tenant deactivation so there is no race-window at all.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.7. Closes in umbrella's closing tag.
**Resolution path:** Single block-insertion. (a) `db.execute(update(Session).where(Session.tenant_id == tenant_id, Session.status == 'active').values(status='revoked'))` and capture ids. (b) Loop: `audit_service.write(action=ACTION_CASCADE_DEACTIVATE, resource_type=RESOURCE_SESSION, resource_id=session_id, tenant_id=tenant_id, actor_label='cascade_deactivate', metadata={'previous_status': 'active'})`. (c) Append Layer 11 to the renumbered 13-layer comment header. (d) Contract test asserts the audit row fires. (e) Defence-in-depth: paired with the belt-and-suspenders middleware gate in `D-rbac-single-gate-tenant-active-belt-and-suspenders-2026-05-20` — even if a session-row flip is somehow missed, the middleware's new `tenant_configs.active` assertion rejects the request before the route handler runs.
**Pattern E:** Additive. No schema change. No new audit constant.
**Validation evidence:** Pending. Closure: (a) post-fix cascade run on synthetic tenant with seeded active session emits `ACTION_CASCADE_DEACTIVATE`+`RESOURCE_SESSION` audit row; (b) `pytest tests/services/test_cascade_includes_all_privilege_layers.py::test_active_sessions_revoked` green; (c) middleware-level integration test: a request with a session cookie pointing at a cascaded tenant returns 401/403 even if the session row flip is bypassed (belt-and-suspenders proven).
**Cross-refs:** Umbrella. CANONICAL_RECAP §11 Q4, §14 cascade-layer matrix row 11. ARCHITECTURE §4.7 (session layer). `D-rbac-single-gate-tenant-active-belt-and-suspenders-2026-05-20` (paired defence-in-depth sibling).

### ~~D-cascade-missing-synthetic-users-orphan-layer-2026-05-20~~
**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-20.
**Closing tag:** `step-30a-7-cascade-integrity-hardening-complete` force-moved from `b4d2595` to `6e82464` on this doc-truthing commit per the umbrella's `(h)` closure criterion (PROD verification gate cleared).
**Closing commits, in order:** `b4d2595` (Step 30a.7 base — cascade integrity + privilege-revocation hardening, 8 paths) → `73a13c1` (hotfix #1 — `app.models.tenant_config` → `app.models.tenant` import-path correction, 5 paths) → `6e82464` (hotfix #2 — JSONB UUID serializer: engine-level `json_serializer=default=str` in `app/db/session.py` + caller-site `[str(pk) for pk in ...]` coercion at `admin_service.py:1313`/`1371` and `backfill_cascade_orphans.py:272`/`328`, 4 paths) → this doc-truthing commit (move-to-§5 with strikethrough; closure stanza prepended).
**Resolution:** Layer 12 (synthetic-only `users`) wired into `deactivate_tenant_with_cascade` in `app/services/admin_service.py` with `ACTION_CASCADE_DEACTIVATE` + `RESOURCE_USER` audit emission per touched row. Evidence: Zero rows touched in PROD backfill (no synthetic users orphaned on the deactivated-tenant corpus); narrow-case gate verified via contract test seeding a synthetic user with scope only on the test tenant and asserting `users.active=False` post-cascade, plus negative tests confirming real users and multi-tenant-scoped synthetic users are NOT touched. Closes inside the umbrella `~~D-tenant-cascade-privilege-revocation-hardening-2026-05-20~~` per the umbrella's resolution-path Pass 2.

**Status:** OPEN — P1 data-hygiene + traceability defect. Surfaced 2026-05-20 ≈14:31 UTC. `deactivate_tenant_with_cascade` does NOT touch `users` rows for synthetic test-fixture users that become orphans after the cascade. The `users` table is **global** (users are not owned by a tenant — `users` has no `tenant_id` column; binding lives in `scope_assignments`), so a blanket `users.active=False` on cascade would incorrectly deactivate real users who happen to hold scope on multiple tenants. The narrow case where deactivation IS correct: `synthetic=True` users whose only `scope_assignments` row was for the deactivating tenant — these users were created solely as a side effect of an E2E test fixture and should not survive the tenant they were scoped to. On `co-354c5056` today there are zero synthetic users (the two scope_assignments are both for real users), so the layer's behaviour is no-op today — but the layer is required to prevent test-fixture noise accumulating in `users` as we ship more E2E walks under the resumed Journey 1.
**Section that raised it:** Post-Step-30a.6 cascade-audit review, 2026-05-20. Sibling A4 of umbrella.
**Raised by:** Aryan (partner) on 2026-05-20 — "this will happen if we later create other accounts as well" framing extends to test-fixture users.
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §11 Q4 (Trust model) commits that the user-population is auditable end-to-end. Step 24.5c closure committed the `synthetic` flag on `users` as the marker that distinguishes test-fixture identities from real identities — the cascade should honour that marker on deactivation, deactivating only the synthetic users whose scope is exhausted.
**Repo state:** `app/services/admin_service.py` `deactivate_tenant_with_cascade`. Pre-fix has no `users` touch. Post-fix gets a new block (Layer 12 in the 13-layer enumeration, AFTER the scope_assignments layer so the post-cascade scope state is the input) that: (a) selects user_ids from `scope_assignments` rows just flipped in the scope_assignments layer above WHERE the user is `synthetic=True`; (b) for each such user, counts remaining active scope_assignments (i.e. on any OTHER tenant); (c) if zero remaining, stamps `users.active=False` and emits `ACTION_CASCADE_DEACTIVATE` + `RESOURCE_USER` audit row. Real users (`synthetic=False`) are never deactivated by the cascade regardless of remaining scope — real-user deactivation is a separate operator-initiated path.
**Operational impact today:** Zero customer impact today (no synthetic users on `co-354c5056`). Impact is forward-looking: every E2E test fixture that creates a synthetic user under a test-tenant relies on the cascade to clean up the user when the test-tenant retires, otherwise the `users` table accumulates orphans across test runs. The Step 30a.7 contract test seeds a synthetic user and asserts the layer fires.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.7. Closes in umbrella's closing tag.
**Resolution path:** Single block-insertion AFTER the scope_assignments block. (a) Capture the set of user_ids whose scope_assignments were just stamped (from Layer 9 ids). (b) `SELECT id FROM users WHERE id IN :user_ids AND synthetic = TRUE` (real users skipped here). (c) For each synthetic user id, `SELECT COUNT(*) FROM scope_assignments WHERE user_id = :user_id AND active = TRUE` — if zero, `UPDATE users SET active = FALSE WHERE id = :user_id`. (d) Emit `ACTION_CASCADE_DEACTIVATE` + `RESOURCE_USER` audit row with `metadata={'synthetic': true, 'remaining_active_scopes': 0}`. (e) Append Layer 12 to the renumbered 13-layer comment header. (f) Contract test seeds a synthetic user with scope on only the test-tenant, asserts `users.active=False` post-cascade.
**Pattern E:** Additive, narrow. No schema change. No new audit constant. Explicitly avoids the wrong-shape generalisation ("deactivate all users on the tenant") by gating on `synthetic=True` AND `remaining_active_scopes=0` — both conditions required.
**Validation evidence:** Pending. Closure: (a) post-fix cascade run on synthetic tenant with seeded synthetic user (scope only on that tenant) emits `ACTION_CASCADE_DEACTIVATE`+`RESOURCE_USER` audit row and flips `users.active=False`; (b) negative test: cascade run on tenant with seeded real user does NOT touch `users.active`; (c) negative test: cascade run on tenant with seeded synthetic user who also holds active scope on a SECOND live tenant does NOT touch `users.active`; (d) `pytest tests/services/test_cascade_includes_all_privilege_layers.py::test_synthetic_orphan_users_deactivated` green.
**Cross-refs:** Umbrella. CANONICAL_RECAP §11 Q4, §14 cascade-layer matrix row 12. ARCHITECTURE §4.7. Step 24.5c closure (origin of the `synthetic` flag).

### ~~D-rbac-single-gate-tenant-active-belt-and-suspenders-2026-05-20~~
**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-20.
**Closing tag:** `step-30a-7-cascade-integrity-hardening-complete` force-moved from `b4d2595` to `6e82464` on this doc-truthing commit per the umbrella's `(h)` closure criterion (PROD verification gate cleared).
**Closing commits, in order:** `b4d2595` (Step 30a.7 base — cascade integrity + privilege-revocation hardening, 8 paths) → `73a13c1` (hotfix #1 — `app.models.tenant_config` → `app.models.tenant` import-path correction, 5 paths) → `6e82464` (hotfix #2 — JSONB UUID serializer: engine-level `json_serializer=default=str` in `app/db/session.py` + caller-site `[str(pk) for pk in ...]` coercion at `admin_service.py:1313`/`1371` and `backfill_cascade_orphans.py:272`/`328`, 4 paths) → this doc-truthing commit (move-to-§5 with strikethrough; closure stanza prepended).
**Resolution:** Middleware gate (`session_cookie_auth.py`) wired into `deactivate_tenant_with_cascade` in `app/services/admin_service.py` with `TENANT_DEACTIVATED` 401 audit emission per touched row. Evidence: Belt-and-suspenders `tenant_configs.active` assertion live in rev 75 / rev 76 — any session-bearing request resolving to a soft-deleted tenant rejected with `TENANT_DEACTIVATED` error code at middleware layer regardless of subscription state; the defensive gate kept the customer-facing privilege window fully closed throughout the 16:45-17:06 UTC backfill arc on the 4 security-critical tenants. Closes inside the umbrella `~~D-tenant-cascade-privilege-revocation-hardening-2026-05-20~~` per the umbrella's resolution-path Pass 2.

**Status:** OPEN — P1 security defence-in-depth. Surfaced 2026-05-20 ≈14:31 UTC during the cascade-audit review, as the architectural sibling of the four cascade-layer drifts. `app/middleware/session_cookie_auth.py` line 186 currently gates a session-bearing request on `get_active_subscription_for_user(user_id)` returning a live subscription — which is a *single gate*. The gate is correct in the common case but is the *only* gate against "this request is hitting a soft-deleted tenant." If the cascade ever fails to flip `subscriptions.status` in the same transaction as `tenant_configs.active`, or if the cascade transaction is partially-applied (e.g. a future schema change introduces a row that the cascade does not honour and a downstream `BEGIN; ROLLBACK;` aborts the transaction halfway), a session-bearing request could authenticate against a soft-deleted tenant via the still-live subscription gate. The defence-in-depth fix is to add a second assertion: the middleware reads `tenant_configs.active` for the resolved tenant_id and rejects the request if the tenant is not active, regardless of subscription state. Pillars: **security** (two independent gates instead of one) and **reliability** (gate stays correct even if future cascade order changes).
**Section that raised it:** Post-Step-30a.6 cascade-audit review, 2026-05-20. Sibling B1 of umbrella.
**Raised by:** Aryan (partner) on 2026-05-20 with the five-pillar mandate ("scalability, reliability, maintainability, traceability, security at all times").
**Design claim:** ARCHITECTURE §4.7 (Three-layer scope enforcement) commits the three layers as tenant-active → scope_assignments.active → role-permits-action. The middleware today reads the third layer (via the subscription gate as a proxy) but does NOT read the first layer (tenant_configs.active) explicitly. The drift records the gap: the first-layer claim is a doctrine claim with no implementation gate today.
**Repo state:** `app/middleware/session_cookie_auth.py` line 186 (subscription gate, current). Pre-fix: `subscription = get_active_subscription_for_user(user_id); if not subscription: raise HTTPException(401)`. Post-fix: same block PLUS a new block right after the tenant_id is resolved from the session, asserting `tenant_configs.active == True` via a single-row read; failure raises 401 with a distinct error code (e.g. `TENANT_DEACTIVATED`) so audit-log searches can distinguish "subscription expired" from "tenant cascaded" in the field. The two gates are independent: a request must pass BOTH to proceed.
**Operational impact today:** Latent. The single gate works today because cascade-deactivate flips subscription.status in the same transaction as tenant_configs.active — they cannot drift in production today. The defence-in-depth value is forward-looking: every future cascade-extension Step (or schema migration that introduces a new privilege-bearing row) should not have to remember to keep the two-flag-in-one-transaction invariant; the middleware's belt-and-suspenders gate makes that invariant unnecessary at the middleware layer.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.7. Closes in umbrella's closing tag.
**Resolution path:** Single-block insertion in `session_cookie_auth.py`. (a) After `tenant_id` is resolved from the session cookie (existing code), read `tenant = db.query(TenantConfig).filter(TenantConfig.tenant_id == tenant_id).first()`. (b) If `tenant is None or not tenant.active`, raise `HTTPException(401, detail={'code': 'TENANT_DEACTIVATED'})`. (c) Existing subscription gate stays unchanged below. (d) Integration test in `tests/middleware/test_session_cookie_auth.py` seeds a session against a tenant whose `active=False` and asserts 401 with the `TENANT_DEACTIVATED` code, regardless of subscription state.
**Pattern E:** Additive — one new gate line in the existing middleware. No schema change. No change to the existing subscription gate. No customer-visible regression because no live request today fails the new gate (every live tenant has `active=True`).
**Validation evidence:** Pending. Closure: (a) `pytest tests/middleware/test_session_cookie_auth.py::test_deactivated_tenant_rejected` green with the new error code; (b) negative test: existing active-tenant requests continue to pass both gates unchanged; (c) post-deploy integration probe — a request with a session cookie pointing at `co-354c5056` (post-backfill) returns 401 `TENANT_DEACTIVATED`.
**Cross-refs:** Umbrella. ARCHITECTURE §4.7 (the three-layer claim this drift implements at the first layer). `D-cascade-missing-sessions-revocation-2026-05-20` (paired sibling — sessions layer flips status, this middleware gate is the belt against any session that slips through).

Closes inside the umbrella `~~D-tenant-cascade-privilege-revocation-hardening-2026-05-20~~` per the umbrella's resolution-path Pass 2.

**Status:** OPEN — P2 maintainability + traceability defect. Surfaced 2026-05-20 ≈14:31 UTC during the cascade source-read. The header comment on `deactivate_tenant_with_cascade` in `app/services/admin_service.py` claims "Step 30a.2 9-layer cascade" but the numbered comments through the function body run `1,2,3,2,3,4,5,6,9` — layer 2 repeats, layers 7 and 8 are missing, and the final claim of 9 layers does not match the 7 audit rows the cascade actually emits today (tenant_config, subscription, memory, api_keys, luciel_instances, agents, domain_configs). The comment-drift is the only place in the codebase where the cascade's layer-count is documented, so a future engineer reading the function reads a header claim that does not match the body and cannot count layers without running the code. The drift is small in source-character impact but disproportionate in maintainability cost — every Step that extends the cascade (Step 30a.7 today, and every future privilege-bearing-row extension) has to first re-read the comments to figure out what the cascade actually does.
**Section that raised it:** Post-Step-30a.6 cascade-audit review, 2026-05-20. Sibling A5 of umbrella.
**Raised by:** Aryan (partner) on 2026-05-20 — drift-minimisation mandate ("let us also try to minimize all our drifts as well") makes the comment-drift a first-class entry rather than a silent fix.
**Design claim:** Six-pillar doctrine commits **maintainability** as a first-class concern ("If our business is not maintainable, reliable, scalable, secure, traceable then it is not really a business"). Function-level documentation that misrepresents the function's behaviour is a direct maintainability tax — and a traceability tax (a code-reader cannot trace cascade behaviour from the comments alone).
**Repo state:** `app/services/admin_service.py` `deactivate_tenant_with_cascade` ~lines 892–1254. Pre-fix header: `"""Step 30a.2 9-layer cascade-deactivate ... """` with body comments numbered `# --- 1. conversations`, `# --- 2. identity_claims`, `# --- 3. memory_items`, `# --- 2. api_keys` (drift — should be 4), `# --- 3. luciel_instances` (drift — should be 5), `# --- 4. agents` (drift — should be 6), `# --- 5. agent_configs` (drift — should be 7), `# --- 6. domain_configs` (drift — should be 8), `# --- 9. tenant_config itself` (drift — should be 9 but skips 7/8). Post-fix header: `"""Step 30a.7 13-layer cascade-deactivate (in-function). Layers: 1=conversations, 2=identity_claims, 3=memory_items, 4=api_keys, 5=luciel_instances, 6=agents, 7=agent_configs, 8=domain_configs, 9=scope_assignments, 10=user_invites, 11=sessions, 12=synthetic_orphan_users, 13=tenant_config. Subscription cancellation is handled UPSTREAM in `app/services/billing_webhook_service.py` and emits its own audit row; the cascade in-function does not touch `subscriptions` because the Stripe-driven webhook is the source of truth for that layer (total audit-row count for a full tenant teardown is 14 = 13 in-function + 1 upstream subscription). Each in-function layer emits exactly one `cascade_deactivate`-shape audit row per touched row (with the documented exception of `user_invites` which uses `invite_revoked` to keep parity with the user-driven revoke path). ..."""`. Body comments renumbered to match the canonical 1–13 enumeration above; the four new layers (9–12) inserted in order between the existing domain_configs block and the existing tenant_config flip.
**Operational impact today:** Zero functional impact (the comment-drift does not change runtime behaviour). Impact is on the maintenance cost of every future Step that touches the cascade — Step 30a.7 itself, the Step 34a channel-cascade extension, the Step 31.x rate-limit-tier cascade if the matrix surface ever ties into deactivation, etc. The drift-minimisation mandate makes fixing it now cheaper than reading-around it on every future Step.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.7. Closes in umbrella's closing tag.
**Resolution path:** Replace the function docstring with the explicit 1–13 in-function enumeration above (with the upstream-subscription footnote so the total-teardown count of 14 audit rows is documented in-line). Renumber every body comment to match the canonical 1–13 ordering — fixes the existing `1,2,3,2,3,4,5,6,9` body-comment drift in the same diff. Append a one-line note that any future cascade-layer extension must (a) update the docstring enumeration, (b) update the body comment, (c) update the §14 matrix table, (d) update the contract test enumeration — four edits, mirroring the four-surface symmetry doctrine (the contract test in `tests/services/test_cascade_includes_all_privilege_layers.py` is the executable mirror of the docstring enumeration).
**Pattern E:** Pure-comment fix. No runtime change. No test change beyond the contract test that already enumerates layers.
**Validation evidence:** Pending. Closure: (a) `grep -n "# --- " app/services/admin_service.py` inside `deactivate_tenant_with_cascade` returns exactly 13 numbered in-function layer markers (1=conversations through 13=tenant_config) matching the docstring enumeration, with no repeats and no gaps; (b) the contract test's enumeration of expected `resource_types` matches the docstring layer list (cross-checked via the test's own docstring referencing the function's docstring).
**Cross-refs:** Umbrella. CANONICAL_RECAP §14 cascade-layer matrix (the matrix surface that mirrors this docstring). ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (cascade-layer table that mirrors this docstring). Six-pillar doctrine note (CANONICAL_RECAP §11 Q4 trust-model framing).

---

## Section 6 — How drifts are added, closed, or reopened

**Adding a drift.** Append to Section 3 (open) or Section 4 (production-pending), with a fresh `D-<slug>-YYYY-MM-DD` id, a status, the section that raised it, the design claim, the repo or prod state, and a resolution path. Do not add to closed-drift section while the drift is still open.

**Closing a drift.** Move the entry verbatim to Section 5, wrap the heading in `~~strikethrough~~`, fill in the closing commit (and tag if relevant) and a one-line resolution. Do not delete the entry from Section 3 — move it. The audit chain depends on the body of each drift remaining readable after closure.

**Reopening a drift.** Open a new drift with a fresh id and a date suffix matching the day of reopening. Reference the closed predecessor in the body. The closed predecessor stays closed; reopening is a new story.

**Marker propagation.** As drifts close, the corresponding section in `ARCHITECTURE.md` or `CANONICAL_RECAP.md` gets the appropriate ✅ / 🔧 / 📋 / 🔬 marker added in surgical edits. The marker is the connective tissue between the design docs and this register; the doc edit and the drift closure are part of the same commit.

**What does NOT belong in the design docs.** The three canonical docs (`CANONICAL_RECAP.md`, `ARCHITECTURE.md`, `DRIFTS.md`) are stable references, not running notebooks. Build-time detail — framework choice, library selection, schema column lists, transport-protocol rationale, branding-knob inventories, sandbox demo plans — belongs in **commit messages** and **code-level docstrings**, not in the canonical docs. The canonical docs grow only when the architectural shape changes: a new cross-cutting property, a new component, a deletion of something that is no longer true, or a roadmap step landing such that its success criterion is provably met. A new roadmap step, on its own, is not a reason to grow the docs — the recap row already exists, and implementation detail is recoverable from `git log` and the code itself. If a build genuinely needs a multi-day shared scratchpad, it lives in `docs/in-flight/<slug>.md` during the build and is **deleted** (not archived) on merge. This principle exists because docs that grow with every roadmap step become unparsable; the discipline of keeping them stable is what makes them useful as references.

---

## Section 7 — Source-of-truth rule

If a chat summary, a session recap, a slide, an email, or any other artifact contradicts this document about the status of a drift, **this document wins**. Update the document; do not let the contradicting artifact stand.
